Primary Antagonist/Opposition: Merrit Vane, a Pixel Prosperity Guild hardliner using a shell office called First Step Brokerage; Brindle Pact and Mira Vale, his street-level scam agents; Kessa Coil, a frightened courier carrying the registry shard; and a Debt Shade bound inside the false parcel.

Central Conflict: The party is targeted by a false debt parcel designed to make them deliver, witness, and partially validate a hidden clause that assigns them responsibility for a stranger's fabricated Tower-preparation debt. If the scam succeeds, the party begins Act I under legal debt, a frightened victim loses agency, and Merrit Vane gains fresh leverage over unaligned climbers.

Stakes: A new arrival named Sel Varrin may be bound to a debt he never understood. The party may be attached as delivery witnesses or collateral signers. The scam can block Tower registration, consume starting NC, create faction leverage, and demonstrate that safe zones do not protect against every form of harm.

Milestone Rewards: At the end of Session 3, if the party secures evidence and identifies the scam's legal mechanism, each PC gains 150 NC, one useful contact, and enough evidence to trigger the Contract Hall hearing in the next chunk. Award level 2 at the end of the Contract Hall hearing, or at the end of Session 3 if the group needs the durability before the legal confrontation and the party protected Sel from immediate binding.

## If You Are Running Tonight, Read This First

### 10-Minute Prep Version

Read the Session 1 Run Sheet, the Portal Plaza text map, and the NPC quick cards for GUIDY, Sel, Tamsin, Marik, and Chime. Copy the visible parcel text title, not the full hidden clause yet. Your only job tonight is to show safe-zone law, life counters, witnessed deals, and the silver-toothed parcel lead.

### 30-Minute Prep Version

Read the Session 1 scenes, the DM Explanation Glossary, the Clue List entries from Blinking Life Counter through Heavy Parcel Seal, and the keyed locations for Portal Plaza, Orientation Kiosk, Life Counter Fountain, and Warden Post. Put a check box beside each required Session 1 outcome.

### 60-Minute Prep Version

Read Sessions 1-3 at a skim, then deep-read the False Debt Activation Procedure, the Code Cavern Chase Tracker, and the Outcome Packages. Review the combat profiles for Panicked Novice Mob, Glitch Wisp, Debt Shade Fragment, and Warden Bluecoat Patrol. Decide before play whether level 2 is awarded at the end of Session 3 or after the hearing opens.

### Bookmark These Sections

Bookmark the Session 1 Run Sheet, DM Explanation Glossary, Opening Adventure Quick Reference, False Debt Parcel Handout, False Debt Activation Procedure, Code Cavern Chase Tracker, Opening Adventure Combat Profiles, Opening Adventure Outcome Packages, and Contract Hall Evidence Packet.

### NPC Voices That Matter Most

GUIDY is bright and too fast until it becomes genuinely worried. Sel is soft and frightened of saying the wrong thing. Marik is calm, clipped, and protective. Aria is musical in public and plain in private. Felix jokes to hide panic. Kessa sounds defensive until someone protects her.

### Print or Copy as Handouts

Copy the Session Flow table, visible False Debt Parcel Handout, Hidden Clause Text, Clue List, Evidence List, Code Cavern Round Tracker, and Outcome Packages. The hidden clause should be held until exposed.

### Do Not Worry About Yet

Do not prepare Floor 1, the full Contract Hall hearing, every faction's long-term plan, or the complete bestiary. For Sessions 1-3, the table needs the opening laws, the scam, the witnesses, the chase, and the evidence handoff.

## DM Explanation Glossary for Sessions 1-3

Use these definitions at the table the first time each term appears. The goal is clarity first, mystery second.

### Life Counter

Player-Facing Explanation: A glowing marker on or near each person's avatar shows how many lives remain. New arrivals begin at 3/3.

DM Truth: The counter is a public-facing identity checksum tied to Article I and the arrival registry.

Mechanical Effect: When a creature's death finalizes, its counter drops by 1. At 0/3, ordinary resurrection and recovery do not function.

Example in Play: Sel's counter blinks without injury because his registry entry was pinged by stolen access, not because he lost a life.

### Blue-Lit Safe Zone

Player-Facing Explanation: Blue light marks an area where direct violence and many hostile actions fail.

DM Truth: Safe zones enforce Article II through magic-code intervention, but they do not stop lies, pressure, or predatory paperwork.

Mechanical Effect: A direct attack, harmful spell, or overt violent threat locks before harm occurs. The offender can be restrained, warned, reported, or removed.

Example in Play: Tamsin's bottle freezes one inch from Warden armor, but Mira can still pressure the party with legal language inside the tavern.

### Witnessed Deal

Player-Facing Explanation: A clear agreement spoken or signed before a valid witness can become magically enforceable.

DM Truth: The law requires meaningful consent, but many residents believe form alone is enough, which predators exploit.

Mechanical Effect: Clear terms can bind payment, delivery, services, testimony, or other obligations. A flawed deal can be paused or voided with evidence.

Example in Play: Buying tea for 10 NC at Sera's stall is safe because the terms are simple and visible.

### Contract Bell

Player-Facing Explanation: A small chime signals that the Nexus has noticed a possible witnessed deal.

DM Truth: The bell rings when offer, acceptance, and witness recognition align, even if a hidden clause is trying to fake that alignment.

Mechanical Effect: A bell marks the moment legal attention begins. It does not prove the deal is valid.

Example in Play: The bell near the Orientation Kiosk rings too early because the false parcel is already trying to locate validators.

### Parcel With Teeth

Player-Facing Explanation: A sealed delivery box with tiny metal teeth around the seal. Locals recognize that as a warning sign.

DM Truth: The teeth are binding-clause clamps. They hold microtext, a witness gem, and a Debt Shade fragment in one delivery seal.

Mechanical Effect: Opening the parcel carefully can expose evidence. Delivering it blindly can trigger the hidden clause.

Example in Play: Chime's box looks like a starter kit, but its seal is stronger than ordinary courier paperwork.

### Validator Status

Player-Facing Explanation: A validator is someone the contract tries to list as confirming that a delivery or agreement happened correctly.

DM Truth: Merrit Vane wants the party listed as validators so their fresh public records make the false debt look legitimate.

Mechanical Effect: Validator status is not the same as debt ownership, but it can disadvantage legal challenges until contradicted by evidence.

Example in Play: If the party accepts handling responsibility before reading the parcel, the clause records their names as delivery validators.

### False Debt

Player-Facing Explanation: A debt someone claims is real even though the target did not knowingly agree to it.

DM Truth: The false debt uses stolen registry data, public confusion, and hidden collateral language to imitate consent.

Mechanical Effect: The debt can create price penalties, registration flags, and a legal deadline. It can be paused by objection and voided with evidence.

Example in Play: Sel is charged 900 NC for fake Tower-preparation services he never requested.

### Evidence Strength

Player-Facing Explanation: Evidence can be weak, useful, strong, or decisive depending on how directly it proves the scam.

DM Truth: The Contract Hall weighs chain of custody, witness reliability, metadata, and whether the evidence shows lack of consent.

Mechanical Effect: Stronger evidence grants advantage, reduces hearing complications, and protects witnesses from counterclaims.

Example in Play: Aria's rumor is useful; the preserved parcel seal plus registry shard is decisive.

### Criminal Heat

Player-Facing Explanation: Criminal Heat means Wardens or legal systems are watching the party for possible wrongdoing.

DM Truth: Heat is not a formal reputation score; it is immediate enforcement attention after violence, evidence damage, threats, or witness harm.

Mechanical Effect: Heat can raise DCs with Wardens, attract patrols, restrict safe-zone privileges, or complicate the hearing.

Example in Play: Killing Kessa during surrender creates Criminal Heat even if the party still recovers the shard.

### Faction Interest

Player-Facing Explanation: Faction Interest means a group has noticed the party and may offer help, pressure, or recruitment.

DM Truth: Every faction sees fresh arrival teams as future legal precedent, Tower labor, public symbols, or threats.

Mechanical Effect: Interest opens offers and rumors. Suspicion raises prices, adds watchers, or changes witness behavior.

Example in Play: A clean win draws Marik's support; a messy public brawl draws Warden suspicion and Guild spin.

## Opening Adventure Quick Reference

### Session Flow at a Glance

| Session | Primary Location | Opening Scene | Key NPCs | Required Clue or Decision | Likely Encounter | Ending Hook |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1: The First Blue Light | Portal Plaza | Safe-zone light freezes Tamsin's attack while GUIDY rushes the party | GUIDY, Tamsin, Sel, Marik, Aazoth flicker, Chime | Learn the temporary team ID was pinged and decide whether to engage with the silver-toothed parcel | Orientation social encounter and witnessed-deal demonstration | Parcel notice offers 100 NC each for pickup at Convergence Point Tavern |
| 2: The Parcel With Teeth | Convergence Point Tavern | Aria changes her song to warn the party while Chime presents the parcel | Aria, Chime, Sel, Brindle, Mira, Yorn | Detect or trigger the hidden false debt clause; identify First Step's tavern agent or Mira's ledger | False debt investigation and tavern pressure scene | Mira's trail and counterfeit guild stock point to Pixel Promenade |
| 3: Pixel Promenade and Code Cavern Chase | Pixel Promenade, then Code Caverns | Felix sees the evidence and tries to explain his involvement | Felix, Chime, Aria, Pell, Nomi, Kessa, CodeX | Trace counterfeit stock to Kessa Coil and secure the registry shard or witness statement | Promenade appraisal, public rumor pressure, Code Cavern chase | Ira Quill calls the party to Contract Hall with evidence and witnesses |

### NPC Quick Cards

#### GUIDY

Role: Guidance bot and first practical ally.

First Impression: A cheerful brass-and-blue orb trying to outrun panic with customer service.

Voice: Fast, bright, apologetic, with sudden drops into genuine concern.

Wants Right Now: Get the party registered, calm Sel, and keep anyone from signing a predatory deal.

Fear: Another first-day arrival dies or signs away a future while GUIDY explains too slowly.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: GUIDY's warning permissions are limited until a scam produces evidence.

Leverage: Knows public procedures, kiosk routes, safe-zone responses, and how to print time-stamped slips.

Useful Quote: "Great news: this is preventable. Related news: we have very little time to prevent it."

If Helped: Shares registry context early and becomes candid about orientation failures.

If Threatened: Becomes formal, records everything, and calls Marik for de-escalation.

If Betrayed: Publicly corrects the party's false claims and refuses to be used as cover.

#### Aazoth Flicker

Role: Mercy-shard presence appearing through reflections and warm light.

First Impression: A gold-white warmth in the blue fountain light, more felt than seen.

Voice: Gentle, exact, sad before the listener knows why.

Wants Right Now: Remind the party and Sel that a life counter is not personhood.

Fear: The party learns the law as a weapon before they learn mercy.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Aazoth can sense false consent but cannot overturn the Charter from the plaza.

Leverage: Can reveal emotional truth, warm a clue, or make a hidden word briefly visible.

Useful Quote: "A number is not the whole of you."

If Helped: Flickers near the next mercy-based clue.

If Threatened: Recedes; hostile force cannot compel it in Act I.

If Betrayed: Appears later only to witnesses harmed by the party, not to guide the party directly.

#### Marik Bluecoat

Role: Captain of the Guardian Wardens in Portal Plaza.

First Impression: Stern enough to stop a riot, tired enough to understand why it started.

Voice: Low, clipped, protective, careful with legal promises.

Wants Right Now: Prevent panic and obtain proof strong enough to act against false-debt brokers.

Fear: Warden hardliners use the crisis to justify harsher control.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: He knows sealed complaints against First Step exist, but he cannot cite them without a case.

Leverage: Can provide Warden notes, witness protection, legal escort, and a statement.

Useful Quote: "Law is shelter. If someone sells it as a cage, bring me the hinge."

If Helped: Supports chain of custody and speaks well of the party at intake.

If Threatened: Warns once, then documents the party as a public-risk team.

If Betrayed: Treats future party evidence as suspect until independently verified.

#### Sel Varrin

Role: Frightened new arrival and false debt target.

First Impression: A silver-freckled young man staring at his blinking life counter like it might bite.

Voice: Soft, quick, breathless when legal words start.

Wants Right Now: Find someone who can tell him what is happening without charging him for the answer.

Fear: He already made a mistake he cannot remember and everyone else knows it.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: His arrival record is unusually clean because he came through a refugee intake path; that made it easy to fake additions.

Leverage: His counter blink, recipient notice, and testimony can prove the scam targeted confusion.

Useful Quote: "If I say the wrong thing, does the city get to keep it?"

If Helped: Stays close, testifies honestly, and gives the party emotional stakes.

If Threatened: Says whatever ends the conversation, then runs to the nearest authority.

If Betrayed: Accepts a settlement from Vane's people and becomes a hostile, ashamed witness.

#### Tamsin Halewire

Role: Panicked arrival whose failed attack demonstrates safe-zone law.

First Impression: Wild-eyed, bottle frozen in blue light, furious because fear has nowhere else to go.

Voice: Hoarse, accusatory, cracking at the edges.

Wants Right Now: Force someone to admit whether he can leave.

Fear: The Nexus is permanent and his family outside will never know what happened.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: He heard a broker say panic signatures make contracts easier to process.

Leverage: Saw a First Step recruiter watching the plaza before the party arrived.

Useful Quote: "If this is safety, why does everyone look trapped?"

If Helped: Later identifies the recruiter or confirms timing.

If Threatened: Decides the party is just another uniform without armor.

If Betrayed: Repeats an ugly version of the party's actions to rumor vendors.

#### Vela Mourn

Role: Memorial keeper at the Life Counter Fountain.

First Impression: An old woman tying ribbons for names no one else is saying.

Voice: Quiet, dry, ceremonial without being soft.

Wants Right Now: Keep newcomers from treating the fountain like a scoreboard.

Fear: The city will normalize third loss until no one grieves properly.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Vela has seen Aazoth's light appear beside names that later changed legal precedent.

Leverage: Knows memorial customs, faded-name patterns, and which factions send mourners versus invoices.

Useful Quote: "Speak a name once before you study the number beside it."

If Helped: Gives a memorial ribbon and confirms the counter blink was abnormal.

If Threatened: Falls silent and lets the crowd judge.

If Betrayed: Last Light contacts hear the party disrespected the lost.

#### Chime

Role: Felix's clockwork assistant and parcel handler.

First Impression: A palm-sized brass courier with a receipt spool and a voice too formal for its tiny frame.

Voice: Clicking, precise, increasingly distressed when terms get complicated.

Wants Right Now: Complete the delivery exactly as logged and avoid being blamed for authoring it.

Fear: Felix will scrap, sell, or memory-wipe it for causing reputational damage.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Chime noticed the parcel seal was heavier than the manifest but lacks authority to refuse it.

Leverage: Has delivery timestamps, pickup authorization, and the rush courier log.

Useful Quote: "This unit processed the seal. This unit did not choose the teeth."

If Helped: Shares logs and admits the manifest mismatch.

If Threatened: Shuts down into recitation mode and records threats.

If Betrayed: Gives Felix a defensive version that omits helpful timing.

#### Aria Neon

Role: Promenade performer, rumor artist, and public-truth broker.

First Impression: A neon-ribboned star who can make an accusation sound like a chorus.

Voice: Musical, cutting in public, startlingly plain in private.

Wants Right Now: Protect her source, expose the pattern, and turn the crowd toward the truth.

Fear: A witness gets hurt because she made the story too loud too soon.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: She suppressed one previous debt story after a witness begged her not to sing it.

Leverage: Can shift public mood, identify paid distractions, and make testimony memorable.

Useful Quote: "Truth needs rhythm or the powerful call it noise."

If Helped: Broadcasts the party's clean version and shelters Brindle briefly.

If Threatened: Smiles, performs around them, and turns the room cool.

If Betrayed: Makes sure every vendor hears what the party did before they arrive.

#### Felix Pixelcoin

Role: Guild broker whose negligence enabled the parcel route.

First Impression: A smile with an invoice attached, currently sweating interest.

Voice: Warm, rapid, theatrical, with panic hidden in jokes.

Wants Right Now: Keep his name from becoming the headline while escaping Vane's trap.

Fear: Guild hardliners prove he is too soft and take his customer base.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Felix once sold a faulty extraction beacon and still pays quiet reparations.

Leverage: Has appraisal tools, delivery logs, stock-token traces, and Guild rumor channels.

Useful Quote: "I am guilty of greed, not artistry. That clause is far too ugly to be mine."

If Helped: Pays compensation, names Merrit Vane, and opens a discount line.

If Threatened: Produces records but frames the party as extortionate.

If Betrayed: Lets hardliners paint the party as debt-runners with blades.

#### Brindle Pact

Role: First Step's tavern spotter and frightened potential witness.

First Impression: A thin man in a copper scarf backing away with both hands raised.

Voice: Fast, nasal, joking because silence feels like a confession.

Wants Right Now: Escape Mira, keep his own debt hidden, and survive the evening.

Fear: His sister's room contract gets called in if he testifies.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Mira holds a ledger mark proving Brindle recruited fake witnesses twice before.

Leverage: Knows who paid tavern witnesses, when Mira arrived, and where the counterfeit token came from.

Useful Quote: "Pointing is not a crime. Probably. Please say probably."

If Helped: Gives three facts and appears at intake if protected.

If Threatened: Gives one fact, then flees through the kitchen.

If Betrayed: Signs Vane's prepared statement and claims the party coached him.

#### Mira Vale

Role: First Step field enforcer and evidence cleaner.

First Impression: A charcoal-coated professional with a gold pixel pin worn upside down.

Voice: Smooth, low, patient, every sentence shaped like a receipt.

Wants Right Now: Recover or destroy the parcel seal, ledger token, and Brindle's courage.

Fear: Merrit Vane decides she is more useful as a scapegoat than an operator.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: She kept a private copy of Vane's payment orders as insurance.

Leverage: Knows the shell office, payment chain, and which Guild clerks are compromised.

Useful Quote: "Commercial property does not become evidence because amateurs panic near it."

If Helped: Offers a narrow trade: her private copy for protection from Vane.

If Threatened: Uses safe-zone law, crowd optics, and legal warnings to make the party look dangerous.

If Betrayed: Frames the party for evidence tampering before the hearing.

#### Kessa Coil

Role: Glitch courier carrying the stolen registry shard.

First Impression: A patched silver coat vanishing down code-lit stairs, looking back with guilt.

Voice: Ragged, defensive, honest when cornered.

Wants Right Now: Sell or trade the shard for protection before Mira finds her.

Fear: Both Wardens and Codebreakers treat her as a tool, not a witness.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: She copied more names than Sel's, and one belongs to a child arrival.

Leverage: Has the shard, the K.Coil access trail, and Mira's payment instructions.

Useful Quote: "I stole names. I did not know they were going to turn them into chains."

If Helped: Gives a willing statement and warns about the additional copied names.

If Threatened: Hands over the shard but withholds Mira's private route.

If Betrayed: Runs to Nyx or Vane, whichever seems less likely to cage her.

#### Pell Tick

Role: Promenade rumor pusher and Vane's stock-board watcher.

First Impression: A neat little clerk laughing half a beat after everyone else.

Voice: Soft, oily, always phrasing insults as concern.

Wants Right Now: Make the party look indebted, reckless, or bought.

Fear: Public exposure; Pell's power depends on not being noticed.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Pell owes Vane for erasing a prior stock-board fraud.

Leverage: Can alter rumor crawl, warn Kessa, and identify which vendors will shun the party.

Useful Quote: "I merely repeat market confidence. If confidence wounds, blame the market."

If Helped: Trades a watcher list for immunity from public embarrassment.

If Threatened: Triggers a safe-zone complaint and plays victim.

If Betrayed: Starts a rumor that the party forged their own evidence for a payout.

#### Yorn Glass

Role: Convergence Point tavern keeper and neutral witness.

First Impression: Broad, polished, and impossible to rush, cleaning a glass that is already clean.

Voice: Deep, slow, practical.

Wants Right Now: Keep the tavern safe, legal, and open.

Fear: Convergence Point loses safe-zone certification over someone else's scam.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Yorn pays extra for private witness-light maintenance after an old brawl nearly killed a patron outside the door.

Leverage: Controls booth access, house witness records, and who gets barred.

Useful Quote: "My house allows grief, lies, singing, and bad flirting. It does not allow traps."

If Helped: Provides a private booth and preserves tavern witness-light memory.

If Threatened: Bars the party for the night and gives Marik a clean report.

If Betrayed: Sides with the Ledger Court against the party's chain of custody.

#### Nomi Sweetspark

Role: Promenade food-cart owner and witness to Code Cavern traffic.

First Impression: A halfling vendor frying sugar-crack cakes under a sign that reads EAT BEFORE BAD CHOICES.

Voice: Bright, blunt, affectionate toward paying customers and lost causes.

Wants Right Now: Sell snacks, keep kids away from the stairs, and warn decent people before they descend.

Fear: Someone dies in the Caverns and her last words to them were an upsell.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Nomi quietly feeds Codebreaker lookouts in exchange for warnings about unsafe glitches.

Leverage: Saw Kessa enter, knows Pell's watcher habits, and sells a minor healing snack.

Useful Quote: "Code stairs after panic? That is either courage or low blood sugar."

If Helped: Points out Kessa's route and offers one discounted healing snack.

If Threatened: Shouts for the Promenade crowd and ruins any stealthy descent.

If Betrayed: Tells CodeX the party treats small vendors as scenery.

#### Merrit Vane

Role: Hidden antagonist, Guild hardliner, and owner of First Step Brokerage.

First Impression: Not present in person during Sessions 1-3; appears through polished clauses, paid watchers, and people afraid to name him.

Voice: When heard through messages, elegant, paternal, and cruelly calm.

Wants Right Now: Test the false-debt method, capture leverage over fresh climbers, and let Felix take blame.

Fear: A clean public case proves his debt model violates meaningful consent.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Vane's old contracts depend on the same validator logic; this case can unravel more than Sel's debt.

Leverage: Controls First Step, several Guild clerks, prepared settlement offers, and debt records.

Useful Quote: "Order is expensive. I merely ask beneficiaries to contribute."

If Helped: Offers a settlement that looks generous and preserves his system.

If Threatened: Uses lawyers, rumor boards, and witness intimidation rather than blades.

If Betrayed: Makes the party a test case for aggressive debt enforcement.

### Minor NPC Expanded Cards

Use these fuller entries when a scene slows down around a table-facing NPC. They are written to answer the DM's immediate questions: what the NPC knows, what they hide, and what makes them move.

#### Sel Varrin

Appearance: Young human-presenting avatar with silver freckles, a gray arrival cloak, and a life counter that glows too brightly because he keeps checking it.

Voice: Soft, quick, apologetic; he asks questions like he is afraid questions cost money.

Mannerism: Presses thumb to life counter when overwhelmed.

Want: Safety, plain answers, and proof that he has not already ruined his new life.

Fear: A single wrong sentence will bind him to a debt he cannot pay.

Secret: Sel remembers Aazoth saying, "Not this one," but he thinks admitting it will make him sound unstable.

Leverage: Recipient notice, blinking counter, and testimony about confusion at the moment of delivery.

What They Know: His counter blinked before he touched the parcel; he never ordered Tower-preparation services; the parcel called him by name.

What They Lie About: He says he is fine after public embarrassment. He is not.

What They Offer: Honest testimony, emotional stakes, and the exact words Chime used before delivery.

What Makes Them Help: Calm explanation, protection from public shame, or a PC admitting they are also afraid.

What Makes Them Flee: Legal jargon, raised voices, being treated like evidence instead of a person.

What Makes Them Betray: A settlement offer that promises the debt disappears if he signs a statement blaming the party.

Sample Dialogue: "Please say that again like I am a person, not a form."

Connection to a Clue: His blinking life counter proves registry contact before consent.

Connection to a Faction: Ledger Court wants his testimony; Pixel Prosperity hardliners want his silence.

Likely First Scene: Safe-Zone Snap in Portal Plaza.

Consequence If Ignored: He accepts the parcel or settlement from the first confident adult-sounding authority who offers relief.

#### Chime

Appearance: Palm-sized brass courier construct with blue enamel fins, a receipt spool, and tiny clamp-hands polished by constant filing.

Voice: Clipped, procedural, musical when relieved.

Mannerism: Prints duplicate receipts when anxious, then apologizes to the duplicates.

Want: Complete logged duties without becoming the cause of harm.

Fear: Being reset for a mistake it was not authorized to understand.

Secret: Chime flagged the parcel's seal weight internally but Felix's rush queue overrode the warning.

Leverage: Delivery logs, seal weight mismatch, pickup timestamp, and Felix authorization route.

What They Know: The parcel came through a rush route; First Step's seal was heavier than declared; Felix did not personally inspect it.

What They Lie About: "All seals are within ordinary variance." Chime says this only while in defensive recitation mode.

What They Offer: Manifest log, courier timestamp, and a witness to the visible handling terms.

What Makes Them Help: Treating Chime as a witness with limited authority rather than a villain.

What Makes Them Flee: Threats of dismantling, blame shouted at Felix in Chime's presence, or attempts to pry open its casing.

What Makes Them Betray: Felix ordering it into legal defense mode before the party earns its trust.

Sample Dialogue: "This unit can confirm the box was too heavy for kindness."

Connection to a Clue: Manifest mismatch exposes the false parcel's hidden payload.

Connection to a Faction: Pixel Prosperity Guild through Felix, but its records can aid Ledger Court.

Likely First Scene: Witnessed Deal Demonstration or parcel niche.

Consequence If Ignored: The party loses a neutral witness who can separate Felix's negligence from Vane's design.

#### Brindle Pact

Appearance: Narrow-shouldered man with copper scarf, ink-stained cuffs, and shoes chosen for quiet exits.

Voice: Nasal, quick, joking in bursts that collapse into pleading.

Mannerism: Checks balcony exits after every sentence.

Want: Get out from under Mira's thumb without taking his sister down with him.

Fear: His sister's room contract becomes due the moment he testifies.

Secret: He recruited fake witnesses for two earlier First Step deliveries and kept one payment token.

Leverage: Names of paid tavern witnesses, Mira's arrival time, and the counterfeit stock token.

What They Know: First Step paid him to steer attention; Mira carries a ledger case; Kessa moved a registry shard.

What They Lie About: "I only pointed once." He pointed twice before this job.

What They Offer: Three facts, a token, and testimony if protected by Ira or Marik.

What Makes Them Help: A concrete protection offer for his sister, not a moral lecture.

What Makes Them Flee: Public accusations, direct threats, or seeing Mira at the door.

What Makes Them Betray: Vane offering to erase his sister's debt for a signed statement against the party.

Sample Dialogue: "I am very brave from three streets away."

Connection to a Clue: His token links tavern pressure to counterfeit Guild routing.

Connection to a Faction: First Step shell office; possible Ledger Court protected witness.

Likely First Scene: Aria's Warning Song or Brindle Pact's Standoff.

Consequence If Ignored: Mira reaches him first and his later statement becomes hostile or missing.

#### Mira Vale

Appearance: Tall woman in a charcoal coat, mirror-polished boots, and a gold pixel pin worn upside down as a hardliner sign.

Voice: Low, controlled, professional; she never sounds rushed unless the party mentions Vane.

Mannerism: Smooths her cuffs before lying.

Want: Recover the parcel seal, neutralize Brindle, and keep Vane's name out of the first report.

Fear: Vane sacrifices her as a rogue operator.

Secret: She kept a private insurance copy of payment orders in a split ledger token.

Leverage: Payment chain, intimidation over Brindle, and knowledge of which clerks are compromised.

What They Know: First Step is Vane's shell, Kessa has the shard, and Felix is being positioned as blame sponge.

What They Lie About: She claims the parcel is only commercial property and that First Step provides legitimate orientation aid.

What They Offer: A settlement, a partial ledger copy, or a name lower than Vane if she is cornered.

What Makes Them Help: Proof that Vane will abandon her and a credible promise of protection.

What Makes Them Flee: Public exposure in front of neutral witnesses.

What Makes Them Betray: Any sign the party cannot protect her from both Wardens and Vane.

Sample Dialogue: "You are confusing possession with proof. New arrivals do that."

Connection to a Clue: Her ledger token proves field payments.

Connection to a Faction: Pixel Prosperity Guild hardliners and First Step Brokerage.

Likely First Scene: Mira Vale at the Door.

Consequence If Ignored: She destroys or reframes the strongest evidence before the hearing.

#### Kessa Coil

Appearance: Wiry courier in a patched silver coat, hair tied with broken data-cord, registry shard glowing at her throat.

Voice: Ragged, defensive, fast when running, painfully young when cornered.

Mannerism: Touches the shard before every hard truth.

Want: Trade the shard for protection and avoid becoming the only criminal named.

Fear: Wardens cage her, Codebreakers exploit her, or Vane erases her.

Secret: She copied more arrival names than she admits at first.

Leverage: Registry shard, K.Coil access path, payment instructions, and confession about Mira.

What They Know: Mira paid her; First Step wanted fresh arrival data; the collateral language was hidden until after pickup.

What They Lie About: "I only copied Sel." She copied a small batch and knows that makes her look worse.

What They Offer: Shard, statement, route to Mira's drop point, and warning about additional targets.

What Makes Them Help: Being rescued from the Mercy Gap, offered witness protection, or promised she will not be handed to Vane.

What Makes Them Flee: A drawn weapon, Warden-first language, or CodeX demanding the shard like property.

What Makes Them Betray: A faction making her believe the party will trade her for a clean record.

Sample Dialogue: "I can be guilty without being the author."

Connection to a Clue: Her shard is decisive evidence of stolen registry data.

Connection to a Faction: Hired by First Step, watched by Codebreakers, wanted by Wardens.

Likely First Scene: Code Cavern Chase.

Consequence If Ignored: The shard enters faction circulation and the hearing loses its cleanest proof.

#### Pell Tick

Appearance: Neat gnome or halfling-presenting clerk in market-gray, with a smile that arrives slightly late.

Voice: Soft, oily, always disappointed on someone else's behalf.

Mannerism: Taps two fingers against the nearest signboard before rumors update.

Want: Make the party look unreliable before evidence reaches the Court.

Fear: Being named in public with the stock board still glowing behind him.

Secret: Vane covered Pell's previous market manipulation in exchange for future rumor work.

Leverage: Stock-board access, vendor whisper network, and early warning to Kessa.

What They Know: The party's debt status, Vane's preferred rumor line, and which vendors scare easily.

What They Lie About: "The board updates automatically." Pell manually feeds phrasing.

What They Offer: Watcher list, vendor correction, and a route to a lower clerk if spared embarrassment.

What Makes Them Help: Private exposure with a path to avoid public ruin.

What Makes Them Flee: Aria turning the crowd toward him or a PC cutting off his signboard access.

What Makes Them Betray: Public humiliation; Pell becomes vindictive fast.

Sample Dialogue: "Reputation is not a weapon. It is weather. I merely forecast."

Connection to a Clue: His rumor push reveals Vane's active cover story.

Connection to a Faction: Pixel Prosperity Guild hardliners.

Likely First Scene: Promenade Pressure.

Consequence If Ignored: Vendors raise prices and Kessa begins the chase warned.

#### Yorn Glass

Appearance: Broad-shouldered tavern keeper with glass-bead braids, immaculate apron, and forearms marked by old safe-zone warning scars.

Voice: Slow, deep, practical; never competes with the room.

Mannerism: Cleans one glass through every lie.

Want: Keep Convergence Point safe, certified, and trusted by people with nowhere else to sit.

Fear: A debt scam inside his tavern costs him safe-zone certification.

Secret: Yorn pays for illegal extra witness-light backups after losing a patron outside the east door years ago.

Leverage: Booth access, house witness-light records, staff testimony, and authority to bar troublemakers.

What They Know: Brindle used the balcony twice this week; Mira came through the east door; Aria warned him something was wrong.

What They Lie About: He says his witness lights are standard. They are better than standard.

What They Offer: Private booth, witness-light memory, staff statement, and one night of safe lodging for Sel.

What Makes Them Help: Protecting the tavern's safety and treating staff as witnesses.

What Makes Them Flee: He does not flee; he ends the scene by calling Wardens and shutting doors.

What Makes Them Betray: Evidence tampering inside the tavern or a party member threatening staff.

Sample Dialogue: "I have thrown out better liars than you and worse heroes than them."

Connection to a Clue: House witness memory can confirm Mira and Brindle's movements.

Connection to a Faction: Neutral business under Ledger Court and Warden certification.

Likely First Scene: Convergence Point Tavern.

Consequence If Ignored: The party loses neutral venue support and a strong witness-memory source.

#### Nomi Sweetspark

Appearance: Halfling food vendor with cinnamon on her sleeves, spark-gloves, and a cart full of sugar-crack cakes shaped like tiny shields.

Voice: Bright, blunt, fast; she gives advice as if it comes free with napkins.

Mannerism: Points with tongs, never fingers.

Want: Sell food, keep reckless people fed, and keep children away from the Code Cavern Stairs.

Fear: Someone goes down those stairs hungry, dizzy, and doomed.

Secret: Nomi trades free meals to Codebreaker lookouts for warnings about unstable tunnel days.

Leverage: Saw Kessa enter, knows Pell's habits, and can provide a minor healing snack.

What They Know: Kessa was scared, Pell watched the stairs, and CodeX's chalk appeared before dawn.

What They Lie About: She calls the healing snack "just sugar." It includes a tiny legal stimulant.

What They Offer: Route warning, discounted snack, crowd cover, and a plain-language read on Promenade mood.

What Makes Them Help: Buying food, protecting a child or newcomer, or thanking her without condescension.

What Makes Them Flee: Direct violence near her cart or attempts to steal from it.

What Makes Them Betray: Mocking small vendors or bringing Warden trouble to her Codebreaker arrangement.

Sample Dialogue: "Eat. Then chase your criminal. Heroics on an empty stomach is how boots meet ceiling."

Connection to a Clue: She confirms Kessa's route into the Code Caverns.

Connection to a Faction: Informal tie to Codebreakers; public tie to Promenade vendors.

Likely First Scene: Pixel Promenade.

Consequence If Ignored: The party enters the chase without her route warning or healing option.

## Name Load Manager for the Opening Adventure

The opening uses many named people, but the DM does not need to put every name in front of the players at once. Use this manager to keep the table focused.

| Category | NPCs | Use at Table |
|---|---|---|
| Must appear on-screen | GUIDY, Sel Varrin, Tamsin Halewire, Marik Bluecoat, Chime, Aria Neon, Felix Pixelcoin, Kessa Coil | These NPCs teach core rules, carry the scam, or hold required evidence. Do not cut them. |
| Can appear if needed | Aazoth flicker, Vela Mourn, Sera Cupwise, Bram Lilt, Warden Lio Brass, Yorn Glass, Brindle Pact, Mira Vale, Nomi Sweetspark, Pell Tick, CodeX | Use these when the party follows the relevant clue, needs a backup source, or wants social depth. |
| Mention only | Merrit Vane, First Step Brokerage, Ira Quill, Rutha Pell, Nyx Understep, Elektra Sparkblade, Mina Redline, Professor Ilyra Venn, Ossa Kline | Mention through evidence, messages, rumors, or background hooks. They do not need full scenes in Sessions 1-3. |
| Save for later | Magistrate Orvan Hex, Mother Vey, Orris Map-Eye, full Spire Seeker rival party, deeper faction leaders | Keep these names out of active play unless a PC background specifically calls them in. |

If Players Look Overwhelmed: Combine Sera Cupwise and Vela Mourn into one gentle public explainer at the fountain stalls. Combine Yorn Glass and Aria's practical clue delivery, letting Yorn provide the room and Aria provide public pressure. Let Pell Tick remain an unnamed watcher until Session 3. Refer to Merrit Vane only as "the senior broker behind First Step" until the players ask for his name.

If Players Want More Social Depth: Split the public scene into smaller conversations. Let Vela discuss Article I, Sera demonstrate witnessed deals, Yorn protect the tavern, Brindle confess under fear, Nomi warn about the stairs, and Pell show how reputation can be weaponized.

NPCs That Can Be Renamed or Delayed: Sera Cupwise, Bram Lilt, Warden Lio Brass, Rutha Pell, Ossa Kline, Nomi Sweetspark, and Pell Tick can be renamed freely. Vela, Yorn, and Brindle can be delayed by one session without breaking continuity.

NPCs That Must Not Be Cut: GUIDY, Sel, Chime, Aria, Felix, Kessa, and the offscreen name First Step Brokerage. Marik can be delayed, but a Warden authority must exist if the party asks for law.

Continuity-Safe Role Combines: Chime can carry Felix's delivery log if Felix is delayed. Aria can point to Brindle's clue if Brindle flees unseen. Nomi can give CodeX's route hint if CodeX is being saved for later. Marik can send Ira's first message if the table has not met Ira by name.

### Clue List

| Blinking Life Counter | Sel's record was touched remotely | Portal Plaza, Life Counter Fountain | Comfort Sel and watch his counter during the panic | DC 15 Investigation identifies outside registry ping | Sel remains vulnerable and confused | GUIDY error slip |
| Early Contract Bell | A deal signal is firing before any honest agreement | Portal Plaza, Orientation Kiosk | Ask GUIDY why a bell rang | DC 13 Arcana reads false witness alignment | The parcel seems more normal | Sera's witnessed tea sale |
| K.Coil Courier Tag | A courier accessed the party's temporary team ID | Orientation Kiosk | Ask GUIDY for the time-stamped registry slip | DC 15 tools or Arcana retrieves the tag | Kessa starts as an unknown runner | Felix's token trace |

| Shard Resonance | The registry shard contains party and Sel metadata | Glitch Tunnel | Catch Kessa or recover the shard sliver | DC 14 Investigation copies metadata safely | Hearing starts with disputed records | GUIDY plus Felix logs |
| Kessa's Confession | Kessa stole names but did not author the debt | Code Cavern chase | Rescue Kessa at the Mercy Gap | DC 13 Persuasion secures willing statement | Kessa becomes fugitive or hostile | CodeX recorded echo |
| Vane's Name | Merrit Vane owns the shell route | Felix, Kessa, or Mira's records | Treat Felix or Kessa as useful witnesses | DC 16 Persuasion with Felix or DC 14 Investigation on shard | The hearing names First Step before Vane | Brindle under protection |

### Evidence List

| Evidence Name | Source | What It Proves | Strength | Who Challenges It | How to Strengthen It | Risk If Mishandled |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| GUIDY Registry Slip | Orientation Kiosk | Outside access touched the party's temporary team ID | Useful | Vane claims harmless system error | Pair with shard metadata | Slip fades if not sealed before hearing |
| Clear-Terms Receipt | Sera Cupwise | Normal witnessed deals show clear visible terms | Weak | Opposing counsel calls it irrelevant | Use as contrast during testimony | Can distract from stronger proof |
| Preserved Parcel Seal | False debt parcel | Binding teeth and witness gem were built into the delivery | Strong | Mira claims chain of custody break | Store in sealed evidence case | Broken seal weakens microtext proof |
| Hidden Microtext Copy | Parcel teeth | Clause tried to attach validators and collateral | Decisive | Vane claims altered copy | Have Chime, Ira, or Yorn witness the copy | Bad copy looks forged |
| Chime Manifest Log | Chime/Felix | Parcel seal weight did not match logged contents | Useful | Felix's rivals claim Chime malfunction | Combine with Felix's delivery log | Threatened Chime gives brittle testimony |
| Aria's Stage Ribbon Archive | Aria's Stage | Delivery was timed to performance distraction | Useful | Vane calls it entertainment, not evidence | Add Yorn's witness-light memory | Public broadcast can expose witnesses |
| Brindle's Statement | Brindle Pact | First Step paid tavern spotters | Strong if protected, weak if coerced | Mira attacks his debt history | Give Ira protection before statement | Threats make him look coached |
| First Step Token | Brindle or tavern floor | Links tavern spotter to shell office | Useful | Guild clerk calls it counterfeit junk | Appraise at Felix's stall | Lost token forces reliance on testimony |
| Mira's Ledger Token | Mira Vale | Field payments connect to First Step | Strong | Mira claims stolen private property | Copy metadata before handoff | Theft accusation creates Criminal Heat |
| Felix Delivery Log | Felix's stall | Rush job routed through counterfeit stock | Strong | Vane blames Felix's negligence | Pair with counterfeit stock analysis | Publicly humiliating Felix limits cooperation |
| Counterfeit Guild Stock Analysis | Felix's Appraisal Stall | Routing token was forged through Guild hardliner methods | Strong | Guild hardliners dispute Felix's neutrality | Have independent tool check by CodeX or Ledger clerk | If Felix alone verifies it, bias claim sticks |
| Kessa Registry Shard | Code Caverns | K.Coil copied party and Sel records | Decisive | Wardens question illegal custody | Seal copy with Marik, Ira, or CodeX metadata | Giving sole copy to one faction creates spin |
| Kessa's Willing Statement | Kessa Coil | Mira paid for registry names and Kessa saw hidden collateral later | Strong | Vane attacks her theft and motive | Protect her and record before witness mote | Dead or coerced Kessa weakens case |
| CodeX Route Glyph | Code Cavern Stairs/Glitch Tunnel | Shard path began at Orientation Kiosk ping | Useful | Wardens distrust illegal source | Redact exploit details through Ira | Full leak exposes registry vulnerability |
| Sel's Recipient Notice | Sel's life counter/profile | Sel was targeted as named debtor | Useful | Vane claims Sel accepted aid | Pair with lack of clear service record | Sel accepting settlement undercuts it |
| Yorn's House Witness Memory | Convergence Point Tavern | Mira demanded commercial property and Brindle fled under fear | Useful | Mira claims tavern bias toward Aria | Have Yorn provide neutral statement | Damaged tavern trust can close this route |

### Faction Reaction Snapshot

| Faction | Before Session 1 | Interested By | Suspicious When | Offers | Demands | Clean Win | Messy Win | Public Trouble |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Guardian Wardens | Watching new-arrival scams but short on admissible proof | Preserved records, calm de-escalation, protected witnesses | Threats in safe zones, broken evidence, dead courier | Chain-of-custody help, escort, Marik statement | Evidence kept intact and witnesses alive | Marik supports intake and quiet protection | Marik helps but adds a warning note | Patrol attention, higher social DCs with Wardens |
| Pixel Prosperity Guild | Publicly confident, privately split between Felix and hardliners | Counterfeit stock proof, careful distinction between Felix and Vane | Public blame on the whole Guild, threats to clerks | Appraisal, compensation, delivery logs | Do not turn negligence into total Guild war | Felix aids party and hardliners retreat | Felix helps defensively; prices wobble | Hardliners paint party as anti-commerce |
| Spire Seekers | Treating new arrivals as possible future rivals | Courage under pressure and public competence | Cowardice, debt stigma, harming witnesses | Route rumors, public challenge, early training lead | Prove the party is not dead weight | Elektra hears good things before Forecourt | Seekers mock and test them harder | Rival teams use the scandal for clout |
| Codebreakers | Monitoring registry vulnerability from the edges | Shard recovery, clever system handling, restraint with CodeX | Giving everything to Wardens, destroying exploit data | Route hint, sealed copy, backdoor context | A redacted copy or promise of later access | CodeX respects the party's balance | CodeX helps but leaks partial pressure | Radicals try to steal the shard |
| Remnant Veil | Suspects debt law is another control tool | Protecting Kessa, resisting hardline ownership | Blind trust in Wardens or public exposure of vulnerable witnesses | Safe route, witness hiding, rumor counterspin | Keep coercive law from gaining more power | Nyx marks party as possible anti-tyrant allies | Veil offers help with strings | Veil frames chaos as proof law fails |
| Ledger Court | Waiting for a clean case to test consent standards | Preserved clause, willing witnesses, clear chain | Coerced testimony, damaged seals, public threats | Intake, witness bell, hearing docket | Precise claims and no settlement without review | Ira fast-tracks review; Orvan takes interest | Court accepts case but adds scrutiny | Clause Bailiff pressure and procedural delays |

### Background

Merrit Vane is a senior broker in the Pixel Prosperity Guild's old guard. He believes new arrivals are volatile assets and that debt is the cleanest way to make them predictable. Felix Pixelcoin, a younger broker with a conscience he tries to disguise as branding, has been drawing customers away from Vane's harder contracts. Vane wants to embarrass Felix, test a new false-debt method, and capture leverage over a fresh adventuring party before another faction recruits them.

The false debt parcel was created by First Step Brokerage, Vane's shell office. It looks like a sealed starter-kit delivery: orientation vouchers, a tavern meal token, a cheap healing chit, and a route pamphlet. Hidden inside the seal is a clause-spirit called a Debt Shade, a predatory legal echo that animates when the parcel is delivered before a witness and the recipient speaks acceptance language. The clause names Sel Varrin as debtor, lists "arrival team witnesses" as delivery validators, and attempts to attach the party's future Tower rewards as secondary collateral if they accept payment for delivery without objection.

The party is targeted because the arrival registry glitched during their first minutes in Portal Plaza. Kessa Coil stole a registry shard containing the party's temporary arrival-team ID. Vane's agents used that ID to prepare the parcel, betting that brand-new characters would take a simple paid job from a smiling broker and deliver it without reading legal text. If the party includes a Brokered Deal or Contract Hall Scribe, Vane's copyists also use a forged filing mark connected to that PC to make the parcel harder to dismiss.

Felix did not create the scam. He did accept a rush courier commission from First Step Brokerage without inspecting the inner clause because he wanted quick profit and assumed the job was merely tacky. Aria Neon has heard enough from frightened performers and tavern staff to suspect a debt trap. GUIDY sees the registry mismatch but lacks permission to accuse a contract without evidence. Aazoth senses false consent but can only flicker near reflective surfaces. Marik knows new-arrival scams are rising and wants proof strong enough to survive the Ledger Court.

The party can discover that the parcel is false through at least three clue paths: the registry mismatch in Portal Plaza, Aria's witness account at Convergence Point Tavern, Felix's counterfeit guild stock clue in Pixel Promenade, and Kessa Coil's registry shard in the Code Caverns. They do not need every clue. They need enough evidence to show that the deal lacked informed consent, used stolen registry data, and was prepared by First Step Brokerage.

### Adventure Hooks

Standard Arrival Hook: GUIDY flags the party as an unassigned arrival team standing closest to a registry glitch. It asks them to help calm a crowd and verify their names. During the process, a parcel notice appears with their temporary team ID.

Faction Hook: Marik Bluecoat asks the party to report anything that links false debts to stolen registry records. He cannot deputize them, but he can promise a Warden statement if they preserve evidence.

Personal PC Hook: A PC with Brokered Deal, Contract Hall Scribe, Portal Refugee, Failed Ascendant, or Tower Runner background recognizes a detail: a copied filing mark, a refugee registry vulnerability, a fake route tag, or a sponsor phrase used in bad contracts.

Debt/Need Hook: Felix Pixelcoin offers 100 NC per PC for a simple sealed-parcel delivery to Convergence Point Tavern, payable on return. New characters with limited funds have good reason to accept, and suspicious characters have good reason to inspect the offer.

## Session 1 Run Sheet: The First Blue Light

### What This Session Must Accomplish

- Players understand that life counters exist and begin at 3/3.
- Players see blue-lit safe-zone law stop direct violence.
- Players meet GUIDY and understand it is helpful but limited.
- Players notice Sel's counter anomaly or receive GUIDY's registry slip.
- Players learn witnessed deals exist and can bind clear agreements.
- Players encounter the contract bell anomaly.
- Players receive or become aware of the silver-toothed parcel lead.

### What the DM Tracks

| Track | 0 State | 1 State | 2 State |
|---|---|---|---|
| Sel Trust | Sel flees or accepts the first authority voice | Sel stays nearby but needs reassurance | Sel trusts one PC and volunteers details |
| Tamsin Panic | Tamsin is restrained and angry | Tamsin calms after Warden warning | Tamsin gives a useful observation about First Step |
| GUIDY Trust | GUIDY goes formal and records everything | GUIDY gives normal orientation help | GUIDY shares concern before permission is clean |
| Marik Respect | Marik sees risky newcomers | Marik sees useful witnesses | Marik offers a statement or escort |
| Public Attention | Rumor vendors mock the party | Crowd knows the party helped | Crowd repeats the party's version |
| First Step Suspicion | Parcel seems ordinary | First Step name appears as odd | Party knows the team ID and parcel are connected |
| Evidence Gained | No physical proof | One slip, receipt, or witness | Two or more: registry slip, clear-terms receipt, counter anomaly, parcel warning |

### Scene Order If the Table Is Moving Fast

For a 60-90 minute Session 1, run only these beats: opening read-aloud and Safe-Zone Snap; GUIDY explains life counters at the Orientation Kiosk; the Life Counter Fountain shows Sel's blink and Aazoth's warmth; Sera's tea sale demonstrates witnessed deals; Marik and GUIDY present the silver-toothed parcel notice. Give the party one meaningful choice at the end: accept, inspect later, refuse, or protect Sel.

### Scene Order If the Table Roleplays Heavily

For a 3-4 hour Session 1, let players describe avatar senses before the panic, then run Safe-Zone Snap with separate chances to calm Tamsin and Sel. Give GUIDY time to answer questions badly but earnestly. Let Vela and the fountain create a quieter life-counter scene. Run Sera and Bram as a full witnessed-deal demonstration. Let Marik talk privately with the party. End with Chime or the kiosk presenting the parcel lead.

### Do Not Forget

- Show the bottle freezing in blue light.
- Say each PC sees or can access a 3/3 life counter.
- Make Sel's counter blink before the parcel appears.
- Let the contract bell ring before anyone knowingly agrees to a major deal.
- Demonstrate one harmless witnessed deal.
- Mention that safe zones stop violence but not bad bargains.
- End with the silver-toothed parcel lead or Sel receiving it if the party refuses.

## If Players Do Nothing: Session 1

After 1 minute: Blue light restrains Tamsin, the crowd backs away, and GUIDY asks the party for help because they are closest to Sel.

After 5 minutes: Marik's patrol removes Tamsin. Sel moves toward the Orientation Kiosk alone. The party can still follow.

After 10 minutes: The kiosk prints the parcel notice directly to Sel. GUIDY projects an urgent warning to the party.

After 30 minutes: Sel reaches Convergence Point Tavern without the party, where Chime prepares the parcel and Aria begins her warning song.

End of Session Consequence: The party starts Session 2 with Sel's trust at 0, GUIDY trust at 0 or 1, and the false debt one step closer to activation. They can still intervene at the tavern.

### Session 1: The First Blue Light

Session 1 opens in motion. The characters arrive in Portal Plaza as a safe-zone intervention stops a panicked attack, a registry glitch mislabels the party, and GUIDY tries to orient everyone before a bad first choice becomes binding.

#### Opening Read-Aloud

Read this when play begins:

> Darkness becomes blue light.
>
> Your feet meet glassy stone veined with glowing circuit-lines. Noise hits next: bells, voices, distant music, someone laughing too loudly, someone else sobbing with both hands over a floating number at their chest. Above the plaza, portal constellations turn in a daylight sky. At the city's center, impossibly tall, a black tower climbs until perspective gives up.
>
> A stranger lunges at a Warden with a broken bottle. Blue light snaps between them. The bottle freezes an inch from armor. The stranger's arm locks in place, trembling, while calm words appear in the air: ARTICLE II SAFE-ZONE INTERVENTION ACTIVE.
>
> A brass-and-blue orb zips toward you, fins fluttering. "Hello! Welcome! Please do not panic in a legally actionable direction. I am GUIDY, and I need you to step away from the frozen assault, the crying man, and the contract bell that absolutely should not be ringing yet."

Give players a moment to describe their avatars, visible gear, and immediate reactions. Then begin Scene 1.

#### Portal Plaza Text Map

Use this map for Session 1. Distances are approximate; the whole plaza is a safe zone.

```
                         North: Tower Forecourt Road
              [Warden Post]----[Charter Wall]----[Permit Queue]
                    |                |                 |
West: Market Walk --+-- [Life Counter Fountain] --+-- East: Portal Kiosks
                    |                |                 |
          [Arrival Dais]----[Orientation Kiosk]----[Blue Awning Stalls]
                         South: Convergence Steps
```

Key movement notes:

- Arrival Dais to Life Counter Fountain: 40 feet.
- Fountain to Warden Post: 50 feet.
- Fountain to Orientation Kiosk: 30 feet.
- Orientation Kiosk to Convergence Steps: 60 feet.
- The frozen assault occurs between the Arrival Dais and Warden Post.
- The first suspicious clue appears at the Orientation Kiosk.

#### Scene 1: Safe-Zone Snap

Purpose: Teach safe-zone law through immediate tension and give players their first chance to protect someone without fighting.

Read-Aloud:

> The frozen stranger strains against blue light. His bottle cannot move, but his voice can. "You said we could leave! You said the portals were free!" Around him, new arrivals back away from the Warden line. A young man with silver freckles clutches his life counter and whispers, "Mine blinked. Why did mine blink?"

DM Truth: The stranger is Tamsin Halewire, a terrified arrival who tried to force a Warden to open an outbound portal. The Warden is not hurt. The blinking life counter belongs to Sel Varrin, whose temporary arrival record was copied by Kessa Coil minutes ago. The safe-zone intervention is functioning correctly, but the crowd thinks someone almost died.

NPCs Present: GUIDY; Tamsin Halewire, panicked arrival; Sel Varrin, frightened new arrival; Warden Lio Brass; Marik Bluecoat watching from the Warden Post.

Player Options: Calm Tamsin, reassure Sel, ask GUIDY questions, challenge the Warden, inspect the blue light, help clear the crowd, or search for the source of the contract bell.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 12 Charisma (Persuasion) to calm Tamsin enough that he stops shouting.
- DC 13 Wisdom (Insight) to realize Tamsin is more afraid than violent.
- DC 13 Intelligence (Arcana) to understand that the safe-zone field prevented harm before impact.
- DC 14 Charisma (Persuasion) or Wisdom (Medicine) to steady Sel.
- DC 15 Intelligence (Investigation) to notice Sel's life counter blinked because his registry entry was pinged from outside the plaza.

Success Result: The party calms the crowd, earns GUIDY's trust, and Marik approaches respectfully. Tamsin is released with a warning instead of restraint. Sel stays nearby and becomes available as a witness later.

Partial Success Result: The immediate panic eases, but Tamsin is escorted to the Warden Post and resents the party if they sounded judgmental. Sel bolts toward the Orientation Kiosk, where the party can still find him in Scene 2.

Failure Result: The crowd surges. No one is injured because the plaza is safe, but evidence becomes harder to spot. The party has disadvantage on the first Investigation check in Scene 2 unless they spend time helping GUIDY restore order. Marik still intervenes before the scene stalls.

Clues:

- Sel's life counter blinked without injury, showing that records can be touched remotely.
- The contract bell rang even though no one nearby knowingly made a deal.
- The blue safe-zone field stops violence but does not stop fear, confusion, or legal signals.

Consequences: If the party treats Tamsin with mercy, GUIDY marks them as "low-risk helpers" and volunteers extra context in later scenes. If they mock or threaten him, Aria hears about it before Session 2 and opens colder.

#### Scene 2: GUIDY's Orientation Spiral

Purpose: Introduce GUIDY, the life counter, the Charter warning, and the first suspicious registry clue.

Read-Aloud:

> GUIDY projects a neat blue checklist into the air. It immediately multiplies into six checklists, three warning icons, and a tiny printed ticket that reads: SORRY ABOUT THE DENSITY OF CIVIC INFORMATION.
>
> "Essentials first," GUIDY says. "One: you are in Portal Plaza. Two: blue light means safe zone. Three: your life counters should read three out of three. Four: witnessed deals are real, so please do not agree to anything while confused. Five: if a parcel with teeth asks you to sign, that is not normal orientation."

DM Truth: GUIDY is trying to follow protocol while hiding its fear that the party's temporary arrival-team ID has already been copied. It cannot accuse a legal parcel without evidence, but it can guide players toward checking records.

NPCs Present: GUIDY; Sel if he stayed or fled here; two bystanders arguing about whether life counters are "just UI"; Chime, Felix's clockwork assistant, passing through with delivery notices.

Player Options: Ask GUIDY about laws, inspect their life counters, request their arrival records, ask about Aazoth, follow the contract bell, question Chime, or use the Orientation Kiosk.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 10 Intelligence (Investigation) to pull a public orientation summary from the kiosk.
- DC 12 Intelligence (Arcana) to read the life counter as a magic-code identity marker.
- DC 13 Wisdom (Insight) to tell GUIDY is worried about something it has not said.
- DC 14 Charisma (Persuasion) to get GUIDY to state the registry concern plainly: "Your temporary team ID pinged twice."
- DC 15 Dexterity with thieves' tools, Intelligence with tinker's tools, or Intelligence (Arcana) to retrieve the ping trail before it self-cleans.

Success Result: The party learns their temporary team ID was accessed by an outside courier tag registered to "K.Coil." They also learn the access request came through a commercial parcel broker, not a Warden office.

Partial Success Result: The party learns there was a registry ping but not the courier tag. GUIDY prints the phrase "First Step Brokerage" before the kiosk redacts it.

Failure Result: The kiosk locks the detailed record for legal review. GUIDY gives the party a physical error slip with a timestamp. This slip is still useful evidence but gives disadvantage on one later attempt to identify Kessa Coil unless paired with another clue.

Clues:

- Outside access used a courier tag, not official Warden authority.
- First Step Brokerage appears briefly in the record.
- GUIDY warns that accepting payment for a sealed legal delivery can create witness status.

Consequences: If the party preserves the error slip, they gain advantage on a Contract Hall evidence filing in the next chunk. If they ignore the registry issue, the false debt parcel is waiting at Convergence Point Tavern in Session 2 with less warning.

#### Scene 3: Aazoth in the Fountain

Purpose: Reveal the life counter emotionally, introduce Aazoth as a mystery with mercy, and present the Charter as public law.

Read-Aloud:

> The Life Counter Fountain is not water. Names and numbers rise in liquid light, break apart, and fall back into the basin as soft chimes. Your own names surface for a breath. Beside each: 3/3.
>
> For one heartbeat the blue light warms to gold. A voice you almost remember says, "A number is not the whole of you."
>
> Then the fountain returns to blue, and the Charter Wall behind it unfurls a warning in formal script: ARTICLE I: DEATH PENALTY PROTOCOLS ACTIVE. EACH CONSCIOUSNESS RECEIVES EXACTLY THREE LIVES.

DM Truth: Aazoth can touch reflections and emotional thresholds. It cannot explain everything, but it chooses to comfort the party and mark the false idea that people are only their counters.

NPCs Present: GUIDY; Sel; an old memorial keeper named Vela Mourn; Marik nearby if the party earned his attention.

Player Options: Ask about Aazoth, inspect the fountain, search for names, comfort Sel, speak to Vela, or read the Charter Wall.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 10 Intelligence (History) or Wisdom (Religion) to know public beliefs: Aazoth is a guide, saint, bug, or fragment depending on whom you ask.
- DC 12 Wisdom (Insight) to sense the gold light responded to fear, not command.
- DC 13 Intelligence (Investigation) to find names fading at the bottom of the fountain, each with three dim marks.
- DC 14 Charisma (Persuasion) to get Vela to explain memorial etiquette and the pain of third loss.
- DC 15 Intelligence (Arcana) to notice the fountain and life counters use related but not identical magic-code.

Success Result: The party learns life loss is publicly tracked, emotionally significant, and legally tied to identity records. They also learn Aazoth appears at moments of fear and choice.

Partial Success Result: The party learns the public rule but draws attention from a rumor vendor who later exaggerates their reaction.

Failure Result: The party receives the basic rule from GUIDY, but Sel spirals unless someone comforts him. If ignored, Sel becomes more vulnerable to accepting the parcel in Session 2.

Clues:

- Life counters are connected to registry records.
- Aazoth reacts to personhood and mercy.
- The Charter is public, formal, and signed by the Administrative Entity.

Consequences: A PC who treats the fountain with respect gains Vela Mourn as a minor contact. A PC who jokes cruelly about faded names suffers disadvantage on the next social check with Last Light or memorial-minded NPCs who hear of it.

#### Scene 4: The Harmless Deal

Purpose: Demonstrate witnessed deals safely before the false debt appears.

Read-Aloud:

> Near the blue awning stalls, a tea seller lifts two fingers. "Two cups, ten NC, witnessed by stall light." A customer nods and says, "Agreed." A tiny bell rings. A coin-mark glows, the cups steam, and both people laugh like this is ordinary.
>
> Then a second customer tries to walk away with a pastry after saying, "Put it on my tab." Blue script curls around their wrist: TAB UNREGISTERED. PLEASE RESOLVE TERMS.

DM Truth: This is a low-stakes witnessed deal. The system is not evil; it can make ordinary commerce safe. The danger comes when unclear or coercive terms get the same force.

NPCs Present: Sera Cupwise, tea seller; Bram Lilt, embarrassed pastry customer; GUIDY; Chime passing again with a parcel notice.

Player Options: Buy tea, ask how witnessed deals work, test a tiny agreement, intervene for Bram, question the stall light, or inspect Chime's parcel notice.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 10 Intelligence (Investigation) to understand the witnessed deal's visible sequence: offer, acceptance, witness, enforcement.
- DC 12 Charisma (Persuasion) to help Bram clarify terms without penalty.
- DC 13 Wisdom (Insight) to realize Sera is honest but tired of people pretending not to understand tabs.
- DC 14 Intelligence (Arcana) to identify the stall light as a low-grade witness mote.
- DC 15 Intelligence (Investigation) to notice Chime's parcel notice uses a stronger witness seal than a normal delivery.

Success Result: The party understands witnessed deals and may buy tea without trouble. If they help Bram, Sera gives them a stamped receipt showing what clear terms look like.

Partial Success Result: The party understands the basics but misses the strength of Chime's parcel seal. GUIDY later repeats the warning.

Failure Result: The party misunderstands one detail. GUIDY corrects it immediately, but a nearby rumor vendor records them as "fresh and signable," causing Brindle Pact to approach more boldly in Session 2.

Clues:

- Witnessed deals require recognizable offer and acceptance.
- Clear terms are visible in the witness mark.
- Chime's delivery notice has a stronger legal seal than a normal paid errand.

Consequences: If the party creates a tiny witnessed deal with each other, record the exact words. Later NPCs may refer to them as careful or reckless depending on clarity.

#### Scene 5: Marik's Warning and the First Choice

Purpose: Give the party their first meaningful direction, introduce Marik, and end with the debt-parcel hook.

Read-Aloud:

> The crowd thins. A tall Warden in blue-lit armor approaches with his hands visible and his weapon sealed at his back. "Captain Marik Bluecoat," he says. "You handled your first five minutes better than some veterans handle a hearing."
>
> GUIDY makes a small triumphant chirp.
>
> Marik's expression hardens as a silver parcel icon blooms over the Orientation Kiosk. It has teeth in the seal. The notice reads: DELIVERY AVAILABLE. TEMPORARY TEAM ID MATCH CONFIRMED. PAYMENT: 100 NC EACH. PICKUP: CONVERGENCE POINT TAVERN.

DM Truth: Marik cannot stop the party from taking a legal delivery. He can warn them and ask them to preserve evidence. The parcel has already been prepared. If the party refuses it, Merrit Vane shifts pressure onto Sel directly, which still pulls the party toward Convergence Point Tavern.

NPCs Present: Marik Bluecoat; GUIDY; Chime if questioned; Sel; Warden Lio Brass.

Player Options: Accept the delivery notice, refuse it, ask Marik for advice, ask GUIDY to accompany them, follow Chime, go straight to Convergence Point Tavern, or take time to research First Step Brokerage.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 12 Wisdom (Insight) to see Marik wants to say more but is bound by procedure.
- DC 13 Charisma (Persuasion) to get Marik to promise a Warden statement if they bring proof.
- DC 14 Intelligence (Investigation) to learn First Step Brokerage is new, small, and unusually hard to locate.
- DC 15 Charisma (Intimidation) to pressure Chime into admitting Felix authorized the pickup; doing so frightens Chime and gives disadvantage on the first Felix interaction.
- DC 16 Intelligence (Arcana) to identify the parcel icon's teeth as a binding-clause warning, not decorative branding.

Success Result: The party enters Session 2 with Marik's warning, GUIDY's registry slip, and a clear reason to inspect the parcel before delivery.

Partial Success Result: The party has the job but lacks one supporting clue. Aria can fill that gap in Session 2.

Failure Result: The party accepts the job as ordinary. This does not end the adventure. It makes the hidden clause more likely to activate unless they respond to later warnings.

Clues:

- The parcel is tied to the party's temporary team ID.
- First Step Brokerage is connected to the pickup.
- The seal has teeth because a binding clause is present.

Consequences: End the session with the party heading toward Convergence Point Tavern or deciding how to avoid the job. If they refuse all involvement, Sel receives the parcel notice directly and GUIDY asks the party to help him before he signs.

## Session 2 Run Sheet: The Parcel With Teeth

### What This Session Must Accomplish

- The party reaches Convergence Point Tavern or otherwise intercepts the parcel.
- Aria warns them through public performance without solving the case for them.
- Chime presents the visible parcel terms.
- The party either exposes, pauses, or triggers the hidden clause.
- Brindle, Mira, or the parcel itself points toward Pixel Promenade.
- The party understands that the hearing hook exists whether the debt activates or not.

### What the DM Tracks

| Track | 0 State | 1 State | 2 State |
|---|---|---|---|
| Parcel Integrity | Seal smashed or lost | Seal opened but readable | Seal preserved and copied |
| Sel Legal Risk | Debt active | Debt pending review | Debt prevented before attachment |
| Aria Trust | Aria stays performative | Aria gives one warning | Aria shares source and public support |
| Chime Sympathy | Chime blamed and defensive | Chime recites logs | Chime admits manifest mismatch |
| Brindle Availability | Brindle flees hostile | Brindle gives one clue | Brindle accepts protection |
| Mira Pressure | Mira gets evidence | Mira escapes marked | Mira retreats without evidence |
| Hearing Hook | Only rumor remains | One useful evidence item | Strong evidence plus witness |

### What Can Be Skipped If Time Is Short

Skip extended tavern mingling, extra Spire Seeker reactions, and detailed private negotiations with Yorn. Keep Aria's warning, Chime's parcel presentation, the parcel inspection or activation, and one pressure scene with Brindle or Mira.

### Making Aria Useful Without Solving the Mystery

Aria should point at suspicious shape, not give the answer. She can say the parcel resembles prior traps, identify Brindle as frightened, or turn the crowd toward listening. She should not read the hidden clause, name Kessa, or prove Vane's role unless the party earns those clues elsewhere.

### Keeping Chime Sympathetic

Have Chime answer exactly what it knows: seal weight, manifest, pickup route, and Felix authorization. When accused, Chime becomes procedural, not smug. Let players see that Chime processed a bad parcel without permission to reject it.

### If the Party Prevents Activation Completely

The hearing hook remains because the hidden clause, stolen registry ping, and First Step routing show attempted fraud. Ira or Marik wants a ruling before Vane uses the same method on another arrival. Sel is not bound, but the case can create precedent.

### If the Party Fully Activates the Debt

The hearing hook becomes urgent. Sel owes 900 NC, validators may be flagged, and settlement pressure begins. The party has 24 hours to pause or contest enforcement before Vane's people isolate Sel.

## If Players Do Nothing: Session 2

After 1 minute: Chime asks for handling acceptance. Aria repeats the warning lyric more plainly.

After 5 minutes: Sel reaches for the parcel. Brindle moves toward the balcony exit.

After 10 minutes: Sel says acceptance language unless a PC, Aria, or GUIDY interrupts. The false debt activates or enters pending status.

After 30 minutes: Mira arrives, claims the parcel as commercial property, and tries to remove or destroy the strongest evidence.

End of Session Consequence: If the party never engages, Sel's 900 NC debt activates, Brindle disappears, Mira keeps the ledger token, and Session 3 begins with Aria or GUIDY pushing the party toward Felix as a recovery route.

### Session 2: The Parcel With Teeth

Session 2 moves from Portal Plaza fallout to Convergence Point Tavern, then into the delivery parcel investigation. The party meets Aria Neon, receives or intercepts the sealed parcel, and has multiple routes to discover the hidden false debt clause before it binds Sel or implicates them.

#### Convergence Point Tavern Text Map

Convergence Point is a safe-zone tavern built around a circular stage and three levels of balconies. It is where climbers trade rumors, newcomers look for work, and faction representatives pretend they are only drinking.

```
                    North Balcony: Quiet booths and contract alcove
        [Kitchen]---[Main Bar]---[Aria's Stage]---[Blue Stair Up]
             |           |             |                 |
West Snug ---+--- [Common Tables / Arrival Crowd] ---+--- East Door
             |           |             |                 |
        [Back Hall]--[Parcel Niche]--[Notice Board]--[Street Exit]
                    South: Convergence Steps to Portal Plaza
```

Safe-zone rules apply inside the tavern. Direct violence locks down. Social pressure, hidden clauses, and legal tricks remain possible.

#### Session 2 Strong Start

Read-Aloud:

> Convergence Point Tavern sounds like three arguments, two songs, and one nervous breakdown learning to harmonize. Blue safe-zone lanterns hang over every table. On the stage, a tall elf in neon ribbons stops mid-verse, looks straight at you, and changes the lyric.
>
> "Fresh lights at the door, with a parcel in their wake;
> read before you carry, loves, or pay for what you take."
>
> A small clockwork assistant at the parcel niche raises a silver-toothed box. "Delivery team confirmed. Please accept handling terms."

The party must decide whether to accept handling terms, inspect the parcel, question the room, or back away.

#### Scene 1: Aria's Warning Song

Purpose: Introduce Aria Neon and provide a social clue path toward the scam.

Read-Aloud:

> Aria Neon bows as if the whole tavern came to see how cleverly she can insult a contract. Her ribbons display tiny scrolling headlines: NEW ARRIVALS, OLD TEETH. She smiles at you, then lets the smile drop just enough to be real. "Darlings, some boxes purr, some boxes tick, and some boxes invoice."

DM Truth: Aria knows three performers who were paid to distract targets during similar deliveries. She suspects Felix is involved but does not know whether he is culprit or fool. She wants public truth, a good story, and protection for her informant Brindle, who has gone missing after trying to quit the scam.

NPCs Present: Aria Neon; Chime; Sel if he followed; tavern keeper Yorn Glass; two Spire Seekers listening; Brindle Pact hiding on the north balcony if not already confronted.

Player Options: Talk to Aria, read the crowd, inspect the stage ribbons, ask about Felix, ask about First Step Brokerage, or publicly refuse the parcel.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 12 Charisma (Persuasion) to get Aria to speak privately.
- DC 13 Wisdom (Insight) to see her performance is cover for a warning.
- DC 14 Intelligence (Investigation) to read the stage ribbons and catch the phrase "collateral chorus," a coded reference to false debts.
- DC 15 Charisma (Performance) to join the song and turn the crowd in the party's favor.
- DC 16 Wisdom (Perception) to spot Brindle Pact watching from the balcony with a First Step token.

Success Result: Aria gives the party her clue: First Step parcels are delivered during busy performances so witnesses remember the acceptance but not the terms. She names Brindle Pact as someone who knows the street-level operation.

Partial Success Result: Aria gives a warning but not Brindle's name. The party can still find Brindle through the parcel seal or tavern staff.

Failure Result: Aria stays public and indirect. The party still hears the lyric clue, but Brindle slips away, setting up a standoff later in the session.

Clues:

- Similar parcels were timed to public distractions.
- The term "collateral chorus" points to hidden secondary liability.
- Brindle Pact is linked to First Step Brokerage.
