Consequences: If the party respects Aria's need to protect sources, she becomes a contact. If they publicly accuse her of manipulation, she helps but later frames them as reckless.

#### Scene 2: Accepting or Inspecting the Parcel

Purpose: Put the false debt clause in the party's hands and define how it activates.

Read-Aloud:

> The parcel is the size of a spellbook, wrapped in silver paper that feels warmer than the room. Its seal has six tiny metallic teeth around a blue witness gem. Chime's voice clicks into a recitation. "Handling fee: paid. Delivery reward: pending. Recipient: Sel Varrin. Contents: orientation aid. Please state acceptance of handling responsibility."

DM Truth: The parcel is safe to hold if no one accepts handling responsibility in witnessed terms. The hidden clause tries to mark the party as delivery validators. It activates fully only if delivered to Sel before a witness and Sel says an acceptance phrase such as "I accept," "That's mine," or "I'll take it" while the seal is intact. If the party says "We accept handling responsibility" in front of Chime's witness gem, they are not yet debtors, but the clause gains their names as validators.

NPCs Present: Chime; Aria; Sel; Yorn Glass; Brindle if spotted; GUIDY by remote projection if invited.

Player Options: Refuse the terms, accept and inspect, ask Chime to restate terms, cover the witness gem, take the parcel outside, call Marik, call Ira, open the parcel, or deliver it.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 10 Intelligence (Investigation) to notice the seal is legal, not merely decorative.
- DC 12 Charisma (Persuasion) to make Chime restate the terms in plain speech.
- DC 13 Intelligence (Arcana) to sense the witness gem is active.
- DC 14 Intelligence with calligrapher's supplies, forgery kit, or Investigation to find microtext under the teeth.
- DC 15 Wisdom (Insight) to realize Chime does not understand the full clause.
- DC 16 Dexterity with thieves' tools or Intelligence (Arcana) to disable the witness gem without breaking evidence.

Success Result: The party detects the hidden false debt clause before delivery. They learn the key phrase: "secondary collateral attaches to arrival-team validators upon recipient acknowledgement."

Partial Success Result: The party detects that something is wrong but not the full mechanism. If they continue, Aria or Sel can still create a pause before activation.

Failure Result: The party accepts handling terms without understanding. The clause records them as validators. This creates disadvantage at the later hearing unless they recover the registry shard in Session 3, but it does not automatically bind them to debt.

Clues:

- The parcel names Sel as recipient.
- The microtext tries to attach arrival-team validators.
- Chime is a courier assistant, not the authorizing mind.

Consequences: If the party breaks the seal carelessly, the Debt Shade manifests as a whispering ink-smoke hazard and tries to flee into the tavern's witness lights. If they preserve the seal, they gain strong evidence.

## False Debt Parcel Handout

Give the visible text below to players when a character reads the parcel without exposing the hidden clause. This is the text on the top wrapping and manifest tag.

```text
FIRST STEP BROKERAGE
New Arrival Orientation Aid Parcel

Recipient: Sel Varrin
Temporary Registry Match: Confirmed
Delivery Class: Welcome Assistance / Tower Readiness
Handling Fee: Paid
Delivery Reward: 100 NC per registered handling member, payable upon return of receipt

Visible Contents:
- 1 Convergence Point meal token
- 1 basic route pamphlet
- 1 Tower-readiness consultation voucher
- 1 emergency healing chit
- 1 orientation expense statement

Handling Terms:
The handling party agrees to carry this sealed parcel to the named recipient without damaging the seal, substituting recipient, or claiming parcel contents. The handling party confirms only that the parcel was delivered to the named recipient while the seal remained visible.

Recipient Acknowledgement:
The named recipient confirms receipt of the parcel and attached orientation aid by speaking a clear acceptance before a valid witness.

Questions or disputes may be directed to First Step Brokerage within one business day of receipt.
Thank you for beginning safely.
```

The visible text is intentionally bland. It never says "debt" on the outside. A character who specifically asks, "Is there debt language?" can see that the visible text avoids the word rather than answering the question.

## Hidden Clause Text

The following text appears in hair-thin silver script under the six metal teeth of the seal. The party can expose it with the checks in Scene 2 or by triggering the parcel and preserving the seal. When exposed, give this text to the players.

```text
FIRST STEP BROKERAGE
Supplemental Orientation Finance Clause
Micro-Registry Addendum FS-1A

For value already advanced in the form of route assessment, Tower-readiness review, emergency intake prioritization, risk sorting, parcel preparation, witness access, and recipient location service, the named recipient acknowledges an orientation preparation balance of 900 Nexus Credits.

Recipient acknowledgement of this parcel confirms custody of the attached orientation benefit packet and validates the above balance as a starter obligation.

Any registered handling member who accepts handling responsibility, carries the sealed parcel to the named recipient, receives or seeks delivery reward, or confirms recipient acknowledgement before a witness is recorded as a Delivery Validator.

Delivery Validators affirm that the named recipient received the parcel in readable condition and that no objection to the orientation balance was stated before recipient acknowledgement.

If the named recipient delays, refuses, contests, or defaults on payment before formal review, Delivery Validators agree that up to 20 percent of their first registered Tower reward, sponsorship payment, or Guild disbursement may be reserved as secondary collateral until the orientation balance is satisfied or released.

Emergency review may be requested within one business day. Review does not void the balance unless the reviewing authority finds defective recipient identity, defective witness procedure, stolen registry access, material concealment, or lack of meaningful consent.

By delivery, acknowledgement, or reward claim, the parties confirm these terms under witnessed commercial custom.
```

The hidden clause is manipulative, not nonsense. Once players see it, they should understand the trap: it turns a delivery into validation, turns Sel's confused acceptance into debt, and tries to reserve party Tower rewards if the debt is contested.

## False Debt Activation Procedure

Use this procedure whenever the party interacts with the sealed parcel after Chime presents it.

Trigger: Activation begins when three things align: the seal is intact, a valid witness is present, and either the handling party accepts handling responsibility or Sel speaks recipient acknowledgement. Full activation requires Sel or a convincing substitute to say acceptance language while the witness gem is bright.

Who Notices First: A character watching the seal notices the teeth click first. A character watching Sel notices his life counter flicker first. A character watching the room hears the contract bell first. GUIDY, Aria, or Chime can notice if no PC states they are watching.

Visible Signs:

- The six teeth flex inward like a closing jaw.
- The blue witness gem turns silver-white.
- A contract bell rings once for handling and twice for recipient acknowledgement.
- Hairline script crawls from the seal toward Sel's wrist.
- If party validator status attaches, each affected PC sees a faint gray receipt-mark flash near their life counter.
- If the Debt Shade fragment wakes, black ink-smoke forms a small handprint on the parcel.

Immediate Party Options:

- Object clearly: "We contest this debt and do not validate the balance."
- Cover or turn away the witness gem.
- Calm Sel before he repeats acceptance language.
- Preserve the seal instead of tearing it apart.
- Ask Chime to print the exact terms it is reciting.
- Call for Warden, Ledger Court, or tavern witness review.
- Use magic to reveal writing, protect Sel, interrupt sound, or contain the smoke.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 12 Charisma (Persuasion) to keep Sel from speaking additional acceptance language.
- DC 13 Intelligence (Arcana) to identify the witness gem as the active legal focus.
- DC 14 Intelligence (Investigation) to state a legally meaningful objection from visible terms.
- DC 14 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) to rotate or cover the witness gem before the second bell.
- DC 15 Intelligence with calligrapher's supplies or forgery kit to expose the hidden clause cleanly.
- DC 15 Charisma (Persuasion) to get Chime to print the full recitation log.
- DC 16 Intelligence (Arcana) to contain the Debt Shade fragment without damaging the seal.
- DC 16 Wisdom (Insight) to identify that Sel's acceptance is fear-driven and legally vulnerable.

Success: The debt does not fully attach. The parcel seal, hidden clause, and witness-gem activity become strong evidence. Sel remains free of immediate obligation, and the party avoids validator penalties.

Partial Success: Sel's 900 NC debt appears in pending status, but the party prevents secondary collateral from attaching to their Tower rewards. Enforcement pauses for 24 hours if someone states a clear objection before the third bell.

Failure: Sel receives a 900 NC starter debt. Each PC who accepted handling responsibility or claimed delivery reward gains "Collateral Review Pending" on their public profile. Cautious vendors raise nonessential prices by 10 percent. The party has disadvantage on the first legal argument about chain of consent unless they recover the registry shard or Chime's manifest log.

Debt Amount: 900 NC assigned to Sel as primary debtor. Secondary collateral attempts to reserve 20 percent of the party's first registered Tower reward, sponsorship payment, or Guild disbursement. No NC leaves the party immediately unless they choose to pay.

Legal Status Changes:

- Sel: "Starter Obligation Pending Review" if paused; "Starter Debt Active" if unchallenged.
- Party: no status if they refused handling terms; "Delivery Witness" if they observed but objected; "Delivery Validator" if they accepted handling responsibility; "Collateral Review Pending" if activation completes.
- Parcel: "Disputed Commercial Evidence" if preserved; "Damaged Commercial Property" if smashed.

How to Pause the Debt: State a clear objection before the third bell, preserve the seal, and request review from a Warden, Ledger Court clerk, or registered tavern witness light. A successful DC 14 Persuasion, Investigation, or Arcana check pauses enforcement for 24 hours. Marik, Ira, or Yorn can grant the pause without a roll if the party presents visible hidden text or the GUIDY registry slip.

How to Void It: The debt can be voided cleanly by proving at least two of the following: stolen registry access, hidden material terms, recipient confusion, forged or counterfeit routing, paid false witnesses, or First Step's lack of actual services. The registry shard plus preserved hidden clause is decisive. Without those, three useful pieces of evidence and one credible witness can still win.

If the Party Ignores It: After 24 hours, Sel's profile shows Active Debt. The party's Tower registration, if they accepted handling terms, shows Collateral Review Pending. Felix's public office receives a complaint. Vane offers a settlement that clears the party if they confirm Sel accepted the parcel. If they still ignore it after their next long rest, Sel signs the settlement out of fear unless another NPC protects him.

### One-Page DM Summary: False Debt Mechanics

The parcel is a trap, not a bomb. Its purpose is legal leverage.

Step 1: Chime presents the parcel and asks the party to accept handling responsibility. If they refuse, they can still inspect it. If they accept, they become possible validators but not debtors.

Step 2: The party can inspect the seal. DC 14 Investigation, calligrapher's supplies, or forgery kit reveals microtext. DC 13 Arcana identifies the witness gem. DC 15 Insight shows Chime does not understand the hidden clause.

Step 3: If the sealed parcel reaches Sel and he says acceptance language before the witness gem, activation begins. Let the party react before the third bell.

Step 4: A clear objection plus preservation of the seal pauses enforcement. Smashing the parcel may stop the Shade but weakens evidence.

Step 5: Full failure creates 900 NC debt for Sel and Collateral Review Pending for validating PCs. This is a pressure state, not campaign failure.

Step 6: To void the debt, the party needs evidence. Best evidence: preserved hidden clause, registry shard, Chime log, Brindle statement, Felix delivery log, Mira ledger token, Kessa statement.

At the table, say: "The law has noticed the shape of an agreement. It has not yet proven the agreement was valid."

## False Debt Parcel: Common Player Attempts

Use this matrix to answer likely player ideas quickly. Clever play should produce evidence or advantage, but the parcel remains a legal trap until the party proves why its consent is defective.

| Player Action | Immediate Result | Check/DC If Needed | Clue Revealed | Risk Created | How the Adventure Continues |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Refuse to touch the parcel | Chime asks whether they refuse handling terms; Sel remains the named recipient | No check | Refusal shows handling is optional | Sel may accept it alone | Aria or GUIDY urges them to protect Sel rather than carry the box |
| Take it directly to Marik | Marik can secure it but cannot void it on the spot | DC 12 Persuasion to get immediate Warden intake | Warden notes prior First Step complaints | Chain of custody becomes Warden-controlled | Marik sends them to gather context at the tavern or Promenade |
| Take it directly to Aria | Aria reads the room and warns about performance-timed scams | DC 12 Persuasion for private help | Collateral Chorus clue | Public attention rises | Aria points them to Brindle or Yorn's witness-light memory |
| Open it carefully | Hidden teeth and microtext can be exposed | DC 14 Investigation or relevant tools | Hidden Clause Text | Seal damage if failed by 5 or more | Preserved text becomes strong evidence |
| Smash it | Debt Shade fragment bursts out; visible terms scatter | DC 13 Dexterity save to protect one evidence piece | The parcel contained active clause magic | Evidence strength drops; possible Criminal Heat if in tavern | The party must rely on witnesses and registry trail |
| Cast detect magic | Witness gem, teeth, and microtext glow as enchantment/abjuration-like legal magic | No check with spell; DC 13 Arcana for details | Heavy Parcel Seal | Magic does not reveal wording alone | Party gains advantage on the next seal inspection |
| Cast identify | The caster learns the seal stores a conditional witnessed obligation | Spell works if the caster can touch or examine safely | Validator Status and activation trigger | Touching while speaking carelessly may count as handling if terms were accepted | Party can object before activation with advantage |
| Use thieves' tools | The witness gem can be disabled or loosened | DC 16 Dexterity with thieves' tools | Active witness gem | Failure by 5 breaks seal and wakes fragment | Disabled gem pauses activation but still leaves legal proof |
| Use forgery kit or calligrapher's supplies | The microtext can be lifted cleanly | DC 14 Intelligence with kit | Hidden Microtext | Bad copy can be challenged as altered | Clean copy strengthens hearing evidence |
| Ask Chime to explain every term | Chime recites visible handling terms and admits manifest limits | DC 12 Persuasion if Chime is defensive | Chime Manifest Mismatch | Public blame makes Chime shut down | Chime can become a sympathetic witness |
| Tell Sel not to speak | Sel freezes and looks to the party for plain explanation | DC 12 Persuasion if he is panicking | Recipient acknowledgement is required | Sel may feel controlled if barked at | Sel trust rises if they explain gently |
| Try to trick the parcel with fake acceptance | The witness gem searches for matching registry identity | DC 15 Deception or Arcana | The seal checks identity, not only words | On failure, the trickster becomes a validator candidate | The failed trick proves stolen registry matching matters |
| Try to sell the parcel | Most buyers refuse; a shady broker offers too fast | DC 13 Insight spots the broker as a First Step plant | First Step wants the parcel recovered | Evidence may leave party control | Broker trail points to Mira or Felix |
| Throw it into a safe-zone lamp | The lamp freezes the parcel mid-arc and rings a warning | No check unless thrown violently; DC 13 Arcana to read reaction | Safe zones protect objects from violent evidence destruction | Public attention and Warden questions | Marik or Yorn asks why they tried to destroy evidence |
| Leave the tavern with it | The witness gem dims but does not deactivate | DC 14 Stealth or Deception if Mira is present | Seal is location-aware but portable | Mira follows or sends Pell | Leads to street pressure or direct route to Felix |
| Accuse Chime publicly | Chime goes defensive and prints only visible terms | DC 15 Persuasion to recover trust | Chime is not authorizing mind | Lose Chime sympathy | Felix must provide logs instead |
| Attack Chime or Brindle | Safe-zone law stops direct harm in the tavern | No attack roll in safe zone; DC 13 Charisma save to avoid social fallout | Safe-zone law demonstration | Criminal Heat, witness resentment | Scene shifts to Warden/Yorn intervention; clues move to Aria or Felix |
| Use silence | Spoken acceptance and bell cues are suppressed inside the area | Spell works; DC 13 Arcana to predict witness behavior | Activation needs audible or legible acknowledgement | Chime cannot explain while silenced | Party buys time, but must still expose terms |
| Use dispel magic | The witness gem flickers; low-level casting can suppress but not erase the clause | DC 13 spellcasting ability check if targeting the seal's legal magic | Seal has layered magic | Failure wakes the fragment or damages evidence | Suppression creates a 10-minute inspection window |
| Use mage hand | The hand can hold, turn, or lift the parcel without speaking terms | No check for simple handling; DC 12 Sleight of Hand for precision | Teeth and gem can be inspected safely | Mage hand cannot read microtext by itself | Party avoids validator language while inspecting |
| Use unseen servant | The servant can carry the parcel, but cannot consent or testify | No check | Handling responsibility requires a registered person | Chime asks who accepts responsibility | Good way to move box while refusing terms |
| Use command | A one-word command can stop Sel or Kessa briefly | Target saves normally; use spell DC | Fear-driven compliance is not consent | Coercion worsens witness attitude | Buys time but may weaken moral/legal standing |
| Use charm person or similar magic | The charmed target becomes friendlier but later knows magic was used | Spell save normally | Coerced agreement is legally vulnerable | Criminal Heat if used to force testimony or acceptance | Good for calming if transparent; bad for manufacturing consent |

#### Scene 3: If They Deliver It Blindly

Purpose: Provide the full consequence of an unchecked delivery without ending the adventure.

Read this scene only if the party brings the sealed parcel to Sel and allows normal delivery.

Read-Aloud:

> Sel reaches for the parcel like it might contain a map home. The witness gem brightens. Chime says, "Recipient acknowledgement required."
>
> Sel swallows. "I accept."
>
> The teeth click open. Ink-black smoke curls around his wrist and then snaps toward yours. Words burn in the air: STARTER DEBT ACKNOWLEDGED. COLLATERAL PATHS REGISTERED.

DM Truth: The clause partially activates. Sel is bound as primary debtor for 900 NC of fabricated Tower-preparation services. The party is recorded as delivery validators if they accepted handling terms. The clause attempts to reserve 20 percent of their first Tower rewards as secondary collateral. This reserve is contestable because consent was defective and registry data was stolen.

NPCs Present: Sel; Chime; Aria; tavern crowd; Debt Shade as clause-spirit.

Player Options: Interrupt with magic, argue consent, cover the witness gem, calm Sel, seize the parcel, call for Warden review, or chase the smoke if it flees.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 12 Charisma (Persuasion) to keep Sel from panicking.
- DC 13 Intelligence (Arcana) to identify the Debt Shade as a clause-spirit, not a normal undead.
- DC 14 Charisma (Persuasion) or Intelligence (Investigation) to state a clear objection that pauses automatic enforcement.
- DC 15 Strength (Athletics) or Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) to keep the parcel from snapping shut and destroying microtext.
- DC 16 Wisdom (Insight) to identify that the clause relied on Sel's fear and ignorance.

Success Result: Enforcement pauses for 24 hours pending Ledger Court review. The party has urgency but no immediate NC loss.

Partial Success Result: Sel's debt activates, but the party prevents their Tower-reward collateral from attaching. They must gather evidence quickly.

Failure Result: Sel's debt activates and the party is listed as validators. Each PC's public profile shows "Collateral Review Pending." Prices from cautious vendors rise by 10 percent until they file evidence or clear the debt. The adventure continues toward Pixel Promenade and Code Caverns.

Clues:

- The clause uses First Step Brokerage language.
- The Debt Shade tries to flee toward a Pixel Promenade stock token.
- The activation record references K.Coil's registry shard.

Consequences: Aria publicly calls for calm and gives the party a chance to reclaim the narrative. Felix becomes harder to persuade because his name is now visible in the delivery chain.

#### Scene 4: Brindle Pact's Standoff

Purpose: Present the first direct scam agent and give the party a nonlethal confrontation in a safe zone.

Read-Aloud:

> A thin man in a copper scarf backs toward the north balcony stairs with both hands raised. "No violence, blue room, remember?" His smile shakes. A First Step token glints at his collar. "I was paid to point. Pointing is not a crime."

DM Truth: Brindle Pact recruited tavern witnesses and performers to make deliveries look normal. He is frightened because Mira Vale, Vane's field enforcer, threatened to sell his own debt if he talks. He wants escape, safety, and enough NC to leave town for a week.

NPCs Present: Brindle Pact; Aria; two tavern regulars; possibly GUIDY projection.

Player Options: Offer protection, bribe him, threaten legal exposure, appeal to conscience, call Marik, arrange Aria's public witness, or let him flee and follow.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 12 Wisdom (Insight) to see Brindle fears someone offsite.
- DC 13 Charisma (Persuasion) to get him to admit First Step hired him.
- DC 14 Charisma (Intimidation) to make him drop a clue quickly; this works but makes him resentful and unreliable at the hearing.
- DC 15 Charisma (Deception) to pretend the party already has Warden backing.
- DC 16 Intelligence (Investigation) to identify his token as counterfeit guild stock from Pixel Promenade.

Success Result: Brindle gives three facts: Mira Vale carries the payment ledger; Felix's office received the parcel through a Guild stock token; Kessa Coil moved the registry shard into the Code Caverns.

Partial Success Result: Brindle gives one fact before fleeing. The party can still track the token to Pixel Promenade.

Failure Result: Brindle escapes through the balcony kitchen route. Aria points the party toward Felix's Appraisal Stall, where the token clue can be recovered.

Clues:

- First Step hired tavern witnesses.
- Mira Vale holds a payment ledger.
- Kessa Coil moved the registry shard.
- The First Step token is counterfeit guild stock.

Consequences: If the party protects Brindle, he can testify later. If they terrify him, he still helps but requires Ira's protection before he appears in court.

#### Scene 5: Mira Vale at the Door

Purpose: Give the party a chase or tense standoff option and point them toward Pixel Promenade.

Read-Aloud:

> The tavern's east door opens on a woman in a charcoal coat with a gold pixel pin turned upside down. She sees the parcel, sees Brindle, and stops smiling. "That box is commercial property under active delivery terms," she says. "Hand it over and take your fee."

DM Truth: Mira Vale is Vane's field enforcer. She wants the parcel or destroyed evidence. She will not fight in the safe zone. If cornered, she triggers a distraction and flees toward Pixel Promenade, trying to pass the payment ledger to Kessa's drop point.

NPCs Present: Mira Vale; Brindle; Aria; Chime; Yorn Glass; two nervous bystanders.

Player Options: Negotiate, refuse, stall, call Marik, follow her, expose her publicly, trade the parcel for information, or challenge the legality of her claim.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 13 Wisdom (Insight) to read Mira's real goal: evidence destruction.
- DC 14 Charisma (Persuasion) to keep her talking long enough for Aria to gather witnesses.
- DC 15 Intelligence (Investigation) to spot the ledger case under her coat.
- DC 15 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) to mark the ledger case with chalk or magic during the crowd movement.
- DC 16 Charisma (Intimidation) to make her retreat without the parcel; doing this in a safe zone triggers a blue warning if phrased as a direct threat.

Success Result: The party keeps the parcel evidence and identifies the ledger. Mira flees toward Pixel Promenade, creating a clear Session 3 lead.

Partial Success Result: The party keeps either the parcel or the ledger clue, but Mira gets a head start. The Session 3 chase begins with one failure already marked.

Failure Result: Mira steals or destroys part of the parcel. The party still has witness testimony and registry clues, but they need Kessa Coil's shard in Session 3 to make the legal case strong.

Clues:

- Mira wears a guild pin upside down, signaling a hardliner cell rather than Felix's public office.
- Her ledger case contains payment links to First Step Brokerage.
- She runs toward Pixel Promenade, where counterfeit guild stock can be appraised.

Consequences: End Session 2 with the party pursuing Mira, preparing to confront Felix, or arranging to meet Aria at Pixel Promenade. If the false debt activated, enforcement review expires in 24 hours.

## Session 3 Run Sheet: Pixel Promenade and Code Cavern Chase

### What This Session Must Accomplish

- The party reaches Pixel Promenade with at least one parcel, token, witness, or rumor clue.
- Felix appraises the counterfeit route and clarifies his negligence.
- Public rumor pressure shows reputation has mechanical teeth.
- The party follows Kessa's trail to the Code Caverns.
- The chase produces Kessa, the shard, a shard sliver, a ledger scrap, or a CodeX echo.
- The session ends with evidence sorted for Contract Hall.

### What the DM Tracks

| Track | 0 State | 1 State | 2 State |
|---|---|---|---|
| Felix Candor | Felix stalls and protects himself | Felix admits negligence | Felix names Vane and provides logs |
| Public Rumor | Party looks indebted | Rumor is mixed | Party controls public story |
| Pell Warning | Pell warns Kessa | Pell is spotted late | Pell is stopped or flipped |
| Chase Progress | 0-2 successes | 3-4 successes | 5 successes |
| Kessa Attitude | Frightened/hostile | Defensive witness | Willing witness |
| Shard Status | Missing or damaged | Sliver or copy | Intact or sealed metadata |
| Faction Pull | One faction controls evidence | Evidence split uneasily | Party controls chain of custody |

### When Felix Lies

Felix lies or deflects when asked whether his office is responsible, whether he should have noticed the seal, or whether the Guild has a debt problem. His first instinct is to call it "a routing irregularity." A DC 12 Insight check shows the lie is self-protection, not authorship.

### When Felix Tells the Truth

Felix tells the truth when shown counterfeit stock, Chime's manifest mismatch, or proof that Vane is setting him up. He admits he accepted a rush job, did not inspect the inner clause, and recognizes the old-guard routing style.

### Preventing a 45-Minute Accounting Argument

Give the party three clear outputs from Felix's appraisal: the token is counterfeit, the last scan points to K.Coil near Code Cavern Stairs, and Merrit Vane benefits if Felix takes the blame. If players keep drilling into ledger minutiae, Felix says, "The rest is hearing material. The courier is moving now."

### Starting the Chase Quickly

Start the chase as soon as the party identifies K.Coil or reaches the Code Cavern Stairs. Let them make one preparation check, then read the chase opening. Do not require them to solve the whole Promenade before Kessa runs.

### Ending the Chase Cleanly

When the party reaches 5 successes, 3 failures, or the Mercy Beat resolves, stop the chase and move to the Glitch Courier Confrontation. Do not let it drift into endless tunnel checks. Sort evidence immediately afterward.

### Making Kessa a Scared Witness

Have Kessa shout truth while fleeing: "I did not write the debt," "Mira said it was fees," and "Vane does not leave witnesses." If the party protects her from a hazard, lower her social DCs by 2. If they attack her after she says she did not author the debt, she becomes evidence-bearing but hostile.

## If Players Do Nothing: Session 3

After 1 minute: Felix tries to buy time and Pell updates the rumor board.

After 5 minutes: Kessa receives warning and descends deeper into the Code Caverns.

After 10 minutes: Mira's ledger token is moved to a secondary drop. Felix can still trace K.Coil, but the chase begins with one failure.

After 30 minutes: Kessa trades the shard to a hidden buyer or Veil route. The party can recover only partial evidence unless they accept CodeX's help.

End of Session Consequence: The hearing still opens, but Vane's side controls the first public story: reckless newcomers lost the courier and invented a debt conspiracy to avoid payment.

### Session 3: Pixel Promenade and Code Cavern Chase

Session 3 takes the party through Pixel Promenade's public commerce and performance culture, introduces Felix Pixelcoin as compromised but useful, reveals counterfeit guild stock, and drops the party into a Code Cavern chase after Kessa Coil and the stolen registry shard.

#### Pixel Promenade Text Map

Pixel Promenade is a vendor-lined boulevard of animated signs, street music, food carts, and legal witness lights. Most vendor stalls are safe-zone-adjacent; alleys and stairwells may not be.

```
                          North: Grand Exchange Gate
        [Felix's Stall]---[Coin Arch]---[Appraisal Lamps]
              |                |              |
West Alley ---+--- [Performer Walk / Aria's Corner] ---+--- East Arcade
              |                |              |
        [Stock Board]---[Food Carts]---[Code Cavern Stairs]
                          South: Tavern Road
```

#### Session 3 Strong Start

Read-Aloud:

> Pixel Promenade gleams like commerce learned to dance. Coins chase each other across signboards. Food carts hiss with sugar and spice. A performer juggles illusory daggers under a sign reading SAFE VENDOR ROW: NO VIOLENCE, ALL SALES FINAL UNLESS WITNESSED OTHERWISE.
>
> Felix Pixelcoin stands beneath a golden coin arch, smiling at three customers and sweating through the smile. When he sees the parcel mark or Mira's ledger case, his rings flash red prices he did not mean to display.
>
> "Ah," Felix says. "I can explain at least forty percent of what this looks like."

#### Scene 1: Felix's Appraisal

Purpose: Introduce Felix Pixelcoin, reveal counterfeit guild stock, and give the party a path to Kessa Coil.

Read-Aloud:

> Felix's stall is all polished counters, hovering price tags, and emergency discount signs ready to deploy like shields. A small placard reads: HONEST APPRAISAL, DISHONESTLY GOOD RATES. Felix lowers his voice. "If this is about First Step, I would like the record to show I hate being technically implicated."

DM Truth: Felix accepted the parcel as a rush job routed through a guild stock token. He did not inspect the hidden clause. He knows the token is counterfeit once shown the evidence. He wants to protect his reputation, avoid Vane's hardliners, and profit from helping the party just enough to call it business.

NPCs Present: Felix Pixelcoin; Chime; Aria if allied; two Guild clerks; a silent watcher reporting to Merrit Vane.

Player Options: Accuse Felix, ask for appraisal, bargain for help, threaten public exposure, request records, ask about Vane, or inspect the stock token.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 12 Wisdom (Insight) to tell Felix is guilty of negligence, not authorship.
- DC 13 Charisma (Persuasion) to get a sincere apology to Sel.
- DC 14 Intelligence (Investigation) to identify the stock token as counterfeit.
- DC 15 Charisma (Intimidation) to force Felix to produce his delivery logs; this damages future relations unless paired with proof.
- DC 15 Intelligence with jeweler's tools, forgery kit, or tinker's tools to trace the token to Kessa Coil's last scan.
- DC 16 Charisma (Deception) to make the silent watcher reveal themself by pretending to have already found Vane's ledger.

Success Result: Felix gives the party delivery logs, 50 NC each as "reputational hazard compensation," and the lead to Code Cavern Stairs. He also names Merrit Vane as an old-guard broker tied to First Step Brokerage.

Partial Success Result: Felix gives the lead but no compensation and frames his help as a favor owed by the party.

Failure Result: Felix panics and stalls. Aria or Chime can still reveal the token scan, but the silent watcher warns Kessa, adding one failure to the chase.

Clues:

- The guild stock token is counterfeit.
- The token was last scanned near Code Cavern Stairs by courier tag K.Coil.
- Merrit Vane's office benefits if Felix is publicly blamed.

Consequences: If the party treats Felix fairly while holding him accountable, he becomes a complicated contact. If they publicly ruin him without distinguishing negligence from malice, Guild hardliners gain ground and future prices rise.

#### Scene 2: Promenade Pressure

Purpose: Let public reputation matter and create a noncombat obstacle before the chase.

Read-Aloud:

> The stock board above the Promenade flickers. For one breath, your names appear beside the phrase COLLATERAL REVIEW PENDING or DELIVERY DISPUTE ACTIVE. Heads turn. Vendors lower voices. Someone whispers, "Already in debt? They just got here."

DM Truth: Merrit Vane's watcher is pushing a rumor to make the party look unreliable. If the party controls the public story, the rumor becomes pressure on First Step. If not, it becomes pressure on them.

NPCs Present: Aria; Felix; silent watcher named Pell Tick; food cart owner Nomi Sweetspark; bystanders.

Player Options: Let Aria perform the truth, make a public statement, ignore the crowd, chase Pell Tick, ask Felix to correct the stock board, or present evidence.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 12 Charisma (Performance) to hold public attention.
- DC 13 Charisma (Persuasion) to explain the scam clearly without sounding defensive.
- DC 14 Intelligence (Investigation) to identify Pell Tick as the rumor source.
- DC 15 Dexterity (Acrobatics) or Strength (Athletics) to cut Pell off through the crowd without violating safe-zone rules.
- DC 16 Charisma (Intimidation) to silence Pell; this triggers a safe-zone warning if it becomes a threat.

Success Result: The public rumor shifts: "New arrivals expose First Step teeth." The party gains advantage on one social check with a Promenade NPC.

Partial Success Result: The rumor becomes mixed. Some vendors remain cautious, but the party avoids price increases.

Failure Result: Vendors treat the party as risky. Nonessential prices rise by 10 percent until the hearing clears their names. Pell warns Kessa.

Clues:

- The stock board can be manipulated through Guild channels.
- Pell Tick reports to someone above Felix.
- Code Cavern Stairs are the next physical lead.

Consequences: This scene determines whether Session 3 feels like public support or public suspicion. Either route still leads to the Code Caverns.

#### Scene 3: Code Cavern Entrance

Purpose: Transition from public marketplace to hazardous exploration and introduce CodeX's presence.

Read-Aloud:

> The Code Cavern Stairs descend behind a vendor row, lit by green-black glyphs that crawl away from your eyes when stared at directly. A warning sign reads: UNSANCTIONED INFRASTRUCTURE. ENTERING MAY VOID COMFORT.
>
> Someone has chalked a cleaner message under it: LOCKED DOORS ARE NOT MORAL ARGUMENTS.

DM Truth: CodeX has marked this entrance and is watching through old infrastructure. Kessa Coil came this way with Mira's ledger copy and the registry shard. The stairs are outside the strongest safe-zone protections.

NPCs Present: CodeX by text-glyph projection; possible Warden tail; Nomi Sweetspark watching from food carts; Pell if not stopped.

Player Options: Descend, call Marik, ask CodeX for terms, set a watch, inspect hazards, or try to find another entrance.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 12 Wisdom (Perception) to hear someone moving below.
- DC 13 Intelligence (Arcana) to detect unstable glitch pockets.
- DC 14 Dexterity (Stealth) to descend without alerting Kessa.
- DC 14 Charisma (Persuasion) to get CodeX to provide a route hint without agreeing to a future favor.
- DC 16 Intelligence (Investigation) to find a secondary maintenance rail that grants advantage on the first chase check.

Success Result: The party starts the chase with a route advantage and hears Kessa arguing with Mira's sending token.

Partial Success Result: The party descends safely but alerts Kessa.

Failure Result: A glitch pulse deals 2 lightning damage to one PC and marks the party's arrival. The chase begins immediately.

Clues:

- CodeX is aware of the false debt route.
- Kessa is frightened and not fully loyal to Vane.
- The registry shard is physical enough to seize or copy.

Consequences: If the party accepts CodeX's help, CodeX asks for a copy of the shard later. If they refuse, CodeX still watches and judges restraint.

#### Scene 4: Code Cavern Chase

Purpose: Run a dynamic skill challenge with hazards, enemies, and evidence stakes.

Chase Structure: The chase requires 5 successes before 3 failures. Each PC can contribute once per round. Repeating the same skill after it has already succeeded increases its DC by 2 unless the player describes a clearly different approach. Spells and class features can grant automatic success if they directly solve a leg of the chase and consume a meaningful resource. Damaging Kessa does not end the chase unless the party also secures the shard.

Base DC: 13 for straightforward checks, 15 for checks that also protect evidence or help another PC, 17 for checks that gain an extra benefit such as cutting off a route, calming Kessa, or disabling a hazard.

## Code Cavern Chase Tracker

Use this tracker at the table if the chase begins. Put six boxes on scratch paper for rounds, five boxes for successes, and three boxes for failures.

Starting Distance: Kessa begins 60 feet ahead of the frontmost PC. She is visible, carrying the blue registry shard at her throat. The tunnels are cramped; a creature more than 90 feet behind loses direct sight until the next round's obstacle.

Chase Goal: Catch Kessa or convince her to stop while preserving the registry shard.

Successes Needed: 5 successes before Kessa escapes.

Failures Before Complication: At 2 failures, a Debt Shade fragment bites the evidence trail. The party must choose: one PC takes 1d6 necrotic damage, or the next evidence-related check is made with disadvantage.

Failures Before Escape: At 3 failures before 5 successes, Kessa escapes through a Veil maintenance slit. The party still recovers a shard sliver or ledger scrap from the final obstacle.

Round Structure:

1. State the current location beat and obstacle.
2. Each PC describes one action: move, clear a hazard, track Kessa, protect an ally, use magic, attack a hazard, calm Kessa, or secure evidence.
3. Resolve checks. Count no more than two successes from direct movement in the same round; other successes must come from tracking, protection, social pressure, magic, tools, or hazard control.
4. Apply visible costs for failures.
5. Kessa reacts. If the party has 3 or more successes, she starts talking. If the party has 2 or more failures, she takes riskier routes.

Player Action Options:

- Chase: Athletics, Acrobatics, Dash action, mobility feature, or clever terrain use.
- Track: Investigation, Survival, Perception, or Arcana to follow shard resonance.
- Protect: Help another PC, block a wisp, catch a falling ally, or carry evidence.
- Pressure: Persuasion to convince Kessa the party can protect her; Intimidation works but makes her statement brittle.
- Control: Tools, spells, or attacks aimed at doors, wisps, locks, or glitch hazards.
- Evidence: Sleight of Hand, Investigation, or Arcana to keep the shard, ledger token, or seal safe during motion.

Movement Options:

- Normal movement keeps pace if the PC also succeeds on the round's obstacle.
- Dash grants advantage on a movement check but disadvantage on Perception or Investigation in the same round.
- Taking a careful route avoids damage on a failure but cannot earn more than one success that round.
- Carrying an ally or bulky evidence raises the default DC by 2 unless another PC helps.

Hazard Table:

| d6 | Hazard | Effect |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Static Step | Failed movement check deals 1d6 lightning damage. |
| 2 | Repeating Wall | First successful check must be repeated by another PC or the route loops. |
| 3 | Contract Echo | A PC hears their last agreement repeated; failed Wisdom save or Charisma check gives disadvantage on their next check. |
| 4 | Shard Flare | Kessa's shard blinds nearby creatures; failed Perception or Arcana check costs one success opportunity. |
| 5 | Wisp Tangle | A glitch wisp imposes Error Pulse unless driven away. |
| 6 | Mercy Drop | Kessa or an ally slips; saving them counts as a success and improves Kessa's attitude. |

Complication Table:

| d6 | Complication | Table Effect |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Pell's Warning Arrives | Kessa begins one round farther ahead; next movement DC +2. |
| 2 | CodeX Opens a Shortcut | Party may gain one automatic success by owing CodeX a minor favor. |
| 3 | Mira's Token Pings | Debt Shade fragment targets the ledger token; protect it or lose one evidence strength step. |
| 4 | Warden Tail Calls Halt | Ignoring the call adds Criminal Heat; stopping costs one failure but gains Warden chain-of-custody support. |
| 5 | Kessa Shouts Truth | A PC may use Persuasion instead of movement this round. Success improves Kessa's final attitude. |
| 6 | Tunnel Splits | Party can split to flank; see split-party rules below. |

Visible Failure Costs:

- First failure: Kessa gains distance, and a visible clue skitters deeper into the tunnel.
- Second failure: Debt Shade fragment complication triggers.
- Third failure: Kessa escapes, leaving partial evidence.
- Any PC who fails a check by 5 or more takes 1d6 damage of a type matching the obstacle, unless another PC spends their action to protect them.
- A natural 1 on an evidence-handling check damages one evidence item unless a resource or inspiration is spent to save it.

When the Party Catches the Courier: Kessa does not fight to the death. She backs up, grabs the shard, and demands protection. Go to Scene 5. If the party caught her through mercy or persuasion, she starts Helpful. If they caught her by tackling or injuring her, she starts Frightened and defensive.

When the Courier Escapes: Kessa vanishes through a slit that seals behind her. The party finds one of the following: cracked shard sliver, torn payment order, Mira's token imprint, or CodeX echo recording. Pick the one that best matches their successful checks. The next hearing begins with useful but incomplete evidence.

If the Party Splits Up: Split PCs into Lead and Cutoff groups. Each group needs at least one success before the end of the next round. If both groups succeed, award one bonus success and Kessa is cornered early. If either group fails, that group faces a hazard alone. If both fail, mark two failures and Kessa reaches the Ledger Lock Door.

If Combat Starts: Roll initiative only for the immediate pocket of danger. Kessa uses Dash, Disengage, or Hide; she does not stand and trade blows. Glitch wisps attack evidence carriers with Static Sting or Error Pulse. Each full combat round without a chase success counts as one chase failure unless a PC uses their action to block Kessa's route, calm her, or secure the shard.

If Someone Uses Magic Creatively: Reward magic that solves the current obstacle and costs a spell slot, limited feature, or risky position. Examples: feather fall prevents damage at the Mercy Drop; detect magic grants advantage to follow shard resonance; command can make Kessa halt for one round but gives her disadvantage on trusting the party later; fog cloud can block wisps but also blocks line of sight; mage hand can catch the shard if the caster can see it. Cantrips usually grant advantage or a safe reroll rather than automatic success unless the obstacle is minor.

### Round Tracker

| Round | Location Beat | Visible Obstacle | Default DC | Success Effect | Failure Effect | Optional Complication |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | Falling Code Steps | Stairs flatten into running light | 13 | Gain on Kessa and avoid damage | 1d6 lightning or bludgeoning; mark 1 failure | Static Step |
| 2 | Split-Script Fork | Three tunnels show Kessa's shadow | 13 | Pick true route; tracking success counts | Wrong turn costs distance; mark 1 failure | Tunnel Splits |
| 3 | Witness Echo Hall | Recent promises repeat from the walls | 13 | Keep focus or turn truth into social pressure | Disadvantage on next check; mark 1 failure if no ally helps | Contract Echo |
| 4 | Wisp Tangle | Glitch wisps dive for shard and ledger token | 14 | Drive wisps off; protect one evidence item | Wisp uses Error Pulse or evidence strength drops | Mira's Token Pings |
| 5 | Mercy Drop | Kessa slips over a shaft of scrolling code | 13 | Save or persuade Kessa; improve final attitude | Kessa drops shard lower; mark 1 failure | Kessa Shouts Truth |
| 6 | Ledger Lock Door | Door reads the stolen token and begins sealing | 15 | Corner Kessa or open door cleanly | Door seals; Kessa escapes on 3 total failures | Warden Tail Calls Halt |

## Soft Fail and Hard Fail for the Chase

Soft Fail: The courier escapes direct capture, but the party gains enough evidence and a future path. Use this when the party reaches 3 failures after making at least one mercy or protection choice, such as saving Kessa at the Mercy Drop, protecting a witness, preserving evidence over speed, or offering protection instead of threats. A Soft Fail leaves the party with a shard sliver, CodeX echo, Mira token imprint, or Kessa's shouted partial confession. The next session opens with a harder but viable hearing.

Hard Fail: The courier escapes, evidence is damaged, and a faction or hostile witness controls the next move. Use this when the party reaches 3 failures through reckless violence, ignoring Kessa's fear, neglecting evidence, or spending multiple rounds attacking instead of pursuing objectives. A Hard Fail leaves only weak evidence and gives Mira, Pell, Vane, or a faction custody of the stronger proof.

Final Bargain Beat: If the party has 4 successes and then fails, do not end the chase instantly. Offer one final bargain beat: Kessa reaches a sealing door, looks back, and asks, "Who keeps me alive if I stop?" One PC can answer with Persuasion, a concrete protection offer, or a relevant spell or feature. Success converts the failure into a caught-but-frightened Kessa. Failure lets her escape with a Soft Fail unless the party answers with violence, which makes it a Hard Fail.

## Kessa Mercy Beat

At 3 successes or after any PC protects Kessa from a hazard, read or paraphrase:

> Kessa's boot slips on a stair that becomes light. For a breath she hangs over a shaft of scrolling green code, one hand clutching the blue shard hard enough to cut her palm. "Mira said it was intake fees," she gasps. "Vane said nobody gets hurt if the paperwork is clean. He lied. He always lies. If I stop, they do not let me stay a witness."

Persuasion DC: DC 13 if a PC has protected her during the chase, DC 15 if the party has only pursued, or DC 17 if she has been damaged by party attacks.

Insight DC: DC 12 reveals she is guilty but scared; DC 15 reveals her greatest fear is being handed to the most convenient authority rather than protected.

Intimidation Consequence: Intimidation can force compliance on DC 15, but her statement becomes brittle. The next hearing treats her as frightened testimony unless Ira repairs trust.

If Players Offer Protection: Kessa throws the shard to a PC or stops running. She asks for Ira, Marik, CodeX, or Aria by role if not by name: "someone legal," "someone who can hide me," or "someone people believe."

If Players Threaten Her: She keeps the shard close, gives one shouted clue, and runs. If caught, she starts hostile and requires protection before she speaks clearly.

If Players Attack: She uses Dash or Protect the Shard. If reduced below half HP, she shouts one true clue and attempts to escape through the most dangerous route. If knocked to 0, use the Courier Dead outcome package.

Read-Aloud:

> The tunnel opens into a ribbed passage of black stone and green code. Ahead, a courier in a patched silver coat looks back, eyes wide. A shard of blue registry glass hangs from her neck. "I did not write the debt!" she shouts.
>
> Then the floor turns into running light, and she bolts.

DM Truth: Kessa Coil stole the registry shard for Mira Vale, then realized the parcel could bind people to false debt. She planned to sell the shard to CodeX for protection. She is not innocent, but she is a possible witness. Vane's Debt Shade fragments and glitch wisps try to keep her from talking.

NPCs and Enemies: Kessa Coil; 2 glitch wisps for 4 PCs; one Debt Shade fragment represented by a hazard rather than full Debt Shade unless the party is 5-6 PCs or the false debt fully activated; CodeX as distant observer.

Chase Legs and Checks:

1. Falling Code Steps. DC 13 Dexterity (Acrobatics) to keep footing; DC 15 Strength (Athletics) to carry or pull an ally across. Failure costs one healing surge equivalent: the PC takes 1d6 bludgeoning or lightning damage and the group gains one failure.
2. Split-Script Fork. DC 13 Intelligence (Investigation) to pick Kessa's path; DC 15 Wisdom (Survival) to track scuff sparks; DC 17 Intelligence (Arcana) to collapse the wrong route behind the party, preventing a Debt Shade fragment from flanking.
3. Witness Echo Hall. Voices repeat the party's recent agreements. DC 13 Wisdom saving throw or Charisma (Persuasion) to hold focus; DC 15 Charisma (Performance) to drown the echoes with a true statement. Failure imposes disadvantage on that PC's next check and adds one failure if no ally helps.
4. Glitch Wisp Swarm. DC 13 Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) or attack roll to swat a wisp away from the shard; DC 15 Intelligence with tinker's tools or Arcana to scramble their pulse. On failure, a wisp uses Error Pulse against one PC.
5. Mercy Gap. Kessa slips and hangs over a shaft of scrolling code. DC 13 Strength (Athletics) to grab her, DC 14 Dexterity (Acrobatics) to reach her safely, or DC 15 Charisma (Persuasion) to convince her to throw the shard before she falls. If the party attacks instead of helping, she drops the shard into a lower tunnel and survives with a grudge.
6. Ledger Lock Door. DC 14 Intelligence (Investigation) to fit Mira's ledger token into the lock; DC 15 Dexterity with thieves' tools to bypass; DC 17 Intelligence (Arcana) to open it without alerting Vane's watcher. Failure seals the door for one round and triggers a static burst for 1d6 lightning damage to one front-line PC.

Success Result: The party catches Kessa or convinces her to stop, secures the registry shard, and gains her statement that Mira Vale paid her to copy temporary arrival-team IDs for First Step Brokerage.

Partial Success Result: If the party reaches 5 successes after 2 failures, they secure either Kessa or the shard, not both. If they choose Kessa, she can testify but Vane's side may dispute the missing shard. If they choose the shard, they have hard evidence but Kessa remains vulnerable to pressure.

Failure Result: At 3 failures before 5 successes, Kessa escapes deeper or is extracted by a Veil route. The party still recovers a cracked shard sliver or ledger scrap from a hazard. It is enough to reach the Contract Hall, but the next hearing starts with opposing counsel arguing that the evidence is incomplete.

Clue Rewards:

- Registry shard with party temporary team ID, Sel's ID, and K.Coil access stamp.
- Payment ledger token linking Mira Vale to First Step Brokerage.
- Kessa's statement naming Merrit Vane as the ultimate buyer of fresh arrival debt.
- CodeX route glyph showing the shard was copied from the Orientation Kiosk ping.

Consequences: Mercy toward Kessa creates a future witness. Cruelty or lethal force may remove a witness and empower Vane's claim that the party is dangerous. Preserving the shard gives advantage on the opening evidence motion in the next chunk.

#### Scene 5: Glitch Courier Confrontation

Purpose: Resolve Session 3 with a moral and legal choice instead of a simple chase ending.

Read-Aloud:

> Kessa Coil presses herself against a wall of moving code, one hand on the blue shard at her throat. "I took names," she says. "I did not take lives. Mira said the debts were orientation fees. Then I saw the collateral language."
>
> A hooded figure appears in the tunnel text beside you, eyes made of shifting commands. CodeX says, "The shard can prove the scam. It can also prove the registry is vulnerable. Decide who gets to know."

DM Truth: Kessa wants protection from Vane, Mira, and possibly the Wardens. CodeX wants a copy of the shard to expose or exploit the vulnerability. Marik would secure it as evidence. Aria would broadcast the story. Ira would file it carefully to protect Sel.

NPCs Present: Kessa Coil; CodeX projection; possibly Aria, Felix, or Marik if summoned after the chase.

Player Options: Turn Kessa over to Wardens, protect her as witness, give CodeX a copy, refuse CodeX, destroy the shard after copying evidence, bargain with Kessa, or confront Mira immediately.

Checks and DCs:

- DC 12 Wisdom (Insight) to see Kessa is telling the truth about not knowing the full clause at first.
- DC 13 Charisma (Persuasion) to secure Kessa's willing statement.
- DC 14 Intelligence (Investigation) to copy the shard without altering metadata.
- DC 15 Charisma (Intimidation) to make Kessa comply; this creates a brittle statement that Ira must repair later.
- DC 16 Intelligence (Arcana) to create a sealed evidence copy and a redacted safety copy for CodeX or Marik.
- DC 17 Charisma (Persuasion) to convince CodeX that public legal process is better than immediate leak.

Success Result: The party leaves with the shard, Kessa's statement, and a chosen evidence custodian. They also earn one contact: CodeX, Marik, Aria, Felix, or Ira depending on their choice.

Partial Success Result: The party leaves with evidence but angers one faction. If they deny CodeX any access, Codebreakers become suspicious. If they deny Marik, Wardens distrust their chain of custody. If they hand everything to Felix, Aria questions their judgment.

Failure Result: The evidence leaves their direct control. CodeX leaks a partial copy, Marik seizes the shard, or Kessa flees with it. The party still has enough to demand a hearing because Sel, Aria, Brindle, or the registry slip can testify, but they lose advantage in the first legal scene.

Clues:

- Merrit Vane is the senior broker behind First Step Brokerage.
- Mira Vale handled field enforcement.
- Kessa Coil stole registry data but can become a witness.
- The false debt requires a Contract Hall ruling to clear cleanly if activated.

Consequences: End Session 3 with Ira Quill's message arriving through a witness bell or GUIDY relay:

> "Bring the parcel, shard, witness names, and anyone still willing to tell the truth. Contract Hall, first open docket. Do not let anyone discuss settlement without me."

This is the handoff to the next chunk.

## Keyed Locations for Opening Adventure

### Portal Plaza

Read-Aloud: Blue light washes across a wide plaza of glassy stone and glowing circuit-lines. Portal constellations drift overhead. At the center, a fountain of names and numbers chimes softly beneath the impossible shadow of the Tower.

DM Details: Portal Plaza is the main arrival point and a strong safe zone. It contains the Arrival Dais, Life Counter Fountain, Orientation Kiosk, Warden Post, Charter Wall, portal kiosks, and roads to Convergence Point Tavern and Tower Forecourt.

Notable NPCs: GUIDY, Marik Bluecoat, Warden Lio Brass, Vela Mourn, Sel Varrin, Tamsin Halewire.

Exits: North to Tower Forecourt Road; south to Convergence Steps; east to portal kiosks; west to Market Walk.

Objects of Interest: Life Counter Fountain, Charter Wall, orientation slips, blue safe-zone lamps, arrival registry tiles.

Checks/DCs: DC 10 Investigation for public directions; DC 12 Arcana for safe-zone function; DC 13 Insight for crowd mood; DC 15 Investigation for registry anomalies.

Clues: Temporary team ID ping; First Step Brokerage redaction; life counters linked to registry; contract bell anomaly.

Possible Complications: Crowd panic, safe-zone warning, rumor vendor attention, Warden suspicion, Sel fleeing.

Treasure or Service: Free orientation summary, emergency directions, basic safe-zone healing for minor injuries, Vela's memorial etiquette, GUIDY's error slip.

At-Table Additions: Interactive objects include the Arrival Dais registry tiles, blue safe-zone lamp posts, and loose printed warning slips fluttering from GUIDY's ticket spool. Complications: a Panicked Novice Mob blocks the Convergence Steps, or a rumor vendor begins narrating the party's reactions out loud. Overheard lines: "Three lives sounds generous until you count funerals," and "Do not take jobs from boxes with silver teeth." Hidden detail: one registry tile flashes K.Coil for half a second after Sel's counter blink. Faction appearance: Marik arrives with a Bluecoat Patrol, while a Guild watcher pretends to sell map pins. Ability, spell, or tool use: calm emotions, thaumaturgy, Performance, or Persuasion can steady the crowd; thieves' tools or Arcana can recover a damaged registry spark. Clue or evidence source: the GUIDY error slip and the K.Coil flash both point to stolen registry access.

### Orientation Kiosk

Read-Aloud: A brass-and-blue kiosk unfolds like a patient flower, projecting menus of law, maps, emergency phrases, and warnings that keep politely rearranging themselves around your questions.

DM Details: The kiosk provides public information and limited registry access. It cannot reveal sealed legal records, but glitches expose traces before redaction.

Notable NPCs: GUIDY often hovers here; Chime passes through with parcel notices.

Exits: Fountain west, Arrival Dais southwest, Convergence Steps south.

Objects of Interest: Registry slot, printed error slips, emergency override panel, public map.

Checks/DCs: DC 10 Investigation for basic law; DC 13 Arcana for life-counter data; DC 15 tools or Arcana for ping trail; DC 16 Investigation for First Step trace after redaction.

Clues: K.Coil courier tag; First Step Brokerage name; parcel seal warning.

Possible Complications: Kiosk locks, prints incomplete data, alerts Warden clerk, or gives a cheerful but alarming warning.

Treasure or Service: Error slip, map token, one free emergency phrase card.

At-Table Additions: Interactive objects include the registry slot, emergency override button, and public map lens that zooms toward marked districts. Complications: the kiosk redacts First Step Brokerage mid-sentence, or a waiting arrival tries to accept the party's parcel notice by mistake. Overheard lines: "The kiosk knows my name but not my home," and "If it prints red, take it to a clerk." Hidden detail: the kiosk stores one unredacted frame in its thermal printer ribbon. Faction appearance: a Warden clerk asks for the error slip; a Codebreaker glyph offers to recover the deleted frame for a favor. Ability, spell, or tool use: mending can restore a torn slip; comprehend languages reveals old legal shorthand; tinker's tools can pull a spool impression. Clue or evidence source: the unredacted frame shows First Step Brokerage and the K.Coil courier tag.

### Life Counter Fountain

Read-Aloud: Names rise in liquid blue light, each paired with three small marks. Some marks shine. Some are dim. A few names sink before you can read them, leaving only ripples.

DM Details: The fountain displays public life-count data and memorial traces. It is emotionally important to residents. Aazoth can flicker here.

Notable NPCs: Vela Mourn, Sel Varrin, Aazoth's reflection.

Exits: All plaza directions.

Objects of Interest: Life reflections, faded-name basin, memorial ribbons, Charter Wall sightline.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Religion or History for memorial customs; DC 13 Investigation for faded names; DC 15 Arcana for counter-registry relationship.

Clues: Life counters are real registry-linked markers; Aazoth responds to fear and mercy; Sel's blink was abnormal.

Possible Complications: Public grief, disrespect causing reputation harm, rumor vendor recording reactions.

Treasure or Service: Vela can provide a memorial ribbon that grants advantage on one respectful social check with Last Light or a bereaved NPC.

At-Table Additions: Interactive objects include memorial ribbons, reflection pools that show life marks, and the faded-name basin. Complications: a grieving resident mistakes a PC for someone who failed to save a loved one, or a spectator treats the fountain like entertainment and draws public anger. Overheard lines: "The third chime is quieter than the first two," and "Aazoth shows up when the law forgets faces." Hidden detail: Sel's reflected name briefly appears with a gray thread leading toward the Orientation Kiosk. Faction appearance: a Covenant of the Last Light mourner asks whether the party believes Article I is mercy or punishment. Ability, spell, or tool use: Religion or History reads memorial customs; detect magic separates life-counter magic from registry magic; an herbalism kit or healer's kit can aid an overwhelmed mourner. Clue or evidence source: the gray thread confirms Sel's counter was touched from outside the fountain.

### Warden Post

Read-Aloud: Blue armor stands behind a low stone counter under a halberd symbol. The holding cells are visible, clean, and deliberately uncomfortable to look at. A sign reads: LAW IS SHELTER. DO NOT MAKE IT A WALL.

DM Details: The Warden Post handles safe-zone incidents and public complaints. Marik uses it to de-escalate rather than punish when possible.

Notable NPCs: Marik Bluecoat, Warden Lio Brass, Warden clerk Rutha Pell.

Exits: Portal Plaza center, Tower Forecourt Road, holding corridor.

Objects of Interest: Incident ledger, safe-zone restraint glyph, public complaint bell.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Persuasion for basic help; DC 14 Insight to read Warden priorities; DC 15 Investigation to compare incident timestamps; DC 16 Persuasion to secure Marik's future statement.

Clues: New-arrival false debts are rising; Wardens need proof; First Step complaints exist but are sealed.

Possible Complications: Hardline Warden overhears, public complaint delays action, Tamsin's anger distracts Marik.

Treasure or Service: Written Warden intake note, legal escort to a public location, temporary protection for a witness.

At-Table Additions: Interactive objects include the incident ledger, complaint bell, and blue restraint glyph etched into the counter. Complications: a hardline Warden argues that all new arrivals should be barred from delivery work, or Tamsin files a complaint that distracts Marik from the party's evidence. Overheard lines: "Safe-zone law caught the bottle, not the cause," and "First Step again? Seal that note." Hidden detail: sealed complaint numbers on the ledger show three prior First Step incidents in the last tenday. Faction appearance: Guardian Wardens can offer escort; a Ledger Court runner can request that evidence go directly to intake. Ability, spell, or tool use: Insight reads which Warden can be moved; calligrapher's supplies copy a complaint number cleanly; zone of truth is unavailable without a hearing but asking for it impresses Marik. Clue or evidence source: the complaint numbers establish a pattern before Sel's case.

### Convergence Point Tavern

Read-Aloud: Blue lanterns glow over a circular tavern filled with climbers, clerks, performers, and arrivals pretending not to listen to each other. A stage rises from the center like a witness stand with better lighting.

DM Details: The tavern is a safe zone and social crossroads. It is loud enough to hide pressure and public enough to create witnesses.

Notable NPCs: Aria Neon, Yorn Glass, Chime, Brindle Pact, Sel Varrin.

Exits: South to Portal Plaza, east to Pixel Promenade, north balcony to quiet booths, back hall to service alley.

Objects of Interest: Aria's stage, parcel niche, notice board, contract alcove, blue lanterns.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Persuasion for rumors; DC 13 Insight for crowd mood; DC 14 Investigation for parcel records; DC 16 Perception to spot Brindle.

Clues: First Step parcels timed to performances; Brindle recruited witnesses; Chime's seal is too strong for a simple delivery.

Possible Complications: Public rumor, safe-zone warning, Mira's demand, Brindle fleeing, Sel accepting under pressure.

Treasure or Service: Meal tokens worth 10 NC, Aria's rumor network, Yorn's private booth for one hour.

At-Table Additions: Interactive objects include the parcel niche, notice board, and blue lantern chains that double as witness lights. Complications: Brindle tries to flee through the kitchen, or Mira invokes commercial-property language to make evidence seizure look like theft. Overheard lines: "Aria changed the bridge; that means trouble," and "A welcome parcel should not need a witness gem." Hidden detail: Yorn's private witness-light backup captured Mira entering before Chime presented the parcel. Faction appearance: a Spire Seeker table watches the party's courage, while a Ledger Court clerk quietly notes who touched the parcel. Ability, spell, or tool use: Performance can turn the crowd; unseen servant can hold the parcel without speaking terms; cook's utensils or brewer's supplies earn Yorn's quick trust. Clue or evidence source: the witness-light backup and parcel niche log prove timing.

### Aria's Stage

Read-Aloud: Neon ribbons hang from the stage rafters, displaying lyrics, gossip, and tiny legal disclaimers. The floorboards remember applause and secrets in equal measure.

DM Details: Aria uses the stage to shape public perception. It is also fitted with performance witness lights that can become evidence if correctly invoked.

Notable NPCs: Aria Neon; two backup musicians, Lume and Cass; tavern regulars.

Exits: Common floor, backstage curtain, north balcony stairs.

Objects of Interest: Ribbon displays, stage witness lights, lyric archive, tip basin.

Checks/DCs: DC 13 Performance to influence crowd; DC 14 Investigation to decode ribbon clues; DC 15 Persuasion to get Aria's private help; DC 16 Arcana to copy witness-light memory.

Clues: "Collateral chorus"; performance timed to delivery; Brindle's balcony position.

Possible Complications: Crowd turns scene into spectacle, Aria protects a source by withholding a name, stage lights record an embarrassing statement.

Treasure or Service: Aria can broadcast a correction, provide disguises, or grant advantage on one public reputation check.

At-Table Additions: Interactive objects include ribbon lyrics, tip basin, and a stage witness lamp disguised as a spotlight. Complications: a heckler repeats Vane's rumor line, or Aria's source panics when the party names Brindle aloud. Overheard lines: "If Aria rhymes your name with 'clause,' leave town," and "The chorus changed when the box came in." Hidden detail: the ribbon archive stores the exact moment Chime's witness gem brightened. Faction appearance: Spire Seekers amplify a dramatic truth; Remnant Veil listeners offer to hide a witness after the show. Ability, spell, or tool use: Performance can give the party advantage with the room; minor illusion can replay a clue; weaver's tools or calligrapher's supplies can preserve ribbon text. Clue or evidence source: the ribbon archive supports the claim that delivery was timed to distraction.

### Pixel Promenade

Read-Aloud: Shops, signs, and illusions compete for the right to be noticed first. Coin icons ripple over awnings. Street performers sing over haggling voices while vendor witness lights blink like patient eyes.

DM Details: The Promenade is commerce and reputation made public. Vendor rows are protected, but alleys and Code Cavern stairs are less safe.

Notable NPCs: Felix Pixelcoin, Chime, Aria, Nomi Sweetspark, Pell Tick, silent Guild clerks.

Exits: North to Grand Exchange, south to tavern road, east arcade, west alley, Code Cavern Stairs.

Objects of Interest: Coin Arch, stock board, appraisal lamps, food carts, Code Cavern warning sign.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Persuasion for vendor rumors; DC 14 Investigation for stock token; DC 15 Perception for watcher; DC 16 Performance to shift public story.

Clues: Counterfeit guild stock; Pell's rumor manipulation; K.Coil scan at Code Cavern Stairs.

Possible Complications: Prices rise, public suspicion, silent watcher warns Kessa, Felix stalls.

Treasure or Service: Fair appraisal, 50 NC compensation from Felix, food-cart healing snack that functions as one potion of healing if bought for 50 NC.

At-Table Additions: Interactive objects include the stock board, coin arch, and food-cart row with safe-zone sales lamps. Complications: Pell updates the rumor crawl before the party can speak, or vendors demand collateral before selling to marked debtors. Overheard lines: "Collateral pending means charge up front," and "Felix smiles more when he is guilty of something smaller than accused." Hidden detail: the stock board's last manual edit came from Pell's clerk ring. Faction appearance: Pixel Prosperity clerks try to control the story; Aria or a Spire Seeker can make the crowd listen. Ability, spell, or tool use: jeweler's tools or Investigation appraise counterfeit stock; Performance challenges the rumor crawl; prestidigitation can mark Pell's ink trail. Clue or evidence source: the board log and counterfeit token connect First Step to Kessa's scan.

### Felix's Appraisal Stall

Read-Aloud: Felix's stall gleams with price tags, magnifying crystals, and a sign that changes slogans every few seconds. The current slogan reads: IF IT CURSES YOU, I CHARGE EXTRA TO FIND OUT HOW.

DM Details: Felix can identify counterfeit guild stock and provide delivery logs. He is guilty of negligence and afraid of Vane.

Notable NPCs: Felix Pixelcoin, Chime, two Guild clerks.

Exits: Promenade center, private ledger curtain, Grand Exchange courier slot.

Objects of Interest: Appraisal lamps, stock ledger, rush courier log, counterfeit token tray.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Insight for Felix's guilt type; DC 14 Investigation for counterfeit stock; DC 15 tools for token trace; DC 16 Persuasion for Vane's name.

Clues: Merrit Vane benefits; First Step used counterfeit guild stock; Kessa Coil was last scan.

Possible Complications: Felix demands discretion, Guild clerk reports to Vane, Chime feels blamed and shuts down.

Treasure or Service: 50 NC per PC compensation on good terms, free appraisal, future 10 percent discount if party clears Felix without hiding his negligence.

At-Table Additions: Interactive objects include appraisal lamps, token scale, and the rush delivery ledger behind the curtain. Complications: a Guild clerk tries to close the stall for audit, or Felix offers money before he offers truth and makes himself look worse. Overheard lines: "If Felix says 'technically,' listen harder," and "Vane's people use old stock, not bright stock." Hidden detail: the token scale shows two serial shadows: Felix's public route and Vane's private reroute. Faction appearance: Pixel Prosperity hardliners send a clerk; Ledger Court can request a sealed copy if Ira has been contacted. Ability, spell, or tool use: identify or Arcana reads the token's routing magic; jeweler's tools expose the serial shadow; Insight separates Felix's guilt from Vane's design. Clue or evidence source: delivery ledger plus token scale produces strong evidence.

### Code Cavern Stairs

Read-Aloud: The stairs descend under the Promenade into green-black light. The air cools and tastes like copper. Someone has scratched route arrows into the wall, but several arrows point at each other in quiet disagreement.

DM Details: The stairs leave strong safe-zone protection. CodeX watches through glyphs. Kessa recently passed through.

Notable NPCs: CodeX projection, Nomi Sweetspark at the top, possible Warden tail.

Exits: Up to Pixel Promenade, down to Glitch Tunnel, side maintenance rail.

Objects of Interest: Warning sign, route glyphs, old access panel, Kessa's scuff sparks.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Perception for movement below; DC 13 Arcana for glitch pockets; DC 14 Stealth for quiet descent; DC 16 Investigation for maintenance rail.

Clues: CodeX mark; Kessa route; registry shard resonance.

Possible Complications: Glitch pulse, watcher warning, CodeX bargain, Warden order to stop.

Treasure or Service: Route hint from CodeX; maintenance rail advantage on first chase leg.

At-Table Additions: Interactive objects include the warning sign, CodeX chalk mark, and maintenance rail with old grip-runes. Complications: a Warden tail orders the party to wait for authorization, or Pell's warning glyph flashes ahead of them. Overheard lines: "The stairs eat confident people first," and "CodeX marks safe paths with arguments, not arrows." Hidden detail: Kessa's boot left silver courier wax on the third rail post. Faction appearance: Codebreakers offer a shortcut; Wardens offer chain of custody at the cost of speed. Ability, spell, or tool use: Survival tracks scuff sparks; Arcana reads glitch tides; thieves' tools release the maintenance rail brake. Clue or evidence source: courier wax links Kessa to the shard route.

### Glitch Tunnel

Read-Aloud: The tunnel walls are black stone overlaid with broken green script. Every few seconds, the floor forgets whether it is stairs, glass, or running light.

DM Details: This is the chase route. It contains hazards that pressure movement, attention, and evidence protection.

Notable NPCs: Kessa Coil, CodeX projection, glitch wisps, Debt Shade fragment.

Exits: Code Cavern Stairs, lower maintenance door, ledger lock door, shadow route used by Nyx.

Objects of Interest: Split-script fork, witness echo hall, falling code steps, shard resonance trail.

Checks/DCs: Use chase DCs. DC 13 for movement, DC 15 for protected progress, DC 17 for extra advantage.

Clues: Kessa's shouted confession; shard metadata; Mira's ledger token; First Step payment trail.

Possible Complications: Wisp Error Pulse, evidence damage, Kessa falling, CodeX requesting a copy, Debt Shade fragment whispering promises.

Treasure or Service: Registry shard, ledger token, CodeX contact, Kessa's witness statement.

At-Table Additions: Interactive objects include split-script forks, echoing witness walls, and the Ledger Lock Door. Complications: a Debt Shade fragment targets the strongest evidence, or a glitch wisp separates the rear PC from the group. Overheard lines: Kessa shouts, "I did not know about collateral," and a wall echo repeats, "Delivery Validators affirm." Hidden detail: Mira's token imprint appears on the lock when the ledger case gets close. Faction appearance: CodeX projects through tunnel text; Nyx's Veil route briefly opens if Kessa escapes. Ability, spell, or tool use: feather fall saves the Mercy Drop; mage hand can catch a falling shard; Arcana can stabilize a fork; Athletics can carry an ally over running light. Clue or evidence source: shard metadata, Mira token imprint, and echo-recorded confession.

### Contract Hall Exterior

Read-Aloud: The Contract Hall rises in black-blue stone carved with millions of names, each line precise enough to feel sharp. Witness bells hang under the eaves. Some ring when no hand touches them.

DM Details: CHUNK 01 ends before the hearing. The exterior provides the handoff location and establishes legal gravity.

Notable NPCs: Ira Quill by message or at the steps; a Clause Bailiff at the doors; nervous witnesses including Brindle or Kessa if protected.

Exits: Ledger Court plaza, evidence intake door, public hearing queue, witness protection side entrance.

Objects of Interest: Witness bells, docket board, evidence intake slot, public settlement alcoves.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Investigation to find correct docket; DC 13 Insight to identify settlement predators; DC 14 Persuasion to keep a witness calm; DC 15 Arcana to seal evidence until intake.

Clues: First open docket; settlement offers are already waiting; Vane's side has legal representation.

Possible Complications: Witness intimidation, lowball settlement offer, Clause Bailiff demands chain of custody, rumor crowd gathers.

Treasure or Service: Ira's legal intake, witness protection token, hearing date, clean transition to next chunk.

At-Table Additions: Interactive objects include witness bells, evidence intake slot, and public docket board. Complications: a settlement broker approaches Sel before Ira arrives, or a Clause Bailiff refuses damaged evidence without chain-of-custody testimony. Overheard lines: "Never settle on the steps," and "If Vane sent flowers, someone is about to lie." Hidden detail: the docket board already lists First Step Brokerage under sealed preliminary review. Faction appearance: Ledger Court clerks manage intake; Guardian Wardens offer custody; Pixel Prosperity hardliners send a settlement page. Ability, spell, or tool use: calligrapher's supplies prepare clean evidence labels; Insight spots hostile witnesses; detect magic identifies forged seal residue. Clue or evidence source: the docket board proves the Court has prior First Step concern, though it does not reveal sealed details.

## Table Map Notes for Opening Locations

### Portal Plaza

PCs Probably Begin: On the Arrival Dais or just south of it, close enough to see Tamsin, Sel, GUIDY, and the Life Counter Fountain.

Important NPC Begins: Tamsin is between the Arrival Dais and Warden Post; Sel is near the fountain edge; GUIDY enters from the Orientation Kiosk.

Exits: North to Tower Forecourt Road, south to Convergence Steps, east to portal kiosks, west to Market Walk.
