Danger Enters: The danger is panic and legal confusion, not a blade. The contract bell anomaly comes from the kiosk; public pressure comes from the crowd.

If the Party Runs: They can leave the plaza, but GUIDY follows and Sel moves toward the parcel alone.

If the Party Calls Wardens: Marik arrives sooner, creating order but making some arrivals less willing to talk.

If the Party Splits Up: One group can calm Tamsin while another protects Sel or checks the kiosk. Reward this with faster clue access.

### Convergence Point Tavern

PCs Probably Begin: At the south entrance or common tables, with the parcel niche visible across the room.

Important NPC Begins: Aria is on stage, Chime is at the parcel niche, Sel is near the common tables, Brindle watches from the north balcony.

Exits: South to Portal Plaza, east to Pixel Promenade, back hall to service alley, balcony stairs to quiet booths.

Danger Enters: The parcel activates through speech and witness light; Mira enters through the east door when evidence is threatened.

If the Party Runs: They can carry the parcel out, but Mira or Pell follows, and Sel may remain vulnerable.

If the Party Calls Wardens: Wardens can pause public violence, but they cannot void the parcel without evidence.

If the Party Splits Up: One group can inspect the parcel while another talks to Aria or corners Brindle. If no one watches Sel, he may speak acceptance language.

### Pixel Promenade

PCs Probably Begin: At the south road from the tavern, facing the Coin Arch and Felix's stall.

Important NPC Begins: Felix is under the Coin Arch; Pell is near the stock board; Nomi is near the Code Cavern Stairs.

Exits: North to Grand Exchange, south to tavern road, east arcade, west alley, down through Code Cavern Stairs.

Danger Enters: Public rumor updates on the stock board, and Kessa's trail starts moving before the party finishes arguing.

If the Party Runs: They can rush to the stairs and skip some social fallout, but Felix's logs or Pell's watcher clue may be lost.

If the Party Calls Wardens: A Warden tail can protect chain of custody but may spook Kessa and CodeX.

If the Party Splits Up: One group can handle Felix while another watches Pell or Nomi. If nobody watches the stairs, Kessa begins the chase with a warning.

### Code Caverns

PCs Probably Begin: At the top of the Code Cavern Stairs, then descend into the Glitch Tunnel.

Important NPC Begins: Kessa starts 60 feet ahead in the tunnel; CodeX appears through wall text; wisps appear around evidence or locks.

Exits: Up to Pixel Promenade, deeper through the Ledger Lock Door, side maintenance rail, hidden Veil slit if Kessa escapes.

Danger Enters: Glitch hazards change terrain, wisps attack evidence, and the Debt Shade fragment pressures the strongest proof.

If the Party Runs: Running is the default, but running without tracking or protecting evidence increases failure risk.

If the Party Calls Wardens: Wardens secure the top of the stairs and chain of custody, but Kessa fears being trapped and starts one round farther ahead.

If the Party Splits Up: Split into Lead and Cutoff groups. Both need a success before the end of the next round, or the failed group faces a hazard alone.

## Opening Adventure Combat Profiles

These profiles support Sessions 1-3 only. They favor low damage, visible objectives, morale, and noncombat exits. Use them when a scene turns physical outside a strong safe zone, when a hazard needs initiative, or when the party forces a confrontation.

### Glitch Wisp

Intended Level/Tier: Level 1 hazard-minion.

Suggested CR/XP: CR 1/8, 25 XP.

Encounter Difficulty for 4 Level-1 PCs: 1 wisp is trivial, 2 wisps are easy, 3 wisps plus a hazard can become medium.

Safe Maximum at Once: 2 wisps for a normal Session 3 chase beat. Using 4 or more risks too many disadvantage effects.

AC 13; HP 7; Speed 0 ft., fly 40 ft.

Abilities: Str -3, Dex +3, Con +1, Int -1, Wis +1, Cha +0.

Saving Throws: Dex +5. Skills: Stealth +5, Perception +3. Senses: darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 13. Languages: understands Code Cant but cannot speak.

Traits: Flicker Step. Opportunity attacks against the wisp have disadvantage. Evidence Static. The wisp has advantage on checks to harass a creature carrying exposed evidence.

Actions: Static Sting. Melee Spell Attack: +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. Hit: 4 lightning damage. Error Pulse (Recharge 5-6). One creature within 15 feet makes a DC 12 Intelligence saving throw. On a failure, the target has disadvantage on its next ability check before the end of its next turn.

Reactions: Scatter. When reduced to 3 HP or fewer, the wisp moves up to 15 feet without provoking opportunity attacks.

Tactics: Targets evidence carriers, lights, locks, and witness devices before wounded PCs.

Morale: Flees if two wisps are destroyed or if a PC stabilizes the local code with Arcana.

Noncombat Resolution: DC 13 Arcana, tinker's tools, or thieves' tools disperses one wisp for the scene.

Scaling Note: 3 PCs use 1 wisp. 4 PCs use 2 wisps. 5 PCs use 2 wisps plus one evidence hazard. 6 PCs use 3 wisps split between different objectives.

### Debt Shade Fragment

Intended Level/Tier: Level 1-2 legal hazard, not a full monster.

Suggested CR/XP: Hazard, no XP unless fought as a creature; if defeated in combat, treat as CR 1/4, 50 XP.

Encounter Difficulty for 4 Level-1 PCs: Easy as a single objective hazard; medium if paired with 2 wisps.

Safe Maximum at Once: 1 fragment. More than 1 is dangerous because it pressures evidence and reactions, not just HP.

AC 12; HP 18; Speed 30 ft., climb 20 ft. along written surfaces.

Abilities: Str -1, Dex +2, Con +1, Int +0, Wis +1, Cha +2.

Saving Throws: Wis +3, Cha +4. Skills: Deception +4, Stealth +4. Senses: darkvision 60 ft., debt sense 30 ft., passive Perception 11. Languages: Common and legal formulae; speaks in clauses.

Traits: Clause Hide. While touching written text or a seal, the fragment can Hide as a bonus action. Debt Sense. It knows which visible creature has the largest active unpaid obligation, but not private emotional debts.

Actions: Ink Lash. Melee Spell Attack: +4 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. Hit: 5 necrotic damage, and the target's next check to protect evidence is made at -1. Call Marker (Recharge 6). One creature within 30 feet makes a DC 12 Wisdom saving throw. On failure, the creature cannot take reactions until the start of its next turn.

Reactions: Bite the Record. When a creature within 10 feet succeeds on an evidence check, the fragment forces that creature to choose: take 3 necrotic damage or reduce the evidence item's strength by one step until repaired.

Tactics: Attacks documents, seals, and confidence. It avoids killing blows.

Morale: Dissolves if the hidden clause is read aloud clearly or if reduced to 5 HP.

Noncombat Resolution: DC 14 Investigation to expose the flawed clause or DC 14 Persuasion to state a valid objection disperses it.

Scaling Note: 3 PCs make it a hazard with 10 HP and no Call Marker. 4 PCs run as written. 5 PCs add one Clause-Tick Imp. 6 PCs add a second evidence objective it can threaten.

### Clause-Tick Imp

Intended Level/Tier: Level 1 nuisance creature.

Suggested CR/XP: CR 0, 10 XP.

Encounter Difficulty for 4 Level-1 PCs: Trivial alone, easy as a complication with one other low-threat creature.

Safe Maximum at Once: 2 imps. Using 3 or more can overload action economy through item theft.

AC 12; HP 9; Speed 30 ft., climb 30 ft.

Abilities: Str -2, Dex +2, Con +0, Int +1, Wis +0, Cha +1.

Saving Throws: Dex +4. Skills: Sleight of Hand +4, Stealth +4. Senses: darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 10. Languages: Common, Code Cant.

Traits: Fine Print Body. The imp can squeeze through a gap as narrow as 1 inch if a document, sign, or label crosses the gap. Annoying Legalism. Creatures have disadvantage on opportunity attacks against it while it is carrying a paper object.

Actions: Paper Cut. Melee Weapon Attack: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. Hit: 3 slashing damage. Snatch Receipt. The imp targets one unattended Tiny paper or token object within 5 feet. A creature holding the item can prevent this with a DC 12 Dexterity saving throw.

Reactions: Notarized Dodge. When missed by an attack, the imp moves 5 feet.

Tactics: Steals receipts, seals, and tokens, then runs toward a legal light.

Morale: Surrenders if cornered and offered a blank form or shiny seal.

Noncombat Resolution: DC 12 Animal Handling, Arcana, or Deception tricks it into trading the stolen item.

Scaling Note: 3 PCs use 1 imp only if combat is already easy. 4 PCs use 1 imp with a wisp. 5 PCs use 2 imps. 6 PCs use 2 imps with separate stolen items.

### Glitch Courier

Intended Level/Tier: Level 1-2 chase opponent template.

Suggested CR/XP: CR 1/8, 25 XP.

Encounter Difficulty for 4 Level-1 PCs: Easy if cornered alone; the real challenge is the chase objective.

Safe Maximum at Once: 1 courier plus hazards. Do not run multiple couriers against level 1 PCs unless they flee rather than attack.

AC 13; HP 16; Speed 35 ft.

Abilities: Str +0, Dex +3, Con +1, Int +1, Wis +1, Cha +0.

Saving Throws: Dex +5. Skills: Acrobatics +5, Stealth +5, Sleight of Hand +5, Survival +3. Senses: passive Perception 11. Languages: Common, Code Cant.

Traits: Route Runner. The courier ignores nonmagical difficult terrain in urban or tunnel chases. Panic Sprint. Once per chase, the courier gains 20 feet of distance but drops a clue.

Actions: Light Blade. Melee Weapon Attack: +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. Hit: 4 piercing damage. Flash Tag. Ranged Weapon Attack: +5 to hit, range 20/60 ft., one target. Hit: 3 lightning damage, and the target cannot take reactions until the end of its next turn.

Reactions: Slip Turn. When a creature ends movement within 5 feet, the courier moves 10 feet if an exit is visible.

Tactics: Runs, distracts, and drops obstacles. Fights only to escape.

Morale: Stops if offered credible protection and shown evidence that Vane will abandon them.

Noncombat Resolution: DC 13 Persuasion during a mercy beat or DC 14 Athletics/Acrobatics to corner without injury.

Scaling Note: 3 PCs reduce HP to 12. 4 PCs run as written. 5 PCs add one glitch wisp. 6 PCs give the courier one prepared shortcut that requires a second objective to block.

### Kessa Quickwire

Intended Level/Tier: Level 1 named courier and witness.

Suggested CR/XP: CR 1/8, 25 XP if defeated as combat; award no XP for harming her if she is functioning as a witness.

Encounter Difficulty for 4 Level-1 PCs: Easy in combat, but morally and legally costly.

Safe Maximum at Once: Kessa alone, with at most 1-2 wisps as environmental pressure. Do not have Kessa focus fire.

AC 13; HP 18; Speed 35 ft.

Abilities: Str +0, Dex +3, Con +1, Int +1, Wis +1, Cha +1.

Saving Throws: Dex +5, Wis +3. Skills: Acrobatics +5, Insight +3, Sleight of Hand +5, Stealth +5. Senses: passive Perception 11. Languages: Common, Code Cant.

Traits: Registry Shard. While Kessa carries the shard, checks to track her by Arcana or Investigation have advantage if the pursuer has seen the shard flare. Frightened Witness. If reduced below half HP, Kessa disengages and shouts one true clue.

Actions: Courier Knife. Melee Weapon Attack: +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. Hit: 4 piercing damage. Static Pellet. Ranged Weapon Attack: +5 to hit, range 30/90 ft., one target. Hit: 3 lightning damage, and the target's speed is reduced by 5 feet until the end of its next turn.

Reactions: Protect the Shard. When a creature would grab the shard, Kessa makes a contested Dexterity check with +5.

Tactics: Avoids lethal force, protects the shard, and uses dangerous routes rather than attacks.

Morale: Surrenders to protection, mercy, or proof that Mira lied. Flees from Warden threats.

Noncombat Resolution: DC 13 Persuasion if rescued, DC 15 Persuasion if injured, DC 17 Intimidation for compliance with hostile testimony.

Scaling Note: 3 PCs use Kessa without wisps. 4 PCs add chase hazards. 5 PCs add 1 wisp. 6 PCs add a second route objective and keep Kessa's damage unchanged.

### Brindle Nullmark

Intended Level/Tier: Level 1 social runner.

Suggested CR/XP: CR 0, 10 XP if defeated as combat; no XP for bullying or harming him in a safe zone.

Encounter Difficulty for 4 Level-1 PCs: Trivial physically; the challenge is social and legal.

Safe Maximum at Once: Brindle alone. Add Mira or crowd pressure instead of more attackers.

AC 12; HP 11; Speed 30 ft.

Abilities: Str -1, Dex +2, Con +0, Int +1, Wis +1, Cha +2.

Saving Throws: Dex +4. Skills: Deception +4, Insight +3, Persuasion +4, Stealth +4. Senses: passive Perception 11. Languages: Common, Guild Cant.

Traits: Safe-Zone Cowardice. Brindle has advantage on checks to disengage socially in a safe zone but disadvantage on saving throws against fear outside one. Paid to Point. If pressured, he drops one clue before attempting to flee.

Actions: Distracting Plea. One creature within 30 feet that can hear Brindle makes a DC 12 Wisdom saving throw. On failure, Brindle gains advantage on his next check to flee or hide from that creature. Dagger. Melee Weapon Attack: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. Hit: 3 piercing damage.

Reactions: Not My Fault. When accused publicly, Brindle moves up to half his speed toward the nearest exit.

Tactics: Avoids combat. Uses crowds, balconies, and kitchen doors.

Morale: Cooperates when protected; collapses under credible danger.

Noncombat Resolution: DC 13 Persuasion for truth, DC 14 Intimidation for one fact plus resentment, DC 15 Insight to learn what protection he needs.

Scaling Note: 3 PCs Brindle starts willing if Aria vouches. 4 PCs run as written. 5 PCs add Mira pressure during the scene. 6 PCs split Brindle's escape from Mira's demand.

### Mira Softlock

Intended Level/Tier: Level 2 social enforcer.

Suggested CR/XP: CR 1/4, 50 XP.

Encounter Difficulty for 4 Level-1 PCs: Medium if she fights outside a safe zone; hard if paired with wisps or imps.

Safe Maximum at Once: Mira alone as an active combatant. If she has helpers, they should flee, steal evidence, or pressure witnesses rather than attack every round.

AC 14; HP 24; Speed 30 ft.

Abilities: Str +0, Dex +2, Con +1, Int +2, Wis +1, Cha +3.

Saving Throws: Dex +4, Cha +5. Skills: Deception +5, Insight +3, Investigation +4, Persuasion +5. Senses: passive Perception 11. Languages: Common, Guild Cant, Legal Cant.

Traits: Safe-Zone Operator. Mira has advantage on Charisma checks to frame herself as the reasonable party inside a safe zone unless the party presents physical evidence. Ledger Insurance. Once per scene, when accused, she can reveal a minor true fact to redirect attention.

Actions: Softlock Baton. Melee Weapon Attack: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. Hit: 5 bludgeoning damage. Contract Snare (Recharge 6). One creature within 30 feet makes a DC 13 Charisma saving throw. On failure, the creature has disadvantage on its next check to make a public accusation before the end of its next turn.

Reactions: Legal Deflection. When a creature makes a successful social check against Mira in public, she forces that creature to produce evidence or reduce the success to partial success.

Tactics: Avoids unsafe combat, pressures witnesses, steals evidence, and retreats before initiative favors the party.

Morale: Flees if Vane's name is spoken with proof or if Brindle is protected by a recognized witness.

Noncombat Resolution: DC 15 Persuasion with evidence makes her trade; DC 16 Insight reveals she fears Vane.

Scaling Note: 3 PCs lower HP to 18 and remove Contract Snare. 4 PCs run as written. 5 PCs add a Clause-Tick Imp. 6 PCs add a second objective: protect Brindle while confronting Mira.

### Pell Tick

Intended Level/Tier: Level 1 rumor operator.

Suggested CR/XP: CR 0, 10 XP if combat occurs; social exposure is the intended resolution.

Encounter Difficulty for 4 Level-1 PCs: Trivial physically; medium social complication if the crowd believes him.

Safe Maximum at Once: Pell alone with a crowd. Do not add damaging allies unless the party has left the safe zone.

AC 12; HP 10; Speed 25 ft.

Abilities: Str -2, Dex +2, Con +0, Int +2, Wis +1, Cha +2.

Saving Throws: Int +4, Cha +4. Skills: Deception +4, Investigation +4, Persuasion +4, Sleight of Hand +4. Senses: passive Perception 11. Languages: Common, Guild Cant.

Traits: Board Whisperer. Pell can alter one public rumor crawl if adjacent to a market signboard. Coward's Distance. Pell has advantage on checks to hide in a crowd after someone else becomes the focus.

Actions: Cutting Aside. One creature within 30 feet that can hear Pell makes a DC 12 Charisma saving throw. On failure, the creature has disadvantage on its next Persuasion check with bystanders. Pinprick Knife. Melee Weapon Attack: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. Hit: 2 piercing damage.

Reactions: Public Victim. When threatened in a safe zone, Pell calls attention to the threat, giving the threatening creature disadvantage on its next social check in that scene.

Tactics: Spreads rumor, warns Kessa, and avoids physical danger.

Morale: Folds under private proof but doubles down under public humiliation.

Noncombat Resolution: DC 14 Investigation exposes his board access; DC 13 Persuasion in private turns him into a watcher-list source.

Scaling Note: 3 PCs Pell acts alone. 4 PCs run as written. 5 PCs add one Guild clerk ally. 6 PCs make the rumor board and chase warning simultaneous objectives.

### Warden Bluecoat Patrol

Intended Level/Tier: Level 1-3 authority group.

Suggested CR/XP: CR 1/8 each, 25 XP each, but they are not intended as XP targets.

Encounter Difficulty for 4 Level-1 PCs: 1 patrol member is easy; 2 are medium; 3 can become hard because restraint changes action economy.

Safe Maximum at Once: 2 patrol members in Sessions 1-3. Use a third only to block exits, not to pile attacks onto PCs.

AC 16; HP 13 each; Speed 30 ft.

Abilities: Str +2, Dex +0, Con +1, Int +0, Wis +1, Cha +1.

Saving Throws: Wis +3. Skills: Insight +3, Perception +3, Athletics +4. Senses: passive Perception 13. Languages: Common, Legal Cant.

Traits: Safe-Zone Training. A patrol member has advantage on checks to restrain without damage in a blue-lit safe zone. Nonlethal Mandate. Patrol attacks in Sessions 1-3 are nonlethal unless attacked with lethal force outside a safe zone.

Actions: Halberd Haft. Melee Weapon Attack: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. Hit: 5 bludgeoning damage. Restrain. One creature within 5 feet must succeed on a DC 12 Strength or Dexterity saving throw or be grappled until the end of the patrol member's next turn.

Reactions: Blue Interpose. When a creature within 5 feet is targeted by an attack, the patrol member imposes disadvantage on the attack if holding a shield or halberd.

Tactics: Separate threats, protect civilians, call Marik, and preserve evidence.

Morale: Does not flee in safe zones. Withdraws outside safe zones if outnumbered and no civilian is at risk.

Noncombat Resolution: DC 12 Persuasion for cooperation, DC 14 Insight to identify the ranking Warden, DC 15 Deception to redirect without proof.

Scaling Note: 3 PCs use 1 patrol member plus warning light. 4 PCs use 2. 5 PCs use 2 plus a clerk. 6 PCs use 3 but keep them focused on restraint.

### Panicked Novice Mob

Intended Level/Tier: Level 1 crowd hazard.

Suggested CR/XP: Hazard, no XP unless the table awards story XP for calming the crowd.

Encounter Difficulty for 4 Level-1 PCs: Easy if calmed, medium if ignored during another objective.

Safe Maximum at Once: 1 mob hazard. More than one can separate low-level PCs too aggressively.

AC 10; HP special; Speed 25 ft.

Abilities: Str +1, Dex +0, Con +0, Int -1, Wis -1, Cha +0.

Saving Throws: none. Skills: none as a group. Senses: passive Perception 9. Languages: Common and mixed arrival languages.

Traits: Crowd Body. The mob is not a creature to kill. Treat it as a moving hazard occupying a 20-foot square. A creature entering or starting its turn in the mob's space must succeed on a DC 12 Strength or Dexterity saving throw or be pushed 10 feet and knocked prone. Calmed by Clarity. Three successful calming or organizing checks disperses the mob.

Actions: Surge. The mob moves 15 feet toward the loudest perceived exit or authority. Creatures in its path make the Crowd Body save.

Reactions: Panic Echo. When someone shouts "death," "debt," or "trapped," the mob shifts 5 feet.

Tactics: The mob is fear in motion. It blocks exits, separates allies, and threatens evidence by accident.

Morale: Disperses when GUIDY, Marik, or the party gives clear instructions and a visible safe route.

Noncombat Resolution: DC 12 Persuasion, Performance, careful Intimidation, or Insight to calm one section; DC 13 Athletics to clear a path without harm.

Scaling Note: 3 PCs require 2 successes to calm. 4 PCs require 3. 5 PCs require 4 or split into two clusters. 6 PCs require 4 with simultaneous Sel and Tamsin pressure.

## Opening Adventure Encounters

### Encounter 1: Orientation Social Encounter

Goal: Calm Portal Plaza, learn the basic laws, and secure the first registry clue.

Setup: Run during Session 1 Scenes 1-2. The party stands between panicked arrivals, GUIDY's checklist, and Warden procedure.

Difficulty and XP: Easy social encounter; no combat XP. Award progress through clues, trust tracks, and inspiration rather than XP.

Expected Resource Cost: Time, attention, and possibly one spell or feature used to calm the crowd.

Stop Combat Early: Direct violence is stopped by safe-zone law before damage lands.

Convert Combat: If a player escalates, make it a Warden restraint and apology scene, then return to Sel's counter anomaly.

Creatures/NPCs: GUIDY, Tamsin Halewire, Sel Varrin, Warden Lio Brass, Marik Bluecoat. No combat creatures.

Tactics or Behavior: Tamsin escalates verbally unless calmed. Sel withdraws unless reassured. GUIDY offers warnings in too many words. Marik watches for whether the party protects people or performs authority.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Persuasion calms Tamsin; DC 13 Insight reads fear; DC 14 Medicine or Persuasion steadies Sel; DC 15 Investigation catches registry ping.

Success: Party gains GUIDY's trust, Marik's respect, Sel as a witness, and the K.Coil or First Step clue.

Partial Success: Party calms the scene but loses one clue or one NPC's full trust.

Failure: Wardens restore order, but the party starts with public uncertainty. GUIDY still gives a basic warning so the adventure moves.

Scaling: For 3 PCs, have GUIDY directly state one clue after the first successful check. For 4 PCs, run as written. For 5 PCs, add a second panicked arrival with a different concern. For 6 PCs, split the scene between Tamsin and Sel so multiple PCs act at once.

Reward/Consequence: Advantage on one later GUIDY-assisted check for success; disadvantage on first tavern rumor check if the party escalated panic.

### Encounter 2: Witnessed Deal Demonstration

Goal: Teach witnessed deals safely and foreshadow hidden clauses.

Setup: Run at the blue awning stalls in Session 1 Scene 4. Sera Cupwise sells tea through a clear witnessed deal while Bram Lilt mishandles a tab.

Difficulty and XP: Trivial social demonstration; no combat XP.

Expected Resource Cost: 10 NC if a PC buys tea, or a social check if they help Bram.

Stop Combat Early: Safe-zone light prevents theft from becoming a fight.

Convert Combat: Treat aggression as a public warning that teaches safe-zone law and costs Public Attention.

Creatures/NPCs: Sera Cupwise, Bram Lilt, GUIDY, Chime.

Tactics or Behavior: Sera is honest and direct. Bram is embarrassed. Chime tries to pass unnoticed. The witness mote enforces only stated terms.

Checks/DCs: DC 10 Investigation understands sequence; DC 12 Persuasion helps Bram; DC 14 Arcana reads witness mote; DC 15 Investigation spots Chime's stronger seal.

Success: Party understands witnessed deals and gains a clear-terms receipt as comparison evidence.

Partial Success: Party learns the basics but misses Chime's seal.

Failure: GUIDY corrects the misunderstanding, but Brindle hears they are inexperienced.

Scaling: For 3 PCs, Sera volunteers the key lesson. For 4 PCs, run as written. For 5 PCs, add a second customer trying to exploit vague terms. For 6 PCs, add a playful witnessed-deal test between two NPCs so more characters can engage.

Reward/Consequence: Clear-terms receipt grants advantage on one false clause explanation at the tavern or hearing.

### Encounter 3: False Debt Investigation

Goal: Detect the hidden false debt clause before or after activation.

Setup: Run around the parcel in Session 2 Scene 2 or 3. The parcel is sealed, warm, and legally active.

Difficulty and XP: Easy investigation if careful; medium hazard if the Debt Shade Fragment manifests. Award 50 XP only if the fragment is defeated through combat, though evidence progress is the real reward.

Expected Resource Cost: One spell slot, tool use, social favor, or risk to parcel integrity.

Stop Combat Early: End the fragment's threat when the hidden clause is read clearly, the witness gem is covered, or a valid objection is spoken.

Convert Combat: Let a successful legal objection or Arcana check disperse the fragment instead of requiring damage.

Creatures/NPCs: Chime, Sel Varrin, Aria Neon, possible Debt Shade clause-spirit.

Tactics or Behavior: Chime recites terms without understanding. Sel wants hope. The Debt Shade hides inside text and activates through acceptance language.

Checks/DCs: DC 14 Investigation or calligrapher's supplies finds microtext; DC 13 Arcana reads witness gem; DC 15 Insight sees Chime's ignorance; DC 16 tools disables the gem cleanly; DC 14 Persuasion pauses activation after delivery.

Success: Party preserves parcel evidence and prevents binding.

Partial Success: Party prevents party collateral but Sel's debt may activate pending review.

Failure: False debt activates. Enforcement review is still contestable through evidence gathered in Session 3.

Scaling: For 3 PCs, lower the microtext DC to 13 and have Aria provide one hint. For 4 PCs, run as written. For 5 PCs, add a Debt Shade fragment that attempts to erase a clue. For 6 PCs, the fragment and a hostile witness pressure Sel simultaneously.

Reward/Consequence: Preserved parcel grants strong evidence. Activation creates public collateral review and urgency.

### Encounter 4: Tavern Social Pressure Scene

Goal: Handle Brindle Pact and Mira Vale without safe-zone violence.

Setup: Run Session 2 Scenes 4-5. Brindle wants escape. Mira wants evidence.

Difficulty and XP: Medium social encounter; no XP unless a fight occurs outside safe-zone protection. If Mira fights outside a safe zone, treat her as CR 1/4, 50 XP.

Expected Resource Cost: Reputation risk, a promise of protection, or one social resource such as a spell or favor.

Stop Combat Early: Mira retreats when Vane's link is named with proof or when neutral witnesses side with the party.

Convert Combat: A chase, public accusation, or protected-witness bargain should replace a damage race.

Creatures/NPCs: Brindle Pact, Mira Vale, Aria Neon, Yorn Glass, tavern crowd.

Tactics or Behavior: Brindle bargains from fear. Mira uses legal language, safe-zone protection, and public pressure. Aria turns truthful statements into crowd memory.

Checks/DCs: DC 13 Persuasion gets Brindle's admission; DC 14 Intimidation gets quick compliance with resentment; DC 16 Investigation identifies token; DC 15 Sleight of Hand marks Mira's ledger; DC 14 Persuasion stalls Mira.

Success: Party keeps evidence, gains Brindle's testimony, and identifies Pixel Promenade.

Partial Success: Party keeps one evidence path but loses either Brindle or ledger lead.

Failure: Mira destroys or steals part of the parcel, but the route to Felix remains through Aria or Chime.

Scaling: For 3 PCs, Brindle gives one fact immediately if promised protection. For 4 PCs, run as written. For 5 PCs, add Pell Tick recording the conversation. For 6 PCs, split Mira's pressure and Brindle's attempted escape.

Reward/Consequence: Brindle as future witness, Aria contact, or public rumor depending on conduct.

### Encounter 5: Pixel Promenade Appraisal Scene

Goal: Identify counterfeit guild stock and connect First Step to Kessa Coil and Merrit Vane.

Setup: Run at Felix's Appraisal Stall in Session 3 Scene 1.

Difficulty and XP: Easy-to-medium social/investigation encounter; no combat XP.

Expected Resource Cost: Time, public patience, or leverage over Felix.

Stop Combat Early: Vendor-row safe-zone lights lock attacks; Felix surrenders records before risking a brawl.

Convert Combat: Turn aggression into Public Rumor loss and a demand for proof from Felix's clerks.

Creatures/NPCs: Felix Pixelcoin, Chime, Pell Tick, Aria, Guild clerks.

Tactics or Behavior: Felix deflects until he sees evidence. Pell tries to warn Vane's network. Aria can make the truth public. Chime wants someone to say it was not entirely their fault.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Insight reads Felix; DC 14 Investigation finds counterfeit; DC 15 tools traces token; DC 16 Persuasion gets Vane's name; DC 16 Deception flushes Pell.

Success: Party gains logs, compensation, Kessa's last scan, and Vane's name.

Partial Success: Party gains Kessa lead but Felix frames help as a favor.

Failure: Felix stalls and Pell warns Kessa, adding one chase failure.

Scaling: For 3 PCs, Chime assists with the token trace. For 4 PCs, run as written. For 5 PCs, add one Guild clerk loyal to Vane. For 6 PCs, have public rumor pressure occur simultaneously at the stock board.

Reward/Consequence: 50 NC each from Felix on success, plus potential future discount or Guild hostility.

### Encounter 6: Code Cavern Chase

Goal: Catch Kessa Coil, secure the registry shard, and survive glitch hazards.

Setup: Run Session 3 Scene 4 as a skill challenge requiring 5 successes before 3 failures.

Difficulty and XP: Medium chase encounter for 4 level-1 PCs. If combat occurs, 2 Glitch Wisps are 50 XP total; adding the Debt Shade Fragment as combat raises the scene to about 100 XP plus hazards, still within medium if damage is spread.

Expected Resource Cost: 1-2 spell slots, hit points from hazards, or evidence strength if the party fails.

Stop Combat Early: When the party reaches 5 successes, Kessa is cornered, or a Mercy Beat succeeds.

Convert Combat: Every combat round must also include pursuit, evidence protection, or negotiation; otherwise it counts as chase failure.

Creatures/NPCs: Kessa Coil, 2 glitch wisps for 4 PCs, Debt Shade fragment hazard, CodeX projection.

Tactics or Behavior: Kessa flees but shouts partial truth. Glitch wisps target checks and evidence. The Debt Shade fragment attacks promises, witnesses, and shard handling rather than focusing damage.

Checks/DCs: Base DC 13; DC 15 for protected progress; DC 17 for extra benefit. Use Acrobatics, Athletics, Investigation, Survival, Arcana, Persuasion, Performance, tools, saves, and creative class features.

Success: Party secures Kessa and shard.

Partial Success: Party secures Kessa or shard.

Failure: Kessa escapes, but shard sliver or ledger scrap remains.

Scaling: For 3 PCs, require 4 successes before 3 failures and use 1 glitch wisp. For 4 PCs, run as written. For 5 PCs, add a third glitch wisp or an additional simultaneous evidence hazard. For 6 PCs, require 6 successes before 3 failures and split the party between Kessa and ledger lock.

Reward/Consequence: Registry shard, Kessa's statement, CodeX contact, or incomplete evidence depending on outcome.

### Encounter 7: Glitch Courier Confrontation

Goal: Decide Kessa's fate and evidence custody.

Setup: Run after the chase in Session 3 Scene 5.

Difficulty and XP: Medium social decision; no combat XP for harming Kessa. If combat starts, use Kessa's CR 1/8 only as a last resort and focus on escape.

Expected Resource Cost: Evidence custody, faction trust, or a promise of protection.

Stop Combat Early: Kessa surrenders when offered credible protection; CodeX withdraws if the party refuses a copy but preserves evidence.

Convert Combat: Make the scene a custody negotiation, witness-protection choice, or faction bargain.

Creatures/NPCs: Kessa Coil, CodeX, optional Marik, Aria, Felix, or Ira by message.

Tactics or Behavior: Kessa wants protection. CodeX wants a copy. Marik wants chain of custody. Aria wants public truth. Felix wants limited damage. Ira wants clean evidence and living witnesses.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Insight reads Kessa; DC 13 Persuasion gets statement; DC 14 Investigation copies metadata; DC 16 Arcana creates sealed evidence copy; DC 17 Persuasion convinces CodeX to wait for legal process.

Success: Party controls evidence and gains a contact.

Partial Success: Party controls evidence but angers one faction.

Failure: Evidence leaves party control, but enough testimony remains for a hearing.

Scaling: For 3 PCs, CodeX offers a clear two-option deal. For 4 PCs, run as written. For 5 PCs, add a Warden tail demanding custody. For 6 PCs, have Kessa and CodeX make simultaneous demands.

Reward/Consequence: Evidence custody determines advantage, faction reputation, and witness safety in the next chunk.

## Opening Adventure Rewards

Nexus Credit Rewards: Felix pays 50 NC per PC as compensation if the party proves counterfeit stock and treats him as negligent rather than the scam author. Marik can authorize 25 NC per PC for preserved registry evidence if the party files with Wardens. Aria can raise 10-30 NC per PC in public support if the party protects Sel and Brindle. The main Session 3 completion reward is 150 NC per PC from combined legal, public, and faction support once evidence is secured.

Reputation Rewards: Gain +1 with GUIDY's network if the party protects new arrivals and shares field notes. Gain +1 with Guardian Wardens if they preserve evidence and avoid unsafe escalation. Gain +1 with Aria's Promenade circle if they protect witnesses and tell the truth publicly. Gain +1 with Codebreakers if they expose registry vulnerability without handing every copy to Wardens. Lose 1 with a faction if the party frames that faction unfairly, destroys evidence, or hands a witness to known predators.

Faction Rewards: Marik offers a statement for the hearing. Aria offers public messaging. Felix offers appraisal and future discount if treated fairly. CodeX offers a route hint or encrypted copy service. Ira offers legal intake if the party brings evidence and witnesses.

Clue Rewards: The party can finish with the GUIDY registry slip, clear-terms receipt, preserved parcel seal, microtext copy, Brindle's statement, Mira's ledger token, counterfeit guild stock token, Felix's delivery log, Kessa's registry shard, Kessa's statement, and CodeX route glyph. They do not need all of these, but three strong evidence types make the next hearing easier.

Equipment Rewards: Possible rewards include one potion of healing from Nomi Sweetspark's food cart, a witness bell from Ira's message, a route chalk kit from CodeX, a clear-terms receipt from Sera, or a sealed evidence case from Marik.

Tower Access Progress: Clearing or contesting the false debt prevents it from blocking Tower registration. If unresolved, the party can still approach the Tower, but the Forecourt terminal flags "Collateral Review Pending" and routes them back to Ledger Court before legal entry.

Relationship Changes: Sel becomes grateful, ashamed, or frightened depending on how the party treated him. GUIDY becomes more candid. Marik begins measuring whether the party can be trusted with legal pressure. Aria decides whether they are story-worthy or merely loud. Felix becomes ally, debtor, or future antagonist. Kessa becomes witness, fugitive, or resentful loose end.

Milestone Guidance: If the party prevented false debt activation, protected Sel, and secured the registry shard, they may reach level 2 at the end of Session 3. If the debt activated, evidence is incomplete, or the table enjoys legal tension at level 1, award level 2 after the Contract Hall hearing in the next chunk.

## Opening Adventure Outcome Packages

Use the closest package when Session 3 ends. Adjust single details only to match the party's actual evidence and relationships.

### Clean Win

The party detects the false debt, preserves the parcel seal, catches or persuades Kessa, avoids public harm, and leaves with Sel protected.

NC Reward: 150 NC per PC total. This includes 50 NC from Felix, 25 NC Warden evidence stipend, 25 NC in public support or tavern credit, and 50 NC paid through Ira's intake fund after evidence is logged.

Reputation: +1 with GUIDY's network, +1 with Guardian Wardens or Ledger Court, and +1 with Aria's Promenade circle. No Criminal Heat.

Faction Reactions: Marik praises their restraint. Felix helps while accepting limited fault. Aria makes the party's version public. CodeX respects their evidence handling even if denied a full copy.

Evidence Strength: Decisive if they have the preserved parcel seal, hidden clause, and registry shard. Strong if they lack one of those but have Kessa or Brindle.

NPC Relationship Changes: Sel becomes Loyal. Chime becomes Helpful. Brindle appears for intake if protected. Kessa gives a willing statement. Mira withdraws. Pell hides.

Tower Access Progress: False debt does not block registration. The party may receive a clean identity note for the Forecourt after the hearing.

Item Rewards: Sealed evidence case, witness bell, and one route chalk kit or Nomi healing snack.

Milestone Guidance: Award level 2 at the end of Session 3 if the table wants the legal hearing at sturdier low-level play. Otherwise award level 2 after the hearing begins in their favor.

### Messy Win

The party solves the scam but causes public trouble, damages property, loses one clue, frightens a witness, or angers a faction.

NC Reward: 75 NC per PC. Felix pays only 25 NC each or frames it as a nuisance payment. Warden stipend is held until evidence intake. Public support does not appear.

Reputation: +1 with one helped faction, -1 or Suspicious status with one offended faction. Add Criminal Heat 1 if they triggered safe-zone warnings or damaged evidence.

Faction Reactions: Marik helps but documents concerns. Aria's public correction includes a pointed lyric about recklessness. Felix cooperates defensively. CodeX may demand a copy before offering route help.

Evidence Strength: Strong if the key evidence survived; useful if the seal broke or Kessa escaped.

NPC Relationship Changes: Sel is grateful but shaken. Chime may need coaxing. Brindle or Kessa requires witness protection before speaking. Mira claims the party mishandled commercial property.

Tower Access Progress: Registration is not blocked after the hearing, but the Forecourt terminal may show "Review Recently Cleared," drawing faction attention.

Item Rewards: One witness bell or sealed evidence case, not both. Nomi sells healing snacks at full price.

Milestone Guidance: Hold level 2 until the Contract Hall hearing resolves or until the party completes a corrective act, such as protecting a witness.

### Debt Activated

The party accidentally validates the false debt by accepting handling terms and letting Sel acknowledge the parcel before a witness.

Immediate Debt Amount: Sel receives a 900 NC Starter Debt. Validating PCs receive Collateral Review Pending, reserving up to 20 percent of their first Tower reward until legal review.

Legal Status: Sel is Starter Debt Active unless the party paused enforcement. PCs are Delivery Validators if they accepted handling responsibility. If they objected before the third bell, PCs are Delivery Witnesses instead.

Faction Reaction: Wardens urge immediate review. Ledger Court opens a dispute file. Pixel Prosperity hardliners push settlement. Aria warns the crowd not to confuse activation with justice.

How It Can Be Paused: Clear objection plus preserved seal; DC 14 Persuasion, Investigation, or Arcana; or direct support from Marik, Yorn, or Ira.

How It Can Be Challenged: Prove stolen registry access, hidden material terms, false services, paid witnesses, or coercive confusion. Registry shard plus hidden clause is enough to challenge cleanly.

How It Affects Session 4: The hearing opens under urgency. Vane's side offers to clear party collateral if they abandon Sel's claim. Ira warns them not to settle on the steps.

How It Affects Tower Access: Legal Tower registration is flagged until the hearing pauses or clears collateral. Illegal entry attempts create Warden response and faction gossip.

Reward Adjustment: No NC payout until review. If the party later clears the debt, award 150 NC per PC as delayed compensation and legal restitution.

### Lost Chase

Kessa escapes before the party reaches 5 chase successes.

Evidence Remaining: One partial item remains: shard sliver, ledger scrap, CodeX echo, Mira token imprint, or Kessa's shouted confession. Also keep any evidence gathered before the chase.

Evidence Lost: Full registry shard and Kessa's willing statement are unavailable at the start of the hearing.

How to Recover the Thread: CodeX can locate Kessa for a favor; Nyx can hide her and request a meeting; Marik can issue a limited witness notice; Aria can make Kessa's safest option public.

Who Lies About What Happened: Mira claims Kessa fled because the party threatened her. Pell claims the party invented the shard after losing it. Vane claims First Step is being framed by illegal Codebreaker data.

How the Next Session Changes: The hearing begins with a motion over incomplete evidence. The party needs Brindle, Chime, or Felix to speak clearly before Orvan allows deeper review.

Reward Adjustment: 75 NC per PC now; the remaining 75 NC becomes restitution if they recover Kessa or secure equivalent proof.

### Courier Dead

Kessa dies during the chase or confrontation.

Legal Consequences: Add Criminal Heat 2 if the death resulted from party attacks after Kessa tried to surrender. Add Criminal Heat 1 if the death was accidental during hazardous pursuit. Wardens require statements before the party leaves the district.

Moral Consequences: Aazoth's next flicker is cold and distant. Sel asks whether clearing his debt was worth a life. CodeX becomes harder to trust.

Faction Reactions: Wardens scrutinize force. Ledger Court questions witness loss. Remnant Veil may try to use Kessa as proof that law routes kill vulnerable people. Pixel hardliners frame the party as violent debt-dodgers.

Evidence Consequences: The shard can remain decisive if recovered intact, but the living explanation of how it was stolen is gone. Any claim about Kessa's intent becomes contested.

Replacement Clue Route: Use CodeX echo recording, Mira's ledger token, and Chime's manifest mismatch. Brindle becomes more important. If Kessa dropped the shard, its metadata can still name K.Coil and Mira's payment route.

Criminal Heat: Yes, unless the party clearly tried to save Kessa and witnesses confirm it. Heat affects Warden and Court DCs by +2 until addressed.

Reward Adjustment: No public support reward. Legal restitution waits until the Court separates debt evidence from the death inquiry.

### Party Goes Straight to the Tower

The party leaves the debt trail and heads for the Tower Forecourt before resolving the parcel.

How to Allow It: Let them reach the Forecourt, see the Tower, and interact with the registration terminal. Do not block the scene before they feel the choice.

What They Lack: Clean team identity, Tower registration clearance, evidence packet, and any sponsor or extraction guidance.

What Danger Increases: The terminal flags their temporary team ID. If debt activated, Collateral Review Pending appears. If debt did not activate, a warning reads: "Unresolved registry ping attached to team record."

How the False Debt Follows Them: Vane's system attempts to reserve Tower rewards or block registration. A Forecourt clerk tells them the issue must be reviewed before legal entry. If they try illegal entry, Warden response creates Criminal Heat and a public rumor that they are debt-flagged climbers.

How to Reconnect to Act I: Put Ira's witness bell, GUIDY's warning, or Marik's escort at the Forecourt terminal. The party can return to Contract Hall with a stronger personal reason: the scam now blocks the thing they wanted.

Reward Adjustment: No NC reward yet. If they return and clear the record, award the normal package plus a Forecourt clerk note that helps with later registration.

## Choose the Next Session Opener

Use this table to open the next session at the Contract Hall without losing momentum. It maps the Session 3 outcome to the first image, speaker, pressure, choice, evidence status, and faction complication.

## Opening Adventure Failure Recovery

If the party ignores GUIDY: GUIDY follows at a distance and prints increasingly worried warning slips. Put the registry clue in Chime's parcel notice or Aria's song. GUIDY becomes hurt but not useless.

If the party attacks someone in a safe zone: Blue light stops the attack before serious harm. The offender is restrained for 1 minute, receives a public warning, and must succeed on a DC 13 Charisma saving throw or suffer disadvantage on their next social check in that scene from embarrassment and system pressure. Marik intervenes. The adventure continues with public trust reduced.

If the party delivers the parcel blindly: Run Session 2 Scene 3. Sel's false debt activates and the party may become validators. This creates urgency, price pressure, and legal stakes, not a dead end.

If the false debt activates: Give the party 24 hours before full enforcement. They need evidence from Pixel Promenade and Code Caverns to pause or overturn it. Sel may suffer stress, public shame, and temporary restrictions, but he should not lose a life from paperwork in this opening unless the party deliberately abandons him to violent enforcement later.

If the party fails to find clues: Move the next clue into the next scene. Aria sings the warning. Felix finds the counterfeit token. Kessa shouts the confession. Ira's witness bell asks for the parcel. Missing a clue should cost time, reputation, or leverage, not halt the adventure.

If the party loses the chase: Kessa escapes, but drops a shard sliver, ledger scrap, or route glyph. The next hearing starts harder, and Kessa may be pressured by Vane before she can testify. The party can recover by protecting another witness or accepting CodeX's risky help.

If the party kills the courier: If Kessa dies outside a safe zone, the party loses a living witness and may trigger a life-loss investigation. The registry shard remains, but Marik and Ira treat the party with caution. CodeX becomes colder. Kessa's death should matter, especially if she was trying to surrender. If the death was clearly accidental during hazards, focus on chain of custody and grief rather than punishment.

If the party refuses faction help: Keep the evidence path independent. GUIDY, public records, physical clues, and Sel's testimony can carry the case. Factions react to being refused, but none should be required for success.

If a PC dies in Act I: Mark one life lost. Return the PC at Portal Plaza or the nearest safe recovery point after the scene resolves. Give them a scar tied to the cause: debt mark, glitch stutter, blue-light burn, witness echo, or fountain chill. Let the death create a clue or consequence. For example, a PC killed by a Debt Shade hears the phrase "First Step is not the first name" before returning.

If the party wants to go straight to the Tower: Let them reach the Tower Forecourt road, then have the terminal flag their temporary team ID and any pending collateral review. GUIDY and a Forecourt clerk explain that legal registration requires clean identity records. This routes them to the false debt evidence without denying their goal. If they insist on illegal entry, safe-zone and Forecourt enforcement block the attempt and create Warden heat.

## Contract Hall Evidence Packet

This packet exists so the next chunk can begin at the Contract Hall without reconstructing Sessions 1-3. At the end of Session 3, sort the party's proof into one of the following states.

### Likely Evidence After a Clean Win

- Preserved parcel seal with hidden microtext exposed.
- GUIDY registry slip showing outside access.
- Kessa registry shard or sealed metadata copy.
- Kessa's willing statement.
- Felix delivery log and counterfeit stock analysis.
- Brindle statement or Yorn witness-light memory.
- Sel's recipient notice and testimony.

Starting Legal Position: Strong. The Court can immediately consider whether consent was defective and whether First Step used stolen registry data.

### Likely Evidence After a Messy Win

- Parcel seal, possibly damaged.
- One of: registry shard, shard sliver, or CodeX echo.
- Felix log or Chime manifest mismatch.
- One frightened witness: Sel, Brindle, Chime, or Kessa.
- Public rumor record, possibly unfavorable.

Starting Legal Position: Useful but contested. The Court first asks whether the party preserved evidence cleanly and whether any witness was coerced.

### Likely Evidence After a Lost Chase

- Pre-chase evidence from Portal Plaza, tavern, and Felix.
- Partial shard sliver, ledger scrap, Mira token imprint, or CodeX echo.
- No willing Kessa statement at the opening of the hearing.

Starting Legal Position: Incomplete. The Court can pause enforcement but may not void the debt without witness testimony or stronger metadata.

### Likely Evidence After Debt Activated

- Activation record showing Sel's 900 NC debt.
- Party validator or witness status record.
- Parcel seal if preserved.
- Sel's testimony about confusion.
- Any registry or routing evidence recovered afterward.

Starting Legal Position: Urgent. The first legal question is whether enforcement pauses before settlement pressure lands on Sel.

### Likely Witnesses

Sel Varrin can testify that he did not order services and did not understand the parcel. Chime can testify about manifest mismatch and handling language. Aria can testify about prior pattern and public timing. Brindle can testify about paid tavern witnesses if protected. Felix can testify about counterfeit stock and rush routing. Kessa can testify about registry theft if alive and protected. Yorn can testify about tavern witness-light memory.

### Hostile Witnesses

Mira Vale claims the party mishandled commercial property. Pell Tick claims public doubt came from normal market confidence. A Guild hardliner clerk claims Felix's office processed the parcel, so Vane is irrelevant. A settlement broker claims Sel accepted aid and regrets the cost only after outside coaching.

### Missing Evidence

If the parcel seal was destroyed, the hidden clause must be proven through Chime, Sel, or activation record. If the shard is missing, stolen registry access must be proven through GUIDY, Felix logs, CodeX echo, or Kessa. If witnesses fled, the Court may grant a pause but require witness protection or a second evidence filing.

### Forged Evidence Risk

Vane's side may introduce a cleaned manifest showing ordinary orientation services, a forged receipt bearing Sel's mark, a rumor-board capture making the party look indebted before the parcel, or a statement from Brindle recanting under pressure. The DM should mark forged evidence with one tell: wrong timestamp, wrong seal weight, missing witness chime, or language too polished for the named signer.

### What the Ledger Court Will Ask First

1. Who currently holds the parcel seal, shard, and logs?
2. Was the recipient informed of the debt before acknowledgement?
3. Did handling members accept validator status knowingly?
4. Was registry data accessed lawfully?
5. Is immediate enforcement likely to cause irreparable harm?

### What Merrit Vane Will Try to Suppress

Vane wants to suppress the K.Coil registry path, the hidden microtext, Mira's private ledger token, proof that First Step is his shell office, and any witness statement showing fear or confusion before acceptance. If he cannot suppress an item, he reframes it as negligence by Felix, theft by Kessa, or hysteria by new arrivals.

### How Each Faction Wants to Spin the Hearing

Guardian Wardens: "This proves registry protection must tighten, but lawful review works."

Pixel Prosperity Guild: Felix's circle says, "Expose the hardliners and preserve honest trade." Vane's circle says, "A few reckless newcomers misunderstood normal finance."

Spire Seekers: "This is why climbers need stronger teams before accepting sponsorship."

Codebreakers: "The registry is vulnerable because the system is locked away from public audit."

Remnant Veil: "The law creates cages and then blames people for panicking inside them."

Ledger Court: "This case can clarify that witnessed form without meaningful consent is defective."

## First Chunk Handoff Summary

Canon Established: The Central Nexus is a fantasy-cyber refuge governed by the Charter. PCs begin with three lives, 500 NC, and public life counters. Safe zones stop direct violence but not social or legal harm. Witnessed deals can bind, but valid consent matters. Aazoth is a mercy presence tied to arrival and personhood. GUIDY is a caring but limited guidance bot. The Tower of Ascension has one hundred floors and Floor 100 can change Nexus law. The opening false debt scam targets new arrivals through stolen registry data and hidden clauses.

NPCs Introduced: GUIDY, Aazoth's flicker, Marik Bluecoat, Warden Lio Brass, Sel Varrin, Tamsin Halewire, Vela Mourn, Sera Cupwise, Bram Lilt, Chime, Aria Neon, Yorn Glass, Brindle Pact, Mira Vale, Felix Pixelcoin, Nomi Sweetspark, Pell Tick, Kessa Coil, CodeX, Ira Quill by message, Merrit Vane by evidence.

Factions Introduced: Guardian Wardens, Pixel Prosperity Guild, Ledger Court, Codebreakers, Remnant Veil, Salvage Union, Spire Seekers, Nexus Scholars, Covenant of the Last Light.

Clues Created: Registry ping from K.Coil, First Step Brokerage redaction, contract bell anomaly, clear-terms receipt, silver-toothed parcel, hidden collateral microtext, Brindle's First Step token, Mira's ledger case, counterfeit guild stock, Kessa's last scan at Code Cavern Stairs, registry shard, Kessa's statement, CodeX route glyph, Merrit Vane's name.

Unresolved Hooks: Contract Hall hearing; clearing Sel's false debt; identifying and confronting Merrit Vane; deciding evidence custody; repairing or exploiting Felix's reputation; protecting Brindle and Kessa; determining how First Step accessed registry vulnerabilities; resolving any party collateral review; deciding whether CodeX receives shard data.

Mechanics Introduced: Three lives, life counters, safe zones, witnessed deals, Nexus Credits, reputation shifts, failure-forward investigation, public rumor pressure, chase skill challenge, evidence custody, contact rewards, and early faction reactions.

Expected Next Chunk: The next chunk should begin with the Contract Hall Exterior and run the Contract Hall hearing as a full legal-social adventure. It should include Ira Quill, Magistrate Orvan Hex, Clause Bailiff pressure, Merrit Vane's legal representative, evidence presentation, witness protection, false settlement offers, debt relief outcomes, level 2 guidance, and a transition to Tower Forecourt registration.

Tone Notes: Keep the mix of neon wonder, civic absurdity, real danger, and moral pressure. Let humor come from character and bureaucracy, not from undercutting stakes. Make legal scenes feel playable and tense rather than like homework.

Balance Notes: Sessions 1-3 are written for 4 1st-level PCs. Combat is light because safe zones and investigation dominate. The Code Cavern chase can deal chip damage and include glitch wisps, but it should not become a lethal slugfest unless the party chooses violence in an unsafe place. For 3 PCs, reduce chase length and enemies. For 5-6 PCs, add simultaneous objectives, not only more hit points.

<!-- CHUNK 02 START -->

# CHUNK 02: Contract, Judgment, Portal Access, and the Door That Says Return

## Chunk 02 Overview

Level Range: Characters may begin this chunk at level 1 or level 2. The Contract Hall hearing is safe for level 1 characters because its pressure is legal, social, and procedural. The default recommendation is to award level 2 after the Contract Hall ruling, before portal-world selection and any Tower Forecourt registration scenes. Level 2 is not remotely sufficient for a serious Executioner attempt.

Expected Sessions: 2 sessions of 3-4 hours each. Session 4 covers the Contract Hall hearing. Session 5 covers post-hearing fallout, downtime, Tower Forecourt registration, portal access, and the Executioner terminal warning.

Primary Locations: Contract Hall in Ledger Court; a short post-hearing downtime location of the party's choosing; Tower Forecourt.

Major NPCs: Ira Quill, Magistrate Orvan Hex, Clause Bailiff Twelve-Bells, Merrit Vane, Advocate Seraphex Glass, Sel Varrin, Kessa Coil, Chime, Aria Neon, Felix Pixelcoin, Marik Bluecoat, Brindle Pact, Mira Vale, CodeX or Nyx Understep, Mina Redline, Elektra Sparkblade, GUIDY.

Major Factions: Ledger Court, Guardian Wardens, Pixel Prosperity Guild, Codebreakers, Remnant Veil, Spire Seekers, Salvage Union, Covenant of the Last Light.

Main Question: Can the party turn messy first-day evidence into a legal ruling without letting law become another weapon against frightened witnesses?

Required Outcomes:

- Resolve the false debt's immediate legal status.
- Establish whether Sel is free, paused, indebted, or under settlement pressure.
- Determine whether the party is clean, protected, reckless, debt-flagged, heat-flagged, or still under review.
- Introduce Orvan Hex, Ira Quill, Clause Bailiff Twelve-Bells, and Merrit Vane's opposition.
- Award or confirm level 2 before portal-world play or any long-term Tower preparation.
- Register, delay, or block legal Spire access while making clear that the first true floor is an extreme threat.
- Present the Executioner Protocol warning.
- End with the party choosing preparation, portal-world entry, retreat from the Spire terminal, or a clearly warned ACKNOWLEDGE RISK decision.

Possible Outcomes: Full debt void, debt paused, party named protected witnesses, party named reckless validators, settlement accepted, appeal required, Vane publicly exposed but not stopped, Vane's representative creates new evidence, clean registration, sponsored registration, probationary registration, debt-flagged registration, heat-flagged registration, Codebreaker backdoor registration, temporary denial, portal-world redirection, or illegal-entry fallout.

Milestone and Leveling Guidance: Award level 2 immediately after the Contract Hall ruling if the party meaningfully participated in the hearing, protected at least one witness, presented evidence, or accepted consequences from a messy case. If the party already reached level 2 at the end of Chunk 01, use the level-up scene as a stabilization surge: each PC gains inspiration, clears one minor exhaustion or stress mark, and receives one faction message.

Where Chunk 02 Begins: On the steps of Contract Hall, with public pressure already moving. A settlement broker approaches before the party reaches evidence intake.

Where Chunk 02 Ends: At the Spire terminal and portal access decision point, after registration, final consent prompts, the Executioner warning, and the Tower's first response to the party's debt, heat, and sponsorship status. Do not run The Executioner in this chunk. The intended early-campaign exit is toward portal worlds, allies, gear, followers, and preparation.

## Continuity From Chunk 01

Use this table before Session 4. Pick the row that most closely matches the party's ending state. If multiple rows apply, use the worst legal complication and the strongest evidence status.

## If You Are Running Tonight, Read This First

### 10-Minute Prep

Read the Chunk 02 Overview, Continuity table, Session 4 Run Sheet, Contract Hall Mechanics, and Possible Rulings. Pick the party's starting row from the Continuity table. Start on the Contract Hall steps with the settlement broker.

### 30-Minute Prep

Read the Contract Hall Location Chapter, NPC quick cards for Ira, Orvan, Twelve-Bells, Seraphex, Sel, Kessa, Chime, Felix, and Marik, plus the Evidence and Clue Matrix. Mark three evidence items the party definitely has and two witnesses likely to speak.

### 60-Minute Prep

Read all of "The Bell That Rings Back," the Contract Hall Encounters, Clause Bailiff Pressure Scene, Post-Hearing Downtime Beat, Session 5 Run Sheet, Tower Registration Procedure, Sponsor and Faction Offers, Executioner Protocol Warning, and Tower Access Outcome Packages. Pick likely sponsor offers based on the hearing outcome.

### Sections to Bookmark

Bookmark Continuity From Chunk 01, Session 4 Run Sheet, Hearing Tracks, Player Actions During Hearing, Opposition Actions, Evidence and Clue Matrix, Possible Rulings, Session 5 Run Sheet, Tower Registration Procedure, Sponsor and Faction Offers, Tower Forecourt Shopping and Services, Executioner Protocol Warning, and Final Threshold Scene.

### Handouts to Copy

Copy the hearing track sheet, evidence matrix rows for evidence the party has, Player Handout: Executioner Protocol Warning, Tower Registration Procedure prompts, sponsor offer table, and shopping/services table.

### NPC Voices That Matter Most

Ira Quill is soft, precise, and fierce when consent is abused. Orvan Hex is formal, exact, and tired of sloppy cruelty. Twelve-Bells speaks in numbered warnings. Seraphex Glass is elegant and poisonous. Merrit Vane is paternal, calm, and never surprised in public. Sel sounds smaller near legal words. Kessa sounds defensive until someone protects her. Felix performs charm to cover shame. Marik keeps sentences short because lives are at stake.

### What Not To Worry About Yet

Do not prepare The Executioner encounter, later Spire maps, deep faction clocks, or the final meaning of Ascension. This chunk only needs the hearing, registration, warning, gear, offers, portal access choices, and the Threshold Door that can be refused.

### What To Ask Players Before Starting

Ask each player: "Which evidence item are you personally carrying, and who did your character most want to protect after the chase?" If the previous session ended chaotically, also ask: "Did your character sleep, argue, hide, or keep watch before coming to Court?" Their answers set witness confidence and public legitimacy.

## Session 4 Run Sheet: The Contract Hall Hearing

### What This Session Must Accomplish

- Start with pressure before the party reaches the hearing chamber.
- Establish the four hearing tracks.
- Let the party present evidence through at least two routes.
- Put at least one witness under pressure.
- Show Merrit Vane's opposition directly or through Seraphex Glass.
- Use Clause Bailiff Twelve-Bells as a legal hazard.
- End with a ruling that changes debt, reputation, witness status, and Tower access.
- Award or confirm level 2 after the ruling.

### What the DM Tracks

| Track | Start | What Raises It | What Lowers It | Why It Matters |
|---|---:|---|---|---|
| Evidence Strength | By outcome | Clean evidence, corroboration, metadata | broken seal, missing chain, forged claims | Determines how strong the ruling can be |
| Witness Safety | By outcome | protection, calm, recess, Ira support | intimidation, public exposure, threats | Determines whether witnesses speak fully |
| Public Legitimacy | By outcome | clear statements, Aria, Marik, transparency | rumor, violence, confusion, settlement tricks | Determines whether the ruling changes reputation |
| Legal Pressure | By outcome | objections, settlement offers, bailiff warnings | party overreach, missed response, bad conduct | High pressure narrows options and adds costs |

### Hearing Pressure Clock

Start at 0. At 3, Orvan demands concise proof. At 5, Twelve-Bells intervenes. At 6, the hearing forces an immediate ruling from the current track state. Increase by 1 when the party rambles, repeats unsupported claims, attacks character without proof, or ignores an opposition action.

### Witness Safety Clock

Start at 3 unless the continuity row says witnesses are already endangered. At 0, one witness recants, flees, or can only speak through Ira. At 5, a witness gives a brave extra truth. Increase through protection and calm. Decrease through intimidation, exposure, and public blame.

### Faction Interference Clock

Start at 1. At 3, one faction makes an overt offer or threat. At 5, two factions begin arguing in public and Public Legitimacy drops by 1 unless the party restores order. Increase when evidence affects faction power.

### Evidence Integrity Clock

Start at 3. At 0, the strongest evidence item is challenged as damaged or unreliable. At 5, the Court seals evidence cleanly and Vane loses one chain-of-custody challenge. Increase with careful intake and labels. Decrease when evidence is passed around, damaged, magically altered, or privately copied without disclosure.

### Scene Order If Moving Fast

Run Settlement Broker on the Steps, Evidence Intake Challenge, Opening Statements, one combined Witness Examination, Opposition Overreach, Clause Bailiff Intervention only if triggered, and Final Ruling. Use three hearing rounds.

### Scene Order If Roleplaying Heavily

Run the steps, docket board, evidence intake, witness waiting gallery, hearing chamber entrance, opening statements, two or three witness examinations, one recess or faction interference beat, opposition overreach, Clause Bailiff pressure, and final ruling. Use five hearing rounds.

### Do-Not-Forget List

- Offer settlement before the party gets comfortable.
- Ask who is holding each evidence item.
- Make Sel or another witness visibly scared.
- Let Ira help without solving the case.
- Let Seraphex challenge the party's weakest link.
- Use at least one faction reaction in public.
- Track Legal Pressure visibly.
- State the ruling in clear mechanical terms.

## Adventure: The Bell That Rings Back

The Bell That Rings Back is a legal-social adventure for the aftermath of "First Login, First Debt." It can be run at level 1 or level 2. It resolves immediate false-debt pressure, creates the party's first public legal identity, and opens lawful access to the Tower Forecourt.

### Adventure Overview

Level: 1-2.

Expected Session Count: 1 session for the hearing, plus part of Session 5 for fallout if the table roleplays heavily.

Primary Location: Contract Hall in Ledger Court.

Main NPCs: Ira Quill, Magistrate Orvan Hex, Clause Bailiff Twelve-Bells, Advocate Seraphex Glass, Merrit Vane, Sel Varrin, Kessa Coil, Chime, Aria Neon, Felix Pixelcoin, Marik Bluecoat, Brindle Pact, Mira Vale, CodeX or Nyx.

Opposition: Merrit Vane's legal strategy, represented by Advocate Seraphex Glass; Guild hardliners; procedural doubt; witness fear; Clause Bailiff enforcement.

Central Conflict: The party must prove that the false debt relied on defective consent, altered or misleading records, or harmful enforcement before the law turns a scam into a valid obligation.

Stakes: Sel's 900 NC debt, party validator status, public trust, witness safety, Felix's Guild standing, Kessa's protection, and whether First Step can keep targeting new arrivals.

Rewards: Debt void or pause, 100-250 NC restitution by outcome, level 2, protected witness status or clean identity note, faction reputation changes, portal/Spire registration clarity, and a legal precedent that can echo in portal worlds and later Spire floors.

Failure States: Debt remains active, appeal required, party named reckless validators, settlement accepted under pressure, evidence sealed for review, Kessa or Brindle recants, Vane escapes cleanly, or Tower registration becomes probationary or debt-flagged. None of these end the campaign.

### Background

Merrit Vane created First Step Brokerage as a buffer between his Guild standing and predatory new-arrival debt experiments. First Step sells "orientation aid" that looks like practical help but is structured to convert confusion into obligation. The hidden clause was supposed to bind Sel as primary debtor and turn the party into delivery validators. Once validators existed, Vane could use their fresh arrival records to make the contract appear witnessed by neutral newcomers.

The evidence threatens Vane because it does more than clear one debt. If the Court rules that hidden material terms and stolen registry access defeat witnessed consent, many older First Step contracts become vulnerable to review. Vane's wealth and Guild leverage depend on those contracts staying boring.

Orvan Hex cares because he believes precision is mercy when imprecision is a trap. He has upheld harsh contracts before, and he knows the Ledger Court profits from residents believing legal form is enough. This case lets him clarify that a witness bell does not sanctify a lie.

Ira Quill cares because they have seen frightened people sign away choices and then get blamed for reading too slowly. Ira wants the Court to say aloud that shaking hands do not make clean consent. They also want witnesses protected from settlement pressure before testimony.

The Ledger Court is politically trapped. If it voids the debt too broadly, the Pixel Prosperity Guild accuses it of undermining commerce. If it enforces the debt, Wardens and Last Light critics accuse it of blessing predation. If it targets Vane without clean evidence, Guild hardliners call it faction theater. If it ignores stolen registry access, Codebreakers leak the vulnerability and cause panic.

The Pixel Prosperity Guild cannot openly defend Vane without risk because Felix's logs, counterfeit stock, and hardliner signs make the Guild look split. Public defense of Vane could turn ordinary shoppers against Guild credit. Quiet defense, settlement pressure, and blame-shifting are safer.

The Wardens cannot simply arrest everyone because the Charter treats witnessed deals as legal events, not street crimes, until fraud is proven. Marik needs a ruling, sealed evidence, or confession before he can make arrests that survive appeal. If he moves too early, Vane casts the Wardens as anti-commerce enforcers abusing frightened newcomers.

### Strong Start

Begin on the Contract Hall steps before the party enters.

Read-Aloud:

> The Contract Hall does not look built. It looks argued into existence: black-blue stone, silver script, witness bells under the eaves, and a stairway polished by generations of anxious feet. Above the public doors, a docket board writes and rewrites names in light.
>
> Sel stands halfway up the steps, staring at a debt mark that pulses on his wrist or at the blank place where it almost appeared. A settlement broker in pearl-gray robes reaches him first, holding out a document already folded to the signature line.
>
> One witness bell rings. Then it rings again, backward.
>
> A soft voice cuts through the crowd. "Do not sign anything on the steps." Ira Quill pushes through with ink-black fingertips and eyes fixed on the paper. "Not one word, not one nod, not one polite little yes."
>
> At the top of the stairs, an elegant advocate smiles as if the case has already ended. "Advocate Seraphex Glass, appearing for First Step Brokerage. We are prepared to resolve this misunderstanding with compassion."

DM Truth: The settlement offer is designed to clear party collateral while leaving Sel bound to a smaller but still false debt and preventing evidence review. The backward bell means the Court detected a deal attempting to happen under contested consent. Seraphex wants the party to react angrily in public.

NPCs Present: Ira Quill, Sel Varrin, Advocate Seraphex Glass, a settlement broker named Caldrin Voss, Clause Bailiff Twelve-Bells at the doors, two Ledger clerks, public watchers, possible Marik or Felix depending on continuity.

Player Options: Stop Sel from signing, read the settlement, challenge Seraphex, call Ira, ask for protected intake, present evidence immediately, stay silent and observe, or confront the broker.

Checks/DCs:

- DC 12 Wisdom (Insight) to see Sel is being rushed.
- DC 13 Intelligence (Investigation) to identify the settlement as a waiver of evidence review.
- DC 14 Charisma (Persuasion) to calm Sel without sounding controlling.
- DC 15 Charisma (Intimidation) to make the broker step back; success adds Legal Pressure +1 because threats on Court steps matter.
- DC 15 Intelligence with calligrapher's supplies or Legal Cant to spot the phrase "without admission of defect."
- DC 16 Charisma (Persuasion) to turn the public moment against Seraphex without triggering a bailiff warning.

Success: Sel does not sign. Witness Safety +1, Public Legitimacy +1, and Ira brings the party to evidence intake.

Partial Success: Sel does not sign, but Seraphex frames the party as emotional. Witness Safety holds, Legal Pressure +1.

Failure: Sel signs a preliminary settlement or nearly signs before Ira stops him. Evidence Strength is not reduced, but Legal Pressure +1 and Sel's testimony starts at disadvantage until reassured.

Clues: Settlement tries to waive review; backward bell signals contested consent; Seraphex wants public overreaction.

Consequences: The party enters the Hall with a visible legal posture: careful protectors, messy but sincere advocates, or volatile newcomers.

Faction Reactions: Wardens approve calm intervention. Guild hardliners approve settlement pressure. Ledger Court watches whether the party respects procedure. Aria can turn a clean refusal into public support.

How the Scene Changes by Chunk 01 Outcome: If Clean Win, the settlement is insulting and weak. If Debt Activated, it is tempting because it offers immediate relief. If Courier Dead, it includes a clause about "violent recovery conduct." If Party Sides With CodeX, it demands the destruction of illegal data. If Party Sides With Felix, it tries to make Felix pay part of the settlement.

## Contract Hall Location Chapter

The Contract Hall is a safe legal zone, not a combat dungeon. It restrains violence, records speech, and turns procedural choices into consequences. The areas below can be used during the hearing or during recess.

### Area C1. Ledger Court Steps

Read-Aloud: Wide black-blue steps climb toward doors carved with witness bells. Every spoken promise seems to echo one breath longer than it should.

DM Details: Public pressure lives here. Deals offered on the steps are legal but viewed with suspicion by reform-minded clerks.

Exits: Down to Ledger Court plaza; up to Public Docket Board and evidence intake doors; side path to settlement alcoves.

NPCs Present: Settlement broker Caldrin Voss, Ira Quill, Sel, public watchers, Seraphex Glass, possibly Marik or Aria.

Interactive Objects: Witness bells, public rail, settlement document, docket glow reflected on the steps.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Insight reads rushed consent; DC 13 Investigation reads settlement waiver; DC 14 Persuasion steadies a witness; DC 15 Performance addresses the crowd cleanly.

Clues: The backward bell means the Court detects contested consent; the settlement waives evidence review.

Complications: A hostile observer shouts that the party is dodging debt; Seraphex tries to get a PC to threaten the broker.

Faction Appearances: Wardens monitor crowd order; Guild observers count public sympathy; Aria may arrive to control rumor.

Violence or Threats: Direct violence freezes under Court-blue light. Threats trigger Twelve-Bells warning from the doorway.

After the Ruling: If the party wins, reformers gather on the steps. If they lose or settle, brokers become bolder here until challenged later.

### Area C2. Public Docket Board

Read-Aloud: A wall of light lists hearings, sealed reviews, and names that rearrange whenever a bell rings. Some names are clear. Some are blurred by privacy seals.

DM Details: The docket board shows what the Court admits publicly. It can reveal prior First Step review without exposing sealed details.

Exits: Steps, Evidence Intake Alcove, Witness Waiting Gallery.

NPCs Present: Ledger clerks, public witnesses, Pell Tick if still active, a hostile Guild observer.

Interactive Objects: Docket light, privacy seals, public comment slot, queue tokens.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Investigation finds the current case; DC 14 Legal Cant or History identifies sealed preliminary reviews; DC 15 Arcana reads whether a seal was recently altered; DC 16 Persuasion gets a clerk to confirm procedure.

Clues: First Step appears under sealed preliminary review; the party's case can be merged with prior complaints.

Complications: Pell or a Guild observer tries to post a public comment framing the party as violent; privacy seals blur key names.

Faction Appearances: Ledger Court clerks defend procedure; Codebreakers notice redaction patterns; Wardens dislike tampering.

Violence or Threats: Threats near the board create Public Legitimacy -1 because the board records public conduct.

After the Ruling: The ruling summary appears here. A strong ruling becomes public precedent; a weak ruling appears as "review pending."

### Area C3. Evidence Intake Alcove

Read-Aloud: A narrow alcove of blue glass contains scales, seal clamps, copying lamps, and a clerk who looks personally offended by fingerprints.

DM Details: Evidence intake determines Evidence Integrity. This is where mishandled evidence can recover or become vulnerable.

Exits: Docket Board, Clerk's Rail, Emergency Witness Room.

NPCs Present: Intake Clerk Vennel Sharp, Ira Quill, Chime if present, Marik if holding custody.

Interactive Objects: Seal clamp, copying lamp, chain-of-custody ribbon, evidence scale, witness stamp.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Investigation labels evidence clearly; DC 13 calligrapher's supplies copies text without smearing; DC 14 Arcana seals magical residue; DC 15 Persuasion gets intake priority; DC 16 thieves' tools detects tamper marks without worsening them.

Clues: Seal weight mismatch, witness gem residue, shard metadata stability.

Complications: Damaged parcel evidence triggers a clerk challenge; CodeX data requires redaction before admission.

Faction Appearances: Wardens support chain of custody; Codebreakers object to full disclosure; Guild observers try to call evidence "commercial property."

Violence or Threats: Evidence alcove shutters close and Twelve-Bells marks the offender with a silence warning.

After the Ruling: Admitted evidence is sealed in Court custody or released to protected witnesses by ruling.

### Area C4. Witness Waiting Gallery

Read-Aloud: Benches line a long gallery where voices drop by instinct. Blue curtains divide witnesses who do not want to look at each other.

DM Details: Witness safety is tested here. It is a safe zone, but social pressure, fear, settlement offers, and shame still work.

Exits: Evidence Intake, Hearing Chamber, Emergency Witness Room, settlement alcoves.

NPCs Present: Sel, Kessa, Brindle, Chime, Aria, Felix, Marik, nervous public witness, hostile Guild observer.

Interactive Objects: privacy curtains, water basin, witness bell pulls, testimony tokens, comfort lamps.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Persuasion calms Sel; DC 13 Insight spots intimidation; DC 14 Perception catches a whispered threat; DC 15 Intimidation drives off a pressure agent but adds Legal Pressure +1; DC 15 Medicine or Religion helps a panic response.

Clues: Witnesses reveal who pressured them; Brindle may name Mira; Kessa may mention extra copied names.

Complications: Brindle recants, Kessa tries to flee, Sel considers settlement, Chime enters recitation mode.

Faction Appearances: Ira protects witnesses; Remnant Veil offers hiding; Wardens offer custody; Guild observers offer settlements.
