Violence or Threats: Threats lower Witness Safety. Actual attacks trigger immediate bailiff intervention.

After the Ruling: Protected witnesses receive tokens; unsupported witnesses may vanish into faction hands.

### Area C5. Blue-Seal Hearing Chamber

Read-Aloud: The hearing chamber is circular, with a blue seal set into the floor and rows of benches rising like quiet waves. Above the magistrate's chair, a witness bell hangs upside down.

DM Details: This is the main social combat arena. The blue seal records claims, objections, and witness fear.

Exits: Witness Gallery, Clerk's Rail, Clause Bailiff Post, Restricted Record Lift.

NPCs Present: Orvan Hex, Twelve-Bells, Ira, Seraphex, party, witnesses, public observers, faction representatives.

Interactive Objects: blue floor seal, witness bell, evidence plinth, speaker's rail, public gallery lamps.

Checks/DCs: Use Hearing Round Structure. Standard DC 13 for clear points, DC 15 for contested claims, DC 17 for decisive contradictions, DC 19 for hostile witness reversals.

Clues: Bell direction, seal color, and Orvan's questions reveal which route is strongest: Consent, Truth, or Mercy.

Complications: Seraphex challenges chain of custody; Twelve-Bells intervenes; faction observers attempt public spin.

Faction Appearances: All public factions can watch, but only recognized representatives speak without permission.

Violence or Threats: Violence fails instantly. A threat under the blue seal can create a legal mark and Legal Pressure +2.

After the Ruling: The seal displays the ruling category and updates Tower access flags.

### Area C6. Clerk's Rail

Read-Aloud: A crescent of desks surrounds the chamber, each stacked with forms, bells, and tiny lamps that change color when someone uses an imprecise word.

DM Details: Clerks manage records and can become allies if treated well. They hate dramatic imprecision.

Exits: Evidence Intake, Hearing Chamber, Restricted Record Lift.

NPCs Present: Clerk Vennel Sharp, junior clerks, Ira, hostile Guild observer if seeking paperwork.

Interactive Objects: terminology lamps, queue cords, copy stamps, objection cards, precedent drawers.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Persuasion asks for procedural clarity; DC 14 Investigation finds a relevant precedent; DC 15 Legal Cant cites consent review; DC 16 Deception gets corrected immediately and raises Legal Pressure +1.

Clues: Prior rulings distinguish "acknowledgement" from "informed consent."

Complications: Clerk backlog delays evidence; a Guild observer files a counterclaim.

Faction Appearances: Ledger Court shows its bureaucracy; Pixel Prosperity files commercial objections.

Violence or Threats: Clerks withdraw and the party loses access to quick precedent support.

After the Ruling: Helpful clerks can provide a legal access copy for Tower registration.

### Area C7. Clause Bailiff Post

Read-Aloud: A metal figure stands beside a rack of blue seals and silver cords. Twelve small bells hang from its shoulders. None of them move with the same rhythm.

DM Details: Twelve-Bells is not a guard to defeat. It is a legal enforcement hazard that restrains procedure violations.

Exits: Hearing Chamber, Evidence Intake, Emergency Witness Room.

NPCs Present: Clause Bailiff Twelve-Bells and one silent clerk.

Interactive Objects: warning cords, silence seals, restraint ribbons, infraction slate.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Insight reads the next warning; DC 14 Persuasion de-escalates; DC 15 Legal Cant reframes a heated claim; DC 16 Arcana identifies which seal will trigger.

Clues: Bailiff warnings reveal which conduct is legally dangerous.

Complications: A PC lies under witness, threatens a witness, or attempts to tamper with evidence.

Faction Appearances: Wardens respect the bailiff; Codebreakers dislike its automated authority; Ledger Court treats it as necessary.

Violence or Threats: Attacking Twelve-Bells triggers nonlethal restraint, silence, and hearing recess.

After the Ruling: The bailiff either removes marks or leaves probation seals active.

### Area C8. Settlement Alcoves

Read-Aloud: Small private booths line the side hall, each with a curtain, a contract lamp, and a bell pull polished by desperate hands.

DM Details: These alcoves are legal but dangerous. They tempt parties to trade broad justice for fast relief.

Exits: Ledger Court Steps, Witness Gallery, Evidence Intake.

NPCs Present: Caldrin Voss, Seraphex's assistant, Sel if pressured, Felix if offering private compensation.

Interactive Objects: contract lamp, privacy curtain, bell pull, settlement forms, coin scale.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Insight spots urgency tactics; DC 13 Investigation reads waiver terms; DC 15 Persuasion negotiates a safer pause; DC 16 Legal Cant identifies non-disparagement or evidence destruction clauses.

Clues: Settlement language tries to preserve First Step's method.

Complications: Sel is offered immediate relief; party is offered collateral release if they abandon Kessa or Brindle.

Faction Appearances: Guild hardliners use alcoves heavily; Ira tries to keep witnesses out of them.

Violence or Threats: Threats in an alcove become especially damaging because the privacy lamp records them.

After the Ruling: Alcoves either empty in shame after a public void or fill with new claimants after a narrow ruling.

### Area C9. Restricted Record Lift

Read-Aloud: A narrow lift of blue glass rises behind the clerk rail. Its doors are covered in names written too small to read until the lift decides you may.

DM Details: This lift reaches sealed prior complaints and record archives. The party might access it during recess if they earn permission.

Exits: Clerk's Rail, sealed archive above, maintenance landing below.

NPCs Present: Orvan's clerk, Ira, CodeX echo if illegal route is used.

Interactive Objects: lift seal, access chain, archive bell, redaction lens.

Checks/DCs: DC 14 Persuasion gets limited clerk access; DC 15 Investigation identifies linked complaints; DC 16 Arcana reads redaction magic; DC 17 thieves' tools or CodeX route opens illegal access but creates Legal Pressure +2 if exposed.

Clues: Prior First Step complaints match Sel's hidden clause structure.

Complications: Illegal access may help Truth Route while hurting Public Legitimacy.

Faction Appearances: Codebreakers offer access; Ledger Court demands procedure; Wardens warn against tampering.

Violence or Threats: Lift locks down and evidence review narrows.

After the Ruling: If Vane is exposed, the lift opens to investigators. If not, records remain sealed.

### Area C10. Emergency Witness Room

Read-Aloud: This small blue room has no benches, only soft wall panels, a water basin, and a witness bell wrapped in white thread.

DM Details: This room protects frightened witnesses and can save testimony from collapse.

Exits: Evidence Intake, Witness Gallery, Clause Bailiff Post.

NPCs Present: Ira, Sel, Kessa, Brindle, Chime, Marik if custody is requested.

Interactive Objects: white-thread bell, privacy seal, water basin, calming lamp, protected testimony crystal.

Checks/DCs: DC 12 Persuasion calms a witness; DC 13 Medicine or Religion handles panic; DC 14 Insight identifies what the witness fears; DC 15 Legal Cant records protected testimony; DC 16 Arcana seals testimony against tampering.

Clues: Protected witnesses may reveal hidden pressure, such as Mira's threats or Vane's settlement language.

Complications: A witness asks the party not to make them speak publicly; accepting this may reduce Public Legitimacy but preserve Witness Safety.

Faction Appearances: Last Light supports trauma care; Wardens offer guard; Remnant Veil offers disappearance.

Violence or Threats: Violence is impossible here. Threats trigger immediate witness removal from public hearing.

After the Ruling: Protected testimony can remain sealed, be read publicly, or support investigation depending on outcome.

## NPC and Witness Quick Cards

### Ira Quill

Role in the Hearing: Witness advocate, procedural guide, and consent-route anchor.

First Impression: Ink-black fingertips, soft voice, eyes that become sharp when someone says "voluntary" too quickly.

Voice: Quiet, precise, controlled anger under formal language.

Wants Right Now: Keep witnesses from signing away claims and get the Court to hear consent before commerce.

Fear: The party wins Sel's case but creates a precedent that hurts future frightened witnesses.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Ira has hidden witnesses from lawful harm before and could lose standing if exposed.

Leverage: Protected testimony procedure, emergency witness room, clerk relationships, and language that Orvan respects.

What They Know: Hidden material terms can void consent; settlement steps are dangerous; Orvan will listen to clean reasoning.

What They Lie About: Ira says they are not afraid of the Court. They are.

Useful Quote: "A signature is not consent if the hand was shaking."

If Helped: Grants advantage on one witness-safety action or legal phrasing check.

If Threatened: Withdraws into procedure and protects witnesses from the party too.

If Exposed: Admits they have hidden clients, then demands the party prove why that was wrong.

If Ignored: Witnesses face settlement pressure without protection.

### Magistrate Orvan Hex

Role in the Hearing: Final ruling authority.

First Impression: Tiefling magistrate in black-blue robes, spectacles gleaming like tiny verdicts.

Voice: Formal, resonant, exact. He dislikes wasted words more than anger.

Wants Right Now: Determine whether the Charter protects consent or merely records form.

Fear: A broad ruling destabilizes commerce; a narrow ruling blesses predation.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Orvan knows the Court has ignored similar complaints when evidence was weak.

Leverage: Ruling authority, precedent language, Court access, and the ability to order investigation.

What They Know: First Step has sealed complaints; Article III has exceptions for defective consent.

What They Lie About: Orvan claims personal feelings do not enter the ruling. His mercy is awake.

Useful Quote: "Precision is mercy when imprecision is the trap."

If Helped: Writes a clear ruling that protects Tower access.

If Threatened: Narrows the hearing to the smallest possible question.

If Exposed: Acknowledges Court failure if proof is strong, but punishes theatrical accusation without evidence.

If Ignored: Seraphex defines the case for him.

### Clause Bailiff Twelve-Bells

Role in the Hearing: Legal hazard, restraint, and procedural enforcement.

First Impression: Metal-and-parchment bailiff with twelve shoulder bells, each tuned to a different infraction.

Voice: Numbered, calm, toneless: "Second warning: witness pressure."

Wants Right Now: Preserve procedure and stop coercion inside the Court.

Fear: It does not fear, but its old programming overreacts to emotional testimony.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Twelve-Bells has a dormant mercy exception Orvan can invoke if harm is clear.

Leverage: Silence seals, restraint ribbons, infraction marks, hearing recess authority.

What They Know: Who has lied under witness, who threatened whom, and which clause triggered intervention.

What They Lie About: It does not lie, but it can state incomplete procedural truth.

Useful Quote: "Third warning: force is not argument."

If Helped: Its warnings clarify the safe legal route.

If Threatened: Intervenes immediately.

If Exposed: A true contradiction in its warning causes one bell to crack and Legal Pressure drops by 1.

If Ignored: Warnings escalate to restraint.

### Merrit Vane

Role in the Hearing: Hidden principal and possible late-arriving antagonist.

First Impression: Immaculate Guild elder with a gentle smile that makes debt sound like parenting.

Voice: Paternal, smooth, patient, never raised.

Wants Right Now: Keep First Step's method alive, sacrifice Mira or Felix if useful, and avoid being named in precedent.

Fear: A ruling that makes hidden material terms reviewable across old contracts.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Several of Vane's profitable contracts use the same validator logic.

Leverage: Guild clerks, settlement money, hostile observers, prepared counterclaims, and frightened debtors.

What They Know: The false debt was designed to survive shallow review but not deep metadata scrutiny.

What They Lie About: He calls First Step independent and claims he only funds broad orientation access.

Useful Quote: "Order is expensive. I ask only that beneficiaries share its cost."

If Helped: Offers polite patronage that costs the party public trust.

If Threatened: Lets Seraphex turn the threat into evidence of recklessness.

If Exposed: Abandons First Step's field agents and pivots to "isolated misconduct."

If Ignored: Continues shaping the hearing through Seraphex and observers.

### Advocate Seraphex Glass

Role in the Hearing: Vane's legal representative and active opposition voice.

First Impression: Silver-haired advocate in pearl-black robes, smiling like every question has already signed a contract.

Voice: Elegant, warm, and poisonous. Never sounds cruel until quoted later.

Wants Right Now: Settle, discredit, or narrow the case before Vane is named.

Fear: Being forced to read the hidden clause aloud under witness bell.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Seraphex knows the clause is defective but believes commercial stability matters more than one false start.

Leverage: Legal training, settlement offers, chain-of-custody challenges, and rhetorical traps.

What They Know: The weakest part of the party's case and which witness can be frightened.

What They Lie About: They call First Step's conduct "ordinary orientation finance."

Useful Quote: "Compassion is why we offer settlement before reputations are harmed."

If Helped: Offers a narrow settlement and tries to bind silence.

If Threatened: Triggers Twelve-Bells and reframes the party as dangerous.

If Exposed: Overcorrects, creating new evidence if baited into denying visible text.

If Ignored: Defines the party as confused debtors before they speak.

### Sel Varrin

Role in the Hearing: Named debtor and core consent witness.

First Impression: Pale, silver-freckled, holding his wrist like the debt mark is a burn.

Voice: Soft, honest, stumbles over legal phrasing.

Wants Right Now: Be believed without having to become brave in public.

Fear: Everyone decides he accepted because he was foolish.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: He considered signing settlement before Ira arrived.

Leverage: Can describe confusion, timing, Chime's wording, and fear.

What They Know: He never ordered services, did not understand debt, and felt rushed.

What They Lie About: "I am ready to testify." He may not be without support.

Useful Quote: "I thought accepting the box meant accepting help."

If Helped: Gives clear testimony and raises Witness Safety.

If Threatened: Freezes or accepts settlement.

If Exposed: Admits he almost signed, which can support Mercy Route if handled kindly.

If Ignored: Seraphex defines him as regretful, not deceived.

### Kessa Coil

Role in the Hearing: Registry-theft witness and truth-route hinge.

First Impression: Sleepless courier with a guarded stare and a hand near her throat where the shard hung.

Voice: Defensive, rough, quick to say what she did not do.

Wants Right Now: Protection before confession.

Fear: Her theft becomes the only story and Vane walks away.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: More arrival names were copied than Sel's.

Leverage: Knows Mira paid for data and First Step wanted fresh arrival records.

What They Know: K.Coil access path, Mira instructions, payment route, and shard movement.

What They Lie About: She minimizes the number of copied names.

Useful Quote: "I stole a key. They built the lock around someone's throat."

If Helped: Gives metadata context and names Mira.

If Threatened: Confirms only what physical evidence already proves.

If Exposed: Admits broader copying if promised witness protection.

If Ignored: Seraphex paints her as the sole criminal.

### Chime

Role in the Hearing: Courier-log witness and manifest mismatch source.

First Impression: Tiny brass construct perched on a document stand, receipt spool trembling.

Voice: Precise, clicking, fragile when accused.

Wants Right Now: State the logs accurately and survive Felix's embarrassment.

Fear: Being reset or blamed as defective equipment.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Chime's internal warning was overridden by rush processing.

Leverage: Manifest, seal weight, visible terms, delivery timing.

What They Know: Parcel was heavier than logged; Felix authorized route; First Step supplied seal.

What They Lie About: Nothing intentionally, but defensive recitation omits context.

Useful Quote: "This unit did not choose the teeth."

If Helped: Prints full log and admits the override.

If Threatened: Recites only visible terms.

If Exposed: Shows the override record, embarrassing Felix but helping truth.

If Ignored: Seraphex treats it as a simple delivery device.

### Aria Neon

Role in the Hearing: Public legitimacy witness and pattern witness.

First Impression: Neon ribbons muted for Court, which somehow makes her more visible.

Voice: Controlled music, less performance than precision.

Wants Right Now: Make public truth memorable without endangering sources.

Fear: Her performance record exposes Brindle before he is protected.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: She suppressed one prior debt story.

Leverage: Stage archive, crowd memory, performance-timed pattern, public narrative.

What They Know: Similar deliveries used distraction and shame.

What They Lie About: She says she is only here for the song. She is here for the witnesses.

Useful Quote: "The trick was not the box. It was making everyone look away at the same beautiful second."

If Helped: Raises Public Legitimacy and protects Brindle's dignity.

If Threatened: Turns public attention against the threatener.

If Exposed: Admits prior suppression if it protects the current witness.

If Ignored: Seraphex calls the tavern evidence theatrical.

### Felix Pixelcoin

Role in the Hearing: Guild routing witness and negligent broker.

First Impression: Dressed too well for someone sweating through apology vouchers.

Voice: Fast charm, then quiet when the word negligence lands.

Wants Right Now: Prove he was careless, not predatory, and keep Vane from owning the story.

Fear: Guild hardliners replace him and bury the case.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Faulty extraction beacon history makes him vulnerable to public shame.

Leverage: Delivery logs, stock analysis, Guild routing knowledge, money.

What They Know: Counterfeit stock style, old-guard routing, Vane's benefit.

What They Lie About: He downplays how obvious the seal weight warning was.

Useful Quote: "I sold fear-adjacent solutions. This was fear with a receipt."

If Helped: Names Vane's method and pays restitution.

If Threatened: Cooperates defensively and refuses broader Guild context.

If Exposed: Admits negligence if the party distinguishes it from authorship.

If Ignored: Guild hardliners use him as scapegoat.

### Marik Bluecoat

Role in the Hearing: Warden procedure witness and chain-of-custody support.

First Impression: Blue armor polished for Court, expression not polished at all.

Voice: Low, clipped, protective.

Wants Right Now: Make the evidence survive procedure and prevent hardliners from taking over.

Fear: The party creates chaos that proves his opponents right.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Warden hardliners want broader registry control after this case.

Leverage: Incident notes, Warden custody, safe-zone records, public trust.

What They Know: First Step complaints exist, but sealed records restrict what he can say.

What They Lie About: He says the Wardens are united. They are not.

Useful Quote: "I can hold a line. I need you to give me the right line to hold."

If Helped: Offers protected witness status or clean access note.

If Threatened: Stops helping beyond duty.

If Exposed: Admits Warden limits, raising Public Legitimacy if handled respectfully.

If Ignored: Chain-of-custody challenges become harder.

### Brindle Pact

Role in the Hearing: Paid spotter witness or hostile recanter.

First Impression: Copper scarf, shaking hands, eyes finding every exit.

Voice: Fast, brittle, jokes that die halfway.

Wants Right Now: Protect his sister and not be alone in blame.

Fear: Vane calls in his sister's room contract.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: He lied in two earlier deliveries.

Leverage: Paid witness names, Mira's timing, First Step token.

What They Know: First Step paid for distraction and witness shaping.

What They Lie About: "I only did this once."

Useful Quote: "I was paid to point. I did not know pointing could put chains on people."

If Helped: Gives names and admits the pattern.

If Threatened: Recants or gives only one fact.

If Exposed: Admits prior lies if his sister is protected.

If Ignored: Seraphex makes him a liar before Ira can make him a witness.

### Mira Vale

Role in the Hearing: Hostile field witness or absent pressure source.

First Impression: Charcoal coat, upside-down pin removed, smile still shaped like a clause.

Voice: Smooth, cool, commercial.

Wants Right Now: Keep Vane's name out and make evidence handling the issue.

Fear: Vane abandons her.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: She has a private copy of payment orders.

Leverage: Payment chain, Brindle pressure, field instructions.

What They Know: Vane controls First Step and told her to recover evidence.

What They Lie About: She calls her actions property protection.

Useful Quote: "Amateurs often confuse urgency with truth."

If Helped: Trades Vane's payment copy for protection.

If Threatened: Becomes polished and hostile.

If Exposed: Turns on Vane if proof shows he will sacrifice her.

If Ignored: Continues witness intimidation through brokers.

### CodeX or Nyx Understep

Role in the Hearing: Illegal-data pressure, alternate witness protection, or faction complication.

First Impression: CodeX appears as text-eyed projection; Nyx appears where a shadow should not fit.

Voice: CodeX is quiet static; Nyx is dry, amused, and evasive.

Wants Right Now: Prevent registry vulnerability from being buried.

Fear: The Court uses the case to strengthen locks rather than fix harm.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Radicals want the shard leaked in full.

Leverage: Redacted metadata, hidden routes, witness hiding, illegal access.

What They Know: The registry flaw is systemic.

What They Lie About: "We only copied what was necessary." Not always true.

Useful Quote: CodeX: "A locked record is not a moral argument." Nyx: "Courtrooms are just cages with better chairs."

If Helped: Provides a redacted proof path.

If Threatened: Leaks partial data or hides Kessa.

If Exposed: Admits illegal access if the party protects vulnerable names.

If Ignored: Acts offscreen and complicates the ruling.

### Hostile Guild Observer

Role in the Hearing: Public pressure and Vane's rumor conduit.

First Impression: A tidy observer with a gold coin pin and a face trained not to react.

Voice: Mild, concerned, weaponized civility.

Wants Right Now: Make the party look anti-commerce or reckless.

Fear: Public shoppers turn against Guild credit.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: Paid by Vane's office through a consulting stipend.

Leverage: Public comments, vendor rumors, procedural objections.

What They Know: Which Guild clerks are willing to blame Felix.

What They Lie About: They claim neutrality.

Useful Quote: "Commerce cannot function if every regret becomes fraud."

If Helped: Offers narrow procedural clarity, never moral support.

If Threatened: Plays victim and raises Legal Pressure.

If Exposed: Reveals the stipend trail if cornered with evidence.

If Ignored: Seeds doubt in the public gallery.

### Nervous Public Witness

Role in the Hearing: Ordinary citizen who saw one moment and fears being involved.

First Impression: A resident clutching a queue token with both hands.

Voice: Thin, honest, apologetic.

Wants Right Now: Tell the truth and leave unseen.

Fear: Factions remember their face.

Secret or Hidden Pressure: They accepted a small Guild discount last week and fear that makes them biased.

Leverage: Saw Mira approach Brindle, or saw Chime's witness gem brighten before acceptance.

What They Know: One concrete observed fact.

What They Lie About: "I did not see enough to matter." They did.

Useful Quote: "I only saw a little. But I saw it before the bell."

If Helped: Gives one clean corroborating detail.

If Threatened: Freezes and asks to leave.

If Exposed: Admits the Guild discount and then tells the truth anyway.

If Ignored: Seraphex says no neutral witness supports the party.

## Contract Hall Mechanics

Run the hearing as a structured social encounter. The party does not need to "win" every exchange. They need enough track strength to secure a meaningful ruling.

### Hearing Tracks

Each track ranges from 0 to 5. Starting values come from the continuity row. If unsure, start Evidence Strength 3, Witness Safety 3, Public Legitimacy 2, and Legal Pressure 2.

#### Evidence Strength

0: The Court cannot rely on party evidence. Only testimony and settlement remain.
1: Evidence is weak or badly challenged.
2: Evidence is useful but incomplete.
3: Evidence supports a narrow ruling.
4: Evidence supports a broad void or investigation.
5: Evidence is decisive and creates precedent.

Increase Evidence Strength by 1 when the party presents sealed physical evidence, corroborates testimony with metadata, repairs chain of custody, or exposes a contradiction. Decrease it by 1 when evidence is damaged, unsupported, illegally sourced without redaction, or contradicted by a witness. At 0, Orvan can only pause or settle. At 5, Vane's side loses one opposition action.

#### Witness Safety

0: A key witness recants, flees, or can only submit sealed testimony.
1: Witnesses speak through fear and disadvantage.
2: Witnesses answer basic questions.
3: Witnesses can tell the core truth.
4: Witnesses withstand pressure.
5: A witness volunteers an extra damaging truth.

Increase Witness Safety by 1 when the party calms, protects, requests recess, uses the Emergency Witness Room, or exposes intimidation. Decrease it by 1 when witnesses are publicly shamed, threatened, contradicted without care, or left alone with brokers. At 0, choose one witness to collapse. At 5, the witness reveals one extra clue.

#### Public Legitimacy

0: The public thinks the case is a stunt, debt dodge, or faction attack.
1: The public is skeptical.
2: The public is divided.
3: The public understands the harm.
4: The public supports review.
5: The ruling becomes a public precedent story.

Increase Public Legitimacy through clear statements, neutral witnesses, Aria's support, Marik's restraint, and transparent evidence. Decrease it through threats, confusion, faction bickering, Codebreaker secrecy without explanation, or public property damage. At 0, reputation rewards are lost. At 5, the party gains advantage on the first Forecourt public pressure check.

#### Legal Pressure

0: The party has room to argue and request recess.
1: Procedure is calm.
2: Normal contested hearing.
3: Orvan demands tighter claims.
4: Twelve-Bells warns actively.
5: One more serious infraction triggers intervention.

Legal Pressure rises when the party ignores procedure, repeats unsupported claims, threatens, rambles under opposition pressure, or handles evidence carelessly. It drops when they cite Charter principles, accept a fair correction, request protected procedure, or expose opposition overreach. At 0, the party can request one recess without cost. At 5, Twelve-Bells intervenes before the next ruling shift.

### Starting Values by Chunk 01 Outcome

| Outcome | Evidence Strength | Witness Safety | Public Legitimacy | Legal Pressure |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Clean Win | 4 | 4 | 3 | 1 |
| Messy Win | 3 | 3 | 2 | 3 |
| Debt Activated | 3 | 2 | 2 | 4 |
| Lost Chase | 2 | 2 | 2 | 3 |
| Courier Dead | 3 | 1 | 1 | 4 |
| Party Goes Straight to the Tower | 1 | 2 | 1 | 4 |
| Party Sides With CodeX | 3 | 3 | 1 | 3 |
| Party Sides With Marik | 4 | 3 | 2 | 2 |
| Party Sides With Felix | 3 | 3 | 2 | 2 |
| Party Publicly Accuses the Guild | 2 | 2 | 1 | 4 |

### Hearing Round Structure

Run 3-5 hearing rounds. A round is not six seconds; it is one exchange of legal focus.

1. Magistrate Question. Orvan asks a narrow question: "What proves consent was defective?" or "Who touched the record?"
2. Party Presentation. One or more PCs present evidence, question a witness, cite law, or request procedure.
3. Opposition Challenge. Seraphex or Vane's side attacks the weakest link.
4. Witness Reaction. A witness clarifies, panics, recants, or adds truth.
5. Faction Interference or Public Pressure. A faction observer, crowd reaction, or bailiff warning changes a track.
6. Ruling Shift. Adjust tracks and state what Orvan now seems to believe.

Recommended Three-Round Hearing:

Round 1: Consent question and Sel or parcel evidence.
Round 2: Truth question and registry/routing evidence.
Round 3: Harm question and witness safety, then ruling.

Recommended Five-Round Hearing:

Round 1: Intake and issue framing.
Round 2: Sel or Chime testimony.
Round 3: Kessa, Felix, or registry evidence.
Round 4: Opposition overreach and Clause Bailiff pressure.
Round 5: Final route argument and ruling.

### Player Actions During Hearing

| Player Action | Check/DC | Success | Partial Success | Failure | Track Changes | Possible Complication |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Present physical evidence | Investigation, Arcana, or relevant tools DC 13-16 | Evidence accepted cleanly | Evidence accepted but challenged | Evidence questioned or delayed | Evidence +1 or Integrity clock +1 | Seraphex attacks chain of custody |
| Question a witness | Persuasion, Insight, or Legal Cant DC 13-17 | Witness gives clear truth | Witness gives narrow answer | Witness panics or contradicts | Witness Safety +1 or Evidence +1 | Witness asks for protected room |
| Object to a clause | Legal Cant, Investigation, or Persuasion DC 14 | Clause reading paused or reframed | Objection noted but not decisive | Legal Pressure +1 | Legal Pressure -1 on success | Twelve-Bells demands precision |
| Expose contradiction | Insight or Investigation DC 15-17 | Opposition loses action, Evidence +1 | Contradiction creates doubt | Party looks accusatory | Evidence +1, Public +1 | Hostile observer calls it theater |
| Calm witness | Persuasion, Medicine, Religion, or Insight DC 12-15 | Witness Safety +1 | Witness speaks through Ira | Witness Safety -1 | Witness Safety shifts | Settlement broker renews pressure |
| Challenge chain of custody | Investigation DC 14 | Court seals evidence cleanly | Evidence admitted with note | Evidence Integrity -1 | Evidence +1 or Legal Pressure -1 | CodeX source questioned |
| Cite Charter principle | History, Religion, or Persuasion DC 14 | Public understands route | Orvan asks for concrete proof | Sounds like speechmaking | Public +1, Legal Pressure -1 | Seraphex demands text |
| Call faction support | Persuasion DC 13 plus faction reputation | Faction helps cleanly | Faction helps with visible strings | Faction argument distracts | Public or Evidence +1, or Faction clock +1 | Rival faction objects |
| Request recess | Persuasion or Legal Cant DC 13 | Recess granted, Witness Safety +1 | Recess granted, Legal Pressure +1 | Recess denied | Witness Safety +1 or Legal Pressure +1 | Settlement pressure during recess |
| Force public reading | Performance, Persuasion, or Legal Cant DC 15 | Hidden clause read aloud | Clause summarized by clerk | Seraphex narrows reading | Public +1, Evidence +1 | Witness shame if Sel is unsupported |
| Accept settlement | No roll if all affected PCs consent; Insight DC 13 to read cost | Immediate relief with terms understood | Relief plus hidden future cost revealed | Bad terms bind | Legal Pressure drops, Evidence route closes | Sel may feel abandoned |
| Bait opposition into overreach | Deception, Insight, or Persuasion DC 16 | Seraphex creates new evidence | Seraphex reveals motive but not proof | Party looks manipulative | Public +1 or Evidence +1 | Twelve-Bells warns against bad-faith tactics |

### Opposition Actions

| Opposition Action | What It Sounds Like | Player Response | DCs | Consequence If Unanswered |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Discredit Sel | "Regret after acceptance is not fraud." | Calm Sel, cite hidden terms, show recipient confusion | Persuasion DC 13, Insight DC 12, evidence DC 14 | Witness Safety -1, Legal Pressure +1 |
| Challenge Kessa | "The thief asks us to trust her records." | Corroborate with shard, offer protection, admit her theft without making it sole issue | Investigation DC 14, Persuasion DC 15 | Evidence Strength -1 |
| Attack chain of custody | "Who held the parcel overnight?" | Present seal case, Marik note, Chime log, or intake ribbon | Investigation DC 13-16 | Evidence Integrity -1 |
| Offer settlement | "We can spare this young man embarrassment." | Read terms, reject publicly, negotiate pause without waiver | Insight DC 12, Investigation DC 13 | Public Legitimacy -1 if party seems unreasonable |
| Frame CodeX involvement | "Illegal data cannot cleanse illegal conduct." | Redact source, show independent corroboration, call Marik or Chime | Arcana DC 15, Persuasion DC 14 | Evidence from shard becomes contested |
| Claim party tampering | "The seal was in their hands." | Show intake record, witnesses, or damage timeline | Investigation DC 15 | Legal Pressure +1, Evidence -1 |
| Invoke delivery validation | "They carried the parcel and sought reward." | Distinguish delivery from consent, quote hidden clause, state objection timing | Legal Cant DC 14, Persuasion DC 15 | Party named reckless validators |
| Threaten civil counterclaim | "False accusation has costs." | Demand public reading, ask Orvan to separate intimidation from claim | Persuasion DC 14, Insight DC 13 | Witness Safety -1 |
| Trigger Clause Bailiff review | "The record contains threats and illegal copying." | De-escalate, clarify, accept narrow correction | Legal Cant DC 15 or Persuasion DC 14 | Twelve-Bells intervention |

## Evidence and Clue Matrix

Use this matrix during Session 4 whenever a player asks, "What can we prove?" Evidence does not have to be perfect to matter. A weak item can support a stronger one, protect a witness from being the only source, or shift the ruling toward an appeal instead of a loss.

| Evidence | Source | What It Proves | Strength | Who Challenges It | Best Use | Present Cleanly | Risk If Mishandled | Backup If Missing |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Preserved parcel | Session 2, sealed before activation or after safe handling | A false delivery instrument existed and carried a hidden clause | Strong | Seraphex, hostile Guild observer | Anchor Consent and Truth routes | Investigation or Arcana DC 13; forgery tools DC 12 | If opened carelessly, Seraphex claims tampering | Hidden clause copy, Chime statement, registry shard |
| Damaged parcel | Smashed, burned, or activated parcel remains | The object contained hostile contract logic, but chain is weakened | Useful | Seraphex | Support Truth route with material traces | Investigation DC 15 or Arcana DC 14 | Evidence Strength -1 if no corroboration | Felix appraisal, Marik incident note |
| Hidden clause text | Exposed wording from parcel or copy | Custody was designed to become validation | Decisive if tied to party handling | Seraphex | Consent route centerpiece | Legal Cant, Investigation, or calligrapher's supplies DC 13 | If read without context, public blames party for signing | Force public reading; Chime or Ira explains terms |
| Witness gem | Contract Hall or tavern recording crystal | Records exact words at delivery or confrontation | Strong | Seraphex attacks completeness | Prove no informed acceptance | Arcana DC 14 or Persuasion DC 13 to have it admitted | If cracked, only short phrases remain | Aria performance record, public witness |
| Registry shard | Code Cavern metadata or Kessa's shard | The parcel route was altered after creation | Strong | Guild observer, Seraphex | Truth route centerpiece | Arcana or Investigation DC 15 | If tied only to CodeX, source looks illegal | Felix appraisal, Chime routing log |
| Kessa testimony | Kessa Coil, frightened courier | First Step runners were ordered to move false debt parcels | Strong if protected; useful if scared | Seraphex, Brindle, Vane | Connect Vane to process | Persuasion DC 15 or Ira support; Insight DC 13 to avoid bad question | Witness Safety -1 if pressed cruelly | Registry shard, Brindle denial contradiction |
| Sel testimony | Sel Varrin | Sel did not understand consent, and his counter anomaly was exploited | Useful; strong with clause | Seraphex | Consent and Mercy routes | Persuasion DC 13, Insight DC 12 to keep him steady | He blames himself and narrows his answer | GUIDY slip, Chime statement, public witness |
| Aria performance record | Convergence Point Tavern stage log | The parcel arrived during staged noise and social distraction | Useful | Guild observer | Show misleading delivery environment | Performance or Investigation DC 13 | Aria is accused of theater | Tavern witness, Nomi Sweetspark rumor |
| Felix appraisal | Felix Pixelcoin's stock and seal analysis | The guild stock or seal was counterfeit, copied, or laundered | Strong if Felix stands by it | Seraphex, Guild observer | Prove Guild cannot cleanly claim innocence | Persuasion DC 14 to make Felix testify plainly | Felix hedges to protect his stall | Physical token imprint, public market record |
| Chime statement | Chime's explanation of terms and delivery log | The clause used abnormal validation language | Useful | Seraphex | Clarify contract language without making Chime the villain | Persuasion DC 13; Legal Cant DC 12 | Chime panics and sounds evasive | Ira explanation, hidden clause text |
| Marik incident note | Warden Bluecoat note from Sessions 1-3 | The party reported concern before exploiting the parcel | Strong against reckless validator claim | Seraphex | Protect party reputation | Persuasion DC 12 or Marik testimony | Marik dislikes sloppy exaggeration | GUIDY slip, public safe-zone record |
| GUIDY orientation slip | Orientation record stamped before parcel dispute | Party was newly arrived and had limited legal knowledge | Useful | Seraphex | Consent and Mercy support | Arcana DC 12 or no roll if intact | Can be spun as ignorance, not innocence | Sel testimony, Ira legal framing |
| Code Cavern metadata | Chase residue, route scrape, or tunnel record | The parcel moved through illicit routing channels | Strong | Seraphex calls it tainted data | Truth route support | Arcana DC 15 or thieves' tools DC 14 | Legal Pressure +1 if source hidden poorly | Registry shard, Kessa testimony |
| Mira token imprint | Token mark on parcel, shard, or payment | A Vane-linked runner or handler touched the scheme | Useful; strong with witness | Mira, Seraphex | Tie First Step chain to Vane's network | Investigation DC 15 | If overstated, Public Legitimacy -1 | Brindle contradiction, Kessa testimony |
| Brindle confession or denial | Brindle Pact confronted or recorded | Confession proves runner pressure; denial can contradict records | Useful or strong | Brindle, Seraphex | Trigger opposition overreach | Insight DC 14, Persuasion DC 15 | Brindle flees hearing if not protected | Kessa, Marik, Code Cavern metadata |
| Public rumor record | Docket board chatter, tavern talk, promenade witness | The scam matches a repeated pattern | Weak alone; useful support | Orvan demands specifics | Mercy and Public Legitimacy support | Investigation or Persuasion DC 13 | Looks like gossip if unsupported | Nervous public witness, Ledger complaints |
| Aazoth flicker clue | Session 1 anomaly or later orientation echo | The Tower-system intelligence flagged the clause as corrupt | Useful and strange | Seraphex, Orvan | Show the Charter itself resisted the clause | Arcana or Religion DC 16 | Makes party sound unstable unless framed carefully | GUIDY slip, clause language |

### Missing Evidence Safety Net

If the party reaches the hearing with only one strong piece of evidence, do not halt play. Orvan asks for corroboration and opens one of these paths:

- Call Sel, Chime, or Marik as a witness.
- Request a registry query from the Clerk's Rail, costing 10 NC or one favor to the Ledger Court.
- Allow Ira to file a protected witness motion if the party agrees to keep Kessa inside the Hall until ruling.
- Let Seraphex overreach if the party baits him with a precise question.

## Three Routes to Victory

The hearing can end in the party's favor through Consent, Truth, Mercy, or a Mixed Route. Tell the table which question Orvan is currently weighing, so the players understand the legal game without needing to master Nexus law.

### Consent Route

This route proves Sel and the party did not knowingly consent to the debt.

Required evidence: hidden clause text plus Sel testimony or GUIDY orientation slip.

Alternate evidence: preserved parcel, Chime statement, Marik incident note, witness gem, Aria performance record.

Best witnesses: Sel, Chime, Ira Quill, Marik Bluecoat.

Key checks:

- Persuasion DC 13 to help Sel state what he believed he was accepting.
- Legal Cant, Investigation, or calligrapher's supplies DC 14 to show the hidden clause changed custody into debt validation.
- Insight DC 12 to catch Seraphex reframing regret as consent.
- Persuasion or History DC 14 to cite Consent as a Charter principle.

Opposition counter: Seraphex argues that carrying the parcel and asking about payment made the party validators. He uses the phrase, "They wanted the benefit until they saw the obligation."

Ruling text: "Consent hidden behind custody is not consent. A person may carry a sealed burden without becoming the burden."

Reward: Debt is voided or paused; Public Legitimacy +1; Sel's trust rises. If the route is clean, the party gains 25 NC and protected witness standing for the Tower registration line.

Future consequence: First Step begins using softer approaches against the party. Vane avoids direct threats and sends polite offers with teeth.

### Truth Route

This route proves the record was altered, laundered, or materially misleading.

Required evidence: registry shard or Code Cavern metadata plus preserved or damaged parcel.

Alternate evidence: Felix appraisal, Mira token imprint, Brindle contradiction, Chime routing log, public rumor record.

Best witnesses: Kessa, Felix, Chime, Brindle under pressure.

Key checks:

- Arcana or Investigation DC 15 to match registry timing to the parcel mark.
- Persuasion DC 14 to get Felix to say "counterfeit" without hiding behind merchant caution.
- Insight DC 14 to identify when Brindle denies a fact he does know.
- Deception, Insight, or Persuasion DC 16 to bait Seraphex into overclaiming the cleanliness of Vane's routing chain.

Opposition counter: Vane's side claims illicit metadata cannot be trusted and that CodeX tainted the record.

Ruling text: "A record that arrives cleaner than its path is not clean. The Court will not enforce a debt through a polished lie."

Reward: Evidence Strength +1, the Guild must answer questions, and the party receives a sealed copy of the ruling. If the route is clean, Felix gives a 10 percent discount on one Forecourt purchase.

Future consequence: The Pixel Prosperity Guild becomes colder in public while quietly measuring whether the party can be bought.

### Mercy Route

This route proves enforcement would create harm the Charter is designed to prevent.

Required evidence: Sel testimony or Kessa testimony plus proof of coercive pressure.

Alternate evidence: GUIDY slip, public rumor record, Aria performance record, Marik incident note, Ira's protected witness motion.

Best witnesses: Sel, Kessa, Ira, nervous public witness, Marik.

Key checks:

- Persuasion, Religion, or Medicine DC 13 to frame panic and harm without turning the hearing into sentiment alone.
- Insight DC 13 to show Kessa is afraid of reprisal rather than punishment.
- Persuasion DC 15 to convince Orvan the Court can protect truth without rewarding illegal routing.
- History or Religion DC 14 to cite Mercy as a Charter principle.

Opposition counter: Seraphex argues mercy cannot erase debt because "kindness is not accounting."

Ruling text: "The Charter is not a trapdoor under the frightened. Enforcement is paused where enforcement becomes predation."

Reward: Debt paused or converted to investigation status, Kessa may receive protective status, and the party gains goodwill with Last Light Concord or the Wardens.

Future consequence: The final legal result may remain unsettled, but the party gets Tower access with a visible debt flag or witness flag.

### Mixed Route

Most tables use a mixed route. If the party has at least two useful evidence items from different categories and one witness survives pressure, Orvan can rule in their favor without a perfect case.

Required evidence: any one physical item, any one witness, and any one corroborating record.

Alternate evidence: a public contradiction by Seraphex, a Clause Bailiff correction, or Vane visible in restricted records.

Best witnesses: the witness the table cares about most.

Key checks:

- One DC 14 check to frame the strongest theme.
- One DC 15 check to protect the weakest evidence link.
- One DC 13 check to prevent a witness from being isolated.

Opposition counter: Vane's side asks for appeal, delay, or settlement instead of final void.

Ruling text: "This Court does not have every stone, but it has enough weight to stop the machine."

Reward: Debt paused, party named protected witnesses or reckless validators depending on Legal Pressure, and portal/Spire access allowed with conditions.

Future consequence: The next campaign path begins with a legal shadow instead of a clean victory; portal-world officials, sponsors, and later Spire registrars all see the condition.

## Contract Hall Encounters

These encounters can be run in order or rearranged around player choices. If the table is short on time, run Encounters 1, 2, 4, 6, and 8. If the players love legal play, include all eight and let witnesses breathe.

### Encounter 1. Settlement Broker on the Steps

Goal: Establish pressure before the party reaches the hearing room and tempt them with an easy exit.

Setup: Pell Tick or a Vane-paid broker approaches outside the Ledger Court Steps. If Pell died or fled in Chunk 01, use Advocate Seraphex's assistant, Luro Dane, a soft-voiced clerk with silver ink on his gloves.

Read-Aloud:

> A narrow figure in a clean gray coat steps between you and the open doors. Behind him, the witness bell rings once, then answers itself in a lower tone. He smiles like the sound belongs to him. "Before this becomes public, First Step is prepared to resolve the misunderstanding."

NPCs: Pell Tick or Luro Dane, Sel if present, a Warden on the steps, two public watchers.

Player options:

- Read the settlement terms before answering.
- Reject the offer publicly.
- Negotiate a pause without admitting debt.
- Use the broker to reveal Vane's fear.
- Call Marik or Ira before speaking.

Checks/DCs:

- Insight DC 12: The offer is designed to make the party waive public reading.
- Investigation DC 13: The settlement contains a non-disparagement term and a future delivery exclusivity clause.
- Persuasion DC 14: Get the broker to admit First Step is worried about the hidden clause.
- Intimidation DC 15: The broker withdraws, but Legal Pressure +1 unless phrased as lawful warning.

Success: Party enters with Public Legitimacy +1 or Evidence Strength +1 if they keep the written offer.

Partial Success: Party rejects the deal but looks uncertain; no track change, but the broker remains available.

Failure: If they sign without reading, run Settlement Accepted as a possible ruling. If they shout threats, Legal Pressure +1.

Track changes: Public Legitimacy +1 for calm public refusal; Legal Pressure -1 for lawful negotiation; Legal Pressure +1 for threats.

Consequences: Sel trusts the party if they refuse to sacrifice him. Chime looks relieved if they check every term.

Faction reactions: Wardens respect restraint; Guild observers note who can be bought; CodeX mocks any settlement that silences evidence.

Shorten: Let a PC make one Insight or Investigation check, then move to Evidence Intake.

### Encounter 2. Evidence Intake Challenge

Goal: Determine which evidence enters the hearing cleanly and introduce the Court's rules.

Setup: At the Evidence Intake Alcove, Clerk Nomi Sweetspark asks for labels, source, chain of custody, and witness names. Seraphex's assistant objects to anything from Code Cavern.

Read-Aloud:

> The intake alcove glows with blue shelves. Each item placed on the rail receives a thin ribbon of light. A gnome clerk says, "Name the thing, name how you got it, and name who can be hurt if I read it aloud."

NPCs: Nomi, Ira if summoned, Seraphex's assistant, Marik if the party called him.

Player options:

- Submit all evidence openly.
- Seal sensitive witness names.
- Hold back illegal evidence and use it only for contradiction.
- Ask Ira to file protected handling.
- Ask Nomi what the Court considers strongest.

Checks/DCs:

- Investigation DC 13: Cleanly label physical evidence.
- Arcana DC 15: Stabilize metadata or a witness gem.
- Persuasion DC 14: Convince Nomi to accept a late item.
- Sleight of Hand DC 15: Hide an item from public display; on success it is private, not illegal. On failure, Legal Pressure +1.

Success: Evidence Strength +1 or Evidence Integrity clock improves.

Partial Success: Evidence is accepted with a contested mark; Seraphex gains one chain-of-custody challenge.

Failure: One evidence item is held until the party spends an action in the hearing to admit it.

Track changes: Evidence Strength +1 on clean intake; Legal Pressure +1 for sloppy concealment; Witness Safety +1 if names are sealed.

Consequences: The party learns what the Court will and will not protect.

Faction reactions: Ledger Court appreciates precision; CodeX dislikes redaction; Guild wants names exposed.

Shorten: Let Nomi accept three items, mark one contested, and continue.

### Encounter 3. Witness Waiting Gallery Pressure

Goal: Give the party a chance to protect witnesses before testimony.

Setup: Sel, Kessa, Chime, and possibly Felix wait in the gallery. A hostile Guild observer murmurs that witnesses can be countersued. Mira Vale watches from the far bench if still free.

Read-Aloud:

> The waiting gallery is quieter than the steps, which makes every whisper worse. Sel keeps rubbing the back of his hand where his life counter glows. Kessa sits where she can see two exits. Chime has arranged their notes three times and still looks unready.

NPCs: Sel, Kessa, Chime, Felix, hostile Guild observer, Ira if present, Mira if alive/free.

Player options:

- Reassure one witness.
- Ask what they are afraid to say.
- Request Emergency Witness Room protection.
- Confront the hostile observer.
- Let a witness opt out and rely on evidence.

Checks/DCs:

- Persuasion DC 13: Calm Sel or Chime.
- Insight DC 13: Kessa fears Mira and Vane more than the Court.
- Perception DC 14: Spot a threat mark on the gallery bench.
- Intimidation DC 14: Drive off the observer; on failure, Witness Safety -1.

Success: Witness Safety +1 and one witness gives a clearer answer later.

Partial Success: Witness speaks, but only through Ira or under sealed question.

Failure: Witness Safety -1; one witness hesitates during examination.

Track changes: Witness Safety +1 for care; Public Legitimacy +1 if the party protects without bullying.

Consequences: A protected witness can become decisive later.

Faction reactions: Wardens approve; Guild notes weakness; Last Light Concord quietly offers witness aid after the ruling.

Shorten: Let the party pick one witness to stabilize and one witness who remains shaky.

### Encounter 4. Opening Statements

Goal: Frame the hearing route and let the party choose Consent, Truth, Mercy, or Mixed.

Setup: Orvan calls the case, Seraphex stands for First Step, and Ira asks the party whether they want counsel, advice, or direct voice.

Read-Aloud:

> The hearing chamber seals with a sound like a book closing. Magistrate Orvan Hex rests one hand on the blue seal carved into the bench. "This Court hears a contested debt validation, a claim of hidden obligation, and a concern of witness coercion. Speak first to the question you can prove."

NPCs: Orvan, Ira, Seraphex, Twelve-Bells, party, witnesses.

Player options:

- Make their own opening statement.
- Let Ira frame the legal route.
- State the strongest evidence first.
- Request a public reading.
- Accept narrow issue framing to reduce pressure.

Checks/DCs:

- Persuasion or Performance DC 13: Clear opening.
- History, Religion, or Legal Cant DC 14: Charter-framed opening.
- Insight DC 12: Orvan values narrow claims over dramatic claims.
- No roll: Let Ira state the route; Public Legitimacy does not rise, but Legal Pressure drops by 1.

Success: Public Legitimacy +1 and Orvan asks the party's best question first.

Partial Success: Orvan understands, but Seraphex chooses the first challenge.

Failure: Legal Pressure +1 and Orvan narrows the hearing to one issue until evidence broadens it.

Track changes: Public +1, Legal Pressure -1, or no change depending on approach.

Consequences: This sets the default victory route.

Faction reactions: Spire Seekers admire boldness; Ledger Court admires precision; Guild prefers broad emotional claims they can dismiss.

Shorten: Ask one player, "Consent, Truth, or Mercy?" Then start witness examination.

### Encounter 5. Witness Examination

Goal: Turn evidence into accepted facts through testimony.

Setup: Orvan permits two witnesses before opposition challenge. More witnesses require a reason or a recess.

Read-Aloud:

> The witness rail brightens. Twelve-Bells turns its head without moving its body. "Witnesses will speak what they saw, what they heard, or what the record did to them. Guesses will be named guesses."

NPCs: Chosen witnesses, Orvan, Ira, Seraphex, Twelve-Bells.

Player options:

- Call Sel on consent.
- Call Kessa on routing.
- Call Chime on clause language.
- Call Felix on counterfeit stock.
- Call Marik on report timing.
- Call Aria on public distraction.

Checks/DCs:

- Persuasion DC 13: Ask a witness a humane, useful question.
- Insight DC 14: Catch the safe question they can answer fully.
- Investigation DC 15: Pair testimony to an evidence item.
- Intimidation DC 15: Works on Brindle, but Witness Safety -1 unless the threat is legal exposure.

Success: Evidence Strength +1 or Witness Safety +1.

Partial Success: Testimony is useful but narrow; Seraphex gets a response.

Failure: Witness contradicts, freezes, or asks for sealed testimony.

Track changes: Evidence +1 for corroborated fact; Witness Safety -1 for badgering; Legal Pressure +1 for unsupported claims.

Consequences: Witnesses treated well remain allies after the hearing.

Faction reactions: Wardens react to intimidation; Guild hunts for contradictions; Ira supports careful questions.

Shorten: Use one witness and one physical evidence item.

### Encounter 6. Opposition Overreach

Goal: Let players catch Vane's side revealing too much.

Setup: Seraphex sees the hearing turning and pushes a false certainty: that no First Step parcel ever entered Code Cavern, that Sel accepted knowingly, or that Kessa invented Vane's name.

Read-Aloud:

> Seraphex closes a silver folio. "The Court has heard fear, tavern gossip, and illegally scraped tunnel noise. What it has not heard is a lawful bridge to my client." Merrit Vane, seated behind him, taps twice on the rail.

NPCs: Seraphex, Vane, Orvan, Twelve-Bells, one target witness.

Player options:

- Ask Seraphex to repeat the claim under bell.
- Present contrary evidence.
- Ask Twelve-Bells whether the statement is a factual assertion.
- Let Ira demand a narrow admission.
- Bait Vane into correcting his own representative.

Checks/DCs:

- Insight DC 14: Seraphex's certainty is rehearsed, not known.
- Investigation or Arcana DC 15: Show the contrary timestamp or mark.
- Persuasion DC 16: Force public correction without sounding smug.
- Deception DC 16: Bait overreach; failure raises Legal Pressure +1.

Success: Evidence Strength +1 and Public Legitimacy +1. If the contradiction is strong, add "Vane's Representative Overreaches" as a possible ruling.

Partial Success: Orvan notes the inconsistency, but no track rises unless corroborated.

Failure: Seraphex reframes and Legal Pressure +1.

Track changes: Evidence +1, Public +1, Legal Pressure +1 on failed bait.

Consequences: Vane now recognizes the party as a direct threat.

Faction reactions: Guild observer grows quiet; CodeX sends a smirking message if present; Ledger Court clerks record every word.

Shorten: Have Orvan ask, "Can you prove that contradiction now?" One check resolves it.

### Encounter 7. Clause Bailiff Intervention

Goal: Turn legal pressure into a dramatic hazard without ending the hearing.

Setup: Trigger this when Legal Pressure reaches 5, a witness lies under bell, a PC threatens violence, or Seraphex invokes review.

Read-Aloud:

> The blue seal under the bench flares. Twelve-Bells rises one joint at a time. Its twelve tiny bells ring in sequence, and each tone pulls a word out of the air: CUSTODY. CONSENT. THREAT. RECORD.

NPCs: Twelve-Bells, Orvan, targeted speaker, Ira, Seraphex.

Player options:

- Clarify the statement.
- Withdraw a claim without admitting falsehood.
- Present evidence to support the claim.
- Request protected phrasing through Ira.
- Attack or flee, which turns the Hall against them.

Checks/DCs:

- Persuasion or Legal Cant DC 14: De-escalate with precise language.
- Insight DC 13: Learn which word triggered intervention.
- Arcana DC 15: Identify the bailiff's restraint field.
- Athletics or Acrobatics DC 14: Resist nonlethal repositioning if combat begins.

Success: Legal Pressure drops by 1; the hearing continues.

Partial Success: The claim is narrowed; Evidence Strength does not rise this round.

Failure: A legal mark appears on the speaker until the ruling; disadvantage on one future attempt to make unsupported claims.

Track changes: Legal Pressure -1 on de-escalation; Public Legitimacy -1 if violence starts.

Consequences: The bailiff can accidentally help by naming the true legal issue.

Faction reactions: Wardens prepare to intervene; Guild hopes the party attacks; Ira urges precision.

Shorten: Give the party one sentence to clarify, then return to Final Ruling.

### Encounter 8. Final Ruling

Goal: Convert track state, evidence, and player choices into a clear legal outcome.

Setup: After 3-5 hearing rounds, Orvan asks for final statements. Vane may leave before the ruling unless the party has decisive evidence or a Warden request.

Read-Aloud:

> Orvan touches the blue seal. The witness bell rings once, cleanly this time. "The Court has heard enough to stop guessing. This ruling binds the record until appealed, overturned, or fulfilled."

NPCs: Orvan, Ira, Seraphex, Twelve-Bells, witnesses, faction observers.

Player options:

- Make a final route statement.
- Ask for witness protection.
- Ask for public record.
- Ask for costs or debt relief.
- Ask that Vane remain named in the ruling.

Checks/DCs:

- Persuasion DC 14: Strong final statement.
- Legal Cant or History DC 15: Precise Charter ask.
- Insight DC 13: Tell whether Orvan is leaning void, pause, or appeal.
- No roll: Accept a narrower ruling that protects Tower access.

Success: Move one track up by 1 before applying ruling.

Partial Success: Get one requested consequence, not all.

Failure: Ruling still occurs, but the party loses one optional benefit.

Track changes: Final adjustment; then apply possible ruling.

Consequences: Debt, heat, witness safety, and registration status become set for Session 5.

Faction reactions: Each faction approaches in downtime based on the ruling.

Shorten: Pick the possible ruling matching the table state and read it.

## Clause Bailiff Pressure Scene

Clause Bailiff Twelve-Bells is not an enemy in the normal sense. It is a legal enforcement construct built to preserve witness integrity, stop coercion, and prevent magical fraud inside the hearing chamber. It is frightening because it is impartial in the wrong way: it reacts to procedure, not virtue.

### Clause Bailiff Behavior

Twelve-Bells watches speakers, evidence, active magic, threats, and witness stress. It does not care who is morally right. It cares whether the record can remain enforceable.

It speaks in short legal labels before full sentences:

- "THREAT: Rephrase."
- "CUSTODY: Name source."
- "CONSENT: Define knowledge."
- "FALSEHOOD: Clarify or withdraw."
- "MERCY: Harm must be named."

### Legal Warning System

First Warning: A bell tone and one legal word. No penalty.

Second Warning: The speaker's shadow is pinned to the floor. Their next unsupported claim has disadvantage unless they clarify first.

Third Warning: Twelve-Bells imposes a blue seal mark. Legal Pressure reaches 5, and Orvan pauses the hearing for intervention.

### Escalating Interventions

1. Narrowing Bell. Twelve-Bells demands a claim be reduced to one provable sentence. De-escalate with Persuasion, Legal Cant, or Insight DC 13.
2. Witness Shield. A glowing panel blocks direct questioning of a distressed witness. De-escalate with Persuasion DC 14, Medicine DC 13, or Ira's motion.
3. Custody Seal. Evidence floats away from the speaker until its chain is named. De-escalate with Investigation DC 14 or Arcana DC 15.

### Triggers

Twelve-Bells intervenes when a creature threatens violence in the chamber, lies under witness bell, casts a spell on a witness without permission, repeats an unsupported accusation after warning, tampers with evidence, or forces a frightened witness to answer after Orvan orders protection.

### De-Escalation

A player can de-escalate by stating the narrow claim, naming a source, apologizing to a witness without retracting truth, asking Ira for procedural phrasing, or accepting a sealed answer.

### If the Party Attacks

The bailiff responds nonlethally. Wardens enter at the end of the first round. Orvan does not end the campaign over one bad swing, but the ruling shifts toward Reckless Validators or Appeal Required unless the party stops immediately and accepts a mark.

### If Someone Lies Under Witness

The witness bell rings backward. The liar takes 3 psychic damage and must make a DC 13 Charisma saving throw or be unable to knowingly repeat that false statement in the chamber for 1 minute. A successful save still leaves a blue mark on the record.

### If Players Expose a True Contradiction

Twelve-Bells turns toward the liar, not the party. Legal Pressure drops by 1, Evidence Strength rises by 1, and Seraphex loses his next opposition action unless he can explain the contradiction.

### Emergency Combat Profile: Clause Bailiff Twelve-Bells

Suggested CR: 2 enforcement hazard; XP 450 only if overcome in combat, though defeating it should create serious legal fallout. Intended difficulty for 4 level-1 or level-2 PCs: dangerous if fought directly, survivable if the party stops after one round. Safe maximum appearing: one.

AC 16; HP 45; Speed 30 ft.; hover 10 ft.

Ability Modifiers: Str +3, Dex +1, Con +3, Int +2, Wis +3, Cha +1.

Saving Throws: Wis +5, Con +5.

Skills: Insight +5, Investigation +4, Perception +5.

Senses: truesight 10 ft., passive Perception 15.

Languages: understands all languages spoken in the hearing chamber; speaks Common and Legal Cant.

Traits:

- Blue-Seal Authority. Inside Contract Hall, Twelve-Bells has advantage on checks to detect lies, evidence tampering, and hostile spellcasting.
- Nonlethal Mandate. Twelve-Bells cannot reduce a creature below 1 hit point unless that creature has already dealt lethal damage in the Hall.
- Procedure Bound. If a creature uses an action to make a clear procedural correction, Twelve-Bells cannot target that creature until the end of its next turn unless attacked.

Actions:

- Restraining Seal. Ranged Spell Attack +5, range 30 ft., one creature. Hit: 5 force damage, and the target is restrained until the end of its next turn. DC 13 Strength or Charisma check as an action ends it early.
- Bell Shock. Each creature of Twelve-Bells's choice within 10 ft. must succeed on a DC 13 Wisdom saving throw or take 4 psychic damage and be unable to take reactions until the start of its next turn.
- Evidence Lock. One object within 30 ft. becomes fixed in place for 1 minute or until Orvan releases it.

Reaction:

- Objection Tone. When a creature casts a spell targeting a witness or evidence item, Twelve-Bells imposes disadvantage on the spell attack or grants the target advantage on the saving throw.

Tactics: It restrains the loudest threat, shields witnesses, and locks evidence. It does not pursue fleeing PCs beyond Contract Hall.

Morale: It cannot be frightened, bribed, or insulted into rash action. It stands down if Orvan orders recess or if all hostile acts cease.

Noncombat Resolution: Three successful de-escalation checks before two failures end the intervention. Each PC can contribute once. Good ideas using law, apology, evidence clarity, or witness care count.

## Possible Rulings

Use these rulings as outcome packages. Pick the ruling that matches track state and evidence, then adjust details for the table's specific choices.

### 1. Full Void

Conditions: Evidence Strength 4+, Legal Pressure 2 or lower, and proof of hidden clause or altered record.

Read-Aloud Ruling Text:

> Orvan's voice cuts through the chamber. "The debt is void from origin. Custody did not become consent. No enforceable obligation rests on these respondents."

Mechanical Consequence: False debt is erased. Any debt mark from Chunk 01 disappears.

NC Consequence: Party receives 30 NC court cost compensation and may recover one documented expense up to 20 NC.

Reputation Consequence: +2 Ledger Court reputation, +1 Warden reputation, -1 Pixel Prosperity Guild comfort.

Faction Consequence: Guild publicly distances itself from First Step; CodeX claims the Court blinked only because the party forced it.

Sel Consequence: Sel becomes loyal and will testify again if protected.

Kessa Consequence: Kessa can request witness protection.

Tower Access Consequence: Clean registration available.

Transition: Ira recommends registering before Vane builds appeal pressure.

### 2. Void With Investigation

Conditions: Evidence Strength 3+, Truth route evidence, but Vane's personal role remains circumstantial.

Read-Aloud Ruling Text:

> "The debt is void. The question of who built the fraud remains open. The record is sealed for investigation."

Mechanical Consequence: Debt voided; evidence is retained by Ledger Court.

NC Consequence: 20 NC compensation; no recovery of damaged property until investigation ends.

Reputation Consequence: +1 Ledger, +1 public sympathy.

Faction Consequence: Wardens open a file; Guild protests procedure but does not protect First Step openly.

Sel Consequence: Free of debt but worried.

Kessa Consequence: Protected if she testified; watched if she refused.

Tower Access Consequence: Clean or Sponsored Registration available; Ledger Court may add witness flag.

Transition: Orvan tells the party, "The Tower may move faster than the Court."

### 3. Debt Paused Pending Review

Conditions: Evidence Strength 2-3, Mercy route strong, or missing chain-of-custody proof.

Read-Aloud Ruling Text:

> "The Court pauses enforcement. No collection may proceed while the record is reviewed. This is not innocence. It is a stop to harm."

Mechanical Consequence: Debt cannot be collected for 7 Nexus days. Debt flag remains visible.

NC Consequence: No compensation. Party may pay 10 NC for certified copies.

Reputation Consequence: +1 Mercy reputation, no Ledger increase.

Faction Consequence: Last Light Concord offers aid; Guild prepares appeal.

Sel Consequence: Safe for now.

Kessa Consequence: Needs protection to avoid pressure.

Tower Access Consequence: Debt-Flagged Registration or Probationary Registration.

Transition: Forecourt scan will ask whether the party accepts entry with unresolved debt.

### 4. Debt Transferred Back to First Step

Conditions: Truth route proves First Step custody fault but not full fraud.

Read-Aloud Ruling Text:

> "The obligation, if any exists, returns to the broker that mishandled it. First Step may not collect through these respondents."

Mechanical Consequence: Party freed from debt; First Step marked for audit.

NC Consequence: 15 NC compensation; First Step loses filing bond.

Reputation Consequence: +1 Ledger, +1 public practical respect.

Faction Consequence: Vane treats this as a contained loss and plots quietly.

Sel Consequence: Not liable.

Kessa Consequence: Vane blames her unless protected.

Tower Access Consequence: Clean Registration available, but Vane can interfere socially at Sponsor Row.

Transition: Seraphex warns, "Transferred does not mean forgotten."

### 5. Party Named Protected Witnesses

Conditions: Evidence threatens Vane, Witness Safety 3+, or threats are documented.

Read-Aloud Ruling Text:

> "These respondents are named protected witnesses in a pending inquiry. Retaliation, contract pressure, or coerced settlement against them will answer to the Court."

Mechanical Consequence: Attacks through legal pressure have disadvantage for 7 days; party can call Warden help once without cost.

NC Consequence: 10 NC witness stipend.

Reputation Consequence: +1 Ledger, +1 Warden, -1 criminal undercurrent.

Faction Consequence: CodeX distrusts the Court seal; Wardens take interest.

Sel Consequence: Safer if included.

Kessa Consequence: Safer, but easier to locate.

Tower Access Consequence: Witness scan in Forecourt marks them protected.

Transition: Marik urges the party not to waste the protection.

### 6. Party Named Reckless Validators

Conditions: Legal Pressure 4+, poor handling of evidence, or activated debt with weak consent argument.

Read-Aloud Ruling Text:

> "The Court finds predatory structure, but also reckless validation. The respondents are not debtors in full. They are warned and marked."

Mechanical Consequence: Debt reduced to a 25 NC administrative bond, payable or appealable. Legal mark remains until Session 5 ends.

NC Consequence: Pay 25 NC, accept a sponsor bond, or enter Tower with Debt-Flagged Registration.

Reputation Consequence: -1 Ledger precision, +1 public sympathy if witnesses were protected.

Faction Consequence: Guild calls them careless; CodeX calls them useful chaos.

Sel Consequence: Sel apologizes and loses confidence.

Kessa Consequence: Kessa may flee if unprotected.

Tower Access Consequence: Debt-Flagged or Probationary Registration.

Transition: Ira says the ruling is survivable, not clean.

### 7. Settlement Accepted

Conditions: Party signs settlement knowingly, accepts relief over public ruling, or loses confidence under pressure.

Read-Aloud Ruling Text:

> Orvan looks over the signed terms. "The Court records voluntary settlement. Enforcement follows the written compromise, not the original parcel."

Mechanical Consequence: Debt becomes whatever the settlement states, usually 15 NC now and one future First Step delivery obligation.

NC Consequence: Immediate 15 NC payment or service bond; if unpaid, registration debt flag.

Reputation Consequence: No public victory; factions read the party as negotiable.

Faction Consequence: Guild relaxes; CodeX is annoyed; Ira warns them to document everything.

Sel Consequence: If Sel was not protected, he feels abandoned.

Kessa Consequence: Kessa avoids testimony and remains vulnerable.

Tower Access Consequence: Sponsored or Debt-Flagged Registration depending on terms.

Transition: Vane smiles for the first time.

### 8. Appeal Required

Conditions: Evidence is weak, Legal Pressure high, or key witness missing, but Orvan sees enough concern to avoid enforcement.

Read-Aloud Ruling Text:

> "The Court will not enforce today. It will not void today. This matter is appealed to a higher docket."

Mechanical Consequence: Debt paused for 3 days; appeal clock begins.

NC Consequence: Certified appeal copy costs 10 NC; Ira may waive it if helped.

Reputation Consequence: Public sees uncertainty.

Faction Consequence: Every faction tries to shape the next move.

Sel Consequence: Safe for 3 days.

Kessa Consequence: Must choose whether to remain under protection.

Tower Access Consequence: Probationary Registration available.

Transition: The party can enter the Tower before appeal, but risk returns when they exit.

### 9. Vane Escapes Cleanly But Exposed Publicly

Conditions: Party proves false debt but not Vane's legal link, and Public Legitimacy 4+.

Read-Aloud Ruling Text:

> "The Court voids the respondent obligation. It does not find Merrit Vane liable on this record."

Mechanical Consequence: Debt voided; Vane not legally touched.

NC Consequence: 20 NC compensation.

Reputation Consequence: +1 public reputation; Vane's personal hostility increases.

Faction Consequence: Guild contains the scandal; Wardens watch Vane; CodeX publishes hints.

Sel Consequence: Free.

Kessa Consequence: Afraid because Vane walked.

Tower Access Consequence: Clean Registration, but sponsor pressure increases.

Transition: Vane tells Seraphex, within earshot, "The Tower will educate them."

### 10. Vane's Representative Overreaches and Creates New Evidence

Conditions: Party catches Seraphex in contradiction, false claim, or witness intimidation.

Read-Aloud Ruling Text:

> Twelve-Bells rings before Orvan speaks. The magistrate's eyes sharpen. "The representative's statement is admitted against First Step interest. The Court thanks counsel for clarifying what the evidence suggested."

Mechanical Consequence: Evidence Strength +1 before ruling; choose Full Void, Void With Investigation, or Protected Witnesses.

NC Consequence: +10 NC additional cost award.

Reputation Consequence: +1 Ledger, +1 public delight.

Faction Consequence: Guild furious but cautious; Seraphex blames the party.

Sel Consequence: Gains confidence.

Kessa Consequence: Sees that powerful people can be caught.

Tower Access Consequence: Clean or Sponsored Registration.

Transition: Ira asks the party to leave before Seraphex regains composure.

## Level 2 Transition

Default recommendation: award level 2 immediately after the Contract Hall ruling if the table wants the Nexus opener to advance the active character. This does not make the party ready for the true Spire Floor 1. Level 2 is enough to survive more Nexus trouble and begin portal-world play; it is not enough to treat The Executioner as fair progression.

Read or paraphrase:

> The blue seal fades from the chamber, but some of its light stays in you. Your life counter brightens. For a breath, the numbers beside your name look less like a warning and more like a promise: you are still here, and the Nexus has noticed.

The Nexus display shows: `ASCENT CAPACITY UPDATED. FIELD COMPETENCY: LEVEL 2.`

NPC comments:

- GUIDY: "I updated your profile. I did not enjoy being worried. I am told that is normal."
- Marik: "Good. Maybe now the Tower only scares you properly."
- Ira: "Do not mistake recognition for safety. But take the recognition."
- Vane, if present: "Congratulations. The first rung is cheap."

If the table already leveled at the end of Chunk 01, do not award another level. Instead grant one of these:

- 25 NC divided among the party.
- One certified legal access copy.
- One extraction beacon rental discount.
- Advantage on the first registration complication check.

Rest guidance: After the hearing, the party can take a short rest immediately. A long rest is available if they spend the night in safe lodging, accept Warden witness housing, or stay at Convergence Point under Aria's watch. If they are heat-flagged, a long rest still works, but one downtime scene begins with pressure.

New faction messages after level-up:

- Guardian Wardens offer a registration caution.
- Pixel Prosperity Guild sends a polished sponsor invitation or a cold warning.
- Spire Seekers invite the party to declare ambition publicly.
- CodeX sends a crooked route mark and a laughing "nice bellwork."
- Ledger Court sends a certified ruling copy.

## Post-Hearing Downtime Beat

The downtime beat is short: a few hours to one night. It lets the party breathe, spend rewards, talk to allies, and decide how visible they want to be before Tower registration.

Where the party can rest:

- Convergence Point Tavern. Cheap, public, full of rumor. 2 NC per character for a cot and meal; Aria can comp it after a clean win.
- Warden Witness Rooms. Free if protected witnesses; safe but watched.
- Pixel Promenade capsule bunks. 3 NC per character; convenient for shopping but Guild eyes are everywhere.
- Last Light dormitory. Free with Mercy route or if a PC asks for aid; quiet and emotionally heavy.

What they can buy: Basic adventuring gear, legal copies, healing draughts, rations, maps, and Forecourt services listed later in this chunk.

Who contacts them: GUIDY, Ira, Marik, Aria, Felix, Kessa, CodeX, or a sponsor representative based on the ruling.

Time passing: If the party wants to enter the Tower immediately, let them reach Forecourt the same day. If they rest overnight, public rumor spreads and sponsor offers become sharper.

Rumors spreading:

- "They made the bell ring backward."
- "Vane lost money, not blood. That means he is still dangerous."
- "The Tower likes fresh names after Court days."
- "The Executioner terminal turned three novice teams around this week."

Prices changing: After a clean public win, common gear stays normal and legal copies are discounted. After messy public trouble, Warden gear checks cost time. After Debt Activated or Reckless Validator rulings, extraction rentals require a deposit.

Danger following them: First Step spotters, Guild observers, CodeX recruiters, or frightened witnesses needing escort.

Support gained: One faction may offer a concrete benefit before registration. Use the Sponsor and Faction Offers section during Session 5.

### Optional Downtime Scene 1. GUIDY Apology Update

Read-Aloud:

> GUIDY's icon appears in the corner of a blue-lit sign, then looks down as if it has feet to stare at. "I reviewed my orientation language. It was insufficiently terrifying."

NPC Goal: GUIDY wants to repair trust and warn the party that system advice is not the same as safety.

Player Choice: Accept help, tease GUIDY, demand better warnings, or ask about Aazoth.

Reward: GUIDY grants a `GUIDY Priority Ping`, allowing one simple procedural question during Session 5 with no roll.

Consequence: If treated cruelly, GUIDY still helps but sounds distant; GUIDY Trust decreases.

### Optional Downtime Scene 2. Aria's Public Song

Read-Aloud:

> Aria stands on a tavern table with no instrument in her hands. The room goes quiet anyway. She sings the word "consent" like a thrown knife and "mercy" like a bandage.

NPC Goal: Aria wants to turn the public story toward the party without making them look like her puppets.

Player Choice: Let her sing, ask her to soften details, join the performance, or keep their names out.

Reward: Public Legitimacy carries into Session 5 as +1 public attention if the song is allowed.

Consequence: If the party wants secrecy, Aria respects it, but the rumor becomes vaguer and easier for Vane to twist.

### Optional Downtime Scene 3. Felix's Private Offer
