Read-Aloud:

> Felix closes his stall curtain and flips three coins across his knuckles. "I sell maps. I also sell not dying because you bought the wrong map."

NPC Goal: Felix wants the party as customers and as a shield against Guild blame.

Player Choice: Buy a reliable map, ask what he fears, press him on counterfeit stock, or refuse entanglement.

Reward: Felix offers a reliable portal-gate primer for 15 NC instead of 25 NC after a clean or useful hearing.

Consequence: If insulted, Felix sells only public goods and later tells the Guild the party cannot be managed.

### Optional Downtime Scene 4. Marik's Warning

Read-Aloud:

> Marik Bluecoat waits under a lamp that makes every scratch in his armor look older. "You won enough to be noticed. That is not the same as being safe."

NPC Goal: Marik wants the party to register legally and avoid giving Wardens a reason to restrain them.

Player Choice: Ask about heat, request Warden escort, confess hidden evidence, or dismiss him.

Reward: Marik gives one Warden Gear Check pass that grants advantage on a Session 5 gear dispute.

Consequence: If ignored after public violence, Marik will still prevent lethal trouble but will not bend rules for them.

### Optional Downtime Scene 5. Kessa's Fear

Read-Aloud:

> Kessa keeps both hands around a cup she has not drunk from. "If I go home, they know. If I stay here, they know. If I enter the Tower, at least the danger has doors."

NPC Goal: Kessa wants protection without becoming a permanent burden.

Player Choice: Offer escort, connect her to Ira or Marik, invite her to wait at Forecourt, or press her for more evidence.

Reward: If protected, Kessa gives the party a `route-scrap`: advantage on one Code Cavern or registry-related check in a future Act I scene.

Consequence: If abandoned after she testified, Vane's people pressure her and her future testimony becomes harder.

### Optional Downtime Scene 6. CodeX's Illegal Alternative

Read-Aloud:

> A receipt on the table prints itself in black ink: `LEGAL DOORS ARE STILL DOORS. WANT A WINDOW? - X`

NPC Goal: CodeX wants to recruit the party into backdoor access and gather leverage against Ledger Court systems.

Player Choice: Accept a meeting, ignore it, report it to Marik, or send a counteroffer.

Reward: If they engage without committing, they learn one rumor about the Executioner Terminal: it suppresses older warnings.

Consequence: If they accept illegal help, Session 5 can use Codebreaker Backdoor Registration, increasing heat but opening alternate access.

## Session 5 Run Sheet: Tower Forecourt Registration

### What This Session Must Accomplish

- The party chooses whether to register cleanly, with a sponsor, under probation, or through a backdoor.
- The party confirms team name, roster, life counters, debt status, heat status, and emergency contact.
- The party sees the Tower as a civic ritual, not only a dungeon entrance.
- The party receives sponsor pressure from at least two factions.
- The party learns extraction is limited and imperfect.
- The party hears the Executioner Protocol warning.
- The session ends at the Executioner terminal or Threshold Door, where the safest expected early choice is to return and prepare through portal worlds.

### What the DM Tracks

Registration Pressure:

- 0: Staff are patient; the party can ask many questions.
- 1: Line pressure rises; one complication enters.
- 2: A sponsor or Warden forces a public choice.

Faction Recruitment:

- 0: Quiet offers only.
- 1: Two factions compete openly.
- 2: A faction makes acceptance or refusal visible to the crowd.

Public Attention:

- 0: Party is one team among many.
- 1: People recognize them from the hearing.
- 2: Names are whispered; rivals watch.

Tower Anxiety:

- 0: Party is steady.
- 1: One PC or NPC needs a grounding beat.
- 2: The Threshold Door reacts to fear, debt, or heat.

### Scene Order If Moving Fast

1. Permit Arches scan.
2. One sponsor offer.
3. Salvage Desk extraction briefing.
4. Executioner Terminal Warning.
5. Threshold Consent Scan.

### Scene Order If Roleplaying Heavily

1. Memorial Wall Moment.
2. Permit Arches and legal scan.
3. Sponsor Row walk with competing offers.
4. Shopping and gear check.
5. Salvage Desk extraction briefing.
6. Executioner Terminal Warning.
7. Quiet Bench of Last Calls.
8. Threshold Consent Scan.

### Do-Not-Forget List

- Ask for the team name.
- Confirm whether any debt or heat flag remains.
- Let sponsors offer help with visible strings.
- Make extraction sound useful but not guaranteed.
- Read the Executioner Protocol handout.
- Stop at the Threshold Door.

## Adventure: The Forecourt Does Not Cheer

The Tower Forecourt is where ambition becomes paperwork. The Nexus does not celebrate new entrants with trumpets. It scans them, prices them, warns them, recruits them, and asks them to consent.

### Adventure Overview

Level: 2 recommended for the Nexus opener. The registration scene can be run at level 1 safely because it is civic procedure, not the boss fight. Do not scale The Executioner down for these levels.

Expected Session Count: One session.

Primary Location: Tower Forecourt, the civic plaza at the base of the Tower of Ascension.

Main NPCs: GUIDY, Marik Bluecoat, Felix Pixelcoin, a Salvage Union extractor named Hesta Winch, Spire Seeker recruiter Vey Lumen, Ira Quill if the party carries legal flags, and a Sponsor Row representative tied to the party's ruling.

Main Factions: Guardian Wardens, Pixel Prosperity Guild, Spire Seekers, Salvage Union, Codebreakers, Ledger Court, Remnant Veil, Last Light Concord.

Central Conflict: The party must understand Tower access without accepting a disastrous sponsor obligation, ignoring a serious warning, or letting legal flags push them into a lethal ascent before they are ready.

Stakes: Registration status, extraction access, sponsor ties, gear readiness, public reputation, portal-world direction, and whether the party treats the Executioner warning as informed consent.

Rewards: legal access status, possible sponsor benefit, legal access copy, discounted service, faction contact, portal-world redirection, and the final consent prompt for the Executioner terminal.

Failure States: Temporary denial, debt-flagged registration, heat-flagged registration, illegal backdoor entry, sponsor entanglement, or delayed access.

### Background

Legal access to the Tower requires a recognized roster, visible life counter confirmation, debt scan, active warrant scan, consent statement, and emergency extraction preference. The Charter does not allow the Nexus to force a person into the Tower, but it does allow debt, probation, and sponsor contracts to shape the terms of entry.

The party's hearing outcome matters because the Tower reads civic status as risk. A clean ruling makes the doors open smoothly. A paused debt, reckless validator mark, active heat flag, or accepted settlement makes registration slower and gives sponsors leverage.

The Tower recognizes consent and debt because the Tower is tied to the same Charter logic as Contract Hall. The Tower cannot judge moral innocence, but it can detect whether a character is entering under coercion, hidden obligation, or contested legal pressure. It flags those states because Floor 100 requires a final consent architecture that cannot be built on fraudulent entry.

Sponsors appear now because a new team with public attention is valuable. Factions want early influence before the party's portal-world achievements and eventual Spire record become expensive to shape.

The Executioner Protocol warning matters because it is the first proof that the Tower is not a fair ladder of simple fights. Some floors contain autonomous enforcement patterns that punish assumptions. Forty-seven lives were lost learning enough to produce the warning, and even that warning is incomplete.

Rushing entry is dangerous because the party may lack extraction support, legal clarity, basic gear, or a shared plan for retreat. Let bold players enter; make the costs visible first.

## Tower Forecourt Location Chapter

### Area F1. Permit Arches

Read-Aloud:

> Three arches of blue stone stand before the Forecourt proper. Names ripple across them like fish under ice. Each entrant passes through alone, but every shadow comes out connected to the team behind them.

DM Details: The arches scan identity, life counter, debt status, heat, witness protection, and active sponsor claims. The scan is public enough for pressure but private enough that exact debt amounts appear only to the character and staff.

Exits: Back to Nexus streets, forward to Memorial Wall, side lane to Warden Gear Check.

NPCs Present: GUIDY kiosk-face, two permit clerks, Marik if Warden pressure exists.

Interactive Objects: Blue scan arch; brass name stylus; privacy curtain that glitches if heat is high.

Checks/DCs: Arcana DC 13 reads scan categories; Persuasion DC 14 requests privacy; Investigation DC 15 spots an old sponsor claim attached to a settlement.

Services/Prices: Legal scan free; printed registration summary 5 NC; privacy screen fee 3 NC unless protected witness.

Rumors: "The arch hates old names." "Debt walks in before you do."

Complications: A debt flag flashes; a sponsor representative claims pre-registration rights.

Faction Appearances: Ledger Court clerks verify protected status; Guild observers watch debt flags; Codebreakers test the arch from the crowd.

Hearing Outcome Reactions: Clean Win grants smooth scan. Debt Activated or Settlement Accepted adds a red `OBLIGATION REVIEW` band. Courier Dead adds `HEAT REVIEW`.

### Area F2. Memorial Wall

Read-Aloud:

> The wall is black glass set with thousands of pale names. Some names glow bright. Some have gone dim. A few are scratched out so deeply the scratches look fresh.

DM Details: The wall lists entrants who lost final lives or vanished under unresolved protocols. It is a solemn public space, guarded by custom more than force.

Exits: Permit Arches, Sponsor Row, Quiet Bench.

NPCs Present: Last Light Concord mourner, Spire Seeker recruit, Hesta Winch if extraction is discussed.

Interactive Objects: Name-glass panels; offering ledge; search glyph.

Checks/DCs: History DC 13 identifies famous ascendants; Religion DC 14 offers respectful words that calm Tower Anxiety; Investigation DC 15 finds the cluster of 47 Executioner Protocol names.

Services/Prices: Memorial rubbings 1 NC; last-letter storage 2 NC.

Rumors: "The scratched names are the ones the Tower denies." "The forty-seven marks are not decoration."

Complications: A grieving local accuses the party of treating the Tower like sport; a Spire Seeker dares them to speak their ambition aloud.

Faction Appearances: Last Light Concord offers quiet support; Spire Seekers turn grief into challenge.

Hearing Outcome Reactions: Publicly accused Guild teams draw whispers; protected witnesses draw sympathy; heat-flagged parties draw suspicion.

### Area F3. Sponsor Row

Read-Aloud:

> Bright awnings line the Forecourt in a precise crescent. Every banner promises safety, profit, glory, truth, or a clean way out. Every table has a contract weight.

DM Details: Sponsor Row is a social battlefield. Factions offer small benefits now in exchange for first claim on reports, salvage, reputation, or favors.

Exits: Permit Arches, Supply Booth, Recruitment Plinth, Salvage Desk.

NPCs Present: Sponsor representatives, Felix, Vey Lumen, Hesta, Last Light advocate, Codebreaker courier.

Interactive Objects: Contract weights; sponsor banners; public comparison slate.

Checks/DCs: Insight DC 13 spots hidden cost; Persuasion DC 15 improves a term; Investigation DC 14 compares contracts; Performance DC 13 deflects public pressure.

Services/Prices: Sponsor contract filing free; independent filing copy 5 NC.

Rumors: "The best sponsor is the one that expects you to die last." "Independent teams pay with bruises."

Complications: Two sponsors speak over each other; a hostile Guild observer names the party reckless.

Faction Appearances: All major factions can appear here.

Hearing Outcome Reactions: Clean winners get polite bids. Messy winners get controlling bids. Debt-flagged parties get predatory bids unless Ira or Marik intervenes.

### Area F4. Salvage Union Extraction Desk

Read-Aloud:

> A counter of dented iron is covered in hooks, whistles, clipped ropes, and cracked beacons. Behind it, a woman with forearms like winches stamps a form without looking up. "Extraction is a promise to try. Anyone selling more is lying."

DM Details: Hesta Winch explains extraction limits. The Union can retrieve bodies, gear, or conscious teams from approved extraction points, not anywhere inside the Tower.

Exits: Sponsor Row, Gear Check, Threshold Door lane.

NPCs Present: Hesta Winch, two tired haulers, anxious novice team.

Interactive Objects: Beacon rack; extraction map; injury ledger.

Checks/DCs: Medicine DC 13 understands common injuries; Survival DC 14 reads extraction zones; Persuasion DC 13 gets Hesta's blunt advice; Investigation DC 15 notices a recent failed Executioner extraction spike.

Services/Prices: Extraction beacon rental 20 NC deposit and 8 NC fee; body retrieval bond 15 NC; gear tag 3 NC per pack.

Rumors: "The Executioner teaches funerals." "The first beacon is always worth more than the first sword."

Complications: Beacon shortage; a team returns half-covered in silver dust.

Faction Appearances: Salvage Union pushes practical survival; Wardens inspect beacon abuse.

Hearing Outcome Reactions: Protected witnesses get reduced deposit. Debt-flagged parties pay full deposit. Heat-flagged parties must name an emergency contact.

### Area F5. Warden Gear Check

Read-Aloud:

> A blue line marks the inspection lane. Weapons, packs, bottles, scroll cases, and suspiciously innocent lunchboxes pass under a hovering seal. A Warden says, "The Tower may kill you. Contraband makes it creative."

DM Details: Wardens check banned items: active debt-binding contracts, explosive public hazards, malicious witness gems, unstable Code Cavern devices, and forged access seals. Normal adventuring gear passes.

Exits: Permit Arches, Supply Booth, Threshold Door lane.

NPCs Present: Marik or another Bluecoat, gear clerk, impatient team.

Interactive Objects: Hovering seal; evidence return tray; contraband lockbox.

Checks/DCs: Persuasion DC 13 clarifies a questionable item; Arcana DC 14 identifies unstable magic; Sleight of Hand DC 15 hides harmless-but-embarrassing goods, but failure raises heat; thieves' tools DC 15 secures a pack after inspection.

Services/Prices: Contraband hold 2 NC; gear certification 5 NC; Warden witness seal free for protected witnesses.

Rumors: "Someone tried to carry a debt imp through last week." "The Tower eats forged badges."

Complications: A false positive on CodeX gear; a rival team accuses the party of smuggling.

Faction Appearances: Wardens have authority; Codebreakers test limits; Guild complains about delays.

Hearing Outcome Reactions: Courier Dead or public violence triggers deeper inspection. Clean Win grants quick line.

### Area F6. Pixel Prosperity Supply Booth

Read-Aloud:

> The booth is all polished glass, brass corners, and prices written large enough to look honest. Felix stands beside it, not behind it, as if ready to deny ownership at speed.

DM Details: The Guild booth sells reliable basics and suspicious discounts. Felix may help or mislead depending on the hearing.

Exits: Sponsor Row, Gear Check, Recruitment Plinth.

NPCs Present: Felix, Guild cashier, hostile Guild observer if pressure remains.

Interactive Objects: Map drawer; seal scale; price slate.

Checks/DCs: Insight DC 13 catches bad advice; Investigation DC 14 identifies counterfeit map; Persuasion DC 14 gets Felix's private warning; forgery kit DC 15 spots copied legal access seals.

Services/Prices: See shopping table.

Rumors: "The Guild never sells a map without selling a story." "Reliable maps are reliable until the Tower notices."

Complications: Discount tied to sponsor clause; public insult from Guild observer.

Faction Appearances: Pixel Prosperity Guild makes offers here; Spire Seekers mock paid caution.

Hearing Outcome Reactions: Clean route gives a guarded discount. Public accusation makes the booth icy. Siding with Felix makes him personally useful.

### Area F7. Spire Seeker Recruitment Plinth

Read-Aloud:

> A white stone plinth rises above the crowd. Its stairs are shallow enough for speeches and too high for humility. A banner reads: ASCENT BELONGS TO THOSE WHO SAY YES.

DM Details: The Spire Seekers recruit through public challenge. They admire courage, dislike hesitation, and can offer glory-driven support.

Exits: Sponsor Row, Supply Booth, Memorial Wall.

NPCs Present: Vey Lumen, two young runners, public watchers.

Interactive Objects: Challenge bell; oath ribbon; ascent slate.

Checks/DCs: Performance DC 13 makes a strong declaration; Insight DC 14 sees which promise is a trap; Persuasion DC 15 negotiates a less public pledge; History DC 13 recalls a failed Seeker expedition.

Services/Prices: Public sponsor oath free; private coaching 5 NC; rally token free if accepted.

Rumors: "Seekers die smiling, which is not the same as winning." "They know the Tower moods better than the Guild admits."

Complications: Public challenge to enter unsponsored; rival team mocks the party's legal trouble.

Faction Appearances: Spire Seekers dominate, with Last Light Concord quietly disapproving.

Hearing Outcome Reactions: Messy wins draw Seeker interest; clean legal wins draw a challenge to prove they are more than clever.

### Area F8. Quiet Bench of Last Calls

Read-Aloud:

> The bench faces the Tower but is turned slightly away from the crowd. Small message tokens hang from the rail, each glowing with a name, a promise, or an apology no one has opened yet.

DM Details: Entrants record emergency messages, goodbyes, or last instructions. It is a powerful place for roleplay before the threshold.

Exits: Memorial Wall, Threshold Door lane.

NPCs Present: Last Light advocate, GUIDY icon, possibly Kessa or Sel.

Interactive Objects: Message tokens; privacy veil; old carved initials.

Checks/DCs: Religion DC 12 creates a calming rite; Insight DC 13 notices a companion's fear; Arcana DC 14 learns message tokens trigger on final life loss; Persuasion DC 13 helps an NPC make a call.

Services/Prices: Emergency message token 4 NC; last-call meal voucher 2 NC.

Rumors: "Some messages answer before the sender dies." "The Spire terminal remembers who said ACKNOWLEDGE RISK."

Complications: A PC sees a familiar name; a frightened novice asks the party if entry is worth it.

Faction Appearances: Last Light Concord offers emotional care; Remnant Veil watches for people with unfinished business.

Hearing Outcome Reactions: Protected witnesses may record sealed messages; heat-flagged parties attract Warden attention.

### Area F9. Executioner Terminal

Read-Aloud:

> The terminal is a black monolith with no ornament except forty-seven small life-counter marks etched down one side. When you approach, the marks light one by one.

DM Details: The terminal shares the true Floor 1 warning: The Executioner waits beyond the first real Spire threshold. It is not a later-floor rumor, not a metaphor, and not a tutorial lesson. Its purpose in early play is to make informed consent possible and to redirect unprepared parties toward portal-world preparation.

Exits: Sponsor Row, Memorial Wall, Threshold Door.

NPCs Present: GUIDY, Hesta, Vey, Marik, faction observers.

Interactive Objects: Warning screen; life mark column; query slot.

Checks/DCs: Arcana DC 15 reads suppressed fragments; History DC 14 identifies old expedition names; Insight DC 13 reads NPC reactions; Religion DC 15 senses the warning is partly mercy, partly threat.

Services/Prices: Printed warning free; certified expedition warning copy 5 NC.

Rumors: "The terminal says 23 percent and still sounds optimistic." "The 47 are the reason veterans stop talking here."

Complications: A sponsor tries to minimize the warning; a novice panics and leaves.

Faction Appearances: Every faction spins the warning.

Hearing Outcome Reactions: Debt-flagged parties see an extra line: `COERCED ENTRY INCREASES PURSUIT RISK.` Clean parties see standard warning. Codebreaker entries see a flicker: `UNREGISTERED PATHS ARE NOT UNWATCHED.`

### Area F10. Threshold Door

Read-Aloud:

> The Tower door is not tall. That is the worst part. It looks like a door a person could open by accident: dark wood, blue metal bands, one handle, and a thin line of white light under it.

DM Details: The door verifies team oath, consent, roster, life counters, debt flags, heat flags, sponsor declarations, and final entry readiness. In this repaired structure, it leads to the Executioner risk decision, not to a nonlethal tutorial.

Exits: Back to Forecourt, sideways to portal-world gates through the registrar lane, forward to the Executioner threshold only after ACKNOWLEDGE RISK.

NPCs Present: GUIDY, final registrar, any sponsor representative, Marik if heat exists.

Interactive Objects: Door handle; consent plate; team-name ring; life counter beam.

Checks/DCs: Arcana DC 14 reads Tower response; Persuasion DC 13 calms a teammate or NPC; Insight DC 15 senses the door is testing honest consent; Investigation DC 13 confirms the roster.

Services/Prices: Final registration free; delayed re-entry appointment 5 NC if they walk away after scan.

Rumors: "The door remembers first words." "Never joke during consent."

Complications: Debt flag asks for acknowledgement; heat flag summons Warden witness; sponsor contract demands verbal recognition.

Faction Appearances: Accepted sponsors stand close. Refused sponsors watch from the line.

Hearing Outcome Reactions: Clean Registration opens with blue light. Probationary opens with amber. Debt-Flagged opens with red text. Illegal entry causes the handle to become cold and silent.

## Tower Registration Procedure

Run these steps in order unless players interrupt. Each step should feel like a ritual with paperwork, not a menu.

| Step | Table-Facing Prompt | DM Truth | Possible Issue | Check/DC If Contested | Consequence |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Team name | "State the name under which the Tower will record your ascent." | Names become searchable and gain symbolic weight | Joke name, duplicate name, faction-owned name | Persuasion DC 12 to reserve contested name; History DC 13 to know prior use | Name accepted, altered, or flagged |
| Party roster | "Name each entrant and confirm shared entry." | Roster binds team entry and exit records | Missing ally, NPC joining, split party | Investigation DC 12 to correct record | Unlisted entrants cannot use team benefits |
| Life counter confirmation | "Show active counters." | Tower reads life-state and anomalies | Sel-like anomaly, hidden curse, counter flicker | Arcana DC 14 or Medicine DC 13 | Counter anomaly noted; may delay entry |
| Debt scan | "Declare active debt, paused debt, or disputed obligation." | Tower detects civic debt but not all private promises | False debt remains, settlement bond, sponsor lien | Legal Cant or Persuasion DC 14 | Debt flag, probation, or cleared scan |
| Witness scan | "Declare protected witness or protected evidence status." | Protects against retaliation but increases attention | Kessa/Sel included or hidden | Persuasion DC 13 | Witness protection follows into Forecourt record |
| Consent statement | "Say whether you enter freely." | Coerced entry destabilizes Tower record | Debt pressure, threat, sponsor coercion | Insight DC 13 to identify coercion; Persuasion DC 14 to pause | Entry paused or consent recorded |
| Emergency contact | "Name who receives notice if extraction fails." | Contact anchors final-life message and retrieval | No contact, false name, enemy named | No roll unless contested; Deception DC 15 for false contact | Contact recorded; false contact increases heat if found |
| Extraction preference | "Choose body, gear, both, or none for retrieval priority." | Extraction resources are limited | Party refuses, cannot pay deposit | Persuasion DC 13 for reduced fee | Retrieval priority set |
| Sponsor declaration | "Declare sponsor, independent status, or pending offer." | Sponsor terms bind rewards and duties | Hidden contract, public refusal | Insight DC 13; Investigation DC 14 | Sponsor benefit or independent flag |
| Banned items | "Submit restricted items for hold or clearance." | Prevents civic hazards, not normal weapons | CodeX device, debt imp, forged seal | Arcana or Persuasion DC 14 | Item held, cleared, or heat raised |
| Active warrants/heat | "Confirm legal heat." | Heat changes Warden response on exit | Courier death, public violence, illegal evidence | Persuasion DC 15 or Marik support | Heat-Flagged Registration or probation |
| Charter warning | "Hear and acknowledge Consent, Truth, Mercy, and risk." | Tower requires informed entry | Players mock or rush | No roll; Insight DC 12 sees registrar concern | Warning recorded |
| Final consent | "Place hand on the plate and say yes or step back." | Final consent opens threshold transition | One PC hesitates | Persuasion DC 13 to support; no roll to wait | Entry, delay, or roster adjustment |

## Sponsor and Faction Offers

Each offer is valid for one registration day unless the party has a direct faction bond.

| Faction | What They Offer Now | What They Ask Now | Hidden Cost | Visible Benefit | If Accepted | If Refused | If Publicly Insulted | Change by Hearing Outcome |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Guardian Wardens | Warden witness seal, gear check pass, one emergency call | Report illegal contracts found in portal worlds or future Spire attempts | Warden scrutiny on return | Advantage on one heat or gear dispute | Marik stands near registration | Marik remains neutral | Heat checks become stricter | Clean or protected witness outcomes improve offer; courier death makes it colder |
| Pixel Prosperity Guild | Discounted gear and map bundle | First right to appraise unusual loot | They shape item prices | 10 percent off one purchase | Felix helps if friendly | Guild watches purchases | Prices rise by 10 percent | Public accusation makes offer predatory; siding with Felix improves it |
| Spire Seekers | Rally token and public support | Public oath to pursue ascent boldly | Retreat looks shameful | Advantage on one fear or morale check in Forecourt | Vey praises party | Seeker rivals needle them | Public challenge escalates | Messy win increases interest; settlement lowers respect |
| Salvage Union | Reduced extraction deposit | Register retrieval rights clearly | Union claims abandoned gear after deadline | Beacon deposit reduced by 5 NC | Hesta marks their packs | Full price | Extraction priority drops | Protected witness or clean win earns trust |
| Codebreakers | Backdoor scan, hidden route rumor | Carry a data splinter into the Tower | Heat and trust risk | Bypass one registration delay | Codebreaker Backdoor Registration possible | They leave a mocking note | They may expose an embarrassing scan | Siding with CodeX strengthens; Warden alignment weakens |
| Ledger Court | Certified ruling copy and legal access seal | Report contract anomalies found in Tower | Court can subpoena later | Advantage on one debt or consent challenge | Ira files clean paperwork | Standard paperwork | Clerks become chilly | Strong legal win improves; appeal required makes it conditional |
| Remnant Veil | Quiet omen reading and death-right guidance | Bring back names from the Memorial Wall if found | Emotional obligations and secrets | Advantage on one death/life-counter lore check | Veil contact appears later | No immediate cost | They vanish and later test the party | Mercy route improves offer; public cruelty removes it |
| Last Light Concord | Healing support and witness shelter | Protect frightened entrants and return messages | Moral pressure to rescue over profit | One minor healing draught or rest support | Concord advocate blesses entry | They still offer compassion | Public sympathy drops | Mercy and protected witness outcomes improve offer |

## Tower Forecourt Shopping and Services

Prices assume level 2 characters with modest NC from Chunk 01-02. Raise deposits by 5 NC for debt-flagged parties or reduce by 5 NC for protected witnesses when noted.

| Item or Service | Price in NC | Seller | Mechanical Effect | Limit | Warning | Faction Discount |
|---|---:|---|---|---|---|---|
| Extraction beacon rental | 8 NC fee plus 20 NC deposit | Salvage Union | Action to activate at approved extraction point; alerts Union after 1 minute | 1 per party | Does not work in sealed boss spaces or unknown pockets | Salvage Union reduces deposit by 5 NC |
| Blue-zone salve | 6 NC | Last Light Concord | One use; spend 1 minute to let a creature spend a Hit Die without resting | 2 per party | Useless on final-life loss | Last Light gives one free after Mercy route |
| Route chalk | 3 NC | Salvage Union | Advantage on one Survival check to retrace route | 3 sticks | Tower rain, slime, or glitching can erase it | None |
| Witness-sealed pack | 5 NC | Ledger Court | Advantage on one check proving pack contents were not tampered with | 1 per character | Makes contraband obvious | Ledger waives fee for protected witnesses |
| Minor healing draught | 10 NC | Last Light or Guild booth | Heals 1d4 + 1 hp as an action | 2 per character | Counts as potion for action economy | Last Light 2 NC discount |
| Antitoxin patch | 8 NC | Warden booth | Advantage on next save against poison within 1 hour | 1 per character | Must be applied before or immediately after exposure | Warden discount 2 NC |
| Tower ration | 1 NC | Many sellers | One day's food; does not spoil during portal travel or Spire staging | No strict limit | Cheap rations taste metallic | None |
| Rope and anchor kit | 12 NC | Salvage Union | 50 ft. rope, collapsible anchor; advantage on one safe anchoring check | 1 per party | Anchor can jam if abandoned | Salvage Union 3 NC discount |
| Cheap map | 5 NC | Guild booth or street seller | Reveals public portal-gate or Forecourt rumors | Unlimited | One false route mark | None |
| Reliable portal primer | 25 NC | Felix | Grants advantage on one check to choose or prepare for a portal world | 1 per party | Does not apply inside the Spire | Felix may sell for 15 NC |
| Counterfeit map | 3 NC | Street seller | Looks useful; imposes disadvantage on first navigation check unless detected | Unlimited | Investigation DC 13 spots fake | None |
| Legal access copy | 5 NC | Ledger Court | Advantage on one registration dispute tied to ruling | 1 per character | Must match current ruling | Ledger free after Full Void |
| Emergency message token | 4 NC | Quiet Bench | Sends a recorded message if final life is lost or extraction fails | 1 per character | Cannot send tactical updates | Last Light 1 NC discount |
| Last-call meal | 2 NC | Forecourt vendors | Grants 1 temporary hp until next long rest | 1 per character | Does not stack with itself | None |
| Armor repair | 8 NC | Warden-approved smith | Repairs damaged armor; next critical hit against wearer does not worsen damage state if using equipment wear | 1 item | No effect on magical curses | Warden 2 NC discount |
| Weapon tune-up | 6 NC | Guild booth | First natural 1 with tuned weapon during the next registered expedition does not damage weapon | 1 weapon | No bonus to attack | Guild 2 NC discount |
| Spell focus calibration | 10 NC | Ledger arcanist | Advantage on one Arcana check to identify Tower magic | 1 focus | Calibration pings during illicit magic scans | Ledger 2 NC discount |
| Executioner readiness consultation | 12 NC | Spire Seekers or Salvage Union | Ask three prep questions about the Executioner terminal and receive blunt practical answers | 1 per party | Does not make low-level entry safe | Spire or Salvage discount 4 NC |

## The True Spire Floor 1: The Executioner

The Executioner is the actual Floor 1 guardian of the Spire. It is a CR 10 extreme threat, not a tutorial boss, not a symbolic warning, and not a softened first-floor lesson. It is a gatekeeping raid-style encounter designed to kill unprepared climbers.

DM-facing truth: The Spire's first real test is whether a character respects a clear warning. Low-level parties are not expected to defeat The Executioner. If they enter anyway, run the threat honestly. The campaign should support death, retreat, extraction attempts, NPC rescue attempts, public shame, and legendary unlikely success without weakening the boss into a fair level-2 encounter.

Known Executioner canon:

- Large fiend/demon, CR 10, AC 17, HP 185.
- Death Sentence Protocol at half hit points.
- Executioner's Presence suppresses low-level healing and worsens death saves.
- Magic Resistance and Legendary Resistance.
- Multiattack with Judgment Blade and Condemning Grasp.
- Grapples isolated targets and uses Execution Protocol to drop grappled targets to 0 hp.
- Chains of Judgment restrain creatures in a 30-foot radius.
- Legendary actions and lair actions.
- Arena includes lightning strikes, shifting terrain, and spectral witnesses.

The intended early campaign response is preparation through portal worlds: magical weapons, anti-grapple tools, freedom of movement, burst healing, lightning protection, anti-fear support, extraction upgrades, followers, tactical intelligence, and preserved backup lives.

Full runnable Executioner content belongs in the later Spire Floor 1 chunk. This repair section establishes the canon and prevents the early campaign from treating the Spire as a level-2 path.

## Executioner Terminal Warning

This is a major Forecourt scene. It should make players seriously consider returning to the Nexus and choosing a portal world before entering the Spire.

Read-Aloud Terminal Text:

> The black terminal wakes when your life counters near it. Forty-seven etched marks glow along its side, each one briefly becoming a name before the light cuts out.
>
> A flat voice speaks from inside the stone.
>
> "SPIRE FLOOR 1 ACCESS. EXECUTIONER PROTOCOL. DANGER LEVEL: EXTREME. Lives lost gathering this intelligence: forty-seven. Recorded success rate: twenty-three percent."
>
> The terminal pauses.
>
> "Type or speak ACKNOWLEDGE RISK to proceed. Type or speak RETURN to exit to the Central Nexus."

### Player Handout: Executioner Protocol Warning

```
SPIRE TERMINAL - FLOOR 1 ACCESS
EXECUTIONER PROTOCOL

DANGER LEVEL: EXTREME
Lives Lost Gathering This Intelligence: 47
Recorded Success Rate: 23%

THREAT DESIGNATION: THE EXECUTIONER

Visual Confirmation:
Massive humanoid entity, approximately 12 feet tall.
Dark armor-like carapace.
Glowing red sensory organs.
Oversized blade weapon.
Flight capable.

Environmental Data:
Arena configuration: circular chamber, 120 feet diameter.
Weather effects: periodic lightning strikes.
Terrain shifts: confirmed.
Spectral manifestations: previous victims appear as psychological warfare.

Tactical Observations:
Entity becomes significantly more dangerous when wounded.
Grappling attacks precede execution attempts.
Spectral chains restrain targets.
Standard weapons show reduced effectiveness.
Magic resistance confirmed.
Healing abilities are significantly reduced in proximity.
Death saving throws are compromised by entity presence.
Entity separates and executes isolated targets.

Minimum Recommended:
Party Size: 4-6 individuals.
Experience Level: intermediate or higher.
Emergency Extraction Plan: mandatory.
Backup Lives Available: at least 2 per party member.

Equipment Suggestions:
Magical weapons preferred.
Freedom of movement capabilities.
Burst healing reserves.
Lightning protection recommended.
Anti-fear support recommended.

Extraction Procedures:
Emergency extraction is available but must be activated manually.
Incapacitated parties cannot be auto-extracted.
Extraction may result in temporary Spire access restriction.

ENTRY AUTHORIZATION REQUIRED:
Type or speak ACKNOWLEDGE RISK to proceed to Floor 1.
Type or speak RETURN to exit to Central Nexus.

Remember: In the Spire, death has meaning.
Choose your battles wisely.
```

### DM-Only Analysis

The terminal is not exaggerating. The Executioner is on Floor 1. The warning exists to redirect unprepared characters toward portal worlds, faction support, followers, equipment, extraction upgrades, and preserved lives.

What the terminal reveals plainly:

- The threat is named The Executioner.
- The danger level is Extreme.
- The recorded success rate is 23%.
- Forty-seven lives were lost gathering the intelligence.
- The arena is a 120-foot circular chamber with lightning, shifting terrain, and spectral victims.
- The creature grapples, restrains, isolates, suppresses healing, worsens death saves, resists magic, and becomes more dangerous when wounded.
- Entry requires ACKNOWLEDGE RISK.

What the terminal does not solve:

- It does not tell the party how to win at low level.
- It does not provide a safe practice version.
- It does not guarantee extraction.
- It does not prevent foolish entry.

NPC reactions:

- GUIDY becomes quiet and says, "I recommend RETURN. I am not being dramatic."
- Marik says, "That warning is written in lives, not policy."
- Felix says, "If you are shopping for that fight today, I am selling funeral discounts, not hero gear."
- Hesta Winch says, "A beacon is a hand reaching for you. It is not a god."
- Vey Lumen of the Spire Seekers says, "Glory starts with knowing what can kill you."
- Ira Quill says, "Acknowledgement is not consent if you do not understand the terms. Read it again."

Faction spins:

- Guardian Wardens: Return, prepare, and do not create a rescue crisis.
- Pixel Prosperity Guild: Sponsorship can help, but only with real investment.
- Spire Seekers: Preparation makes glory possible.
- Salvage Union: Extraction plans are mandatory and still imperfect.
- Codebreakers: The public record may omit details, but the danger is real.
- Ledger Court: ACKNOWLEDGE RISK creates a clean record of informed entry.
- Last Light Concord: Backup lives are not disposable.
- Remnant Veil: The forty-seven dead are part of the warning.

Player questions and checks:

- "Is The Executioner really Floor 1?" No roll required. Yes.
- "Can we beat it at level 2?" No roll required. The terminal's recommendation says no. A DC 12 Insight or History check confirms survivors are describing mid-tier tactics and gear.
- "Can extraction save us?" Arcana or Survival DC 14: Extraction can help only if activated manually and defended.
- "What gear matters most?" Investigation DC 13: Magical weapons, anti-grapple/freedom effects, burst healing, lightning protection, anti-fear support, and emergency extraction.
- "Can followers help?" History or Persuasion DC 14: Yes, if unlocked, willing, Tower-eligible, and the table uses follower-risk rules.
- "What should we do first?" GUIDY, Marik, Hesta, or a portal custodian can point toward portal worlds and preparation arcs.

## What If They Rush the Tower Anyway?

Let them choose. Do not protect the premise by silently locking the door, and do not betray the premise by weakening The Executioner into a tutorial.

Run this sequence:

1. Show the terminal warning.
2. Ask whether they choose RETURN or ACKNOWLEDGE RISK.
3. Confirm out of character that this is an extreme-threat encounter and not balanced for low-level characters.
4. If they proceed, run the real threat from the Executioner canon.
5. Use established extraction and return rules only. Do not invent a free escape.
6. If they die, mark the life loss honestly.
7. If followers die, make it matter.
8. If they retreat, show public consequences: concern, mockery, Warden reports, sponsor pressure, Salvage Union bills, and renewed portal-world recommendations.
9. If they somehow survive, let it be legendary. Award the public shock, access, and reputation such a victory deserves.

Do not fudge away the Spire's premise. The Spire is allowed to be terrifying because the campaign gives players portal worlds, allies, gear, and time to prepare.

## Forecourt Encounters

### Encounter 1. Sponsor Pressure Walk

Goal: Present faction offers without letting contracts swallow the session.

Setup: As the party crosses Sponsor Row, two to four factions approach based on the hearing outcome.

Read-Aloud:

> Every awning seems to lean toward you. A Warden seal glows blue. A Guild contract weight gleams gold. A Spire Seeker smiles like a dare. Someone from the crowd says your team name before you have decided whether to like it.

NPCs: Marik or Warden rep, Felix or Guild rep, Vey Lumen, Hesta, Codebreaker courier.

Player Options: Accept one offer, refuse all, negotiate terms, ask for written copies, pit factions against each other.

Checks/DCs: Insight DC 13 spots hidden cost; Investigation DC 14 compares terms; Persuasion DC 15 improves a term; Performance DC 13 refuses without losing face.

Success: Party gains one benefit without extra obligation.

Partial Success: Party gains benefit but owes a report, public statement, or salvage preference.

Failure: Faction Recruitment +1 and the next sponsor makes terms more public.

Rewards: Sponsor benefit, discount, contact, or clean independent declaration.

Consequences: Accepted sponsors shape Tower Access Outcome Package.

Faction Reactions: Accepted faction warms; refused faction watches; insulted faction complicates registration.

Shorten: Offer two contracts: practical Warden/Salvage and ambitious Guild/Spire.

### Encounter 2. Memorial Wall Moment

Goal: Ground Tower entry emotionally and introduce the 47 lives before the terminal.

Setup: The party passes the wall. A mourner or Last Light advocate asks whether they want to leave a message.

Read-Aloud:

> The names on the wall do not shout. They do not need to. The black glass holds them at eye level, and for a moment the Forecourt noise feels disrespectful.

NPCs: Last Light advocate, mourner, possibly Sel or Kessa.

Player Options: Search names, leave offering, record message, comfort mourner, walk past.

Checks/DCs: Religion DC 12 offers comfort; History DC 13 identifies an old expedition; Investigation DC 15 finds 47 related names; Insight DC 13 reads a companion's fear.

Success: Tower Anxiety -1 or clue toward Executioner warning.

Partial Success: Emotional beat lands, but a faction uses it for pressure.

Failure: No penalty unless mocked; mocking raises Public Attention and lowers Last Light reputation.

Rewards: Last Light token, clue, or advantage on a later fear-related check.

Consequences: The party's attitude toward death becomes public.

Faction Reactions: Last Light approves care; Spire Seekers approve courage; Guild ignores grief unless useful.

Shorten: Read the wall, offer one question, move on.

### Encounter 3. Salvage Desk Extraction Briefing

Goal: Teach extraction limits before the party needs them.

Setup: Hesta Winch gives the party a blunt briefing at the Salvage Union desk.

Read-Aloud:

> Hesta places a cracked beacon on the counter. "This one worked. The person holding it did not. Learn the difference before you rent anything."

NPCs: Hesta, anxious novice team, Salvage clerk.

Player Options: Rent beacon, ask about Executioner extraction limits, tag gear, refuse, negotiate deposit, or ask which portal worlds teach survival skills.

Checks/DCs: Survival DC 14 understands extraction map; Persuasion DC 13 reduces deposit after good hearing; Medicine DC 13 identifies likely injury patterns; Insight DC 12 sees Hesta respects practical questions.

Success: Party gains extraction clarity and possible deposit discount.

Partial Success: They get the beacon but misunderstand one limit until Hesta corrects them.

Failure: They leave without extraction plan or pay full deposit.

Rewards: Beacon, gear tags, practical rumor.

Consequences: Lack of extraction plan increases risk if the party later attempts the true Spire, especially The Executioner.

Faction Reactions: Salvage Union likes prepared teams; Spire Seekers mock overcaution; Marik approves.

Shorten: Hesta states three limits and one price.

### Encounter 4. Gear Check Dispute

Goal: Resolve legal flags and questionable items before the threshold.

Setup: Warden scan flags a CodeX data splinter, damaged parcel remnant, forged map, or heat mark.

Read-Aloud:

> The hovering seal pauses above your pack. The Warden beside it exhales through his nose. "I would love one quiet line today. Explain this."

NPCs: Marik or Warden inspector, gear clerk, sponsor observer.

Player Options: Explain item, surrender for hold, show legal copy, call Ira, hide embarrassment, argue.

Checks/DCs: Persuasion DC 13 explains; Arcana DC 14 identifies harmless state; Investigation DC 13 matches legal copy; Sleight of Hand DC 15 hides harmless item, but failure raises heat.

Success: Item cleared or safely held; heat stays stable.

Partial Success: Item held until exit; registration continues.

Failure: Heat-Flagged Registration or delay.

Rewards: Warden respect, clean gear record.

Consequences: Heat affects Threshold Door color and sponsor tone.

Faction Reactions: Wardens reward honesty; Codebreakers call surrender cowardice; Guild uses delays to sell convenience.

Shorten: One item, one explanation check, one consequence.

### Encounter 5. Spire Seeker Public Challenge

Goal: Give public ambition a cost and a reward.

Setup: Vey Lumen challenges the party to state why they deserve ascent.

Read-Aloud:

> Vey steps onto the plinth and offers the crowd a grin. "The Tower hears many footsteps. Let it hear a reason."

NPCs: Vey, public watchers, rival novice team.

Player Options: Accept challenge, refuse quietly, redirect to team oath, mock the ritual, let one PC speak.

Checks/DCs: Performance DC 13 inspires; Persuasion DC 14 makes it humble and strong; Insight DC 13 avoids a binding oath; History DC 13 quotes a known ascent lesson.

Success: Gain rally token or Public Attention becomes favorable.

Partial Success: Crowd likes them, but Spire Seeker expectation attaches.

Failure: Rival team gains the crowd; no mechanical penalty unless the party insults the ritual.

Rewards: Rally token: once before the next long rest, add 1d4 to a save against fear or charm.

Consequences: Public words may be repeated by sponsors, rivals, and later Spire records.

Faction Reactions: Spire Seekers approve boldness; Last Light prefers honest fear; Guild measures marketability.

Shorten: Let each PC say one word for ascent.

### Encounter 6. Executioner Terminal Warning

Goal: Deliver the warning and give players agency through questions.

Setup: The terminal lights when the party approaches after registration scan or before final consent.

Read-Aloud:

> Forty-seven marks burn down the terminal's side. The crowd grows thinner here, as if people know not to stand too close to certain truths.

NPCs: GUIDY, Hesta, Marik, Vey, Felix if present.

Player Options: Read handout, ask questions, compare to hearing consent, request printout, ignore terminal.

Checks/DCs: Arcana DC 15 suppressed lines; History DC 14 names; Investigation DC 15 buried expedition; Insight DC 13 NPC reactions.

Success: Gain one Executioner clue and Tower Anxiety -1 through informed caution.

Partial Success: Learn plain warning only.

Failure: No punishment, but a sponsor can minimize the danger and increase Faction Recruitment pressure.

Rewards: Printed warning, clue, serious tone.

Consequences: The party understands that entering The Executioner now is an informed, lethal choice rather than normal progression.

Faction Reactions: See Executioner Protocol Warning section.

Shorten: Read handout and answer two questions.

### Encounter 7. Threshold Consent Scan

Goal: End the chunk with a clear, solemn entry choice.

Setup: The party reaches the door after registration. Any unresolved debt, heat, sponsor, or witness flag appears one final time.

Read-Aloud:

> The final registrar steps back. The door waits. Not like wood. Like judgment holding its breath.

NPCs: GUIDY, registrar, sponsor rep if accepted, Marik if heat, Ira if legal complication.

Player Options: Consent, pause, adjust roster, reject sponsor term, pay debt bond, declare independent status, comfort a hesitant ally.

Checks/DCs: Insight DC 15 senses coercion; Persuasion DC 13 supports a teammate; Legal Cant DC 14 challenges improper sponsor pressure; Arcana DC 14 reads door response.

Success: Door records clean or understood consent.

Partial Success: Door opens with flag color and warning.

Failure: Registration Denied Temporarily, Probationary Registration, or Illegal Entry attempt if they force it.

Rewards: Legal access status, a clear warning state, and permission to step back without losing consent.

Consequences: Determines whether the next play path is portal-world preparation, nonlethal orientation training, delayed registration, or a deliberately lethal Executioner attempt.

Faction Reactions: Sponsors mark claims; Wardens record heat; CodeX watches for backdoor use.

Shorten: Ask three questions: team name, sponsor, consent. Then read Final Threshold Scene.

## Tower Access Outcome Packages

### 1. Clean Registration

Conditions: Debt clear or voided, heat 0-1, no coercive sponsor, final consent clear.

Immediate Result: Tower access approved.

NPC Reaction: GUIDY sounds relieved; Marik nods once.

Faction Reaction: Sponsors respect independence; Guild recalculates.

Cost: Standard fees only.

Benefit: Advantage on the next administrative Spire check or portal-access dispute.

Risk: No sponsor cushion.

Tower Consequence: Door opens blue-white.

Transition to Executioner Terminal: Clean legal access to the warning terminal.

### 2. Sponsored Registration

Conditions: Party accepts sponsor terms.

Immediate Result: Access approved with sponsor seal.

NPC Reaction: Sponsor representative smiles for the crowd.

Faction Reaction: Rival factions mark the party as claimed.

Cost: Report, salvage preference, oath, or data duty.

Benefit: Sponsor item, discount, or advantage specified by offer.

Risk: Sponsor can demand future compliance.

Tower Consequence: Door shows sponsor sigil for one breath.

Transition to Executioner Terminal: Sponsor may send a message before the risk prompt.

### 3. Independent Registration

Conditions: Party refuses sponsors and clears legal scans.

Immediate Result: Access approved without sponsor support.

NPC Reaction: Hesta respects it; Vey calls it either brave or vain.

Faction Reaction: Factions continue courting from a distance.

Cost: No discounts beyond earned reputation.

Benefit: No faction claim.

Risk: Fewer safety nets.

Tower Consequence: Door asks only for team oath.

Transition to Executioner Terminal: The party approaches the terminal under its own name.

### 4. Probationary Registration

Conditions: Appeal pending, legal mark, unresolved witness concern, or moderate heat.

Immediate Result: Access approved with restrictions.

NPC Reaction: Ira warns them to keep records; Marik watches exits.

Faction Reaction: Sponsors offer to "help" with restrictions.

Cost: 10 NC bond or one Warden reporting duty.

Benefit: Legal entry despite uncertainty.

Risk: Trouble inside Tower worsens legal status.

Tower Consequence: Door opens blue with amber edges.

Transition to Executioner Terminal: The terminal records probation before any ACKNOWLEDGE RISK.

### 5. Debt-Flagged Registration

Conditions: Debt paused, reduced, settled, or disputed.

Immediate Result: Access approved if party acknowledges debt status.

NPC Reaction: GUIDY asks twice whether consent is free.

Faction Reaction: Guild offers debt financing; Last Light warns against it.

Cost: Debt remains; extraction deposits rise by 5 NC.

Benefit: Entry proceeds.

Risk: Predatory offers and Tower consent flickers.

Tower Consequence: Door displays red text: `OBLIGATION ACKNOWLEDGED.`

Transition to Executioner Terminal: Debt warnings appear before the ACKNOWLEDGE RISK prompt and cannot force entry.

### 6. Heat-Flagged Registration

Conditions: Public violence, courier death, contraband dispute, or Warden concern.

Immediate Result: Access approved with Warden witness or temporarily delayed.

NPC Reaction: Marik is tired rather than angry.

Faction Reaction: CodeX approves; Guild weaponizes rumor.

Cost: Gear check, 5 NC filing fee, or Warden escort.

Benefit: Legal entry instead of arrest.

Risk: Future misconduct triggers faster enforcement.

Tower Consequence: Door opens with a low bell tone.

Transition to Executioner Terminal: Warden log follows any entry, retreat, or extraction attempt.

### 7. Codebreaker Backdoor Registration

Conditions: Party accepts Codebreaker aid or bypasses a registration delay.

Immediate Result: Access opens through a side scan or corrupted roster path.

NPC Reaction: GUIDY becomes alarmed; CodeX is delighted.

Faction Reaction: Wardens investigate if discovered; Codebreakers claim the party.

Cost: Heat +1 and data splinter obligation.

Benefit: Bypass one debt or heat delay for now.

Risk: Executioner warning flickers harder; legal repair required later.

Tower Consequence: Door opens cold blue with black text fragments.

Transition to Executioner Terminal: The Spire knows the access record is irregular.

### 8. Registration Denied Temporarily

Conditions: Coerced consent, active violent heat, unpaid required bond, or roster dispute.

Immediate Result: Entry delayed until one issue is fixed.

NPC Reaction: Ira or Marik gives the fastest repair path.

Faction Reaction: Sponsors swarm with solutions.

Cost: Time, 5-25 NC, apology, evidence copy, or sponsor bond.

Benefit: Prevents bad entry from becoming dangerous.

Risk: Vane gains time; public attention shifts.

Tower Consequence: Door remains closed but not hostile.

Transition to Executioner Terminal: After one repair scene, return to the terminal warning or choose a portal world.

### 9. Party Refuses Registration

Conditions: Party chooses not to enter yet.

Immediate Result: No Tower entry today.

NPC Reaction: GUIDY accepts; Spire Seekers judge; Last Light respects consent.

Faction Reaction: Sponsors revise offers.

Cost: Delay; some temporary discounts expire.

Benefit: More downtime and legal cleanup.

Risk: Vane moves, witnesses face pressure, appeal clocks tick.

Tower Consequence: Door dims politely.

Transition to Portal Worlds: Begin portal-world preparation when they return.

### 10. Party Attempts Illegal Entry

Conditions: Party attacks staff, bypasses door, forges roster, or uses CodeX route after denial.

Immediate Result: Heat rises by 2. Wardens and Tower systems respond.

NPC Reaction: Marik tries to stop them without lethal force; GUIDY pleads.

Faction Reaction: CodeX may help; every lawful faction distances itself.

Cost: Legal heat, lost sponsor offers, possible item confiscation.

Benefit: Immediate access only if they succeed on a hard path.

Risk: Executioner-related consent corruption, Warden pursuit, no extraction support.

Tower Consequence: Door opens only on a successful Arcana or thieves' tools DC 18 group effort with at least two successes before two failures; otherwise registration is denied and heat applies.

Transition to Executioner Terminal: If they force illegal access, the real Executioner risk begins with irregular entry complications.

## Final Threshold Scene

Run this scene after the party has completed or refused final registration. Stop before any Executioner arena, monster, tactical setup, treasure, or exploration begins.

Read-Aloud:

> The Forecourt falls away one sound at a time: the merchants, the recruiters, the scrape of armor, the paper shuffle of clerks. The Threshold Door fills your vision. Your team name appears across its blue metal bands, letter by letter.
>
> One by one, your life counters answer with pale light.
>
> The Tower asks, in a voice too quiet for the crowd to hear: "Do you enter by your own will, under your own name, with the lives you have remaining?"
>
> The terminal beside the door waits with two choices: `ACKNOWLEDGE RISK` or `RETURN`.

Final Checks:

- Insight DC 13: A hesitant character can name fear without losing entry.
- Arcana DC 14: The door is reading consent, not courage.
- Legal Cant DC 14: A debt or sponsor phrase can be clarified before entry.
- Persuasion DC 13: One PC can support another who is wavering.

Final Questions:

- What team name does the Tower record?
- Does every PC enter freely?
- Is any sponsor declared?
- Is any debt, heat, or witness flag acknowledged?
- Who holds the extraction beacon or legal copy?

What the Party Sees: White-blue light under the door, a narrow vertical line widening, and a black terminal reflecting forty-seven life-counter marks. Do not describe the Executioner arena yet.

What the Tower Asks: Consent, name, roster, acknowledgement of flags, and whether the party truly accepts the Executioner warning or returns to prepare.

How Life Counters Respond:

- Clean: Counters shine steady blue.
- Debt-Flagged: Counters pulse blue-red once.
- Heat-Flagged: Counters show a thin amber ring.
- Sponsored: A sponsor sigil reflects beside the number, then fades.
- Codebreaker Backdoor: Counters flicker black for one heartbeat.

Door and Terminal Reactions:

- Clean or independent registration: The handle warms.
- Sponsored registration: The handle bears a temporary sigil.
- Debt flag: Red text appears and asks for acknowledgement.
- Heat flag: A bell tone sounds and the Warden log updates.
- Refused consent or RETURN: The door closes without shame and the registrar points the party toward portal-world gates, sponsors, gear, and training.

Transition Out of This Chunk: End with the party stepping back toward portal-world preparation, entering optional orientation training, or knowingly speaking ACKNOWLEDGE RISK. Full runnable Executioner content belongs to the later Spire Floor 1 chunk, not to the repaired early-campaign sequence.

What Not to Reveal Yet:

- Executioner arena keyed areas.
- Executioner tactics beyond the terminal warning.
- Any safe tutorial floor beyond the terminal.
- Exact future Spire floor objectives.
- How Floor 100 resolves the Charter.

## Chunk 02 Handoff Summary

Use this handoff to keep continuity tight when writing the next repaired portal-world chunk or when running the optional orientation appendix below.

Ruling Reached: Record the exact ruling from Possible Rulings, including whether debt is voided, paused, transferred, settled, appealed, or marked reckless.

Party Level: Default is level 2 after the Contract Hall ruling. If already level 2, record alternate reward.

Party Registration Status: Clean, Sponsored, Independent, Probationary, Debt-Flagged, Heat-Flagged, Codebreaker Backdoor, Denied Temporarily, Refused, or Illegal Entry.

Sponsor Status: Record accepted sponsor, refused sponsors that matter, and any public insult or faction obligation.

Debt Status: None, paused, reduced bond, settlement, disputed, or sponsor-financed.

Heat Status: 0 for clean; 1 for minor public trouble; 2 for Warden concern; 3 for illegal entry or serious violence.

Evidence Status: Ledger-retained, party-held copies, damaged, sealed, or missing. Note whether Vane's representative created new evidence.

Sel Status: Free, protected, frightened, disappointed, indebted, absent, or still legally exposed.

Kessa Status: Protected witness, hidden, fled, pressured, allied, or missing.

Vane Status: Legally exposed, publicly embarrassed, untouched but angry, under investigation, or temporarily strengthened by settlement.

Marik Attitude: Respectful, cautious, disappointed, protective, or actively monitoring.

Felix Attitude: Helpful, hedging, insulted, pressured by Guild, or privately invested.

Ira Attitude: Professional ally, overextended helper, cautious observer, or frustrated counsel.

Orvan Attitude: Impressed by precision, concerned by chaos, interested in the party as precedent, or wary of their methods.

Faction Reputation Changes:

- Guardian Wardens: Note respect or heat.
- Pixel Prosperity Guild: Note hostility, discount, or containment.
- Spire Seekers: Note public challenge outcome.
- Salvage Union: Note extraction plan.
- Codebreakers: Note backdoor contact or rejection.
- Ledger Court: Note legal trust.
- Remnant Veil: Note death/life-counter interest.
- Last Light Concord: Note mercy and witness care.

Gear Purchased: Record extraction beacon, maps, healing draughts, legal access copies, sponsor items, and message tokens.

Tower Access Condition: Note door color, consent clarity, active flags, and whether entry was legal or irregular.

Unresolved Hooks:

- Merrit Vane may retaliate through sponsors, appeal, or Tower salvage claims.
- Kessa may need protection.
- The Executioner Protocol points toward deeper Tower law.
- CodeX may offer illegal shortcuts.
- Guild stock and counterfeit maps may connect to portal-world supply chains or later Spire preparation.
- Sel's counter anomaly may recur near safe zones.

Spire Setup Needs: Begin later Spire play at the Executioner terminal, carrying registration status, sponsor obligations, debt/heat flags, extraction choices, portal-world preparation, followers, gear, lives, and emotional tone from the Forecourt.

Expected Next Chunk: The repaired roadmap moves next into portal-world systems and portal access. The old Chunk 03 material below is retained only as optional Spire Seeker Orientation Trial content.

# APPENDIX / TRAINING CHUNK: Spire Seeker Orientation Trial 1 - The Threshold That Weighs You

## Training Chunk 03 Overview

The Threshold That Weighs You is no longer canon Spire Floor 1. It is a Spire Seeker Orientation Trial: a nonlethal training simulation built from partial Tower data, Forecourt safety routines, Salvage Union extraction drills, and Spire Seeker pedagogy. It teaches intent, consent, retreat, extraction drills, simulated scars, route discipline, and mercy under pressure. It does not count as a Tower floor clear, does not unlock Spire Floor 2, and does not bypass The Executioner.

Canon Boundary: Every "Floor 1," "first clear," "Tower mark," "checkpoint," or "ascent record" reference inside this appendix is a simulation label used by the Spire Seekers and Forecourt training systems. These references do not describe the real Spire Floor 1. The real Spire Floor 1 is The Executioner.

Level Range: Designed for 2nd-level characters. It remains playable for cautious 1st-level parties with the scaling notes in each encounter, and it can challenge 3rd-level parties by increasing objectives, hazards, and time pressure rather than raw damage.

Expected Sessions: One long session or two shorter sessions. The default structure assumes Session 6 covers the full trial, return to the Nexus, and the start of post-training downtime. If play runs long, end after the Beacon Test Chamber or at the simulated First Checkpoint Antechamber.

Primary Location: Spire Seeker Orientation Hall simulation chamber, modeled after threshold-law data and called "The Threshold That Weighs You."

Expected Party Level: Level 2 after the Contract Hall ruling in Chunk 02.

Expected Party Resources: Most parties have full hit points, full class resources, 1-2 minor healing draughts, normal starting gear, 500 NC minus purchases, possible legal copies, a sponsor token or faction benefit, and maybe one extraction beacon. Do not assume the party bought perfect gear.

Major NPCs or Echoes: GUIDY as a limited signal, Aazoth as a mercy flicker, the Threshold Custodian, Mercy Echo, Broken Climber Echoes, a reflected version of a witness or debt figure, and optional distant echoes of Sel, Kessa, Marik, Felix, or a sponsor depending on Chunk 02.

Major Factions Watching From Outside: Guardian Wardens, Pixel Prosperity Guild, Spire Seekers, Salvage Union, Codebreakers, Ledger Court, Remnant Veil, and Last Light Concord. They cannot freely interfere inside the trial, but their sponsorships, debts, legal flags, and public expectations can shape what the simulation shows.

Main Question: Can the party practice Spire entry discipline without lying to itself about why it wants to climb?

Required Outcomes:

- The party crosses the threshold and declares, reveals, or avoids its purpose.
- The party learns the training model for intent-based Spire pressure.
- The party makes a route choice with real cost.
- The party faces one combat or hazard where the goal is more than killing enemies.
- The party sees retreat and extraction are possible but costly.
- The party reaches the simulated First Checkpoint Antechamber or retreats with consequences.
- The party returns to the Nexus with training record, reward, simulated scar, or unfinished pressure.

Possible Outcomes: Clean First Clear, Slow Safe Clear, Fast Costly Clear, Debt-Shadowed Clear, Mercy-First Clear, Sponsor-Compromised Clear, Extraction Used, Forced Retreat, Illegal Entry Consequence, Near-Death Clear, Party Refuses Floor Rule, or Party Splits.

Where Training Chunk 03 Begins: At a Spire Seeker or Forecourt training threshold after the party chooses a nonlethal orientation trial.

Where Training Chunk 03 Ends: After the simulation is cleared, paused, or exited, the party returns to the Nexus with training reputation, minor preparation benefits, and no actual Spire floor progress.

### Level and Registration Support

If the party is still level 1: Reduce the number of hostile creatures by one in every combat, lower creature hit points by about one-third, and allow the Threshold Custodian to offer one free stabilization pulse in F11. Award level 2 at the simulated First Checkpoint Antechamber or immediately after retreat if the party survived meaningful training pressure.

If the party is level 3: Add one environmental complication to F10 and F11, increase route pressure by 1 at the start, and make the Weighing Door require one additional honest alignment mark. Do not simply add many attacks; the floor should remain about intention, not attrition.

Clean Registration: The Tower opens clearly and gives standard warnings.

Probationary Registration: The floor speaks in cautious amber text when the party contradicts stated purpose.

Debt-Flagged Registration: Debt imagery appears in F8 and F12. It can be faced, named, or carried.

Heat-Flagged Registration: The Tower treats threats, shortcuts, and violence as louder signals. Heat does not prevent success, but it makes careless force costly.

Codebreaker Backdoor Registration: The opening route is colder and stranger. One shortcut appears early, but it carries a black static mark that can complicate extraction.

Refused Sponsorship: The floor asks fewer outside questions but offers fewer external aids.

Accepted Sponsor: The floor weighs whether the party acts for its own purpose or borrowed purpose. This does not punish sponsorship by itself; it punishes pretending the sponsor has no influence.

## Session 6 Run Sheet: First Step Into the Tower

### What This Session Must Accomplish

- Open at the Threshold Door with immediate sensory pressure.
- Establish the trial rule: the simulation weighs intent.
- Force a meaningful route choice.
- Run at least one exploration hazard and one objective-based encounter.
- Show that retreat and extraction work, but cost something.
- Present one vulnerable echo or stranger the party can help, ignore, exploit, or abandon.
- End with training clear, retreat, extraction drill, or a cliffhanger at the simulated First Checkpoint Antechamber.

### What the DM Tracks

Tower Pressure:

- 0: The floor is attentive but calm.
- 1: Contradictions echo; minor hazards intensify.
- 2: Doors become stricter; the next failure creates a scar risk.
- 3: The Weighing Door demands a cost, confession, or retreat.

Party Fear/Trust:

- 0: The party is openly aligned or honest about doubt.
- 1: The party is tense but communicating.
- 2: The party hides motives, splits trust, or lets a vulnerable echo suffer.

Route Stability:

- 0: Current route is stable.
- 1: One path shifts, adding a hazard or delay.
- 2: A chosen shortcut changes the return path.

Extraction Readiness:

- 0: No beacon or no plan.
- 1: Beacon held but not tested.
- 2: Beacon tested or extraction point identified.

Clue Count:

- Track each time the party learns one of the six Trial 1 conclusions. Three or more conclusions understood before F14 grants advantage on the final Weighing Door group check.

### Scene Order If Moving Fast

1. Threshold Declaration at F1.
2. Three-Route Choice at F3.
3. One route room: F4, F5, or F6.
4. Sentence Shard Crossing at F10.
5. Beacon Test Chamber at F11.
6. Mercy Split at F12.
7. The Weighing Door at F14.
8. Return to the Nexus.

### Scene Order If Roleplaying Heavily

1. Threshold Declaration and personal intent questions.
2. Hall of First Weight exploration.
3. Three-Route Gallery debate.
4. Chosen route room and alternate peek.
5. Witness Stair or Debt Mirror.
6. Broken Team Alcove.
7. Sentence Shard Crossing.
8. Beacon Test Chamber.
9. Mercy Split.
10. First Checkpoint Antechamber.
11. Weighing Door.
12. Return, public record, downtime opener.

### Do-Not-Forget List

- The Tower reacts to what the party says and what it does.
- Doubt is not failure. Lying to avoid cost is pressure.
- Let retreat work.
- Let extraction work if they paid for or earn the chance.
- The first combat should pressure an objective, not simply drain hit points.
- Show The Executioner through warning signs only; do not put the real entity into this simulation.
- Stop before the next orientation trial unless the table chooses to continue training.

## Adventure: The Threshold That Weighs You

### Adventure Overview

Level: 2nd level by default, with adjustments for levels 1 and 3.

Expected Session Count: One to two sessions.

Location: Spire Seeker simulation chamber modeled as a threshold-law training floor.

Main NPCs/Echoes: Threshold Custodian, Broken Climber Echo, Mercy Echo, Debt Reflection, GUIDY signal, Aazoth flicker.

Opposition: Sentence Shards, Clause-Echo Wisps, Debt Reflections, Beacon Static Swarms, route hazards, and the Weighing Door itself.

Central Conflict: The party must align action with declared purpose while learning that the Tower cares how they move through danger, not only whether they survive.

Stakes: training mark, first preparation boon, public reputation, simulated scars, extraction-drill record, sponsor reaction, debt/heat shifts, and confidence for later portal-world and Spire preparation.

Rewards: NC training stipend, minor preparation boon, trial mark, route token, lore, faction reputation, possible quieting of debt/heat, and a simulated checkpoint record.

Failure States: Forced retreat, extraction with scar risk, debt-shadowed clear, broken route access, public embarrassment, sponsor pressure, heat increase, or one life lost if the table's choices and dice turn hard. Failure should push play forward, not close the campaign.

### Background

The simulation is built as a threshold court. It weighs intention, not in the sense of reading secret thoughts perfectly, but by comparing declared purpose, observable action, consent status, debt pressure, and how the party treats vulnerable figures inside the trial.

The trial responds to debt, heat, sponsorship, and consent because its training model draws on the Charter principles of Consent, Truth, and Mercy. A debt-flagged entrant may still enter freely, but the simulation asks whether the debt is a purpose, a chain, or a lie. A heat-flagged entrant may still be brave and compassionate, but threats and force ring louder. A sponsored entrant may still be sincere, but borrowed purpose becomes visible when the sponsor's benefit conflicts with the party's stated values.

The first route is never exactly the same twice because the simulation arranges its rooms around the team's first declared purpose. The map below is the stable version for this campaign, but details shift: words on walls, mirror images, echoes, shortcut colors, and the final door's questions.

This orientation trial does not simply kill new parties because it is a supervised calibration exercise. It tests, teaches, and records. It can wound and frighten; it is not gentle. The real Spire is not bound by this safety profile, and The Executioner should never be softened to match this trial.

The Executioner is foreshadowed through bell tones, red text in blue light, reflection-only weapons, and the warning that corrupted consent invites pursuit. The real Executioner does not appear in this trial. If players panic about it, let Arcana or Insight DC 13 confirm that these are sanitized training echoes, not the entity itself.

Aazoth can appear as pale-gold mercy light when the party protects an echo, tells an uncomfortable truth, or refuses to abandon a frightened figure for speed. Aazoth does not solve puzzles, fight enemies, or erase consequences. It gives a clue, steadies a counter, or marks that mercy was recorded.

### Strong Start

Begin exactly where Chunk 02 ended: the Threshold Door opens.

Read-Aloud:

> The door opens inward, and the Nexus falls silent behind you as if someone cupped a hand over the entire city.
>
> The air inside is colder than stone and warmer than breath. Your life counters dim from public blue to a private white, numbers visible only when you look directly at them. The Forecourt noise vanishes. Your sponsor marks, legal flags, debts, heat, and team name flatten into thin lines of light across the floor.
>
> Ahead, three steps descend into a chamber with no ceiling. A sentence writes itself across the first step in wet silver:
>
> `THE TOWER DOES NOT WEIGH WHAT YOU CLAIM. IT WEIGHS WHAT YOU CARRY.`
>
> The step below it writes a second line:
>
> `SPEAK WHY YOU ENTER, OR ENTER WITHOUT THE BENEFIT OF BEING BELIEVED.`
>
> Then the door behind you begins to close.

Immediate Pressure: The party has one minute of table time to decide whether any character speaks a reason for entering before the door seals. They may speak together, individually, refuse, joke, stay silent, or step back.

If a character steps back before the door seals, that character remains in the Forecourt and can rejoin only after the team pauses at F1 and chooses to reopen the threshold. This costs time and raises Public Attention after return, but it is valid consent.

If the whole party steps back, use Party Refuses Registration or delay the floor until they return.

## Trial 1 Core Rule

The Trial 1 simulation responds to declared intent. A route opens when the party acts honestly toward its purpose, but the training system pressures contradictory intent, false consent, careless abandonment, and borrowed purpose that the party refuses to name.

### What the Party Sees

The floor expresses intent through visible physical signs:

- Words appear on steps, doors, and mirrors.
- Life counters dim, brighten, pulse red, or ring amber.
- Route doors change weight, sound, texture, or temperature.
- Echoes speak words the party said earlier.
- Blue safe-zone light becomes white threshold light.
- Sponsor marks, debt marks, and heat marks appear as shadows on the floor.

### What the DM Tracks

Track Tower Pressure from 0 to 3, Honest Alignment Marks from 0 to 3, and Contradictions.

Honest Alignment Marks are gained when the party states a purpose and then acts in a way that genuinely supports it despite cost. Examples include protecting a vulnerable echo after saying they seek mercy, preserving evidence after saying they seek truth, or refusing a sponsor shortcut after saying they enter under their own name.

Contradictions occur when the party's actions sharply oppose its declared purpose while the players try to deny the conflict. Contradiction is not normal tactical compromise. It is meaningful self-deception, coercion, or abandonment.

### Honest Declaration

An honest declaration can be heroic, selfish, frightened, practical, or messy. The Tower accepts honest motives more readily than polished lies.

Examples:

- "We are here to test the Tower safely." The safer route opens clearly. Reckless shortcuts raise pressure.
- "We are here to get rich." The fast route opens. Abandoning allies for loot raises pressure; taking treasure openly does not.
- "We are here to clear a debt." Debt imagery appears. Facing the Debt Mirror honestly can quiet the flag.
- "We are here to save someone." Mercy echoes appear. Ignoring vulnerable figures raises pressure.
- "We are here because a sponsor owns us." The Borrowed Purpose route opens without shame. Claiming freedom while obeying sponsor terms raises pressure.
- "We are here but we do not consent." The door remains open behind the speaker and the floor asks whether they wish to step back. If they continue under coercion, pressure starts at 2.
- "We are here to cheat the floor." The floor opens a shortcut and marks it black. It can be beaten, but the public record will show irregular entry.

### Contradictory Intent

Contradictory intent means the party insists on one purpose while acting in a way that betrays it and refuses to acknowledge the cost.

It triggers when:

- The party claims safety but repeatedly chooses speed without protecting each other.
- The party claims mercy but abandons a helpless echo for convenience.
- The party claims truth but destroys evidence to avoid embarrassment.
- The party claims independence but obeys a sponsor order that harms its stated goal.
- The party claims consent while a PC openly says they do not want to continue.

It does not trigger when:

- The party changes its mind and says so.
- The party chooses a hard compromise openly.
- The party retreats.
- The party fails a check.
- The party makes a tactical choice under pressure.
- The party admits selfish or fearful motives.

### What Triggers Pressure

Raise Tower Pressure by 1 when the party lies to the floor about a major motive, abandons a vulnerable echo after declaring mercy, exploits a debt-bound figure, attacks a nonhostile echo without cause, uses an illegal backdoor to bypass a consequence, or splits the party after being warned that roster unity matters.

Lower Tower Pressure by 1, to a minimum of 0, when the party names a contradiction honestly, accepts a cost, protects a vulnerable figure, repairs a damaged route, uses extraction to save a life rather than preserve pride, or retreats before turning caution into coercion.

### How to Explain This at the Table

Say this plainly:

"This trial is not punishing you for having complicated motives. It is testing whether your actions and declared purpose can exist in the same story. You can choose greed, caution, mercy, ambition, or fear. The danger rises when the simulation sees a contradiction you refuse to name."

Do not force the party toward a single moral answer. Let every purpose open a playable route, then make the cost visible.

## Trial 1 Table Map

Spatial Summary:

F1 leads to F2 and then F3. F3 branches into F4 Safe Truth, F5 Fast Want, and F6 Borrowed Purpose. F4 leads to F7 and then F10. F5 leads directly to F10 with a hazard cost and can unlock a shortcut to F13. F6 leads to F8 and F9, then loops back to F7 or forward to F10. F7, F8, and F9 form a loop around witness, debt, and broken-team clues. F10 leads to F11. F11 can trigger extraction and opens to F12. F12 leads to F13. F13 leads to F14. F14 opens the first checkpoint record and return route.

Branches: F4, F5, F6.

Loop: F7-F8-F9-F7.

Shortcut: F5 can open a costly shortcut to F13 if the party accepts a route scar or sacrifices salvage. Codebreaker Backdoor Registration can reveal a black-static shortcut from F1 to F8, but using it raises Tower Pressure by 1.

Safer Slower Route: F4 Door of Safe Truth through F7.
