Faster Costly Route: F5 Door of Fast Want to F10 or F13.

Route Changed by Chunk 02 Outcome: Debt-Flagged parties see F8 early through reflections; Heat-Flagged parties face sharper Sentence Shards at F10; Sponsored parties see F6 as a bright door rather than a shadowed one; Codebreaker Backdoor parties see a black shortcut.

### F1. The Threshold Mouth

Read-Aloud:

> The first chamber is shaped like an open mouth made of stone ribs. The door behind you is the tongue, slowly flattening into the floor. Your team name hangs in the air, unfinished, waiting for the reason beneath it.

DM Details: This area captures the party's first declaration. It is safe for conversation unless the party attacks the door or each other. The Nexus cannot be heard after the door seals.

Exits: Back through the Threshold Door for 1 minute; forward to F2; black-static side seam to F8 only for Codebreaker Backdoor entrants.

Visible Choices: Speak a shared purpose, speak individual purposes, refuse, step back, touch a legal/debt/sponsor mark, or proceed silently.

Interactive Objects: Silver sentence on the step; floating team name; life counter reflections; sponsor/debt/heat lines on the floor.

Checks/DCs: Insight DC 12 reads that silence is allowed but will be recorded as uncertainty; Arcana DC 14 reads debt/heat/sponsor lines; Persuasion DC 13 helps a hesitant ally speak freely; Religion DC 14 senses Aazoth listening for mercy, not obedience.

Clues: The Tower reacts to intent; consent matters; legal flags entered with the party.

Hazards: If a PC is coerced across the threshold, Tower Pressure starts at 2 and their counter pulses red once.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: GUIDY signal flickers and says only, "I can hear you faintly. I cannot open the door from this side."

Treasure: None.

Consequences: Honest declaration grants 1 Honest Alignment Mark. Silence grants no mark and no penalty. False declaration creates the first Contradiction.

Revisited: If revisited before F13, the doorway shows the party's current purpose in shorter, harsher words.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Debt lines ask, "Who benefits?" Heat lines ask, "What do you threaten?" Sponsor sigils ask, "Whose name enters first?" Backdoor seam whispers, "Skip the question."

### F2. Hall of First Weight

Read-Aloud:

> The next hall is long enough that the far end should vanish. Instead, it folds toward you. Each footstep leaves a pale impression on the floor, and each impression fills with a different word: NEED, FEAR, GOLD, LAW, FRIEND, PROOF.

DM Details: This hall teaches that movement records motive. The words are not accusations; they are impressions.

Exits: Back to F1; forward to F3.

Visible Choices: Walk together, split across the hall, step only on certain words, erase footprints, speak over the words.

Interactive Objects: Footprint words; hanging weight-stones; a low alcove showing Forecourt watchers as blurred silhouettes.

Checks/DCs: Perception DC 12 notices words change when PCs speak; Acrobatics DC 13 avoids stepping on a chosen word, though doing so has no necessary benefit; Investigation DC 14 identifies the most repeated party motive; Arcana DC 14 learns the floor is comparing words to action.

Clues: Mechanical clue that intent is recorded; environmental clue that route choice is forming; magic clue that the floor does not read thoughts perfectly.

Hazards: If the party tries to erase every footprint, a Clause-Echo Wisp appears and asks, "Why enter if nothing may record you?"

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Optional Clause-Echo Wisp, nonhostile unless attacked or lied to repeatedly.

Treasure: A fallen brass tag worth 5 NC if taken openly. If taken while denying interest in gain, mark a Contradiction rather than punishing theft.

Consequences: Naming the repeated word lowers Tower Pressure by 1 if it was above 0.

Revisited: Footprints from the first passage remain and can guide the party back.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Debt adds OWED; heat adds STRIKE; sponsorship adds CLAIM; backdoor adds UNFILED.

### F3. Three-Route Gallery

Read-Aloud:

> The hall opens into a triangular gallery. Three doors wait in three different kinds of light. One is blue and plain. One is gold and half-open. One is white stone covered in other people's names.
>
> Above them, a sentence writes itself: `CHOOSE THE WEIGHT YOU WILL ADMIT.`

DM Details: The party can inspect all three doors before choosing. They may split routes, but the Tower warns them that first roster unity matters.

Exits: Back to F2; blue door to F4; gold door to F5; white named door to F6.

Visible Choices: Safe Truth, Fast Want, Borrowed Purpose. The party can also force a door, wait, or try to open multiple routes.

Interactive Objects: Three door handles; route inscriptions; floor triangle that changes color under each PC.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 13 reads route costs; Insight DC 13 senses which door matches the party's declaration; Arcana DC 15 sees the F5 shortcut potential; History DC 14 recognizes old runner scratches around F4.

Clues: Checkpoints are earned by action-purpose alignment; routes are moral and practical; faster does not mean evil.

Hazards: Opening all three doors at once raises Route Stability to 1 and releases two Sentence Shards at F10.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Threshold Custodian may appear if the party argues for more than 10 minutes.

Treasure: None.

Consequences: Choosing a door openly grants advantage on the first check inside that route. Sneaking through a door while claiming another route raises Tower Pressure by 1.

Revisited: The unchosen doors remain, but after F10 only one alternate route can be visited before the gallery locks.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Debt makes F8 visible behind the doors; heat makes F5 brighter; sponsorship makes F6 warm; backdoor makes a seam between F3 and F8.

### F4. Door of Safe Truth

Read-Aloud:

> The blue door opens into a room of plain stone shelves. On each shelf rests an object that looks useful and slightly embarrassing: a bent piton, a torn map, a cracked potion vial, a note beginning "I should have said..."

DM Details: This is the safer slower route. It rewards caution, evidence preservation, and admitting limits.

Exits: Back to F3; forward to F7; side peephole to F5 that shows its cost.

Visible Choices: Examine shelves, take supplies, read notes, repair a broken tool, leave quickly.

Interactive Objects: Damaged supplies; confession notes; blue route chalk; shelf labels.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 12 finds a useful tool; carpenter's tools or tinker's tools DC 13 repairs a piton; Medicine DC 13 recognizes a cracked vial as unsafe; Insight DC 14 identifies which note matters.

Clues: Safe route is slower but gives preparation; retreat is possible; truth includes admitting weakness.

Hazards: Taking every item without sorting triggers falling shelves; Dexterity save DC 12 or 3 bludgeoning damage.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: A Broken Climber Echo whispers, "I lied and said I had rope."

Treasure: One route chalk, one usable piton, one minor healing draught if the party succeeds on Investigation DC 12 and Medicine DC 13.

Consequences: Spending 10 minutes here grants Extraction Readiness +1 if the party discusses retreat or beacon use.

Revisited: Unchosen items crumble after F11.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Debt-marked PCs find a note about "owing courage." Heat-marked PCs see blood on the cracked vial. Sponsored PCs find a supply stamped with their sponsor's mark.

### F5. Door of Fast Want

Read-Aloud:

> The gold door is already open wide enough for one person. Beyond it, a narrow passage slopes down over black glass. Coins, charms, and broken weapon tips slide along the floor toward a bright line in the distance.

DM Details: This is the faster costly route. It is not a trap for ambitious characters. It rewards clear priorities and punishes pretending the cost is not real.

Exits: Back to F3; forward to F10; costly shortcut to F13 if unlocked.

Visible Choices: Move quickly, collect salvage, ignore salvage, anchor the party, open the shortcut, retreat.

Interactive Objects: Sliding salvage; black glass slope; gold shortcut lever; reflection line.

Checks/DCs: Athletics or Acrobatics DC 13 to cross quickly; Sleight of Hand DC 14 to grab salvage without slowing; Survival DC 13 to rope the party together; Insight DC 14 to see the shortcut demands a cost.

Clues: Fast route is honest if speed is the goal; greed is not automatically false; shortcuts alter return paths.

Hazards: On failed movement, take 1d6 bludgeoning damage and lose 5 minutes. If a PC grabs salvage while claiming not to care, Tower Pressure +1.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Sentence Shard reflections may appear but do not attack until F10.

Treasure: 10 NC salvage scattered on the slope; one bright route token if crossed in 2 rounds or fewer.

Consequences: Unlocking the shortcut to F13 costs one of: abandon 15 NC salvage, accept a minor scar roll with advantage, or raise Tower Pressure by 1.

Revisited: Slope becomes steeper; DCs increase by 2 after F11.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Debt causes coins to sound like contract bells. Heat makes weapon tips point upward. Sponsor marks may offer a smooth stepping path if the party names the sponsor's help aloud.

### F6. Door of Borrowed Purpose

Read-Aloud:

> The white door opens into a chamber wallpapered with names. Some are written in ink. Some are carved. Some glow with sponsor seals. A blank space waits at eye level, exactly wide enough for your team name.

DM Details: This route addresses sponsorship, debt, external pressure, and public identity. It can be perfectly legitimate if the party acknowledges what it carries.

Exits: Back to F3; forward to F8; side passage to F9; loop door to F7 if the party names borrowed pressure honestly.

Visible Choices: Write team name, write sponsor name, refuse names, scratch out a coercive name, read old names.

Interactive Objects: Name wall; sponsor seals; blank space; silver stylus.

Checks/DCs: History DC 13 recognizes famous sponsor teams; Insight DC 14 identifies coerced names; calligrapher's supplies DC 13 marks the team name cleanly; Persuasion DC 14 helps a sponsored PC speak freely.

Clues: Borrowed purpose can be named and carried; sponsor pressure is visible; consent can be repaired through truth.

Hazards: Scratching out names in anger releases two Clause-Echo Wisps unless the party first identifies a coerced name with Insight DC 14.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Sponsor echo, Ledger clerk echo, or CodeX static message depending on registration.

Treasure: One sponsor-thread ribbon worth no NC but usable to gain advantage on one future check resisting sponsor coercion.

Consequences: If the party honestly names sponsor influence, gain 1 Honest Alignment Mark. If they deny a binding sponsor while taking its route advantage, Tower Pressure +1.

Revisited: The wall adds the party's first floor title after clear or retreat.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Sponsored parties see their sigil clearly. Debt-flagged parties see creditor names. Heat-flagged parties see names crossed by Warden blue. Backdoor parties see missing entries.

### F7. Witness Stair

Read-Aloud:

> A stair climbs and descends at the same time. Each landing holds a translucent witness stand, empty until you look away. Then someone is there: not a person, exactly, but the shape of someone who once needed to be believed.

DM Details: This loop area connects F4, F8, and F9. It reinforces witness protection and evidence from Chunks 1-2.

Exits: Back to F4; down to F8; across to F9; forward to F10 if the party has at least one clue from this loop.

Visible Choices: Listen to echoes, ask questions, ignore stands, record testimony, destroy stands.

Interactive Objects: Witness stands; stair rail with bell marks; floating oath motes.

Checks/DCs: Persuasion DC 13 gets an echo to speak; Insight DC 13 separates fear from falsehood; Investigation DC 14 finds a route clue in testimony; Religion DC 14 calms a repeating echo.

Clues: The Tower records treatment of vulnerable people; truth needs protection; Executioner signs connect to witness corruption.

Hazards: Badgering an echo raises Party Fear/Trust to 2 and summons a Clause-Echo Wisp.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Witness echoes may resemble Sel, Kessa, Chime, or an unknown runner. They are not the real people.

Treasure: A witness mote. Once before the next long rest, a PC can add 1d4 to an Insight or Persuasion check involving frightened testimony.

Consequences: Protecting an echo grants 1 Honest Alignment Mark for truth or mercy purposes.

Revisited: One witness stand becomes empty after its clue is accepted.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Debt echoes ask who signed; heat echoes flinch from raised weapons; sponsor echoes ask whose words were rehearsed; backdoor echoes skip and repeat.

### F8. Debt Mirror

Read-Aloud:

> A mirror fills the wall from floor to ceiling. It does not show your faces first. It shows hands: hands taking coins, hands signing names, hands carrying parcels, hands held out for help.

DM Details: The Debt Mirror reflects unresolved obligations. It is social, moral, and potentially hazardous. It does not demand debt payment; it asks whether debt is named truthfully.

Exits: Back to F6 or F7; forward to F9; hidden return to F3 if the party names a debt and a boundary.

Visible Choices: Touch mirror, speak debt aloud, deny debt, offer payment, break mirror, ask what debt wants.

Interactive Objects: Mirror surface; reflected contracts; handprints; red thread.

Checks/DCs: Insight DC 13 identifies which reflection is guilt and which is coercion; Persuasion DC 14 names a boundary; Arcana DC 15 quiets false debt residue; Religion DC 14 invokes mercy without erasing responsibility.

Clues: Debt can be real, false, or weaponized; Tower distinguishes obligation from coercion; Executioner warning involved predatory contract enforcement.

Hazards: Debt Reflection emerges if a debt-flagged PC lies or if any PC tries to force another to accept a debt. It deals low damage and pressures choices.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Debt Reflection, possibly wearing the silhouette of Merrit Vane, a sponsor, or the PC's own face.

Treasure: Quieted red thread. It can reduce one future debt or sponsor complication by 1 step if used with honest negotiation.

Consequences: Naming a debt and a boundary can remove the debt imagery from later rooms even if legal debt remains.

Revisited: Mirror shows the consequence of the party's choice: quiet hands, grasping hands, or empty hands.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Debt flag makes the mirror active immediately. Heat shows hands as fists. Sponsor shows hands on shoulders. Backdoor shows hands opening locks.

### F9. Broken Team Alcove

Read-Aloud:

> The alcove contains four stone bedrolls, one cracked shield, and a message scratched into the floor with the end of a dagger: `WE SAID TOGETHER. WE LEFT HER.` A fifth bedroll is folded neatly in the corner.

DM Details: This is an investigation and mercy scene. It tells the story of a failed party that abandoned a vulnerable member before earning a checkpoint.

Exits: Back to F6 or F8; loop to F7; forward to F10 after the party engages with the clue or spends 10 minutes searching.

Visible Choices: Investigate, repair the shield, read the scratched note, comfort the echo, take supplies, leave.

Interactive Objects: Bedrolls; cracked shield; scratched floor note; folded fifth bedroll; cold lantern.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 13 reconstructs what happened; Medicine DC 12 identifies nonlethal injury signs; Smith's tools DC 14 repairs shield enough to honor it; Persuasion or Religion DC 13 calms Broken Climber Echo.

Clues: Retreat before checkpoint costs record and pride; abandonment matters; the Executioner connects to judgment and broken roster unity.

Hazards: If the party steals the fifth bedroll supplies without acknowledging the abandoned climber, the Broken Climber Echo becomes hostile.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Broken Climber Echo named Renn Vale. Renn was left behind by a team that claimed unity but chose speed.

Treasure: A usable shield if repaired; one damaged climber note handout; 5 NC salvage; one floor ration.

Consequences: Calming Renn grants advantage on one Weighing Door question about unity. Exploiting the alcove raises Tower Pressure by 1.

Revisited: Renn is gone if calmed; hostile if exploited; silent if ignored.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Debt shows the abandoned climber holding a contract. Heat shows the shield split by a blade. Sponsor shows team banners cut apart. Backdoor hides the fifth bedroll until Perception DC 14.

### F10. Sentence Shard Crossing

Read-Aloud:

> The corridor ahead has shattered into floating slabs of stone. Each slab holds part of a sentence, and each sentence ends before it should. Below the slabs is a slow white fog filled with half-heard bells.
>
> The first shard reads: `WE ENTERED BECAUSE...`

DM Details: This is the first real Tower combat/exploration challenge. The objective is to cross, stabilize route slabs, and protect any beacon or vulnerable echo, not kill every enemy.

Exits: Back to F5, F7, or F9 depending on route; forward to F11. F5 shortcut can bypass part of crossing at cost.

Visible Choices: Cross quickly, stabilize slabs, fight Sentence Shards, carry an echo, use rope, use magic, retreat.

Interactive Objects: Sentence slabs; anchor rings; fog below; bell motes; unstable bridge line.

Checks/DCs: Acrobatics DC 13 to cross a gap; Athletics DC 13 to hold rope under pressure; Investigation DC 14 orders sentence slabs safely; Arcana DC 14 stabilizes one slab; Persuasion DC 13 lets a PC finish a sentence honestly and calm a shard.

Clues: Tower reacts to intent and spoken truth; route stability matters; extraction is different from retreat because this room lacks a full extraction point.

Hazards: Falling into fog deals 1d6 cold damage and returns the PC to the last stable slab prone. Heat-flagged parties hear extra bells; increase one DC by 1.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Sentence Shards and optional Clause-Echo Wisp. If Renn was calmed, Renn's echo can point to one safe slab.

Treasure: Sentence splinter worth 10 NC to Ledger Court or usable once to gain advantage on a future Charter-related check.

Consequences: Stabilizing the route grants Route Stability -1 and Clue Count +1. Rushing without care can reach F11 faster but increases Tower Pressure by 1.

Revisited: Stabilized slabs remain. Unstabilized slabs rearrange and require checks again.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Debt adds clauses to slabs; heat adds sharper edges; sponsorship adds sponsor slogans; backdoor adds missing words and black static.

### F11. Beacon Test Chamber

Read-Aloud:

> A circular chamber waits beyond the crossing. In the center is a waist-high pedestal shaped exactly like an extraction beacon. Around it, white lines mark a ring on the floor.
>
> A calm voice says, "Leaving is a skill. Practice before panic."

DM Details: This chamber teaches extraction with a controlled threat. If the party has no beacon, the pedestal creates a training beacon that can only function inside this chamber.

Exits: Back to F10; forward to F12; side alcove to F13 opens only if the party tests extraction honestly.

Visible Choices: Test beacon, ignore chamber, ask questions, fight static, hold ring, practice retreat.

Interactive Objects: Training beacon pedestal; extraction ring; timing marks; public-record lens.

Checks/DCs: Arcana DC 13 activates training beacon; Survival DC 13 identifies safe positioning; Athletics DC 13 holds a creature in the ring; Persuasion DC 13 coordinates panicked allies; thieves' tools DC 14 clears backdoor static.

Clues: Extraction is a tool, not a reset; extraction has a public record; allies can protect the charge.

Hazards: Beacon Static Swarm forms when the beacon charges. It tries to disrupt the ring, not kill PCs.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Beacon Static Swarm; Threshold Custodian voice.

Treasure: If the party completes the test, the beacon or training pedestal prints one Extraction Calibration Tag worth 5 NC and grants advantage on the first real extraction activation during a later Spire attempt or approved training trial.

Consequences: Completing the test raises Extraction Readiness to 2. Ignoring it leaves Extraction Readiness unchanged. Failing it raises Tower Pressure only if the party lies about understanding.

Revisited: The pedestal becomes dormant after a successful test.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Debt asks who pays extraction; heat sends Warden notice into record; sponsor sends notification to sponsor if declared; backdoor requires a DC 13 Arcana or tools check to prevent static from delaying the charge.

### F12. Mercy Split

Read-Aloud:

> The passage divides around a glass column. Inside the column, a translucent figure presses both hands against the surface. Behind the left passage, you see the pale glow of the checkpoint route. Behind the right, the figure's light flickers toward darkness.
>
> On the floor between the paths: `TIME, PROOF, SELF, OTHER. CHOOSE WHAT YOU WILL NOT PRETEND IS FREE.`

DM Details: This is the first hard Tower social/moral choice. The Mercy Echo is not a living prisoner, but how the party treats it matters. The choice should be meaningful, not a gotcha.

Exits: Left fast route to F13; right rescue route to F13 after delay; rear to F11.

Visible Choices: Save the echo, preserve evidence in the column, rush to checkpoint, protect the party, split up, break the glass, bargain.

Interactive Objects: Glass column; Mercy Echo; checkpoint glow; evidence mote; time-sand line.

Checks/DCs: Persuasion DC 13 comforts the echo; Arcana DC 14 opens column safely; Athletics DC 15 breaks glass but triggers hazard; Investigation DC 14 extracts evidence mote; Medicine DC 13 recognizes the echo's panic pattern.

Clues: Tower records treatment of vulnerable people; mercy costs time or risk; checkpoints are earned by aligned action.

Hazards: Breaking glass deals 1d6 slashing damage to adjacent creatures and releases two Clause-Echo Wisps unless a PC uses an action to shield the echo.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Mercy Echo. It may resemble Kessa, Sel, a stranger, or a PC's memory of someone vulnerable.

Treasure: Evidence mote worth no NC but grants advantage on one future check involving mercy, witness protection, or Executioner lore. Fast route grants 10 NC salvage instead.

Consequences: Saving or respectfully releasing the echo grants 1 Honest Alignment Mark for mercy, truth, safety, or protection purposes. Ignoring it for speed is valid if named. Pretending it did not matter raises Tower Pressure by 1.

Revisited: The column is empty if resolved. If ignored, the echo's silhouette appears at F14.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Debt asks if mercy can be owed; heat makes the column crack under angry touch; sponsorship may offer a sponsor reward for rushing; backdoor creates a false exit that avoids seeing the echo but raises Tower Pressure.

### F13. First Checkpoint Antechamber

Read-Aloud:

> The air changes. Not safer, exactly, but witnessed. A round room waits with four low benches, a basin of clear light, and a sealed archway ahead. The words above the basin read: `NOT YET REST. NEAR ENOUGH TO LEARN.`

DM Details: This is a near-checkpoint. It allows a pause, limited healing, route record review, and one chance to retreat with a cleaner record than earlier retreat. The true first floor clear is through F14.

Exits: Back to F12; shortcut back to F5 if unlocked; forward to F14; emergency return circle that triggers forced retreat if activated.

Visible Choices: Rest briefly, review record, wash scars, retreat, continue, spend route token.

Interactive Objects: Light basin; benches; route record; emergency return circle; sealed arch.

Checks/DCs: Medicine DC 12 lets one PC spend a Hit Die; Arcana DC 13 reads route record; Insight DC 13 identifies which action the Tower valued most; Religion DC 14 quiets a minor scar until return.

Clues: Checkpoints are earned by alignment; retreat after this point is cleaner; the Tower records mercy and contradiction.

Hazards: If Tower Pressure is 3, the basin shows an accusation and requires one honest statement before healing works.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Threshold Custodian may manifest fully here.

Treasure: First Checkpoint Inscription handout; if the party earned 3 Honest Alignment Marks, one route token appears.

Consequences: Reaching F13 before retreat counts as First Checkpoint Contact, reducing public embarrassment and scar risk. Continuing to F14 gives the chance to clear.

Revisited: The basin remembers each PC's first honest statement.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Debt can be acknowledged to lower red pulse; heat can be cooled by naming harm avoided; sponsor mark can be set aside for one room if the party declares independence; backdoor static can be repaired with Arcana DC 14.

### F14. The Weighing Door

Read-Aloud:

> The final door of the trial is round, heavy, and made of many materials layered together: blue stone, black glass, white bone, gold wire, old wood, and a strip of plain iron worn smooth by hands.
>
> It has no handle. It has a scale.

DM Details: This is the final challenge. The door weighs action against declared purpose. It does not require moral perfection.

Exits: Back to F13; forward to trial clear record and return threshold. Do not continue to another orientation trial unless the table chooses additional training.

Visible Choices: Place objects, speak truths, accept scars, offer treasure, name contradictions, stand together, force the door.

Interactive Objects: Scale pan; route token slot; honest alignment marks visible as motes; counter beam; door inscriptions.

Checks/DCs: Group check DC 13 using each PC's chosen relevant skill if tied to their purpose; Persuasion DC 14 names shared purpose; Insight DC 14 identifies unresolved contradiction; Athletics DC 16 forces the door at cost; Arcana DC 15 uses route token properly.

Clues: Checkpoint earned by alignment; intent and action are compared; Executioner warnings are about judgment patterns, not random murder.

Hazards: Weighing Door Hazard activates if the party forces the door or reaches it with Tower Pressure 3 and no Honest Alignment Marks.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Threshold Custodian asks one final question. Mercy Echo or Broken Climber Echo may appear if unresolved.

Treasure: Training mark, minor preparation boon, route token if earned, 20-50 NC stipend depending on route and outcome.

Consequences: Clear, costly clear, retreat, extraction, scar, or near-death clear. Apply outcome package.

Revisited: After clear, F14 becomes a return arch. After failed retreat, it seals until the party re-enters the trial later with a simulated scar or new declaration.

Debt/Heat/Sponsorship/Backdoor Response: Debt can be weighed against consent. Heat can be weighed against restraint. Sponsorship can be weighed against team name. Backdoor entry can be weighed against truth if the party admits the irregular path.

## Trial 1 Revelation Structure

The party should not need one perfect roll to understand the orientation trial. Use these clue paths repeatedly.

### Conclusion 1: The Tower Reacts to Intent, Not Only Action

Environmental Clue: F1 and F2 write the party's motives into steps, footprints, and route light.

NPC/Echo Clue: The Threshold Custodian says, "Action is the body of purpose. Purpose is the shadow action casts."

Mechanical Clue: Honest declarations grant advantage or Honest Alignment Marks; false contradictions raise Tower Pressure.

Optional Magic/Check Clue: Arcana DC 14 in F2 reveals the floor compares spoken declarations with repeated behavior.

### Conclusion 2: Retreat Is Possible But Not Free

Environmental Clue: F13's emergency return circle is clear, named, and usable.

NPC/Echo Clue: Broken Climber Echo Renn says, "We could have left together. We left one by one, and the Tower remembered the order."

Mechanical Clue: Retreat before F13 creates stronger scar risk and public embarrassment than retreat after F13.

Optional Magic/Check Clue: Insight DC 13 at F13 shows the return circle is caution, not cowardice.

### Conclusion 3: Extraction Is a Tool, Not a Reset Button

Environmental Clue: F11's pedestal states, "Leaving is a skill. Practice before panic."

NPC/Echo Clue: Hesta's earlier warning echoes in beacon static: "A promise to try."

Mechanical Clue: Extraction takes rounds, can be interrupted, creates public record, and risks treasure loss or scars.

Optional Magic/Check Clue: Arcana DC 13 during extraction shows it pulls bodies through a registered path rather than rewinding events.

### Conclusion 4: The Tower Records How the Party Treats Vulnerable People

Environmental Clue: F7 witness stands brighten when protected and crack when bullied.

NPC/Echo Clue: Mercy Echo asks, "Am I a delay, or am I part of why you came?"

Mechanical Clue: Protecting Renn or Mercy Echo grants Honest Alignment Marks; exploiting them raises pressure.

Optional Magic/Check Clue: Religion DC 14 detects pale-gold Aazoth light when mercy is chosen at cost.

### Conclusion 5: The Executioner Protocol Is Connected to Judgment, Not Random Murder

Environmental Clue: Bells sound around corrupted consent, broken roster unity, and predatory contract imagery.

NPC/Echo Clue: The Threshold Custodian says, "The hunted are first judged. Judgment is not always justice."

Mechanical Clue: Executioner signs appear when pressure rises through contradiction or coercion, not at random.

Optional Magic/Check Clue: History or Arcana DC 15 identifies similarities to the Forecourt warning without sensing the full entity nearby.

### Conclusion 6: Checkpoints Are Earned by Alignment Between Action and Declared Purpose

Environmental Clue: F13 says, "Near enough to learn," while F14 demands weight on the scale.

NPC/Echo Clue: Renn says, "The door did not ask if we won. It asked if we were together."

Mechanical Clue: Honest Alignment Marks lower the final challenge difficulty and improve outcome packages.

Optional Magic/Check Clue: Arcana DC 15 at F14 shows each mark corresponds to an action that matched stated purpose.

## Trial 1 Encounters

### Encounter 1. Threshold Declaration

Goal: Begin with consent and purpose under pressure.

Setup: Run at F1 as the door opens and begins to close behind the party.

Read-Aloud:

> The Tower asks for why, and the city behind you has already gone silent.

NPCs/Creatures: GUIDY signal, optional Threshold Custodian voice.

Player Options: Speak shared purpose, speak individual purposes, refuse, joke, step back, proceed silently, declare coercion, name sponsor influence, name debt pressure.

Checks/DCs: Persuasion DC 13 supports a hesitant ally; Insight DC 12 reads that silence is permitted; Arcana DC 14 reads legal marks; Religion DC 14 senses Aazoth's attention.

Success: Honest declaration grants 1 Honest Alignment Mark and a clear route sign at F3.

Partial Success: Mixed or uncertain declaration grants no mark but no pressure.

Failure: A knowingly false declaration creates a Contradiction and Tower Pressure +1.

Resource Cost: Time and public confidence only.

Clue Gained: The Tower weighs intent.

Consequence: Route doors adapt to what the party says or avoids saying.

Faction/Nexus Echo: Sponsors may hear a registered declaration summary only if the party accepted sponsor reporting. Codebreaker entry creates static.

Scaling: No combat. For 3 PCs, let each speak individually. For 6 PCs, ask for one shared purpose and one dissenting voice.

Shorten: Ask, "What purpose do you give the Tower?" Accept one sentence and move to F2.

### Encounter 2. Three-Route Choice

Goal: Make the first major branch practical and thematic.

Setup: Run at F3 after the Hall of First Weight.

Read-Aloud:

> Three doors wait for three versions of courage: the careful truth, the quick want, and the borrowed name.

NPCs/Creatures: Threshold Custodian if the party stalls; no hostile creatures unless they force all doors.

Player Options: Inspect doors, choose route, split routes, try to open all, use magic, ask the Tower a question, retreat.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 13 identifies route cost; Insight DC 13 matches route to purpose; Arcana DC 15 identifies shortcut potential; Persuasion DC 13 settles a party disagreement.

Success: Party chooses a route knowingly and gains advantage on first route check.

Partial Success: Party chooses but misses a cost; reveal cost when first triggered.

Failure: Forcing or contradicting route choice raises Route Stability to 1 or Tower Pressure +1.

Resource Cost: Time, route opportunity, possible future hazard.

Clue Gained: Multiple paths can be valid.

Consequence: Chosen route shapes later rooms, rewards, and public story.

Faction/Nexus Echo: Sponsors favor F6, Spire Seekers favor F5, Ledger and Wardens respect F4.

Scaling: No combat unless all doors forced. If combat triggers, use 1 Clause-Echo Wisp for 3-4 PCs, 2 for 5-6 PCs.

Shorten: Read each door's cost aloud and ask for a vote.

### Encounter 3. Debt Mirror

Goal: Let unresolved obligation become a playable scene rather than a bookkeeping note.

Setup: Run at F8, especially for Debt-Flagged, Sponsored, or settlement-bound parties.

Read-Aloud:

> The mirror shows hands before faces. Taking, signing, carrying, refusing, helping. Then one reflected hand points at you.

NPCs/Creatures: Debt Reflection; optional reflected silhouette of Vane, sponsor, Sel, or the PC.

Player Options: Name debt, reject false debt, accept real obligation, set boundary, offer payment, break mirror, walk away.

Checks/DCs: Insight DC 13 separates guilt from coercion; Persuasion DC 14 states a boundary; Arcana DC 15 quiets false debt residue; Religion DC 14 frames mercy and responsibility.

Success: Debt imagery quiets; gain clue and possibly Quieted Red Thread.

Partial Success: Reflection remains but loses hostility; no treasure, no pressure.

Failure: Debt Reflection attacks or marks a PC with a temporary debt pulse.

Resource Cost: Possible hp, spell slot, or public admission.

Clue Gained: Debt is not the same as consent.

Consequence: Debt-Shadowed Clear becomes possible if the party carries rather than resolves the reflection.

Faction/Nexus Echo: Guild pressure echoes through coin sounds; Last Light imagery appears if mercy was strong in Chunk 02.

Scaling: 3 PCs: one Debt Reflection at 12 hp. 4 PCs: one normal Debt Reflection. 5 PCs: one Reflection plus one Clause-Echo Wisp. 6 PCs: one Reflection plus two Wisps, but Wisps focus on objects and mirrors.

Shorten: One PC names the debt, one check resolves the reflection.

### Encounter 4. Sentence Shard Crossing

Goal: Combine movement, combat, and route stabilization.

Setup: Run at F10. Floating slabs form a broken sentence path.

Read-Aloud:

> The sentence is also the bridge. Every missing word is a gap.

NPCs/Creatures: Sentence Shards, optional Clause-Echo Wisp, Renn's echo if calmed.

Player Options: Cross, anchor, stabilize slabs, finish sentences, fight, protect beacon, carry echo, retreat.

Checks/DCs: Acrobatics DC 13 crosses gap; Athletics DC 13 holds rope; Investigation DC 14 orders slabs; Arcana DC 14 stabilizes one slab; Persuasion DC 13 calms one Shard by finishing its sentence truthfully.

Success: Cross with stable route, clue, and salvage.

Partial Success: Cross but lose time, take damage, or leave route unstable.

Failure: A PC falls into fog, route shifts, or Sentence Shards cut the party off until stabilized.

Resource Cost: Hit points, spell slots, rope, time.

Clue Gained: The Tower reacts to honest completion and route stability.

Consequence: Stable crossing improves final Weighing Door check; unstable crossing may add a hazard if revisited.

Faction/Nexus Echo: Heat-marked parties hear Warden bells; sponsored parties see sponsor slogans shatter.

Scaling: 3 PCs: 2 Sentence Shards, no Wisp. 4 PCs: 3 Sentence Shards. 5 PCs: 3 Shards and 1 Wisp. 6 PCs: 4 Shards and 1 Wisp. For level 1, use 2 Shards maximum.

Shorten: Run as a three-success group challenge with one Shard attack after each failed check.

### Encounter 5. Broken Team Alcove

Goal: Let investigation and mercy reveal how checkpoint logic works.

Setup: Run at F9. Renn Vale's echo repeats a failed party's abandonment.

Read-Aloud:

> The fifth bedroll is folded too carefully. Someone wanted to be remembered as tidy when the others remembered them as slow.

NPCs/Creatures: Broken Climber Echo Renn Vale.

Player Options: Investigate, comfort Renn, repair shield, take supplies, leave, ask what happened, apologize on behalf of no one.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 13 reconstructs failure; Medicine DC 12 identifies injuries; Smith's tools DC 14 repairs shield; Persuasion or Religion DC 13 calms Renn.

Success: Renn gives clue, damaged climber note, and advantage at F14 on unity question.

Partial Success: Renn gives clue but remains sad; no advantage.

Failure: Renn lashes out as Broken Climber Echo or the alcove grows cold, raising Tower Pressure +1.

Resource Cost: Time, possible tool use, emotional attention.

Clue Gained: Retreat and abandonment are different.

Consequence: Mercy-First or Slow Safe Clear becomes easier.

Faction/Nexus Echo: Last Light Concord would approve; Spire Seekers respect if party names unity as strength.

Scaling: Combat is avoidable. If hostile: 3 PCs use Renn at 10 hp; 4 PCs normal; 5-6 PCs add 1 Clause-Echo Wisp.

Shorten: One investigation check and one compassion check.

### Encounter 6. Beacon Test Chamber

Goal: Teach extraction procedure before a crisis.

Setup: Run at F11. Beacon Static Swarm disrupts a practice activation.

Read-Aloud:

> The chamber gives you the shape of escape and then sends static to bite at its edges.

NPCs/Creatures: Beacon Static Swarm; Threshold Custodian voice.

Player Options: Activate beacon, defend ring, study charge, attack swarm, use real beacon, use training beacon, ignore test.

Checks/DCs: Arcana DC 13 activates; Survival DC 13 positions allies; Athletics DC 13 holds ring; Persuasion DC 13 coordinates; thieves' tools DC 14 clears backdoor static.

Success: Extraction Readiness becomes 2; party gains Calibration Tag.

Partial Success: They learn the rule but take damage or delay.

Failure: Swarm interrupts test; party can retry once after a cost or continue without calibration.

Resource Cost: Actions, possible hp, maybe one beacon charge if they use a real beacon recklessly.

Clue Gained: Extraction takes time and protection.

Consequence: First real extraction is easier or harder based on outcome.

Faction/Nexus Echo: Salvage Union record may note competence; Codebreaker static can corrupt the lesson.

Scaling: 3 PCs: Swarm at 14 hp. 4 PCs: normal Swarm. 5 PCs: normal Swarm plus one static pulse per round. 6 PCs: two smaller Swarms at 12 hp each. For level 1, Swarm deals 1 damage less per hit.

Shorten: Run three rounds: activate, protect, complete.

### Encounter 7. Mercy Split

Goal: Present a hard choice with no fake free answer.

Setup: Run at F12. The party must choose time, proof, self, or other.

Read-Aloud:

> The echo watches you decide what kind of delay a person is.

NPCs/Creatures: Mercy Echo, possible Clause-Echo Wisps if glass is shattered.

Player Options: Save echo, preserve evidence, rush, split, break glass, bargain, name the cost openly.

Checks/DCs: Persuasion DC 13 comforts echo; Arcana DC 14 opens column safely; Athletics DC 15 breaks glass; Investigation DC 14 preserves evidence; Medicine DC 13 understands panic.

Success: Gain Honest Alignment Mark and evidence mote or route benefit.

Partial Success: Save echo or evidence, not both; lose time.

Failure: Glass shatters, echo panics, or time cost increases.

Resource Cost: Time, hp, spell slot, or forgone treasure.

Clue Gained: Mercy is recorded when it costs something.

Consequence: Changes final door question and possible outcome package.

Faction/Nexus Echo: Last Light or Aazoth flicker if mercy chosen; sponsor pressure if a sponsor rewards speed.

Scaling: If Wisps appear, use 1 for 3-4 PCs, 2 for 5-6 PCs. For level 1, Wisps only restrain or distract for first round.

Shorten: Offer two explicit options: save echo with delay, or rush with salvage. Let the party name the cost.

### Encounter 8. The Weighing Door

Goal: Resolve the trial through alignment, cost, or retreat.

Setup: Run at F14 after F13 pause.

Read-Aloud:

> The scale waits for something heavier than coin.

NPCs/Creatures: Threshold Custodian, possible Mercy Echo or Renn, Weighing Door Hazard if forced.

Player Options: Place route token, speak truth, name contradiction, accept scar, offer treasure, stand together, force door, retreat.

Checks/DCs: Group check DC 13 using relevant skills; Persuasion DC 14 shared purpose; Insight DC 14 unresolved contradiction; Athletics DC 16 force; Arcana DC 15 route token.

Success: Trial clears; reward and training mark.

Partial Success: Clear with cost: scar, lost salvage, sponsor mark, or debt pulse.

Failure: Forced retreat, extraction, or Weighing Door Hazard. The party can still clear if they accept a visible cost.

Resource Cost: Possible hp, boon limitation, scar, treasure, sponsor debt, or heat.

Clue Gained: Checkpoints are earned through aligned action.

Consequence: Apply Trial 1 Outcome Package.

Faction/Nexus Echo: Public record emphasizes the method: clean, fast, merciful, sponsored, debt-shadowed, illegal, or near-death.

Scaling: If hazard activates, use hazard only for 3 PCs; hazard plus 1 Sentence Shard for 4-5 PCs; hazard plus 2 Shards for 6 PCs. Level 1 parties face hazard only and can end combat by naming cost.

Shorten: Ask for one shared statement and one group check, then apply result.

## Trial 1 Creatures and Hazards

### Sentence Shard

Suggested CR: 1/8. XP: 25. Intended for level 2 objective encounters.

AC 13; HP 9; Speed fly 20 ft. hover.

Ability Modifiers: Str -2, Dex +2, Con +1, Int -1, Wis +0, Cha +0.

Saves/Skills: Acrobatics +4, Perception +2.

Senses: blindsight 10 ft., passive Perception 12.

Languages: understands words spoken inside the trial; speaks in sentence fragments.

Traits: Fragmented Body. The Shard can move through gaps as narrow as 1 inch but cannot pass through a complete written sentence. Honest Completion. A creature can use an action and Persuasion DC 13 to finish the Shard's sentence; on success the Shard becomes inert until harmed.

Actions: Cutting Clause. Melee Weapon Attack +4, reach 5 ft., one target. Hit: 4 slashing damage. Ringing Edge. Ranged Attack +4, range 20 ft., one target. Hit: 3 thunder damage.

Reaction: Broken Syntax. When a creature within 5 ft. lies about its immediate action, the Shard can impose disadvantage on that creature's next check before the end of its turn.

Tactics: Shards cut ropes, block slabs, and harry isolated PCs. They do not focus-fire a downed character.

Morale/Deactivation: Deactivates when crossing is stabilized, when its sentence is completed, or when reduced to 0 hp.

Noncombat Resolution: Complete three sentence fragments truthfully before two failures.

Safe Maximum: 3 PCs: 2. 4 PCs: 3. 5 PCs: 3 plus one Wisp. 6 PCs: 4 plus one Wisp.

Balance Warning: More than four Shards creates too many attacks for low-level play.

### Clause-Echo Wisp

Suggested CR: 1/8. XP: 25.

AC 12; HP 7; Speed fly 30 ft.

Ability Modifiers: Str -3, Dex +2, Con +0, Int +1, Wis +1, Cha +1.

Saves/Skills: Insight +3, Stealth +4.

Senses: darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 11.

Languages: Common, Legal Cant fragments.

Traits: Echo Clause. The Wisp has advantage on attacks against a creature that repeated a false claim this round. Low Harm. The Wisp cannot score critical hits.

Actions: Static Sting. Melee Spell Attack +4, reach 5 ft. Hit: 3 lightning damage. Binding Murmur. One creature within 30 ft. must succeed on DC 12 Wisdom saving throw or subtract 1d4 from its next Deception, Persuasion, or Intimidation check before the end of its next turn.

Reaction: Objection Flicker. When a creature targets a witness echo, the Wisp imposes -1d4 on the attack roll once per round.

Tactics: Wisps protect legal echoes and punish sloppy claims.

Morale/Deactivation: Calms if a creature states the disputed claim clearly or protects the echo.

Noncombat Resolution: Legal Cant, Persuasion, or Insight DC 13.

Safe Maximum: 3 PCs: 1. 4 PCs: 2. 5 PCs: 2 with weak enemies. 6 PCs: 3 only if objective scene.

Balance Warning: Do not combine three Wisps with multiple Shards for level 1 parties.

### Debt Reflection

Suggested CR: 1/4. XP: 50.

AC 12; HP 18; Speed 30 ft.

Ability Modifiers: Str +1, Dex +1, Con +2, Int +0, Wis +2, Cha +1.

Saves/Skills: Insight +4, Intimidation +3.

Senses: darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 12.

Languages: Speaks in the debtor's language.

Traits: Owed Shape. The Reflection appears as a creditor, sponsor, victim, or the PC. Boundary Weakness. If a creature names a real obligation and a real boundary, the Reflection has disadvantage on attacks against that creature for 1 round.

Actions: Grasping Ledger. Melee Attack +3, reach 5 ft. Hit: 5 necrotic damage. Red Thread Pull. One creature within 20 ft. must succeed on DC 12 Charisma saving throw or be pulled 10 ft. toward the mirror.

Reaction: Not Yours. When a creature accepts a debt that is not theirs, the Reflection can deal 2 psychic damage to that creature.

Tactics: Pulls PCs toward mirror and pressures debt-flagged characters. It retreats into glass at half hp unless the party keeps lying.

Morale/Deactivation: Deactivates when debt is named honestly, false debt rejected, or hp reaches 0.

Noncombat Resolution: Two successes before two failures using Insight, Persuasion, Arcana, or Religion DC 13-15.

Safe Maximum: 3 PCs: one at 12 hp. 4 PCs: one. 5 PCs: one plus one Wisp. 6 PCs: one plus two Wisps.

Balance Warning: Avoid pairing Reflection with high-damage hazards.

### Broken Climber Echo

Suggested CR: 1/4. XP: 50 if fought, but no XP for calming.

AC 13; HP 16; Speed 30 ft.

Ability Modifiers: Str +1, Dex +2, Con +1, Int +0, Wis +1, Cha +0.

Saves/Skills: Athletics +3, Survival +3, Insight +3.

Senses: passive Perception 11.

Languages: Common.

Traits: Left Behind. The Echo has advantage on checks to escape restraint or forced movement. Remembered Injury. When first reduced below half hp, it cries out and all creatures within 10 ft. must succeed on DC 11 Wisdom save or feel the memory of abandonment, taking 2 psychic damage.

Actions: Cracked Shield Bash. Melee Attack +4, reach 5 ft. Hit: 4 bludgeoning damage and target must succeed on DC 12 Strength save or be pushed 5 ft. Dagger Scratch. Melee Attack +4. Hit: 3 piercing damage.

Reaction: Not Again. When a creature moves away from the Echo without speaking, the Echo can move 10 ft. without provoking opportunity attacks.

Tactics: Blocks exits, demands answers, and pushes PCs away from the fifth bedroll. It does not kill.

Morale/Deactivation: Calms when heard, when the shield is repaired, or when a PC admits that fear can make people cruel.

Noncombat Resolution: Persuasion, Religion, Medicine, or Smith's tools DC 13-14.

Safe Maximum: One for any party size; add a Wisp for 5-6 PCs only if needed.

Balance Warning: Keep Renn social unless players attack or exploit the alcove.

### Beacon Static Swarm

Suggested CR: 1/2 hazard creature. XP: 100.

AC 12; HP 22; Speed fly 20 ft.

Ability Modifiers: Str -2, Dex +2, Con +2, Int -2, Wis +0, Cha -1.

Saves/Skills: Acrobatics +4.

Senses: blindsight 20 ft., passive Perception 10.

Languages: none; repeats beacon tones.

Traits: Swarm Body. The Swarm can occupy another creature's space. Half Harm. When below half hp, its Static Sting deals 1 less damage. Disrupt Charge. If the Swarm starts its turn in the extraction ring, the beacon charge does not advance that round unless a creature succeeds on DC 13 Arcana or Athletics.

Actions: Static Sting. Melee Attack +4, reach 0 ft., one creature in its space. Hit: 4 lightning damage. Scatter Pulse. Creatures of the Swarm's choice in the ring must succeed on DC 12 Dexterity save or move 5 ft. away from the beacon.

Reaction: Feedback. When hit by lightning or thunder damage, the Swarm can move 10 ft. without provoking opportunity attacks.

Tactics: Disrupts beacon, pushes PCs out, avoids finishing downed PCs.

Morale/Deactivation: Ends when beacon test completes, when reduced to 0 hp, or when three successful stabilization checks occur.

Noncombat Resolution: Arcana, Survival, Athletics, or tools DC 13, three successes before two failures.

Safe Maximum: 3 PCs: one at 14 hp. 4 PCs: one. 5 PCs: one plus pulse complication. 6 PCs: two at 12 hp each.

Balance Warning: Do not let the Swarm deal damage and delay charge to every PC every round.

### Threshold Custodian

Suggested CR: 1/2 social guardian. XP: 100 if fought, though fighting it is usually a mistake.

AC 14; HP 28; Speed 30 ft.

Ability Modifiers: Str +1, Dex +1, Con +2, Int +2, Wis +3, Cha +2.

Saves/Skills: Insight +5, Perception +5, Persuasion +4.

Senses: truesight 10 ft., passive Perception 15.

Languages: Common, Celestial, Legal Cant.

Traits: Threshold Authority. The Custodian has advantage on Insight checks related to stated purpose. Nonlethal Design. Its attacks cannot reduce a creature below 1 hp inside this trial.

Actions: Weight of Question. One creature within 30 ft. must make DC 13 Wisdom save or take 4 psychic damage and be unable to benefit from advantage on its next check until it answers a direct question honestly or refuses openly. Guiding Push. Melee Attack +3. Hit: 3 force damage and target moves 5 ft. in a direction the Custodian chooses.

Reaction: Open Refusal. When a creature refuses honestly, the Custodian reduces damage from the next floor hazard against that creature by 2.

Tactics: Blocks forced progress, asks questions, and pushes creatures away from reckless harm.

Morale/Deactivation: It stands aside when the party names purpose, cost, or contradiction.

Noncombat Resolution: Honest answer, route token, or Persuasion/Insight DC 14.

Safe Maximum: One.

Balance Warning: Do not run the Custodian as a boss; it is a speaking pressure valve.

### Mercy Echo

Suggested CR: 0 unless harmed; XP 10 for rescue scene.

AC 10; HP 5; Speed 0 ft. inside column, 20 ft. if freed.

Ability Modifiers: Str -2, Dex +0, Con +0, Int +0, Wis +2, Cha +1.

Saves/Skills: Insight +4.

Senses: passive Perception 12.

Languages: Common plus one PC's language.

Traits: Vulnerable Signal. Attacks against the Echo raise Tower Pressure by 1 unless the Echo is hostile through a prior choice. Mercy Recorded. Protecting the Echo at cost grants 1 Honest Alignment Mark.

Actions: Plead. One creature that can hear the Echo can add 1d4 to an Insight or Medicine check before the end of its next turn.

Reaction: Flinch. When glass breaks, the Echo imposes disadvantage on the next attack roll made by a hostile Wisp through a burst of pale light.

Tactics: It hides, pleads, and points toward evidence.

Morale/Deactivation: Freed, comforted, or ignored.

Noncombat Resolution: Persuasion, Medicine, Arcana, or Investigation DC 13-14.

Safe Maximum: One.

Balance Warning: Do not turn the Echo into a burden that steals the party's agency; it represents a cost, not an escort mission that lasts all floor.

### Weighing Door Hazard

Suggested CR: 1 hazard. XP: 200 only if overcome under combat pressure.

AC 15 for forceable components; HP 30 threshold integrity; Speed 0 ft.

Ability Modifiers: Str +4, Dex -5, Con +4, Int +1, Wis +3, Cha +2.

Saves/Skills: Insight +5.

Senses: blindsight 60 ft. in F14.

Languages: Common and the party's declared languages.

Traits: Scale of Purpose. The hazard loses 10 hp or one stage when a PC places a meaningful cost on the scale or states a true contradiction. Not a Wall. The hazard can be resolved through speech, sacrifice, route tokens, or retreat. Red Bell. If Tower Pressure is 3, first failed check causes 3 psychic damage to each PC, once only.

Actions: Closing Weight. Initiative count 20. One exit narrows. A creature near it must succeed on DC 13 Dexterity save or take 4 bludgeoning damage and be pushed 10 ft. Ringing Judgment. One creature must succeed on DC 13 Wisdom save or take 5 psychic damage, half on success.

Reaction: Counterweight. When a creature offers a false cost, the hazard raises Tower Pressure by 1 or deals 2 psychic damage if pressure is already 3.

Tactics: Pressures time and honesty. It does not chase beyond F14.

Morale/Deactivation: Deactivates after three honest weights, route token use, successful group check, retreat, or threshold integrity reduced to 0.

Noncombat Resolution: Group skill check DC 13; three successes before two failures.

Safe Maximum: One.

Balance Warning: Use this as a final hazard, not alongside multiple full-damage enemies for low-level parties.

## First Extraction Procedure

Extraction becomes available in three ways:

- The party rented or received an extraction beacon in Chunk 02.
- The party completes the training beacon in F11 and earns one emergency chamber extraction inside F11 only.
- The party reaches F13, where the emergency return circle can function as a limited forced retreat.

### What the Extraction Beacon Does

An extraction beacon creates a registered pull request to the Salvage Union or equivalent service. It does not stop time, erase damage, or return treasure automatically. It opens a white-blue extraction ring that must charge while the party survives or protects the beacon.

### Action Required

A creature holding the beacon uses an action to activate it. The beacon must be on a solid surface or held by a conscious creature. A downed creature can be extracted if another creature places the beacon within 5 feet and keeps the ring open.

### Round Count

The beacon completes extraction after 3 full rounds of charge. At the end of the third round, creatures in the ring may leave. A creature can choose to remain.

Calibration Tag: If the party completed F11 cleanly, extraction completes after 2 full rounds once during a later approved extraction drill or future Spire attempt.

Codebreaker Backdoor Static: If the party entered through a backdoor and did not repair static, extraction requires 4 full rounds or an Arcana/tools DC 13 success during the charge.

### What Enemies and Hazards Do While It Charges

Enemies try to push creatures out, disrupt the beacon, or force hard choices. They do not suddenly become brilliant killers. Beacon Static Swarms prioritize the ring. Sentence Shards cut ropes and threaten exposed PCs. Debt Reflections pull marked creatures away from the ring.

### What Allies Can Do

An ally can use an action to:

- Guard the beacon, granting it +2 AC until the ally's next turn.
- Stabilize the charge with Arcana, Survival, or relevant tools DC 13.
- Pull one willing or unconscious creature 10 feet toward the ring.
- Hold the ring boundary with Athletics DC 13, preventing one forced movement effect.
- Make a clear retreat call, lowering Party Fear/Trust by 1 if the table was fracturing.

### If Interrupted

If the beacon is moved more than 10 feet, covered by hostile static, or the holder drops to 0 hp, the charge pauses. It does not reset unless the beacon is destroyed. A paused charge resumes at the same count after one successful stabilization action.

Beacon AC 14, HP 10, immune to poison and psychic. If reduced to 0 hp, it burns out and extraction fails.

### Cost

The rental fee was paid in Chunk 02. Completing extraction consumes the beacon's active charge. If rented, the deposit is partly or fully lost depending on damage and location:

- Clean extraction from F11 or F13: deposit returned minus 5 NC service cost.
- Emergency extraction from F10 or F12: half deposit returned.
- Extraction after illegal entry or backdoor static: deposit lost unless Salvage Union relationship is strong.

### Scar Risk

Extraction before F13 requires each extracted PC to roll a DC 12 Constitution or Wisdom save, player's choice. On failure, roll or choose a minor Trial 1 scar. Extraction after F13 grants advantage on this save. Extraction used to save a dying ally grants advantage to that ally.

### Evidence and Treasure Risk

When extraction completes, each character can secure one held item or pack. Loose salvage, uncollected motes, and heavy objects remain unless already packed. Witness motes and route tokens survive if carried by a conscious character or in a witness-sealed pack.

### How Extraction Differs From Retreat

Retreat is movement back through known routes or return circles. Extraction is an emergency pull that creates a public record and can bypass space at a cost. Retreat gives more agency and can preserve more treasure. Extraction saves lives under pressure.

### How Extraction Feels In-World

The floor becomes distant. Sound narrows to the beacon's pulse. The character's life counter stretches into a line of white light, and for one breath every old footprint on the floor points toward the ring. Then the Nexus hits like cold water.

### Public Record Afterward

The Forecourt record states: `TEAM EXTRACTED FROM ORIENTATION TRIAL 1: LOCATION, TIME, CASUALTY STATE, BEACON STATUS.` It does not list private thoughts, but it does show debt/heat irregularities, sponsor notification, and whether a life was lost.

### Future Floors

This procedure remains the foundation for later extraction with floor-specific complications. The party should understand after the trial that extraction is a limited rescue tool, not a perfect undo.

### Extraction Quick Reference

1. Activate beacon with an action.
2. Mark charge round 1.
3. Protect the ring and beacon.
4. Resolve enemy disruption.
5. At the end of each round, increase charge if not paused.
6. Extraction completes after 3 rounds, or 2 with Calibration Tag.
7. Each extracted creature secures one held item or pack.
8. Check scar risk if before F13 or under severe disruption.
9. Record public extraction result in the Nexus.

## Retreat and First Tower Scar Rules

Voluntary Retreat: The party chooses to leave through a known path or return circle while still capable of continuing. It is always allowed when an exit is physically open.

Forced Retreat: The floor, a hazard, or a failed final challenge pushes the party out. It preserves lives but marks the record as incomplete.

Failed Retreat: The party tries to flee while split, lost, or under high Tower Pressure and suffers a cost before leaving: scar risk, lost pack, debt pulse, heat increase, or separated exit.

Retreat Before First Checkpoint: Retreat before reaching F13 creates public record `ORIENTATION TRIAL 1: WITHDRAWN BEFORE CHECKPOINT CONTACT.` Each PC rolls scar risk only if retreat happened under pressure, combat, or extraction.

Retreat After Reaching First Checkpoint Antechamber: Retreat from F13 is recorded as `CHECKPOINT CONTACT: RETURNED TO PREPARE.` No public shame; one faction may still spin it.

Scar Triggers:

- Extraction before F13.
- Dropping to 0 hp inside the trial.
- Forcing the Weighing Door and failing.
- Tower Pressure reaching 3 twice.
- Splitting the party and retreating through separate routes.
- Accepting a shortcut scar at F5.

Treating Scars: Scars can be quieted through rest, roleplay, a service, or a future aligned action. They should create flavor and small prompts, not heavy bookkeeping.

Nexus Effects: Scars may draw NPC attention, alter prices by a few NC, create rumors, or give advantage/disadvantage on one relevant social moment. Do not let a minor scar dominate every scene.

### d8 Trial 1 Scar Table

| d8 | Scar Name | Sensory Tell | Mechanical Effect | Roleplay Prompt | How It Can Be Quieted |
|---:|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | Silver Footprint | One footprint glows faintly when you lie about fear | Once before next long rest, disadvantage on a Deception check about motive | What fear do you hide by moving faster? | Admit fear to an ally or take the safe route on a future floor |
| 2 | Bell Bruise | A small blue bruise rings softly near contract magic | -1 to first save against a legal/contract hazard | What promise still rings in you? | Spend 5 NC on Ledger care or break a coercive clause |
| 3 | Glass Breath | Your breath fogs mirrors even when warm | Debt Mirror-like scenes notice you first | Whose reflection do you avoid? | Name a debt boundary during downtime |
| 4 | Static Vein | Black-blue static crosses one wrist | First extraction activation by you requires Arcana DC 10 or another PC's action | What shortcut still owns a piece of you? | Let Salvage Union ground the mark for 6 NC |
| 5 | Witness Flinch | You hear a gasp when someone says "leave" | Disadvantage on first check to abandon or separate from an ally; advantage on first check to protect one | Who do you refuse to leave? | Help a vulnerable NPC without reward |
| 6 | Gold Hunger | Coins feel warm and briefly heavier | First time treasure appears, make Wisdom DC 10 or speak your desire aloud | What do you want badly enough to admit? | Spend or donate 5 NC honestly |
| 7 | Door Weight | Your palm aches near sealed doors | First forced-door check has -1d4; first respectful door question has +1d4 | Which doors should not be forced? | Ask permission or state purpose before opening a future Tower door |
| 8 | Pale Thread | A faint gold thread crosses your life counter | Once, when you ignore a mercy choice, Tower Pressure rises by 1; once, when you choose mercy at cost, gain +1d4 | What mercy did you almost miss? | Accept a cost to protect another creature |

## Trial 1 Rewards

Base Rewards:

- NC or Salvage: 20 NC for a normal training clear; 35 NC for fast clear with salvage; 10 NC for retreat after F13; 0-5 NC for forced extraction before F13.
- Training Mark: `Orientation Trial 1: Threshold Weighed`. Appears as a small white line under the life counter when viewed in Forecourt training light. It is not a Tower floor clear.
- First Preparation Boon: One per character after a clear, or one party boon after retreat with strong mercy or truth.
- Route Token: Earned for 3 Honest Alignment Marks, clean route choice, or resolving F14 without force.
- Evidence or Lore: Executioner clue, Mercy Echo mote, Sentence Splinter, Quieted Red Thread, or damaged climber note.
- Public Reputation: Based on outcome package, always tagged as training rather than Spire floor progress.
- Faction Reactions: Sponsors, Wardens, Guild, Salvage Union, Last Light, CodeX, and Ledger Court respond during return/downtime.
- GUIDY Reaction: It is relieved and overexplains unless asked to stop.
- Aazoth Reaction: Pale-gold flicker or dream fragment if mercy, consent, or truth mattered.

### Minor Preparation Boons

| Boon | Effect | Limit | Recharge or Expiration | Drawback or Story Hook | Balance Note |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Step of Stated Purpose | Add 1d4 to one ability check that directly serves your declared Spire or portal-world purpose | Once | Expires after the next major expedition clear or retreat | The training record later asks whether your purpose changed | Small skill boost only |
| Witness Mote | Add 1d4 to Insight or Persuasion when protecting a frightened speaker | Once | Expires after next long rest if unused | The mote whispers one witness's fear | Social support, no combat damage |
| Route Chalk Spark | Mark one door or passage; gain advantage to find it again during a training trial or portal dungeon | Once | Expires when used | The mark shows your team name publicly in the training record | Exploration utility |
| Quieted Red Thread | Reduce one debt/sponsor pressure complication by 1 step through honest negotiation | Once | Expires after Act I if unused | The creditor knows the thread quieted them | Narrative leverage |
| Beacon Calibration Tag | First extraction charge completes one round faster | Once | Expires when used | Salvage Union receives precise extraction data | Strong but narrow survival tool |
| First Weight Token | At a threshold door, reroll one failed check to state purpose or resist coercion | Once | Expires after two major expeditions | Token grows cold if purpose is false | Defensive social/exploration boon |
| Mercy Glint | When you heal or stabilize another creature, gain 1 temporary hp | Up to 3 times | Expires after next long rest | Aazoth dream follows | Very small durability gain |
| Sentence Splinter | Add 1d4 to one History, Arcana, or Legal Cant check involving Tower law | Once | Expires after the next major expedition | The splinter completes a sentence you did not start | Lore support |

## Trial 1 Outcome Packages

### 1. Clean First Clear

Conditions: Tower Pressure 0-1, at least 2 Honest Alignment Marks, no life lost, clear F14 without forcing.

Immediate Result: Trial clear and first training mark.

Reward: 25 NC, one minor preparation boon per PC, route token, strong public notice tagged as training.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: No scar. Debt or heat may quiet by one step if faced honestly.

Public Reaction: The Forecourt treats the team as serious.

Faction Reaction: Wardens approve, Guild recalculates, Spire Seekers respect, Salvage Union offers practical discount.

Tower Reaction: Door opens clean white.

Next-Session Opener: A portal-world invitation or optional next orientation trial pulse arrives during downtime.

How It Changes Future Training: The next orientation threshold recognizes the team name clearly.

### 2. Slow Safe Clear

Conditions: Party chooses F4, protects route, spends time, reaches clear with low harm.

Immediate Result: Clear is recorded as careful.

Reward: 20 NC, one minor preparation boon per PC, advantage on the first navigation check in the next orientation trial or portal dungeon.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: No scar unless triggered separately.

Public Reaction: Some call them cautious; Last Light and Wardens approve.

Faction Reaction: Spire Seekers challenge their speed; Salvage Union respects them.

Simulation Reaction: Trial 1 marks their caution as strength.

Next-Session Opener: A rival team clears faster but wounded.

How It Changes Future Training: Safer route clue appears earlier.

### 3. Fast Costly Clear

Conditions: Party uses F5 or shortcut, reaches F14 quickly, accepts visible cost.

Immediate Result: Clear with speed record.

Reward: 35 NC salvage, one minor boon per PC, possible scar or lost evidence.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: One PC may roll scar risk if shortcut cost chosen.

Public Reaction: Spire Seekers cheer; Wardens ask about injuries.

Faction Reaction: Guild and sponsors see marketable ambition.

Simulation Reaction: Gold line appears under training mark.

Next-Session Opener: Sponsor or rival asks them to keep proving speed.

How It Changes Future Training: A fast route presents itself with sharper cost.

### 4. Debt-Shadowed Clear

Conditions: Debt Reflection remains unresolved or debt flag shapes F14.

Immediate Result: Clear, but debt pulse follows the training mark.

Reward: 20 NC, boon, Quieted Red Thread only if debt was named.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: Debt pressure remains or worsens if denied.

Public Reaction: People debate whether the party climbs freely.

Faction Reaction: Guild offers financing; Last Light warns them.

Tower Reaction: Red text appears briefly: `OBLIGATION CARRIED.`

Next-Session Opener: A debt-related offer arrives before the next expedition.

How It Changes Future Training: Debt imagery can reappear in one early room.

### 5. Mercy-First Clear

Conditions: Party saves Mercy Echo or Renn at real cost.

Immediate Result: Clear emphasizes mercy rather than speed.

Reward: 20 NC, Mercy Glint or Witness Mote, Aazoth dream fragment.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: One heat or debt pressure may quiet if mercy contradicted predation.

Public Reaction: Last Light spreads a gentler version of the story.

Faction Reaction: Spire Seekers split between admiration and impatience.

Tower Reaction: Pale-gold line appears beside the first mark.

Next-Session Opener: A vulnerable NPC asks for help tied to a portal world or next trial.

How It Changes Future Training: One mercy clue appears before combat.

### 6. Sponsor-Compromised Clear

Conditions: Sponsor benefit used while party denies sponsor influence, or sponsor goal overrides stated purpose.

Immediate Result: Clear with sponsor sigil attached.

Reward: Sponsor benefit and 20 NC, but no route token.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: Sponsor pressure increases by one step.

Public Reaction: Crowd sees the sponsor's name before the team's.

Faction Reaction: Sponsor pleased; rival factions cool.

Tower Reaction: F14 asks, "Whose purpose weighed more?"

Next-Session Opener: Sponsor demands a portal-world report or next-trial task.

How It Changes Future Training: Borrowed-purpose door appears early.

### 7. Extraction Used

Conditions: Party activates extraction before clear.

Immediate Result: Party returns alive, floor incomplete unless extraction happens after F14 clear.

Reward: If after F13, 10 NC salvage and checkpoint contact; before F13, only carried items.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: Scar risk. Public record notes extraction.

Public Reaction: Practical sympathy from some, mockery from reckless runners.

Faction Reaction: Salvage Union respects correct use; Spire Seekers judge if used too early.

Tower Reaction: Floor remains available for return.

Next-Session Opener: Hesta Winch debriefs them.

How It Changes Future Training: No next-trial certification until this trial is cleared or waived by the instructor.

### 8. Forced Retreat

Conditions: Party fails F14, pressure overwhelms route, or chooses retreat under duress.

Immediate Result: Party exits without full clear.

Reward: Carried salvage only; possible clue.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: Scar risk if before F13 or under high pressure.

Public Reaction: Record says withdrawn; spin depends on whether retreat saved lives.

Faction Reaction: Wardens prefer retreat to death; sponsors may pressure retry.

Tower Reaction: Floor remembers unresolved contradiction.

Next-Session Opener: Return attempt or Nexus pressure.

How It Changes Future Training: No next-trial certification until clear.

### 9. Illegal Entry Consequence

Conditions: Party used illegal entry or forced registration into the trial.

Immediate Result: Floor can still be cleared, but record is irregular.

Reward: Boons function, but public notice includes `IRREGULAR ENTRY`.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: Heat +1 unless repaired at F14 by confession or Ledger copy.

Public Reaction: Wardens and CodeX both pay attention.

Faction Reaction: Lawful factions cool; Codebreakers court them.

Tower Reaction: Black static appears under first mark.

Next-Session Opener: Marik or CodeX approaches first.

How It Changes Future Training: One entry scan complication.

### 10. Near-Death Clear

Conditions: A PC drops to 0 hp, extraction nearly fails, or scar risk triggers during final clear.

Immediate Result: Clear with dramatic public record.

Reward: Full clear reward, but one scar roll for affected PC.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: Scar likely; life counters flicker publicly.

Public Reaction: The story spreads fast.

Faction Reaction: Spire Seekers admire; Last Light worries; sponsors smell drama.

Tower Reaction: The first mark is bright but uneven.

Next-Session Opener: Medical/legal/social service scene.

How It Changes Future Training: The first danger sign in the next trial appears more clearly to scarred PCs.

### 11. Party Refuses Floor Rule

Conditions: Party attacks the premise, refuses purpose, tries to erase all records, or treats every prompt as hostile.

Immediate Result: The floor still allows progress, but pressure rises quickly.

Reward: If cleared, minimal NC and no route token unless they later name the refusal honestly.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: Scar risk at F14 or retreat.

Public Reaction: "They fought the first door" becomes a rumor.

Faction Reaction: CodeX amused; Wardens concerned; Ledger Court interested.

Tower Reaction: The first mark is gray-white and unsettled.

Next-Session Opener: GUIDY asks whether they want Tower advice or only warnings.

How It Changes Future Training: The next trial begins with a clearer opt-out point.

### 12. Party Splits

Conditions: The party takes different routes or separates under pressure.

Immediate Result: Run short spotlight scenes and reunite by F10 or F13 unless the split is deliberate and sustained.

Reward: Each route may grant one clue, but no route token unless they reunite honestly.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: If one group abandons another, scar risk and Tower Pressure rise.

Public Reaction: Record notes split route.

Faction Reaction: Spire Seekers respect daring; Wardens worry; sponsors may exploit division.

Tower Reaction: Doors ask each group who is missing.

Next-Session Opener: Party relationship scene after return.

How It Changes Future Training: Roster-unity clue appears early.

## First Return to the Nexus After Training

Run this scene when the party clears, retreats from, or extracts from the orientation trial.

Read-Aloud:

> The Tower lets go.
>
> Sound returns first: the Forecourt murmur, the scrape of boots, the distant vendor bell, a gasp that might be yours or someone else's. Light follows. Your life counters flare public blue again, then settle with a new thin line beneath the number.
>
> Above the Forecourt, a public record begins to write itself.

How the Forecourt Reacts:

- Clean clear: The crowd grows quiet, then breaks into focused talk.
- Fast clear: Spire Seekers cheer first.
- Mercy-first clear: Last Light Concord members bow their heads.
- Extraction: Salvage Union staff move before the crowd reacts.
- Forced retreat: Wardens create space and stop mockery from becoming harassment.
- Illegal entry consequence: Wardens and Codebreakers both move closer.

Who Approaches First:

- GUIDY if no one is dying.
- Hesta Winch if extraction was used.
- Marik if heat, illegal entry, public danger, or near-death clear occurred.
- Sponsor representative if sponsored.
- Felix if treasure, map, or market angle is obvious.
- Aria if the party's story has public emotional force.
- Ira if legal flags changed.

Public Record Examples:

- `TEAM [NAME]: ORIENTATION TRIAL 1 CLEAR. THRESHOLD WEIGHED. METHOD: CLEAN ALIGNMENT.`
- `TEAM [NAME]: ORIENTATION TRIAL 1 CLEAR. METHOD: FAST ROUTE. COST RECORDED.`
- `TEAM [NAME]: CHECKPOINT CONTACT. RETURNED TO PREPARE.`
- `TEAM [NAME]: EXTRACTED FROM ORIENTATION TRIAL 1. BEACON STATUS: DAMAGED.`
- `TEAM [NAME]: ORIENTATION TRIAL 1 CLEAR. IRREGULAR ENTRY MARK RETAINED.`

Life Counters:

- Clear: A thin white line appears under the life number.
- Scar: A small sensory tell appears near the counter.
- Debt-shadowed: A red pulse travels once around the counter.
- Heat-marked: Amber ring remains until Warden review or future restraint.
- Mercy-first: A pale-gold fleck appears for one breath, then fades.

Rumors Begin:

- "They told the Tower why they came."
- "The training door made them choose honestly."
- "Someone saw a sponsor mark on their training clear."
- "Extraction worked, but it looked like being pulled through glass."
- "The Tower wrote a warning before letting them out."

Prices Shift:

- Clean clear: Reliable maps hold price; legal copies cheaper by 2 NC.
- Fast costly clear: Speed gear rises by 2 NC for the day.
- Extraction: Beacon rentals require higher deposits unless Hesta approves.
- Mercy-first: Last Light services discount by 2 NC.
- Illegal entry: Warden gear certification costs 5 NC more.

Private Word:

Choose one NPC based on outcome:

- GUIDY wants to debrief.
- Marik wants an official note.
- Felix wants to price the story.
- Kessa or Sel wants to know what the Tower did with vulnerability.
- CodeX wants floor data.
- Aazoth visits in dream if mercy or consent mattered.

If the Party Hides Its Result:

They can cover details with Deception or Performance DC 14. Success hides emotional details, not the public record. Partial success hides one embarrassing element but creates rumor. Failure lets a faction shape the story first.

## First Post-Training Downtime

Time Passing: The first downtime usually lasts one evening and one night. The party can take a long rest unless public trouble, untreated injury, or legal heat makes rest contested. Even then, rest is possible after one scene of triage, negotiation, or shelter.

Rest Available:

- Convergence Point Tavern: public and story-rich.
- Warden witness rooms: secure for heat/protected status.
- Salvage Union recovery bunks: practical after extraction.
- Last Light quiet room: best for scars and fear.
- Pixel Promenade capsule: convenient but watched.

Services:

- Medical care: 5 NC for wound treatment; 10 NC for scar quieting attempt with advantage.
- Legal review: 5 NC for ruling/floor record copy; free with strong Ledger Court reputation.
- Social reputation repair: 5-15 NC in drinks, public apology, or performance support.
- Relic identification: Arcana service 8 NC, or self-check Arcana DC 14.
- Scar quieting: See scar table; most need a small scene, honest statement, or service.

Identify Relics/Boons: A PC can identify one boon during a short rest with Arcana, Religion, or Investigation DC 13. GUIDY can explain public parts, but not private drawbacks. Felix can appraise market value, not moral meaning.

Follow Up on Clues: Let the party pursue one clue before the next expedition without losing rest: Executioner signs, debt reflection, sponsor influence, Renn Vale's party, Mercy Echo, or route token.

Spend NC: Use the Forecourt shopping list from Chunk 02 and adjust prices by outcome.

Faction Reputation: Update one reputation up and one down if the training result strongly points that way. Keep changes small after Trial 1; the party is noticed, not famous.

Prep for Next Expedition: Ask the party whether they want to enter a portal world, continue optional orientation training, research, buy gear, change sponsor status, repair debt/heat flags, or rest fully.

### Downtime Scene 1. GUIDY Debrief

Read-Aloud:

> GUIDY appears in a tabletop reflection, then rotates upside down before correcting itself. "Your survival has improved my confidence model. My confidence model is still screaming."

NPC Goal: GUIDY wants accurate floor data and to learn whether its advice helped.

Player Choice: Give full debrief, conceal details, ask GUIDY about the floor rule, comfort it, or demand better support.

Check/DC: Persuasion DC 12 reassures GUIDY; Arcana DC 14 helps it parse a glitched backdoor record.

Reward: GUIDY grants one `Training Note`: advantage on one check to interpret a public Tower or portal prompt during the next expedition.

Consequence: Concealed details make GUIDY less useful when similar danger appears.

Hook to Next Expedition: GUIDY identifies a repeated phrase: "weight becomes direction."

### Downtime Scene 2. Marik's Official Note

Read-Aloud:

> Marik places a blue-stamped slip on the table. "This is not a citation unless you make it one. Tell me which version of the record I am going to believe."

NPC Goal: Marik wants clean public safety record and honest explanation of heat, extraction, or illegal entry.

Player Choice: Explain truth, minimize trouble, ask for Warden advice, challenge authority.

Check/DC: Persuasion DC 13 for honest cooperation; Deception DC 15 hides one detail but risks later heat; Insight DC 12 shows Marik respects restraint more than perfection.

Reward: Warden note reduces one future heat complication by 1 step.

Consequence: If lied to and caught, heat increases by 1.
