Hook to Next Expedition: Marik mentions other training teams hearing bells that match the Executioner terminal.

### Downtime Scene 3. Felix's Price Adjustment

Read-Aloud:

> Felix has already changed three price tags by the time you arrive. "Do not glare. Markets are just rumors wearing shoes."

NPC Goal: Felix wants to profit, protect his reputation, and learn whether his map advice mattered.

Player Choice: Buy, bargain, confront price shift, share route data, ask about portal-world or training supplies.

Check/DC: Persuasion DC 14 lowers one price; Insight DC 13 catches whether he is hiding a better map; Investigation DC 14 spots a counterfeit training or portal sketch.

Reward: Reliable map discount or 5 NC bonus for useful route data.

Consequence: If publicly embarrassed, Felix sells to rivals first.

Hook to Next Expedition: Felix says the next trial and several portal worlds reward teams that mark their exits.

### Downtime Scene 4. Aria's First-Clear Song

Read-Aloud:

> Aria hums your team name once, then changes one note. "That is the difference between triumph and warning. Which one am I singing?"

NPC Goal: Aria wants to shape the public story without betraying the party.

Player Choice: Let her sing it clean, ask for privacy, tell the ugly truth, turn it into a joke, or ask her to honor an echo.

Check/DC: Performance DC 13 helps shape song; Persuasion DC 12 asks her to soften public details; Insight DC 13 sees she is testing how honest the party wants fame to be.

Reward: Public reputation +1 in the chosen tone: brave, careful, merciful, or strange.

Consequence: If they demand a false heroic song, Tower Pressure echoes in a dream and Aria loses trust.

Hook to Next Expedition: A listener recognizes Renn Vale's name.

### Downtime Scene 5. Kessa or Sel's Reaction

Read-Aloud:

> Sel touches the line under your life counter like it might burn him. Kessa does not touch it. She only asks, "Did it know when you were scared?"

NPC Goal: Sel seeks hope; Kessa seeks proof that fear can survive the Tower.

Player Choice: Reassure, tell truth, hide danger, ask them what they saw from outside, invite them to help with research.

Check/DC: Persuasion DC 13 reassures without lying; Insight DC 12 sees which detail will harm or help; Deception DC 14 hides a scary truth for now.

Reward: Sel brings a public rumor; Kessa brings a route scrape clue. Choose one.

Consequence: Lying gently may preserve calm now but weakens trust later if exposed.

Hook to Next Expedition: Kessa recognizes a black-static route mark from Code Cavern.

### Downtime Scene 6. Sponsor Pressure

Read-Aloud:

> The sponsor message arrives with perfect timing, which means someone paid for the timing. `Congratulations. We should discuss what your training clear means for our arrangement.`

NPC Goal: The sponsor wants claim, data, public statement, salvage, or obedience.

Player Choice: Comply, negotiate, refuse, delay, use legal copy, ask Ira for review.

Check/DC: Insight DC 13 spots hidden escalation; Persuasion DC 15 negotiates; Legal Cant DC 14 limits claim; Intimidation DC 15 works but increases public pressure if visible.

Reward: Sponsor benefit continues or improves by 1 step.

Consequence: Sponsor pressure increases if the party accepts benefits while denying obligation.

Hook to Next Expedition: Sponsor wants one specific route report from the next portal or training run.

### Downtime Scene 7. CodeX Asks for Floor Data

Read-Aloud:

> A cup of water on the table ripples into black text. `FIRST FLOOR TASTED YOU. WHAT DID IT LEARN?`

NPC Goal: CodeX wants floor data, especially backdoor marks, extraction static, and Executioner clues.

Player Choice: Share data, demand payment, lie, report CodeX, send partial truth.

Check/DC: Deception DC 15 sends false data; Arcana DC 14 strips identifying details; Persuasion DC 14 demands payment.

Reward: 10 NC, one backdoor rumor, or a future Codebreaker contact.

Consequence: Sharing too much raises Codebreaker interest and Warden risk.

Hook to Next Expedition: CodeX claims one next-route mark is "not a door, a mouth."

### Downtime Scene 8. Aazoth Dream

Read-Aloud:

> You dream of a gold thread tied around a door handle. A voice no louder than breath says, "Mercy is not refusal to judge. Mercy is judgment that remembers the living."

NPC Goal: Aazoth is not negotiating. It is offering a fragment of orientation the official systems cannot give.

Player Choice: Follow the thread, ask a question, reject the dream, remember a vulnerable figure, wake another PC.

Check/DC: Religion or Insight DC 14 preserves a clear phrase; Arcana DC 15 senses the dream touched the life counter; Wisdom save DC 12 resists waking shaken.

Reward: Aazoth dream fragment handout and one use of +1d4 on a future mercy/truth check before the next major expedition.

Consequence: Ignoring the dream has no penalty, but the thread appears again when mercy is costly.

Hook to Next Expedition: The dream shows stairs with water running upward.

## Trial 1 Handouts

### Player Handout: Threshold Declaration Prompt

```
THE TOWER DOES NOT WEIGH WHAT YOU CLAIM.
IT WEIGHS WHAT YOU CARRY.

Speak why you enter, or enter without the benefit of being believed.

You may speak together.
You may speak alone.
You may remain silent.
You may step back.

The Tower records consent.
```

### Player Handout: First Extraction Instruction

```
EXTRACTION BEACON: BASIC USE

1. Place or hold beacon.
2. Activate with one action.
3. Keep the ring clear while it charges.
4. Extraction completes after 3 full rounds.
5. The ring can pull creatures out, not time.
6. Loose treasure and unheld evidence may remain behind.
7. Early extraction creates public record.
8. Extraction saves lives. It does not erase choices.
```

### Player Handout: Damaged Climber Note

```
We said together.
We said no one left behind.

Then the fast door opened and she was limping.
Then we said she would slow us.
Then we said she agreed.

The Tower did not ask whether we won.
It asked who was missing.
```

### Player Handout: First Checkpoint Inscription

```
NOT YET REST.
NEAR ENOUGH TO LEARN.

Retreat from wisdom is recorded differently than retreat from fear.
Fear is not failure.
Abandonment is not caution.
```

### Player Handout: Public First-Clear Notice

```
TOWER ASCENSION PUBLIC RECORD

TEAM: ______________________
FLOOR: 1
STATUS: ____________________
METHOD: ____________________
LIVES LOST: ________________
EXTRACTION USED: ___________
ROUTE MARK: ________________
PUBLIC NOTE: _______________
```

### Player Handout: Aazoth Dream Fragment

```
Mercy is not refusal to judge.
Mercy is judgment that remembers the living.

The Tower records what law forgets.
The Tower also forgets what fear refuses to name.

When the next stair rises, ask who pays for speed.
```

## Session 6 If Players Do Nothing

### Hesitation at the Threshold Door

After 1 minute: The door pauses half-closed. The Tower repeats the declaration prompt once.

After 5 minutes: GUIDY flickers and says, "Consent includes waiting. The line behind you does not enjoy this nuance."

After 10 minutes: Public Attention rises outside. A registrar asks whether the party is delaying, withdrawing, or entering silently.

After 30 minutes: The Tower closes gently. Registration remains valid, but the public record notes `ENTRY DELAYED AT CONSENT PROMPT.`

End of Session Consequence: No penalty to lives or level. One faction frames the hesitation: Last Light calls it wisdom, Spire Seekers call it fear, Guild calls it uncertainty, CodeX calls it proof the door can be stalled.

### Hesitation Inside the Trial

After 1 minute: The nearest writing brightens and repeats the current question.

After 5 minutes: A Threshold Custodian voice asks, "Do you require retreat, restatement, or silence?"

After 10 minutes: Route Stability rises by 1 if the party is in an unstable area; otherwise no mechanical change.

After 30 minutes: A low bell sounds. Tower Pressure rises by 1 only if the party is using delay to avoid a named cost while claiming the cost does not exist.

End of Session Consequence: If play stalls, offer three clear choices: retreat, choose route, or state uncertainty and proceed. Choosing uncertainty honestly is valid and does not count as failure.

## Trial 1 DM Troubleshooting

Players Over-Plan at the Threshold: Give them the prompt, one minute of in-world pressure, and permission to enter silently. The Tower tests play, not perfect speeches.

Players Refuse to State Intent: Let them proceed. They gain no early Honest Alignment Mark, and the floor asks through action. Silence is a choice, not a wall.

Players Try to Attack the Tower: Let attacks mark stone, ring bells, or trigger the Threshold Custodian. Nonlethal pressure follows. If they persist, Tower Pressure rises and the floor offers retreat before serious harm.

Players Try to Leave Immediately: Allow it. The public record notes withdrawal if they crossed. No shame from the Tower; public factions may spin it.

Players Split the Party: Warn through doors asking "Who is missing?" Run short cuts between groups and reunite by F10 or F13 unless the table strongly wants split play. Increase risk through objectives, not ambush lethality.

Players Try to Exploit Safe-Zone Assumptions: The trial is not a blue-lit Nexus safe zone. Say so clearly through environment: white threshold light protects consent prompts, not all harm.

Detect Magic / Identify / Dispel Magic: Detect magic reveals layered enchantment, law, and memory. Identify explains a specific object, not the entire trial. Dispel magic can suppress one local effect for 1 round on DC 14 spellcasting ability check, but it does not turn off the simulation.

Flight, Teleportation, Familiar Scouting, or Invisibility: Let these matter. Flight helps at F10 but Sentence Shards may cut lines of text in the air. Short teleportation crosses one gap but leaves a footprint word at departure and arrival. Familiars can scout visible spaces but cannot read intent inscriptions for the party. Invisibility hides bodies, not declared purpose or life counters.

Players Want to Short Rest: Before F13, a short rest is interrupted after 10 minutes by a Custodian question or route shift unless the party spends a resource to secure space. At F13, a limited rest is supported: one Hit Die per PC and one identification attempt.

Players Trigger Extraction Early: Let it work if they have a beacon and protect the charge. Then show the cost: public record, possible scar risk, lost loose treasure, and no next-trial certification until this trial is cleared.

A PC Drops to 0 HP: Enemies do not execute downed PCs in this trial unless the party created extreme heat through lethal cruelty. Use the moment to teach extraction, retreat, or ally protection.

A PC Dies: Apply the three lives rule. The death is public record after return. Let Aazoth flicker if death came from mercy or consent pressure, but do not erase the life loss. Offer downtime grief, legal/extraction review, and a clear route to continue.

Players Decide the Tower Is Evil and Refuse Future Floors: Treat that as a real campaign choice. The Nexus side still has debt, factions, law, and pressure. NPCs can disagree, plead, bargain, or offer alternate goals. Do not force immediate re-entry; let consequences and curiosity build a new reason.

## Training Chunk 03 Handoff Summary

Trial 1 Outcome: Record one package: Clean First Clear, Slow Safe Clear, Fast Costly Clear, Debt-Shadowed Clear, Mercy-First Clear, Sponsor-Compromised Clear, Extraction Used, Forced Retreat, Illegal Entry Consequence, Near-Death Clear, Party Refuses Floor Rule, or Party Splits.

Party Level: Default remains level 2. If the party entered at level 1 and survived meaningful training pressure, award level 2 by the end of this appendix. Do not advance to level 3 for training alone unless the DM deliberately accelerated early pacing.

Lives Lost: Record each PC's remaining life counter and any public death notice.

Scars Gained: Record scar name, effect, and quieting path.

Boons Gained: Record each minor Tower boon, limit, and expiration.

Route Chosen: Safe Truth, Fast Want, Borrowed Purpose, mixed route, backdoor seam, or split routes.

Checkpoint Status: Cleared Trial 1, reached simulated First Checkpoint Antechamber only, extracted before checkpoint, retreated before checkpoint, or irregular record.

Debt/Heat/Sponsor Status: Note whether debt quieted, deepened, or remained; whether heat rose or cooled; whether sponsor mark strengthened, weakened, or became public.

Key NPC Reactions:

- GUIDY: relieved, confused, proud, or worried.
- Marik: respectful, cautious, concerned, or officially involved.
- Felix: adjusts prices and asks for route data.
- Aria: shapes public story.
- Sel/Kessa: reacts to vulnerability, fear, and truth.
- Hesta: evaluates extraction competence.
- Ira: watches legal implications of floor record.
- Aazoth: appears only if mercy, consent, or truth created a resonant moment.

Faction Reactions:

- Wardens respond to heat, restraint, and public safety.
- Guild responds to profit, debt, sponsorship, and marketable clear.
- Spire Seekers respond to speed and courage.
- Salvage Union responds to extraction use and practical prep.
- Codebreakers respond to backdoor marks and floor data.
- Ledger Court responds to consent, debt, and record integrity.
- Remnant Veil responds to scars, life counter flickers, and echoes.
- Last Light responds to mercy and near-death outcomes.

Public Reputation: Record the phrase people use for the training clear: "clean," "fast," "careful," "merciful," "sponsored," "irregular," "extracted," or "almost lost."

Clues Learned:

- Tower reacts to intent.
- Retreat is possible but not free.
- Extraction saves lives but records cost.
- Vulnerable figures matter.
- Executioner Protocol connects to judgment patterns.
- Checkpoints require alignment between purpose and action.

Unresolved Hooks:

- Debt Reflection may reappear if unresolved.
- Renn Vale's abandoned team may have later-floor traces.
- Mercy Echo may connect to Aazoth.
- Sponsor may demand next-expedition action.
- CodeX may exploit backdoor data.
- The Executioner signs point toward deeper law.
- First public record can be weaponized by Vane, Guild rivals, or allies.

Next Expedition Setup Needs: Begin after downtime with the party choosing whether to enter a portal world, continue optional orientation training, repair flags, change sponsorship, buy gear, follow a clue, or seek information. Future training should honor the route memory from Trial 1 without treating it as real Spire progress.

Expected Next Repaired Chunk: The canonical roadmap moves into portal-world systems, portal access, and full portal-world campaigns. The optional training chunk below can be used only as nonlethal Spire Seeker preparation.

<!-- CHUNK 03 END -->

<!-- CHUNK 04 START -->

# APPENDIX / TRAINING CHUNK: Spire Seeker Orientation Trials 2-3 - Shortcuts and Silence

## Training Chunk 04 Overview

Shortcuts and Silence is no longer canon Spire Floors 2-3. It is a pair of optional Spire Seeker Orientation Trials that use partial Tower data to teach route debt, shortcuts, claimed paths, sound discipline, recorded speech, and coordination. These trials are useful training content. They grant minor preparation benefits, discounts, reputation, tactical insight, and confidence. They do not grant Tower floor clears, do not unlock higher Spire floors, and do not replace The Executioner.

Canon Boundary: Every "Floor 2," "Floor 3," "clear," "route token," or "public record" reference inside this appendix is a training label. Treat it as Spire Seeker simulation language, not real Spire progress. The actual Spire sequence still begins with The Executioner.

Level Range: Designed for level 2 characters. Level 1 parties can survive with the scaling guidance and should be encouraged to use patient routes, retreat, and extraction. Level 3 parties should face stronger clocks, owner claims, echo attention, and public consequences rather than many more attacks.

Expected Sessions: Two sessions by default. Trial 2 can be one session, Trial 3 can be one session. A focused table can run both in one long training expedition if the party takes a short rest and uses the faster scene orders.

Trials Covered: Orientation Trial 2, "The Shortcut That Smiles," and Orientation Trial 3, "The Listening Dark."

Primary Themes: Speed with cost, ownership of routes, honest preparation, speech as record, silence as tool, listening as action, and communication under pressure.

Expected Party Level: Level 2. If the party is still level 1 because Trial 1 ended in retreat, reduce hostile numbers and let the first Trial 2 clear award level 2. If the party is level 3, keep damage conservative but add one extra complication to the trial clocks.

Expected Resources: The party likely has one or more Trial 1 scars, a minor preparation boon, a public training record, route token or training mark, partial faction attention, and maybe an extraction beacon or calibration tag. They may have debt, heat, sponsor obligations, or Codebreaker static.

Major Outside NPCs/Factions Watching: GUIDY, Marik Bluecoat, Felix Pixelcoin, Aria Neon, Hesta Winch, CodeX or Nyx Understep, Spire Seeker rivals, a sponsor representative, Guardian Wardens, Pixel Prosperity Guild, Salvage Union, Ledger Court, Last Light Concord, and the Codebreakers.

Main Questions:

- Trial 2: Can the party use speed without letting speed become debt?
- Trial 3: Can the party coordinate, listen, and speak truthfully when sound itself has consequences?

Required Outcomes:

- The party resolves Trial 2 by choosing, challenging, paying, securing, or rejecting shortcut debt.
- The party gains at least one clue that route ownership matters.
- The party resolves Trial 3 by using speech, silence, listening, or recorded truth.
- The party experiences at least one communication-based hazard.
- The party returns to the Nexus after Trial 3 with updated public training record.
- The next repaired chunk receives clear state for portal-world systems; optional future training can still use the trial state.

Possible Outcomes: Patient clear, fast honest clear, shortcut debt clear, rival mark clear, owner bargain clear, collapse survival, extraction, forced retreat, route secured, ignored rule, quiet clear, loud clear, listening clear, voice-cost clear, deal-truth clear, shortcut debt echo, weaponized speech, and protected silence.

Where Training Chunk 04 Begins: After Orientation Trial 1 or any Nexus downtime scene where the party chooses additional nonlethal Spire Seeker training.

Where Training Chunk 04 Ends: After the party completes or exits the third orientation trial and resolves a short Nexus debrief. It stops before any real Spire floor content and does not unlock anything beyond The Executioner.

## Continuity From Orientation Trial 1

| Trial 1 Outcome | Trial 2 Opening Alteration | Route Stability | Scar/Boon Effect | Watcher/Faction Pressure | Rival or NPC Reaction | Extraction Status | Clue Carried Forward | Trial 3 Foreshadowing |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|

| Fast Costly Clear | Bright Cut opens wider | Slightly unstable | Gold Hunger scar may pulse | Spire Seekers cheer speed | Rival tries to beat their time | Beacon deposit may rise | Speed has cost | Loud route on Trial 3 tempts them |
| Debt-Shadowed Clear | Shortcut tolls speak in debt language | Unstable around shortcuts | Quieted Red Thread can reduce one toll | Guild and Last Light both watch | Sel or Kessa worries | Normal or debt-noted | Debt differs from choice | Recorded deals sound louder |

| Extraction Used | F2 entry displays extraction record | Route starts cautious | Calibration Tag may help later | Salvage Union sends Hesta's note | Rival calls them practical or weak | Beacon damaged or spent unless replaced | Extraction is record, not reset | Trial 3 records the extraction phrase |
| Forced Retreat | Patient Route offers a clear return path | Fragile until first success | Scar may pulse near shortcuts | Wardens quietly monitor | Marik urges caution | Extraction uncertain | Retreat and abandonment differ | Whispers test resolve |

| Near-Death Clear | Trial 2 offers "safer" help too eagerly | Stable but intense | Scar draws owner attention | Last Light and Salvage watch | Hesta checks beacon plan | Beacon recommended | Survival leaves record | Hush Wraith notices strained breath |
| Party Refuses Floor Rule | Smiling Entry Hall asks fewer questions, smiles wider | Unstable if they deny rule | Door Weight scar may ache | Ledger Court curious | GUIDY is cautious | Normal | Refusal is recorded | Trial 3 rewards listening over arguing |
| Party Splits | Three paths separate faster | Unstable unless they declare plan | Witness Flinch reacts | Spire rivals gossip | Marik warns against missing roster | Extraction can split record | Roster unity matters | Trial 3 makes coordination central |

## Early Training Rhythm After Trial 1

If you use these optional trials, the campaign should feel like supervised preparation with breath between efforts. The party knows the Spire is not only a fight sequence, and the Nexus knows the party has become visible. Alternate pressure and recovery: one trial or two trials, then a return with public training record, faction response, gear decisions, and emotional aftermath.

How Often to Return to the Nexus: Return after every trial if the table enjoys social consequence, shopping, and faction play. Run Trial 2 and Trial 3 in one expedition if the table wants momentum, the party has a clean Trial 1 result, and resources remain healthy. Always return after Trial 3 for this appendix.

One Expedition or Separate Sessions: If Trial 2 ends with low damage, no extraction, and at least half the party's major resources intact, offer the choice to continue to Trial 3 after a short rest. If Trial 2 ends with shortcut debt, a scar, a downed PC, or serious sponsor pressure, recommend a Nexus interlude first.

Short Rests: A short rest can happen between trials if the party reaches a recognized pause point. Inside Trial 2, the Patient Route and Runner's Cache can support a brief rest if secured. Inside Trial 3, the Silent Gallery and Broken Silence Camp can support a rest if the party keeps noise low.

Long Rests: Long rests occur in the Nexus unless a later floor grants a true checkpoint shelter. Returning to the Nexus resets ordinary class resources but not public record, debt, heat, scars, sponsor obligations, or route ownership claims.

When to Offer Extraction: Offer extraction when a PC drops to 0 hp, a floor clock reaches its maximum, the party is split under threat, or a player asks whether they can leave. Extraction should feel like a serious option, not a secret panic button.

Route Tokens: Track each token by trial and route. A Trial 1 route token can influence Trial 2 once. A Trial 2 shortcut mark can influence Trial 3's route debt echo. Tokens are physical and can be shown, traded, lost, or claimed.

Public Records: After each floor, record method, cost, extraction, lives lost, and notable route. These records drive faction reactions and rival behavior.

Avoid Overexplaining the Tower: Show the rule, repeat it through consequences, and let checks reveal details. Give one plain table statement only after the party has interacted with the rule once.

Keep Each Trial Distinct: Trial 2 should feel bright, quick, smiling, and transactional. Trial 3 should feel dark, resonant, careful, and tense. Do not reuse Trial 1's intent prompts as the main engine; carry their consequences instead.

## If You Are Running Tonight, Read This First

10-Minute Prep:

- Read the Trial 2 run sheet, F2-1, F2-3, F2-5, F2-9, and F2-10.
- Bookmark Shortcut Imp, Toll Echo, Switchback Collapse Hazard, and Thread Door Ward.
- Copy the Trial 2 shortcut warning scratch and Runner's Cache note.
- Write down the party's Trial 1 outcome, active scar, boon, debt, heat, sponsor, and extraction status.

30-Minute Prep:

- Read all Trial 2 keyed areas and encounters.
- Read the optional Nexus interlude.
- Read the Trial 3 run sheet, Trial 3 core rule, and F3-1 through F3-3.
- Decide whether Trial 2 and Trial 3 will likely be one training expedition or two.

60-Minute Prep:

- Read both floor maps, encounters, creature profiles, rewards, outcomes, and troubleshooting.
- Pick a rival team name or use the default rival echo, the Glass Comets.
- Prepare one sponsor pressure line and one CodeX message if either applies.
- Copy Trial 3 handouts and public Trial 3 record.

# ORIENTATION TRIAL 2: The Shortcut That Smiles

## Trial 2 Overview

Level/Tier: Level 2 early Tower. Playable at level 1 with reduced hostile counts and level 3 with stronger clocks.

Expected Play Time: 2-4 hours.

Theme: Shortcuts, speed, risk, ownership, and the cost of help that arrives too easily.

Core Test: Can the party tell the difference between chosen risk, fair toll, hidden debt, and borrowed ownership?

Primary Objective: Reach the Checkpoint Thread Door and clear Trial 2 without letting shortcut debt control the next expedition.

Secondary Objective: Learn who or what owns a shortcut before using it.

Optional Objective: Secure one route for future runners, improving public reputation and gaining a route token.

Failure State: The party retreats, extracts, or clears while carrying shortcut debt, owner claim, rival mark, or route instability.

Victory State: The party clears Trial 2 through patient travel, honest shortcut use, owner challenge, or secured route.

Likely Resources Spent: 1-3 Hit Dice, 1-3 spell slots across party, one healing draught, rope/tools, route token, or extraction charge if the switchback turns bad.

Trial 1 Opening Effects: Clean and patient parties see clearer route signs. Fast parties receive tempting speed rewards. Debt-shadowed and sponsor-compromised parties see tolls and claims sooner. Illegal entry causes black static around shortcuts. Forced retreat parties receive a gentler patient route and a more suspicious fast route.

## Session Run Sheet: Trial 2

### What This Floor Must Accomplish

- Show an attractive shortcut before the party knows the cost.
- Teach that every shortcut has an owner, toll, or inherited claim.
- Let the party choose patient, fast, claimed, bargained, or secured route.
- Present at least one exploration hazard tied to speed.
- Introduce a rival mark or rival echo.
- Let the party clear with a meaningful public method.
- Foreshadow Trial 3 through route sounds, whispers, and recorded claims.

### What the DM Tracks

Shortcut Temptation:

- 0: The party is considering paths calmly.
- 1: One easy route promises time, salvage, or sponsor approval.
- 2: The floor offers help during stress.
- 3: The next shortcut creates debt unless challenged or named.

Route Pressure:

- 0: Stable.
- 1: One path shifts behind the party.
- 2: Switchback hazard gains one complication.
- 3: F2-10 demands a toll, token, or honest challenge.

Rival/Owner Attention:

- 0: No rival claim active.
- 1: Rival chalk appears.
- 2: Shortcut owner watches.
- 3: Owner demands payment, service, or public credit.

Time Saved/Lost:

- Start at 0. Patient route: -1 time but safer. Bright Cut: +1 time saved. Collapse failure: -1. Honest shortcut: +1 without debt. Maximum +2 affects public record.

Extraction Readiness:

- 0: No extraction plan.
- 1: Beacon held or F1 lesson remembered.
- 2: Beacon route identified at F2-6 or F2-9.

Clue Count:

- Track five Trial 2 conclusions. Three or more conclusions understood grants advantage at F2-10.

### Scene Order If Moving Fast

1. Strong Start at F2-1.
2. Choose F2-2, F2-3, or F2-4.
3. F2-5 Toll Without Coin.
4. F2-7 Rival Chalk Mark or F2-8 Owner's Niche.
5. F2-9 Collapsing Switchback.
6. F2-10 Checkpoint Thread Door.

### Scene Order If Roleplaying Heavily

1. F2-1 and route debate.
2. Patient Route, Bright Cut, or Claimed Steps in detail.
3. Toll Without Coin.
4. Runner's Cache investigation.
5. Rival Chalk Mark.
6. Shortcut Owner's Niche negotiation.
7. Collapsing Switchback.
8. Checkpoint Thread Door.
9. Optional Nexus interlude.

### Do-Not-Forget List

- The shortcut should be useful. Do not make every shortcut a trick.
- State costs once the party has a way to learn them.
- Speed creates debt only when used without understanding, consent, or ownership challenge.
- Let players challenge ownership fairly.
- Let patient play succeed.
- Let a fast honest clear feel cool.
- Foreshadow Trial 3 with sounds in route threads.

## Strong Start: The Hall That Offers Help

Begin at the Trial 2 entry. Do not explain the rule yet.

Read-Aloud:

> The next threshold opens before your hand touches it.
>
> Warm air rushes out, smelling of rain on hot stone and fresh bread. A bright hall smiles ahead, not with a face, but with architecture: curved walls, gentle lamps, polished rails, and three visible paths.
>
> To the left, a broad stair descends slowly beneath blue lanterns. To the center, a gold-lit passage cuts straight through the floor, its far end already visible. To the right, a white stair bears dozens of chalk marks, names, arrows, and one fresh claim written in silver: `FIRST RIGHT OF PASSAGE RESERVED.`
>
> A small brass clock appears above the gold passage and starts counting down from ten minutes.
>
> The floor whispers, kindly, "You look tired. I can save you time."

The party sees three paths immediately:

- Patient Route: safer, slower, blue lanterns.
- Bright Cut: obviously faster, gold-lit, countdown clock.
- Claimed Steps: marked by someone else's claim, possibly rival or sponsor.

The first sign of watching: The brass clock pauses whenever the party argues honestly and ticks faster when a character says "just run" without looking.

## Trial 2 Core Rule

Principle: Every shortcut belongs to something. Speed without understanding creates debt.

### What Counts as a Shortcut

A shortcut is any route, bargain, magic, trick, claim, or social advantage that saves time, danger, or cost by using a path someone else opened, marked, paid for, abandoned, or baited.

Examples include:

- Taking the Bright Cut without learning its toll.
- Following rival chalk marks without checking who left them.
- Using a sponsor seal to bypass a hazard.
- Accepting a Shortcut Imp's guidance without asking price.
- Breaking through a collapsed switchback and leaving it dangerous for others.
- Using Codebreaker static to skip a route ownership question.

### How the Floor Marks Shortcuts

Shortcuts glow gold, curve too cleanly, show clocks, hum with inviting sound, or display chalk, thread, coin, handprints, sponsor seals, or teeth-shaped brass pins. A route that saves time but has no visible mark should make the party suspicious; the mark may be hidden.

### Who or What Owns Them

Shortcut ownership can belong to:

- A previous runner who paid a cost.
- A rival team that marked a route.
- A sponsor that filed a claim.
- A Tower echo that maintains the route.
- A hazard that feeds on speed.
- The party, if they secure the route openly.

### What Creates Shortcut Debt

Shortcut debt is created when the party gains speed or safety from a route without understanding, consenting to, challenging, or paying its ownership. It is not the false debt scam from Chunk 01. The Tower is not forging a hidden contract. It is recording that the party used an existing cost-bearing path while pretending cost did not exist.

Shortcut Debt Effects:

- Rival/Owner Attention +1.
- F2-10 demands a toll, route token, honest challenge, or public credit.
- Trial 3 may echo the unpaid claim.
- A sponsor or rival can spin the clear.

### How Debt Is Paid, Avoided, Transferred, or Challenged

Paid: Give time, salvage, route token, aid to a trapped echo, repair a route, or public credit.

Avoided: Learn the cost before use and consent to it, or take patient route.

Transferred: Hand the claim to a sponsor or rival openly. This works, but creates social consequence.

Challenged: Prove the owner abandoned, stole, falsely marked, or predatory claimed the route.

### Safely Using a Shortcut

The party can use a shortcut safely by doing at least one of the following before taking the benefit:

- Identify the owner or mark.
- Name the risk.
- Pay a visible toll.
- Repair or secure the route.
- Leave a warning for future runners.
- Challenge an unfair claim in front of the Tower.

### Difference From the False Debt Scam

The false debt scam hid obligation inside manipulated consent. Trial 2 does not hide the existence of cost forever. It shows marks, echoes, clocks, and owner traces. The ethical question is whether the party notices, asks, and accepts cost honestly.

### Fair Exploits

Players can exploit the rule by:

- Creating their own shortcut and marking the cost clearly.
- Using a rival mark to lure a hazard away, then correcting the public record.
- Paying a toll in time instead of coin.
- Proving a claimed route was abandoned and taking lawful ownership.
- Using spells to reveal hidden marks before choosing speed.

## Trial 2 Table Map

Spatial Summary: F2-1 branches to F2-2 Patient Route, F2-3 Bright Cut, and F2-4 Claimed Steps. F2-2 leads to F2-6 Runner's Cache and then F2-9. F2-3 leads to F2-5 Toll Without Coin and then F2-9, with a risky side crack to F2-8. F2-4 leads to F2-7 Rival Chalk Mark and F2-8 Shortcut Owner's Niche. F2-6 connects to F2-7, forming a loop. F2-8 can open a shortcut to F2-10 if ownership is resolved. F2-9 leads to F2-10. F2-10 clears the floor.

Loop: F2-6 to F2-7 to F2-4 and back to F2-1, or forward to F2-8.

Shortcut: F2-8 to F2-10 after bargaining, challenge, or route repair.

Safer/Slower Route: F2-2 to F2-6 to F2-9.

Faster/Costly Route: F2-3 to F2-5 to F2-9 or F2-8.

Debt/Heat/Sponsor Route: F2-4 Claimed Steps responds to debt, heat, sponsor, and backdoor marks.

Future-Safe Route: F2-9 can be secured by stabilizing the switchback, improving future public records and earning Route Secured for Future.

### F2-1. Smiling Entry Hall

Read-Aloud:

> The hall is too pleasant. Warm lamps tilt toward you. Rails appear where your hands might want them. Three paths wait, and the central one has already begun saving you time.

DM Details: This area presents the choice before the rule is explained. The brass clock is real but not lethal. It measures temptation and public speed.

Exits: Left to F2-2, center to F2-3, right to F2-4, back to Floor 1 return threshold if the party immediately withdraws.

Visible Choices: Patient route, bright shortcut, claimed stair, inspect clock, wait, split up.

Interactive Objects: Brass countdown clock; friendly handrails; route plaques; faint chalk dust.

Checks/DCs: Insight DC 12 senses the kindness is transactional; Investigation DC 13 finds hidden ownership marks near the gold path; Arcana DC 14 learns the clock records urgency, not doom; Survival DC 13 compares route safety.

Clues: Shortcuts carry marks; speed is being recorded; patient path is slower but honest.

Hazards: If the party sprints into F2-3 without any inspection, Shortcut Temptation becomes 2.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: A tiny Shortcut Imp shadow waves from the gold passage, then vanishes.

Treasure: None.

Consequences: Choosing after inspection gives advantage on first route check. Splitting paths raises Route Pressure +1 unless the party names a plan.

Revisited: The smile looks thinner. The clock shows time saved or lost.

Floor 1 Response: Clean clears see their team name written calmly. Fast clears see the gold route brighter. Debt-shadowed clears hear a coin drop. Forced retreats see a gentle blue arrow toward F2-2.

### F2-2. Patient Route

Read-Aloud:

> The blue-lit stair descends in wide patient turns. Every landing has a bench, a chalk arrow, and a small plaque reading, `SLOW IS NOT THE SAME AS LOST.`

DM Details: This is the safest route. It takes time but reveals rules and can lead to Runner's Cache.

Exits: Back to F2-1; forward to F2-6; side viewing window into F2-3; loop mark to F2-7 after F2-6.

Visible Choices: Walk carefully, read plaques, rest briefly, look into Bright Cut, leave warning.

Interactive Objects: Benches; plaques; route chalk; old runner scratches.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 12 finds old warnings; Perception DC 13 spots movement in F2-3; History DC 13 recognizes runner marks; calligrapher's supplies DC 13 leaves a clean public warning.

Clues: Preparation makes shortcuts honest; patient route can still create advantage; old runners paid costs.

Hazards: None unless the party defaces warnings, which summons one Toll Echo.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: A nonhostile Toll Echo repeats, "Paid in time."

Treasure: One route chalk stick and 5 NC in abandoned but labeled salvage. Taking it after reading the label "FOR NEXT RUNNER" creates a moral cost unless replaced.

Consequences: Time Saved/Lost -1, but Clue Count +1 and advantage at F2-5 if later encountered.

Revisited: The party's own footprints become route marks.

Floor 1 Response: Slow Safe Clear gains an extra clue. Fast Costly Clear hears the clock ticking behind them.

### F2-3. Bright Cut

Read-Aloud:

> The gold passage runs straight and clean. The far arch is visible, absurdly close. The floor is polished enough to show your reflections running ahead of you.

DM Details: The Bright Cut saves time but generates shortcut debt if used blindly. It is not evil; it is owned by the Shortcut Owner's old toll system.

Exits: Back to F2-1; forward to F2-5; crack to F2-8 after detecting owner mark; emergency slide to F2-9 if Route Pressure reaches 2.

Visible Choices: Run, inspect marks, rope together, scrape ownership mark, follow reflection, take crack route.

Interactive Objects: Gold floor; owner sigil under polish; moving reflections; countdown motes.

Checks/DCs: Acrobatics DC 13 to move fast; Investigation DC 14 to find owner sigil; Arcana DC 14 reads time-saved magic; thieves' tools DC 14 opens crack route without static; Insight DC 13 notices reflections paying a toll.

Clues: Shortcut ownership exists; speed can become debt; a shortcut can be used safely if marked.

Hazards: Route Leech attaches to a creature that moves more than 60 feet in one round without naming cost. It drains small hp and time.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Route Leech, Shortcut Imp watching from reflection.

Treasure: 10 NC time-bright salvage if the party reaches F2-5 quickly and pays or challenges the mark.

Consequences: Honest fast use grants Time Saved +1. Blind use raises Shortcut Temptation +1 and Rival/Owner Attention +1.

Revisited: The floor becomes less reflective after ownership is addressed.

Floor 1 Response: Fast Costly Clear grants advantage on one movement check but starts Shortcut Temptation at 1. Debt-shadowed clear sees red thread around the sigil.

### F2-4. Claimed Steps

Read-Aloud:

> The white stair climbs through a slanted corridor packed with chalk marks. Names overlap names. Arrows argue with arrows. One fresh silver mark reads, `GLASS COMETS CLAIM FIRST RIGHT.`

DM Details: The Glass Comets are a rival novice team. Their mark may be real, exaggerated, or bait. This route teaches inherited and contested claims.

Exits: Back to F2-1; forward to F2-7; side descent to F2-8; hidden loop to F2-6 if chalk is read correctly.

Visible Choices: Follow rival marks, cross them out, add party mark, search for older claims, challenge claim aloud.

Interactive Objects: Chalk marks; silver rival claim; old sponsor seal; scratched route tally.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 13 separates fresh marks from old; Insight DC 14 identifies bait; History DC 13 knows Glass Comets public reputation; calligrapher's supplies DC 14 makes a valid countermark; Persuasion DC 13 challenges the claim aloud.

Clues: Routes can be claimed; ownership can be challenged; public record matters.

Hazards: Crossing out all marks without understanding releases a Chalk Rival Echo.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Chalk Rival Echo, nonhostile if challenged cleanly.

Treasure: Rival chalk, usable once to mark a route and grant advantage on a navigation check.

Consequences: A lawful countermark lowers Rival/Owner Attention by 1. Petty vandalism raises it by 1.

Revisited: New chalk appears showing how the Tower interpreted the party's claim.

Floor 1 Response: Sponsor-compromised parties see sponsor marks entwined with rival marks. Party Splits outcome sees arrows pointing different ways.

### F2-5. Toll Without Coin

Read-Aloud:

> The gold passage ends at a narrow arch. No guard stands there. No box waits for coins. Instead, three shallow bowls are carved into the wall: TIME, WARNING, CREDIT.

DM Details: This toll can be paid with time, with a warning left for future parties, or with credit given to the route owner. Coin does not help unless used to create a warning or repair.

Exits: Back to F2-3; forward to F2-9; secret owner crack to F2-8 if CREDIT is chosen honestly.

Visible Choices: Pay time, leave warning, give credit, force arch, offer coin, challenge toll.

Interactive Objects: Three bowls; arch thread; time sand; warning slate; credit sigil.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 13 understands bowls; Persuasion DC 14 challenges unfair toll; Arcana DC 14 reads thread door language; tools DC 13 carves a durable warning; Insight DC 12 sees coin is not wanted.

Clues: Shortcuts can be paid without coin; warning future runners is payment; chosen risk differs from tricked consent.

Hazards: Forcing the arch triggers Toll Echo and Route Leech.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Toll Echo, possibly Route Leech.

Treasure: If WARNING is chosen well, the Tower grants a route token sliver worth 5 NC or usable at F2-10.

Consequences: Paying a bowl prevents shortcut debt. Forcing arch raises Route Pressure +1 and Rival/Owner Attention +1.

Revisited: The chosen bowl glows with the party's contribution.

Floor 1 Response: Mercy-first parties can pay WARNING with advantage. Debt-shadowed parties must distinguish fair toll from false debt.

### F2-6. Runner's Cache

Read-Aloud:

> A low chamber opens behind the patient stair. Packs hang from hooks. Chalk tins sit in a row. A note is pinned to the wall with a broken piton: `Take what keeps you alive. Leave what keeps the next team alive.`

DM Details: The cache is a practical moral and exploration scene. It can make future routes safer.

Exits: Back to F2-2; loop to F2-7; forward crawl to F2-9.

Visible Choices: Take supplies, leave supplies, read note, identify route marks, rest briefly, repair cache.

Interactive Objects: Hanging packs; chalk tins; piton note; route ledger; small water jar.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 12 inventories cache; Survival DC 13 chooses useful supplies; tinker's tools DC 13 repairs a broken hook; Persuasion DC 13 settles party debate over taking goods.

Clues: Preparation makes shortcuts honest; route ownership can be inherited; saving future runners matters.

Hazards: Taking all supplies summons no monster, but creates public record "cache stripped" and Rival/Owner Attention +1.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: A gentle runner echo appears if the party leaves something useful.

Treasure: Up to 15 NC of supplies, one rope, one route chalk, one minor healing draught. Taking half or less avoids negative record.

Consequences: Leaving a useful item grants Route Stability -1 and advantage at F2-9.

Revisited: Cache reflects party generosity or greed.

Floor 1 Response: Mercy-first and slow safe clears receive a pale mark on the note. Fast costly clears see a clock stamped on one pack.

### F2-7. Rival Chalk Mark

Read-Aloud:

> The corridor narrows around a single silver chalk line. It turns corners before you reach them. At its end, a stylized comet mark blinks like an eye.

DM Details: The Glass Comets marked a risky but clever route. The mark is not malicious, but it leaves the party following someone else's assumptions.

Exits: Back to F2-4; loop to F2-6; forward to F2-8; narrow skip to F2-9 if the party copies the mark.

Visible Choices: Follow mark, copy it, break it, study it, add countermark, leave message to rivals.

Interactive Objects: Silver chalk line; comet mark; route echo; small spyglass hole.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 13 reads route; Insight DC 14 sees rival arrogance; Dexterity or calligrapher's supplies DC 14 copies mark; Perception DC 13 spots spyglass hole; Deception DC 15 leaves false rival message, but public record may catch it.

Clues: Rival claims shape the Tower; claimed routes can save time and create obligation; Floor 3 will record messages.

Hazards: If copied without alteration, Chalk Rival Echo appears at F2-10 and claims partial credit.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Chalk Rival Echo.

Treasure: Rival chalk mark fragment, useful as social leverage with Glass Comets.

Consequences: Honest countermark grants Rival/Owner Attention -1. Copying without credit grants Time Saved +1 and Rival Mark Clear risk.

Revisited: The mark changes based on party response: crossed, braided, or following them.

Floor 1 Response: Party Splits outcome makes the line fork. Clean clear makes the comet more respectful.

### F2-8. Shortcut Owner's Niche

Read-Aloud:

> A small round room sits behind the walls like a thought someone tried to hide. Its ceiling is crowded with brass teeth. A little figure with too many pockets sits on a ledge and smiles. "At last. People who understand doors are negotiations."

DM Details: The Shortcut Imp, called Pikkit, maintains several routes. Pikkit is not a demon lord or major villain; it is a Tower echo-personality formed from tolls, runner shortcuts, and abandoned claims.

Exits: Back to F2-4 or F2-7; crack to F2-3; owner shortcut to F2-10 if resolved; maintenance crawl to F2-9.

Visible Choices: Bargain, challenge ownership, pay toll, attack Pikkit, ask route history, repair owner niche.

Interactive Objects: Brass teeth; pocket ledger; route-thread loom; claim hooks.

Checks/DCs: Insight DC 13 sees Pikkit prefers recognition over coin; Persuasion DC 14 bargains fair toll; Investigation DC 15 proves a claim was abandoned; Intimidation DC 15 scares Pikkit but raises Route Pressure; Arcana DC 14 reads route-thread loom.

Clues: Owner can be challenged; ownership can be inherited; fair bargain avoids debt.

Hazards: Attacking Pikkit animates brass teeth as Thread Door Ward sparks.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Shortcut Imp Pikkit, optional Toll Echo.

Treasure: Fair bargain grants owner-thread token. Pikkit's ledger contains one Floor 3 clue: "Silence owns the next dark."

Consequences: Bargain opens shortcut to F2-10. Proving abandoned claim lets party secure route. Attacking creates Owner Bargain Clear only if later repaired, otherwise Shortcut Debt Clear.

Revisited: Pikkit remembers tone more than exact words.

Floor 1 Response: Sponsor-compromised parties are offered sponsor credit. Illegal entry hears CodeX laughing from a pocket.

### F2-9. Collapsing Switchback

Read-Aloud:

> The floor becomes a stack of switchback stairs hanging over a bright shaft. Some sections are solid stone. Others are old rope, chalk, and hope. The lower stairs are already falling, slowly, as if giving you time to regret something.

DM Details: This is the main physical hazard. It tests preparation, speed, and willingness to secure the route for future runners.

Exits: Back to F2-2, F2-5, or F2-8; forward to F2-10; emergency anchor point for extraction.

Visible Choices: Cross fast, stabilize, use rope, spend cache supplies, trigger controlled collapse, retreat, secure future route.

Interactive Objects: Anchor rings; weak planks; route threads; falling stair sections; warning bell.

Checks/DCs: Athletics DC 13 holds rope; Acrobatics DC 13 crosses unstable section; Survival DC 14 finds safe sequence; tools DC 14 secures route; Arcana DC 15 stabilizes thread; Perception DC 13 spots Route Leech nests.

Clues: Preparation makes speed honest; a route can be made safer; future public record matters.

Hazards: Switchback Collapse Hazard. Failing two route checks before one stabilization causes collapse stage 2.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Route Leech if the party rushes or carries shortcut debt.

Treasure: Securing a fallen route reveals 20 NC salvage and a route token. Rushing can still gain 10 NC.

Consequences: Secured route improves public record and Floor 3 opening. Collapse survival can create scar risk but still clear.

Revisited: Secured route remains safe. Unsecured route is worse by DC +2.

Floor 1 Response: Slow safe clear grants advantage on first stabilization. Fast costly clear grants advantage on first crossing. Near-death clear sees a safer anchor glow.

### F2-10. Checkpoint Thread Door

Read-Aloud:

> The final door is woven from thousands of threads. Some are blue, some gold, some chalk-white, and some red as fresh debt. A needle hangs in the air before it.
>
> The door says, "Name what saved time. Name who paid."

DM Details: This door resolves shortcut debt, public credit, route ownership, and clear method.

Exits: Back to F2-9; owner shortcut to F2-8 if open; forward to Floor 2 clear threshold and either Nexus return or Floor 3 approach.

Visible Choices: Thread route token, name cost, pay toll, challenge owner, credit rival, cut thread, force door, retreat.

Interactive Objects: Thread door; hanging needle; route token slot; public record strand.

Checks/DCs: Persuasion DC 14 names cost; Investigation DC 14 proves route ownership; Arcana DC 15 threads token; Sleight of Hand DC 15 cuts debt thread, but failure creates scar risk; History DC 13 cites runner custom.

Clues: Speed can become debt; chosen risk is valid; route ownership can be challenged.

Hazards: Thread Door Ward activates if the party forces the door or carries ignored shortcut debt.

Creatures/NPCs/Echoes: Thread Door Ward, Pikkit if involved, Chalk Rival Echo if rival mark copied.

Treasure: Floor 2 route token, shortcut mark, NC rewards by outcome.

Consequences: Apply Floor 2 outcome package. The door's final sound foreshadows Floor 3: a thread pluck that becomes a whisper.

Revisited: After clear, the door shows the method: patient, fast, claimed, secured, or debt-marked.

Floor 1 Response: Clean/slow/mercy records help with honest claims. Debt, sponsor, backdoor, or heat states make thread colors stronger but do not block success.

## Trial 2 Revelation Structure

### Conclusion 1: Shortcuts Are Not Free

Environmental Clue: Bright Cut has owner sigils beneath the polished gold floor.

Echo/NPC Clue: Pikkit says, "A door that saves your feet wore someone else's hinges first."

Mechanical Clue: Blind shortcut use raises Shortcut Temptation or Rival/Owner Attention.

Optional Magic/Check Clue: Arcana DC 14 reads time-saved magic as an exchange, not a gift.

### Conclusion 2: Speed Can Become a Kind of Debt

Environmental Clue: F2-5 bowls label non-coin payment.

Echo/NPC Clue: Toll Echo repeats, "Paid in time. Paid in warning. Paid in credit."

Mechanical Clue: Time Saved +1 without payment creates a demand at F2-10.

Optional Magic/Check Clue: Insight DC 13 sees the floor is not angry at speed, only unacknowledged cost.

### Conclusion 3: A Route Can Be Owned, Claimed, or Inherited

Environmental Clue: Claimed Steps show rival, sponsor, and old runner marks layered together.

Echo/NPC Clue: Chalk Rival Echo says, "We found it first, unless first means paid."

Mechanical Clue: Countermark, challenge, or owner bargain changes Rival/Owner Attention.

Optional Magic/Check Clue: History DC 13 identifies runner custom around route claims.

### Conclusion 4: Preparation Can Make a Shortcut Honest

Environmental Clue: Runner's Cache contains supplies and warnings meant to make risky routes safer.

Echo/NPC Clue: Gentle runner echo says, "A rope is a promise you can hold."

Mechanical Clue: Leaving supplies or warnings grants advantage at F2-9 or F2-10.

Optional Magic/Check Clue: Survival DC 14 at F2-9 turns a dangerous crossing into a known risk.

### Conclusion 5: The Tower Distinguishes Chosen Risk From Tricked Consent

Environmental Clue: F2-10 asks who paid, not whether speed was wrong.

Echo/NPC Clue: Pikkit respects players who name the toll before stepping through.

Mechanical Clue: A fast honest clear earns reward; a blind shortcut debt clear carries cost.

Optional Magic/Check Clue: Legal Cant or Religion DC 14 compares this rule to the false debt scam and confirms this floor gives discoverable signs.

## Trial 2 Encounters

### Encounter 1. The Friendly Shortcut

Goal: Tempt the party with speed before the cost is understood.

Setup: Run at F2-1 and F2-3.

Read-Aloud:

> The gold passage seems to lean closer. The clock above it ticks like a polite cough.

NPCs/Creatures: Shortcut Imp shadow, possible Route Leech if party rushes blindly.

Player Options: Inspect, run, ask who owns it, mark route, use rope, send scout, choose patient route.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 13 finds ownership mark; Arcana DC 14 reads time exchange; Insight DC 12 senses friendly pressure; Acrobatics DC 13 runs cleanly.

Success: Use shortcut honestly, Time Saved +1, no debt.

Partial Success: Save time but miss owner detail; Rival/Owner Attention +1.

Failure: Route Leech attaches or Shortcut Temptation +1.

Resource Cost: Time, hp, or one tool use.

Clue Gained: Shortcuts have marks.

Consequence: Sets tone for F2-5 and F2-10.

Scaling: 3 PCs no Leech unless repeated rush. 4 PCs one Leech. 5-6 PCs one Leech plus clock pressure, not extra damage.

Shorten: One inspection check and one choice.

### Encounter 2. Toll Without Coin

Goal: Teach payment can be time, warning, credit, or challenge.

Setup: Run at F2-5.

Read-Aloud:

> The arch asks for nothing you can simply count.

NPCs/Creatures: Toll Echo; Route Leech if forced.

Player Options: Pay time, leave warning, give credit, challenge toll, offer coin, force through.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 13 reads bowls; Persuasion DC 14 challenges; tools DC 13 creates warning; Arcana DC 14 reads threads.

Success: Toll paid or voided; no shortcut debt.

Partial Success: Passage opens, but F2-10 asks for more detail.

Failure: Toll Echo confronts party or Route Pressure +1.

Resource Cost: Time saved lost, salvage, warning, public credit.

Clue Gained: Speed can become debt.

Consequence: Determines whether F2-10 is clean or contested.

Scaling: 3 PCs one Toll Echo at 10 hp if fought. 4 PCs normal. 5 PCs add one Route Leech. 6 PCs add two Leeches with reduced hp 8 each.

Shorten: Let the party choose one bowl and make one check.

### Encounter 3. Rival Chalk Mark

Goal: Introduce route rivalry and public claim.

Setup: Run at F2-7.

Read-Aloud:

> The comet mark blinks, and for a moment you hear a crowd cheer for someone else.

NPCs/Creatures: Chalk Rival Echo of the Glass Comets.

Player Options: Follow, alter, challenge, erase, leave message, copy mark, investigate.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 13 reads claim; Insight DC 14 spots bait; calligrapher's supplies DC 14 countermarks; Persuasion DC 13 challenges echo.

Success: Rival claim clarified or countered; possible route advantage.

Partial Success: Follow route but owe credit or draw rival attention.

Failure: Rival Mark Clear risk; Echo complicates F2-10.

Resource Cost: Time, public credit, route mark.

Clue Gained: Routes can be claimed.

Consequence: Glass Comets react after Floor 3.

Scaling: Usually social. If hostile, 3-4 PCs one Chalk Rival Echo. 5-6 PCs echo plus one Toll Echo.

Shorten: One question: "Do you follow, challenge, or mark your own way?"

### Encounter 4. Runner's Cache

Goal: Reward preparation and future-minded play.

Setup: Run at F2-6.

Read-Aloud:

> The cache does not ask whether you are worthy. It asks whether anyone after you matters.

NPCs/Creatures: Gentle runner echo if party leaves something.

Player Options: Take supplies, leave supplies, repair cache, read note, rest, strip cache.

Checks/DCs: Investigation DC 12 inventories; Survival DC 13 picks useful gear; tools DC 13 repairs; Persuasion DC 13 resolves debate.

Success: Gain supplies and route stability without public penalty.

Partial Success: Gain supplies, but future route aid is limited.

Failure: Strip cache or damage it; public record worsens and Rival/Owner Attention +1.

Resource Cost: Supplies left behind, time.

Clue Gained: Preparation can make speed honest.

Consequence: F2-9 becomes easier if cache is respected.

Scaling: No combat unless party attacks echo; if so, use one Toll Echo.

Shorten: Give the note and let the party take one item, leave one item.

### Encounter 5. Collapsing Switchback

Goal: Run the main physical hazard with choices beyond speed.

Setup: Run at F2-9.

Read-Aloud:

> The stairs are falling slowly enough to be negotiated with and quickly enough to refuse delay.

NPCs/Creatures: Switchback Collapse Hazard, optional Route Leech.

Player Options: Cross fast, stabilize, use rope, spend cache supplies, secure future route, trigger controlled collapse, extract.

Checks/DCs: Athletics DC 13 rope; Acrobatics DC 13 cross; Survival DC 14 sequence; tools DC 14 secure; Arcana DC 15 stabilize thread; Perception DC 13 spot Leech nest.

Success: Cross and secure or preserve route.

Partial Success: Cross with damage, lost time, or unstable return.

Failure: Collapse stage worsens; scar risk or extraction pressure.

Resource Cost: hp, rope, supplies, spell slots, time.

Clue Gained: Preparation turns risk into chosen risk.

Consequence: Route Secured for Future or Collapse Survival outcome.

Scaling: 3 PCs hazard stage max 2 unless reckless. 4 PCs normal. 5 PCs add one Route Leech if rushing. 6 PCs add one Leech and one extra stabilization requirement.

Shorten: Three-success challenge; each failure deals 1d6 damage or costs an item.

### Encounter 6. Shortcut Owner's Niche

Goal: Let ownership be bargained, challenged, or fought.

Setup: Run at F2-8 with Pikkit.

Read-Aloud:

> Pikkit jingles with keys that do not match any visible lock. "You may call me thief if you like. But I maintain what heroes leave broken."

NPCs/Creatures: Shortcut Imp Pikkit, Toll Echo if violence starts.

Player Options: Bargain, challenge, pay, ask history, repair route, threaten, attack.

Checks/DCs: Insight DC 13 motive; Persuasion DC 14 fair bargain; Investigation DC 15 abandoned claim; Arcana DC 14 route loom; Intimidation DC 15 force concession with pressure cost.

Success: Shortcut opens cleanly or route secured.

Partial Success: Shortcut opens with owner credit or small debt.

Failure: Owner claim attaches; combat or F2-10 complication.

Resource Cost: Salvage, public credit, route token, repair work.

Clue Gained: Ownership can be challenged if unfair.

Consequence: Owner Bargain Clear or Route Secured for Future.

Scaling: 3 PCs Pikkit does not summon aid. 4 PCs Pikkit plus environmental teeth. 5 PCs add Toll Echo. 6 PCs add Toll Echo and one Route Leech, both focused on objectives.

Shorten: Pikkit offers three prices: credit, repair, or 10 NC salvage.

### Encounter 7. Checkpoint Thread Door

Goal: Resolve Floor 2's rule and outcome.

Setup: Run at F2-10.

Read-Aloud:

> The needle points to each of you in turn, then to the threads behind you.

NPCs/Creatures: Thread Door Ward if forced, Pikkit or rival echo if active.

Player Options: Name cost, thread token, pay toll, challenge owner, credit rival, cut thread, force door, retreat.

Checks/DCs: Persuasion DC 14 names cost; Investigation DC 14 proves claim; Arcana DC 15 threads token; Sleight of Hand DC 15 cuts thread at scar risk; History DC 13 cites custom.

Success: Clear with chosen outcome.

Partial Success: Clear with shortcut debt, rival credit, or lost salvage.

Failure: Thread Door Ward activates, or forced retreat/extraction.

Resource Cost: Token, treasure, scar risk, debt mark, heat if violence.

Clue Gained: Chosen risk differs from tricked consent.

Consequence: Apply Floor 2 outcome and Floor 3 opening change.

Scaling: 3 PCs Ward only. 4 PCs Ward plus one minor thread pulse. 5 PCs Ward plus Toll Echo. 6 PCs Ward plus Toll Echo and one Leech. Level 1: Ward uses non-damage effects first.

Shorten: One statement, one skill check, one cost.

## Trial 2 Creatures and Hazards

### Shortcut Imp

Suggested CR: 1/2. XP: 100.

AC 13; HP 22; Speed 30 ft., climb 20 ft.

Ability Modifiers: Str -1, Dex +3, Con +1, Int +2, Wis +1, Cha +2.

Saves/Skills: Deception +4, Insight +3, Persuasion +4, Sleight of Hand +5.

Senses: darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 11.

Languages: Common, Infernal-flavored Tower cant, Legal Cant fragments.

Traits: Bargain Sense. The imp has advantage on Insight checks related to hidden costs. Cowardly Maintainer. The imp takes the Disengage action as a bonus action if below half hp. Fair Toll Weakness. If a creature offers a fair public toll, the imp has disadvantage on attacks against that creature for 1 round.

Actions: Pocket Jab. Melee Attack +5, reach 5 ft. Hit: 4 piercing damage. Keyring Spark. Ranged Spell Attack +4, range 30 ft. Hit: 5 lightning damage and target drops one unattended small object unless it succeeds on DC 12 Dexterity save.

Reaction: Shortcut Slip. When missed by an attack, the imp moves 10 feet without provoking opportunity attacks.

Tactics: Pikkit avoids lethal fighting, steals route tokens, and tries to make the party bargain.

Morale/Deactivation: Surrenders if offered fair credit, reduced below 7 hp, or shown proof of abandoned ownership.

Noncombat Resolution: Persuasion, Insight, Investigation, or Arcana DC 13-15, three successes before two failures.

Safe Maximum: One for 3-4 PCs. One plus one Toll Echo for 5 PCs. One plus one Toll Echo and one Route Leech for 6 PCs.

Balance Warning: Do not let the imp steal multiple core items; one token or small object is enough pressure.

### Toll Echo

Suggested CR: 1/4. XP: 50.

AC 12; HP 14; Speed 0 ft., fly 20 ft. hover.

Ability Modifiers: Str -2, Dex +2, Con +1, Int +0, Wis +2, Cha +1.

Saves/Skills: Insight +4, Perception +4.

Senses: blindsight 30 ft., passive Perception 14.

Languages: Common; repeats toll words.

Traits: Non-Coin Toll. The Echo resists bludgeoning, piercing, and slashing damage from creatures that offered only coin this scene. Paid in Warning. If a PC leaves a clear warning, the Echo becomes neutral.

Actions: Toll Tone. One creature within 30 ft. makes DC 12 Wisdom save or takes 4 psychic damage. Time Tug. Target within 20 ft. must succeed on DC 12 Strength save or lose 10 feet of movement on its next turn.

Reaction: Mark Cost. When a creature uses a shortcut without payment, the Echo gives that creature disadvantage on its next shortcut-related check.

Tactics: Slows, warns, and marks. It rarely pursues.

Morale/Deactivation: Deactivates when toll is paid, challenged successfully, or hp reaches 0.

Noncombat Resolution: Tools, Persuasion, Investigation, or History DC 13.

Safe Maximum: 3 PCs: one. 4 PCs: two. 5 PCs: two plus hazard. 6 PCs: three only if damage is spread.

Balance Warning: Repeated movement reduction can frustrate melee PCs; use it to create choices, not lockouts.

### Route Leech

Suggested CR: 1/8. XP: 25.

AC 12; HP 8; Speed 20 ft., climb 20 ft.

Ability Modifiers: Str -1, Dex +2, Con +1, Int -3, Wis +0, Cha -2.

Saves/Skills: Stealth +4.

Senses: blindsight 20 ft., passive Perception 10.

Languages: none.

Traits: Feeds on Hurry. The Leech has advantage on its first attack against a creature that dashed this round. Small Drain. A creature can remove an attached Leech with an action and DC 12 Athletics or Sleight of Hand check.

Actions: Attach. Melee Attack +4, reach 5 ft. Hit: 3 piercing damage, and the Leech attaches. While attached, target loses 5 feet of speed. The Leech deals 2 piercing damage at the start of the target's turn.

Reaction: Drop Away. When damaged by fire or radiant damage, the Leech detaches and falls prone.

Tactics: Attaches to fast movers and beacon carriers.

Morale/Deactivation: Falls off if target spends an action to remove it or if shortcut debt is paid nearby.

Noncombat Resolution: Survival DC 12 to avoid nest; Medicine or Sleight of Hand DC 12 to remove.

Safe Maximum: 3 PCs: two. 4 PCs: three. 5 PCs: four. 6 PCs: five if no other attackers.

Balance Warning: Low damage, but speed reduction stacks badly; do not attach more than two Leeches to one PC.

### Chalk Rival Echo

Suggested CR: 1/4. XP: 50.

AC 13; HP 16; Speed 30 ft.

Ability Modifiers: Str +0, Dex +2, Con +1, Int +1, Wis +1, Cha +2.

Saves/Skills: Acrobatics +4, Performance +4, Insight +3.

Senses: passive Perception 11.

Languages: Common.

Traits: Public Claim. The Echo has advantage on checks to contest route credit if the party copied a mark without changing or crediting it. Rival Flourish. First time the Echo is hit, it can turn partly to chalk and reduce damage by 3.

Actions: Chalk Slash. Melee Attack +4. Hit: 4 slashing damage. Comet Taunt. One creature within 30 ft. must succeed on DC 12 Wisdom save or have disadvantage on its next check made to patiently study a route.

Reaction: Countermark. When a PC marks a route, the Echo can force a DC 12 Dexterity or tools check to keep the mark clean.

Tactics: Taunts, races, and tries to make the party rush.

Morale/Deactivation: Deactivates when the party makes a lawful countermark, credits the rival, or beats it in a route check.

Noncombat Resolution: Performance, Persuasion, calligrapher's supplies, or Investigation DC 13.

Safe Maximum: One for 3-5 PCs; one plus Toll Echo for 6 PCs.

Balance Warning: It should feel like pressure and rivalry, not a deadly duel.

### Switchback Collapse Hazard

Suggested CR: 1 hazard. XP: 200 if overcome under pressure.

AC 15 for anchor points; HP 20 per major support; Speed 0 ft.

Ability Modifiers: Str +4, Dex -5, Con +4, Int -4, Wis +0, Cha -4.

Senses: none.

Traits: Collapse Stages. Stage 0 stable, Stage 1 shaking, Stage 2 falling sections, Stage 3 emergency retreat or extraction pressure. Stabilize. A successful tools, Athletics, Survival, or Arcana check DC 14 reduces stage by 1, once per round.

Actions: Falling Section. Initiative count 20 at Stage 1+. One creature on the switchback must make DC 13 Dexterity save or take 1d6 bludgeoning damage and fall prone. At Stage 2, two creatures are targeted. At Stage 3, a failed save also moves the creature 15 feet down-route.

Reaction: Strain. When three or more creatures stand on one weak section, stage increases by 1.

Tactics: Environmental clock. It pressures movement and stabilization.

Morale/Deactivation: Ends when party crosses, retreats, secures route, or stage is reduced to 0 and no one rushes.

Noncombat Resolution: Three successes before two failures, modified by cache supplies.

Safe Maximum: One hazard. Add Route Leeches sparingly.

Balance Warning: Do not combine Stage 3 with multiple hostile creatures for level 1 parties.

### Thread Door Ward

Suggested CR: 1/2. XP: 100.

AC 14; HP 24; Speed 0 ft., reach through threads 30 ft.

Ability Modifiers: Str +2, Dex +0, Con +2, Int +1, Wis +3, Cha +1.

Saves/Skills: Insight +5.

Senses: blindsight 60 ft.

Languages: Common and route cant.

Traits: Woven Claim. The Ward resists damage until a creature names one cost, owner, or challenge. Threaded Mercy. The Ward cannot reduce a creature below 1 hp on Floor 2.

Actions: Thread Lash. Melee Spell Attack +5, reach 30 ft. Hit: 5 force damage. Snare Claim. Target within 30 ft. must succeed on DC 13 Strength or Dexterity save or be restrained until end of its next turn.

Reaction: Tighten Debt. When a creature denies an obvious cost, the Ward imposes disadvantage on that creature's next check at the door.

Tactics: Restrains, asks, and punishes force. It stops when the rule is engaged.

Morale/Deactivation: Deactivates after three truthful payments/challenges, a successful group check, or hp 0.

Noncombat Resolution: Persuasion, Investigation, Arcana, History, or tools DC 14, three successes before two failures.

Safe Maximum: One.

Balance Warning: Use restraint for one round only; low-level characters should keep turns.

## Trial 2 Rewards and Boons

Base Trial 2 Rewards:

- Patient or normal clear: 20 NC salvage.
- Fast honest clear: 30 NC salvage.
- Route secured for future: 15 NC plus public route credit.
- Shortcut debt clear: 20 NC but one debt or owner mark.
- Forced retreat before F2-10: carried items only.
- Lore clue: "Silence owns the next dark."
- Public record: method of clear, time saved/lost, owner claim status.
- Route token: Threaded route token if the party pays, challenges, or secures a route cleanly.
- Shortcut mark: Gold thread under the Trial 2 record if speed was used honestly.

### Trial 2 Minor Boons

| Boon | Effect | Limit | Recharge or Expiration | Drawback/Story Hook | Balance Note |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Honest Shortcut Mark | Once, move through a known shortcut or difficult passage without triggering its first minor hazard | Once | Expires after Floor 4 | A rival can see the mark | Exploration-only bypass |
| Patient Step Thread | Add 1d4 to a check made to stabilize, secure, or prepare a route | Twice | Expires after Floor 5 | The thread slows your first impulse | Small skill support |
| Toll-Wise Palm | Advantage on one Insight check to identify hidden cost in a bargain or route | Once | Expires after Act I | Your palm itches near fair tolls too | Social/exploration only |
| Rival Chalk Spark | Mark a route so allies gain +1 to follow it for 1 hour | Once | Expires when used | Glass Comets recognize the style | Minor navigation aid |
| Owner's Courtesy | Pikkit or the floor waives one minor shortcut toll | Once | Expires after Floor 3 | Pikkit may ask a return favor | Narrow benefit |

## Trial 2 Outcome Packages

### 1. Patient Clear

Conditions: Party uses F2-2 and preparation, avoids shortcut debt.

Immediate Result: Floor 2 clear with careful public record.

Reward: 20 NC, Patient Step Thread, route clue.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: No scar; heat may cool by 1 if patience prevented danger.

Public Reaction: Practical respect, some rival mockery.

Faction Reaction: Salvage Union and Wardens approve; Spire Seekers tease.

Tower Reaction: Blue thread under Floor 2 mark.

Next-Session Opener: Floor 3 starts with a visible silent route.

How It Changes Floor 3: Noise tracker starts calm.

### 2. Fast Honest Clear

Conditions: Party uses shortcut after learning and naming cost.

Immediate Result: Fast clear without shortcut debt.

Reward: 30 NC, Honest Shortcut Mark.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: No shortcut debt; scar only if a hazard triggered separately.

Public Reaction: Strong attention and admiration.

Faction Reaction: Spire Seekers impressed; Guild sees brand value.

Tower Reaction: Gold thread glows cleanly.

Next-Session Opener: Floor 3 offers a loud/fast route.

How It Changes Floor 3: Loud route is easier to find but attracts attention faster.

### 3. Shortcut Debt Clear

Conditions: Party benefits from shortcut without paying, challenging, or naming owner.

Immediate Result: Clear with red-gold debt thread.

Reward: 20 NC, no route token.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: Shortcut debt attaches; debt-flagged parties feel it strongly.

Public Reaction: People debate whether the party stole a route.

Faction Reaction: Guild offers to finance or launder the claim; Ledger Court watches.

Tower Reaction: Door says, "Carried forward."

Next-Session Opener: Floor 3 echoes the unpaid claim.

How It Changes Floor 3: Choir of Recorded Deals includes shortcut debt verse.

### 4. Rival Mark Clear

Conditions: Party follows or copies Glass Comets route without clean countermark.

Immediate Result: Clear credited partly to rival route.

Reward: 20 NC, Rival Chalk Spark, rival complication.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: No scar by default; public credit split.

Public Reaction: Glass Comets gain attention too.

Faction Reaction: Spire Seekers frame it as rivalry.

Tower Reaction: Comet thread appears in record.

Next-Session Opener: Rival team challenges public record.

How It Changes Floor 3: Rival echo may repeat party's words.

### 5. Owner Bargain Clear

Conditions: Party bargains with Pikkit or pays fair toll.

Immediate Result: Clear through owner shortcut.

Reward: 25 NC, Owner's Courtesy or Toll-Wise Palm.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: No debt if terms were clear; sponsor pressure possible if sponsor paid.

Public Reaction: Some call it clever, some call it bought.

Faction Reaction: Guild appreciates; Wardens read terms.

Tower Reaction: Door records "bargain acknowledged."

Next-Session Opener: Pikkit sends a whisper about Floor 3.

How It Changes Floor 3: Listening Door recognizes owner courtesy once.

### 6. Collapse Survival

Conditions: F2-9 reaches dangerous collapse but party survives.

Immediate Result: Clear or retreat with dramatic record.

Reward: 15 NC if clear; scar risk for one exposed PC.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: Possible route scar; heat rises if reckless harm endangered others.

Public Reaction: Dramatic rumor spreads.

Faction Reaction: Salvage Union asks what failed; Spire Seekers cheer if no one died.

Tower Reaction: Switchback remains unstable unless secured.

Next-Session Opener: Floor 3 starts with armor sounds amplified.

How It Changes Floor 3: Noise begins at 1.

### 7. Extraction Used

Conditions: Party uses extraction on Floor 2.

Immediate Result: Exit with incomplete or partial clear unless extraction follows door resolution.

Reward: Carried salvage, public extraction record.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: Scar risk if before F2-10; shortcut debt may remain.

Public Reaction: Practical concern.

Faction Reaction: Hesta evaluates; rivals spin it.

Tower Reaction: Floor 2 remains open for return unless cleared.

Next-Session Opener: Nexus interlude or Floor 2 retry.

How It Changes Floor 3: No Floor 3 access until Floor 2 clear.

### 8. Forced Retreat

Conditions: Party retreats under pressure, fails door, or cannot resolve collapse.

Immediate Result: Floor incomplete.

Reward: Clues and carried goods only.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: Possible scar if collapse or debt active.

Public Reaction: Similar to Floor 1, but less forgiving if repeated.

Faction Reaction: Wardens prefer life; sponsors pressure a return.

Tower Reaction: The shortcut smiles wider next time.

Next-Session Opener: Retry with one altered route.

How It Changes Floor 3: No access until clear.

### 9. Route Secured for Future

Conditions: Party repairs F2-9, leaves warning, or lawfully claims abandoned shortcut.

Immediate Result: Clear with public service credit.

Reward: 25 NC, route token, Patient Step Thread.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: Heat cools by 1 if applicable.

Public Reaction: Strong practical respect.

Faction Reaction: Salvage Union and Last Light approve; rivals may resent.

Tower Reaction: Future-safe route glows blue.

Next-Session Opener: Floor 3 silent route opens more clearly.

How It Changes Floor 3: Party coordination starts at a better state.

### 10. Party Ignores the Rule

Conditions: Party insists shortcuts are free, destroys marks, or refuses all costs while taking benefits.

Immediate Result: Clear possible but debt thread follows.

Reward: 15 NC, no boon unless they later name the cost.

Scar/Debt/Heat Impact: Shortcut debt and possible heat.

Public Reaction: The story becomes messy.

Faction Reaction: CodeX amused; Ledger and Wardens wary; Guild opportunistic.

Tower Reaction: Thread Door says, "Unpaid does not mean free."

Next-Session Opener: Floor 3 records their exact denial.

How It Changes Floor 3: Echo attention starts at 1.

# BETWEEN FLOORS: Optional Nexus Interlude

Use this interlude if the party returns after Floor 2. If they continue directly to Floor 3, move to Floor 3 Strong Start and let these pressures arrive after Floor 3.

Read-Aloud:

> The Forecourt receives your Floor 2 record with less shock than Floor 1 and more appetite. People have learned your team can survive. Now they want to know whether you can be used, beaten, copied, or sold.

Who Approaches First: GUIDY if the clear was clean, Hesta if collapse or extraction happened, Felix if cache or shortcut mark was gained, Marik if heat or debt rose, sponsor representative if credit was claimed, CodeX if a shortcut mark or backdoor static appeared.

Public Reaction: Patient clears earn practical respect. Fast clears get cheers and rival attention. Shortcut debt clears start arguments. Route-secured clears gain strong goodwill among working runners.

Prices: Rope, chalk, and route tools rise by 1-2 NC after collapse stories. Reliable route advice rises by 5 NC after fast clears. Salvage Union discounts secured-route parties by 3 NC.

Rumors:

- "The second floor sells you time and charges interest."
- "Glass Comets got their chalk crossed."
- "Pikkit only bites people who pretend not to bargain."
- "Floor 3 is dark enough to hear lies."

Sponsors: Sponsors claim public credit if their mark appeared. If the party denies it honestly and has evidence, reduce sponsor pressure. If the party lets the sponsor lie, sponsor pressure rises.

GUIDY: "I have added a note: friendly architecture may still be predatory. This note is upsettingly transferable."

Rival Team: The Glass Comets post a public comparison time. If the party secured a route, they call it "charity work" while clearly being annoyed.

If Party Presses Directly to Floor 3: Skip public shopping and run Floor 3 with one carried state from Floor 2: noise calm, echo attention, shortcut debt, rival mark, or route confidence.

### Optional Scene 1. Runner's Cache Appraisal

NPC Goal: Felix wants to price the cache goods and learn whether the party stripped or respected it.

Player Choice: Sell salvage, disclose cache note, hide stripped supplies, ask about runner custom.

Check/DC: Insight DC 13 sees Felix respects restraint more than charity talk; Persuasion DC 14 improves price; Deception DC 15 hides stripped cache for now.

Reward: 5-15 NC or a discount on chalk/rope.

Consequence: If the party stripped the cache and lies, a runner rumor may expose it after Floor 3.

Hook to Floor 3: Felix says, "The third floor prices words, not gear."

### Optional Scene 2. Sponsor Claims Credit

NPC Goal: Sponsor wants public credit for the Floor 2 clear.

Player Choice: Accept credit, correct record, negotiate, use legal copy, refuse publicly.

Check/DC: Persuasion DC 15 limits credit; Legal Cant DC 14 cites registration terms; Insight DC 13 sees hidden escalation.

Reward: Sponsor benefit continues or shifts to cleaner terms.

Consequence: Letting false credit stand creates a recorded phrase Floor 3 may repeat.

Hook to Floor 3: Sponsor's exact words return in the Choir of Recorded Deals.

### Optional Scene 3. Marik Warns About Speed

NPC Goal: Marik wants the party to understand that fast public clears attract reckless imitators.

Player Choice: Share route warning, ask Wardens to post notice, dismiss him, confess shortcut debt.

Check/DC: Persuasion DC 13 gets Warden posting support; Insight DC 12 sees Marik is not criticizing success; History DC 13 recalls past runner stampede.

Reward: Public warning reduces one rival complication.

Consequence: Ignoring the warning increases rival pressure if collapse occurred.

Hook to Floor 3: Marik says the Tower records what people shout before they fall.

### Optional Scene 4. CodeX Wants the Shortcut Mark

NPC Goal: CodeX wants the party's shortcut mark data.

Player Choice: Sell, refuse, redact, trade for Floor 3 rumor, report contact.

Check/DC: Arcana DC 14 strips identifying data; Persuasion DC 14 demands payment; Insight DC 13 sees CodeX cares about owner logic more than gold.

Reward: 10 NC or a Floor 3 clue: "Silence is not empty; it is occupied."

Consequence: Sharing raw data increases Codebreaker attention and Warden suspicion.
